Thy voice, a balm that doth my sorrows steep,
Thy counsel, wise, to guide me from distress.
In thy true heart, my deepest secrets sleep,
Secure from harm, and free from all duress.
For in this world, where fickle friendships fade,
And loyalties are bought and sold for gain,
Thy steadfast love, a fortress newly made,
Doth shield me ever from the world's sharp pain.
So let us pledge our troth, and never part,
But keep each other's welfare in our heart.

###127###
The busy world, with all its vain pursuits,
Doth chase for gold, and earthly, fleeting fame,
And trample down the tender, verdant shoots
Of simple joy, and whisper virtue's name.
They sow their seeds in barren, stony roots,
And hope for harvest, but to bear the shame
Of empty hands, and bitter, sour fruits,
When time's swift scythe doth claim their earthly claim.
But I do seek a treasure, more profound,
A wealth of love, a peace that shall endure,
Where true affection may at last be found,
And faith's bright promise ever shall be sure.
So let them grasp at shadows, if they will,
My soul shall feast on love, and be content still.

###128###
When I do look upon thy gentle face,
And see the stars that in thine eyes do gleam,
My heart doth leap, and finds its rightful place,
Lost in the rapture of a waking dream.
Thy rosy cheeks, where beauty doth embrace,
Thy lips that smile, a captivating stream
Of sweetest grace, that time cannot erase,
Nor envious years their brightness over-teem.
So must I praise thee, till my dying breath,
And laud thy virtues, till my tongue is still,
For thou art fairer than all life and death,
A perfect form, that doth my spirit fill.
And should I fail to speak thy praises true,
My very soul would weep for lack of you.

###129###
The fleeting hours, like shadows, swiftly glide,
And steal away the bloom of youth's bright morn.
The joys we chase, do often turn and hide,
And leave us lonely, weary, and forlorn.
The schemes we weave, with careful, cunning pride,
Are torn asunder ere the day is born.
The worldly wealth, we hoard with anxious stride,
Is but a dust, when all our hopes are shorn.
So let us build our house on firmer ground,
On love's sure rock, that time cannot assail.
Let kindness be the only wealth we've found,
And faithfulness, that never shall prevail
Against the tempests of this mortal strife,
But be the anchor of our transient life.

###130###
When absence doth thy beauteous form conceal,
And miles between our loving hearts do lie,
My soul doth yearn, and all its pains reveal,
Beneath the vastness of the weeping sky.
No earthly comfort can my spirit heal,
No pleasant sight can make my sorrow fly.
I count the moments, till again I feel
Thy warm embrace, and see thee with mine eye.
The days are long, the nights are dark and deep,
And every thought doth turn to thy dear face.
My lonely vigil I do sadly keep,
And pine for thee, in this deserted place.
Yet know this truth, though distance may divide,
My love for thee shall evermore abide.

###131###
The world's applause, a siren's tempting sound,
Doth lure men on to peril and to woe.
They seek the heights, where fleeting glories bound,
And plant their banners, where the tempests blow.
They build their castles on the shifting ground,
And think them safe, but soon the waters flow,
And sweep them down, where no relief is found,
Their empty dreams to darkness they bestow.
But let me dwell where quiet joys reside,
And simple truths my humble spirit find.
Let modest virtue be my constant guide,
And leave the fleeting honours to mankind.
For in the soul, true riches we may keep,
While worldly vanities do softly sleep.

###132###
Thy voice, a melody that doth entrance,
Thy smile, a dawn that breaks the darkest night.
When I do gaze upon thee, in a trance,
My soul doth soar on wings of pure delight.
No fairer creature, in this earthly dance,
Could e'er be found, to gladden mortal sight.
Thy every movement doth my heart advance,
And fills my being with a wondrous light.
So let me serve thee, till my life is done,
And offer up my devotion, pure and true.
For in thy love, a victory is won,
That makes my very existence feel anew.
And should I falter, in this task assigned,
My spirit then would truly be unkind.

###133###
The winter's chill, that nips the tender bud,
Doth speak of change, and nature's stern decree.
The icy grip, that stills the flowing blood,
Reminds the soul of frail mortality.
The frozen earth, where no green thing doth stud,
A barren sight for all the eye can see.
The naked trees, that stand in solitude,
Lament the loss of summer's company.
Yet in this bleakness, hope doth still reside,
A promise whispered of the coming spring.
The hidden life, that doth within abide,
Will soon emerge, and joyful tidings bring.
So too my heart, though sorrow may pervade,
Shall bloom anew, when winter's reign is stayed.

###134###
When envious Fortune doth her favour lend
To those who do not merit such a boon,
And honest worth, she doth with scorn transcend,
And casteth shadows on the brightest noon.
The wicked thrive, and worldly riches spend,
While virtue struggles, late or ever soon.
The unjust cause doth often gain the end,
And fairness withers like a faded rune.
But trust in Time, whose judgment is serene,
And though he tarry, he shall sure arrive.
He will reveal what now is kept unseen,
And cause the truth and righteousness to thrive.
So let us wait, with patience in our breast,
And leave the outcome to his final test.

###135###
Thy eyes, like pools, where stars themselves do dwell,
Reflect the heavens, in their depth profound.
Thy voice, a charm, that doth my senses quell,
And holds me captive, with its dulcet sound.
Thy gentle touch, a magic I can tell,
Where sweetest ecstasies do brightly bound.
My heart, thy willing servant, doth compel
My every thought, to where thy grace is found.
So let me kneel, and offer up my vow,
To be thy lover, till the end of days.
No other object shall my spirit bow,
But only thee, in all thy wondrous ways.
And should my love prove false, or turn to dust,
Then let me perish, by my own just lust.

###136###
The fleeting joys that human hearts pursue,
Like painted butterflies, do flutter by.
They gleam and dazzle, with a colour new,
And vanish swift, beneath the passing sky.
The gilded hopes, that seem so bright and true,
Do melt like frost, when summer doth draw nigh.
The worldly treasures, we do hold to view,
Are but as shadows, that the winds will dry.
But let us seek a treasure, more esteemed,
A lasting peace, within the soul's deep core.
A love that shines, more brightly than it seemed,
And binds us fast, forevermore.
For in this realm, where truest worth is found,
Our spirits shall in endless bliss abound.

###137###
When I do think on all the days we've shared,
And count the moments, precious and so dear,
My heart doth swell, with memories unimpaired,
And banishes all doubt and anxious fear.
The sun that shone, the trials that we dared,
Have forged a bond, that time cannot make sere.
Thy steadfast love, hath ever me prepared,
To face the world, and hold thy presence near.
So let us tread, this path of life as one,
With kindred souls, and hearts that beat as one.
Until our earthly race is truly run,
And our last earthly, fleeting task is done.
Then shall we find, beyond the veil of night,
A union made, of everlasting light.

###138###
The passing years, like rivers, onward flow,
And bear us swiftly to the ocean vast.
The youthful bloom, that did so brightly glow,
Is dimmed by age, its brilliance overcast.
The strength we had, begins at last to go,
And weary limbs, their vigour have surpassed.
The hair grows white, the furrows deepen slow,
And life's swift journey, hastens to its last.
Yet in this change, a wisdom we may find,
To cherish moments, ere they disappear.
To leave no trace of folly far behind,
But live with purpose, banishing all fear.
For though our bodies may to dust return,
The lessons learned, shall ever brightly burn.

###139###
When envious eyes do gaze with scornful mien,
And whisper falsehoods, where no fault is found,
My spirit sinks, by unjust censure keen,
And feels the weight of sorrow's heavy bound.
My honest deeds, though pure and brightly seen,
Are twisted thus, on rumour's blighted ground.
No shield of truth can pierce their clouded screen,
Nor innocence, their judgment can confound.
Yet I shall stand, though calumny assail,
And bear my burden with a noble grace.
For in the end, my conscience shall prevail,
And truth's bright beam shall light this darkened space.
So let them rail, their malice shall not stain,
The inner peace, that time cannot restrain.

###140###
Thy love, a beacon in the storm's dark rage,
Doth guide my vessel to a peaceful shore.
When doubt doth rise, and troubles do engage,
Thy constant faith doth strengthen me the more.
No fickle tide can turn this faithful page,
No passing whim can make my spirit soar
To other loves, or from this happy stage,
Where our two souls in sweet accord do pour.
So let us build, on this foundation strong,
A love that time itself shall not decay.
Where every breath, and every whispered song,
Doth speak of us, until our dying day.
And when our journey ends, and spirits flee,
Our love shall live, eternally.

###141###
When all the world doth seem a stage of woe,
And heavy cares do press upon my soul,
Thy gentle smile, a comforting soft glow,
Doth make my broken spirit once more whole.
The seeds of joy, that in thy presence grow,
Do banish shadows, and my heart control.
No fairer sight, that mortal eyes do know,
Can bring such solace, or such sweet enrol.
So let me rest, within thy loving care,
And cast aside all troubles of the mind.
For in thy arms, all burdens I can bear,
And leave the weary, fretful world behind.
And thus refreshed, by love's most tender art,
I find new strength, within my grateful heart.


###142###
When first I saw thy visage, fair and bright,
My heart did leap, as doth a bird in spring,
And banished from my soul all former night,
To thee my thoughts did ever gladly cling.
Thy voice, a melody so sweet and clear,
Doth charm my senses and my spirit raise,
Dispelling all my doubt and every fear,
And filling me with love's enchanted haze.
But ah, this joy is tinctured with regret,
For what I wish, I know I can't attain,
A love so pure, I fear I shall forget,
And in this longing, find my endless pain.
   Yet still I love, though fate my hopes deny,
   And in thy beauty, live and long to die.

###143###
The sun doth rise, and gild the eastern sky,
A golden orb, to chase the shadows deep,
But in my breast, a darker sun doth lie,
That wakes my sorrow from its weary sleep.
For since thou art departed from my sight,
The world is draped in colours pale and dim,
No joy can penetrate this endless night,
Nor music lift me from this doleful whim.
I search in vain for comfort, but 'tis gone,
As summer's bloom doth wither in the frost,
And I am left, a wanderer alone,
My dearest treasure utterly now lost.
   So let me mourn, till life itself shall cease,
   And in the grave, find my eternal peace.

###144###
Thy brow is like a marble, smooth and white,
Where thoughts of beauty ever seem to dwell,
Thy eyes, twin stars that shine with purest light,
And cast upon my soul a magic spell.
Thy lips, like roses, kissed by morning dew,
Do promise sweetness, and a tender grace,
And all thy form, a vision fair and true,
Doth fill with rapture every time and place.
But art thou real, or but a painted dream,
A fleeting phantom, born of my desire,
That fades when I approach its golden gleam,
And leaves me burning with unquenched fire?
   I know not, yet I love, and would embrace,
   The phantom beauty of thy lovely face.

###145###
My love for thee, a river strong and deep,
Doth flow with ardour, never to be stayed,
And all my vows, I solemnly do keep,
To thee, my darling, in this earthly glade.
No storm can shake the roots of this my love,
No winter chill can freeze its fervent heat,
It is a gift, sent from the heavens above,
A solace for my heart, so bittersweet.
But ah, what if my love be cast aside,
And thou shouldst turn thy gaze to other shores,
Then would my very soul be petrified,
And I would weep, and curse my cruel stars.
   Yet hope remains, though veiled in darkest doubt,
   That love's true compass will still guide us out.

###146###
The hours steal by, on silent, winged feet,
And bear me onward to my destined end,
Each moment lost, a loss I can't defeat,
A treasure vanished, that I can't re-lend.
The years, like leaves that fall from autumn trees,
Do scatter all my youth and vigour past,
And leave me bowed by time's relentless breeze,
A lonely mariner, with sails downcast.
My strength doth fail, my sight begins to wane,
My once-bright wit grows clouded and obscure,
And all my efforts to recall remain,
As faint as echoes, that will not endure.
   So let me ponder on what I have known,
   Before my final, silent seed is sown.

###147###
Shall I compare thee to a summer's day?
Thou art more lovely, and more temperate far,
Rough winds do shake the darling buds of May,
And summer's lease hath all too short a star.
Sometime too hot the eye of heaven shines,
And often is his gold complexion dimm'd;
And every fair from fair sometime declines,
By chance, or nature's changing course untrimm'd;
But thy eternal summer shall not fade,
Nor lose possession of that fair thou ow'st;
Nor shall Death brag thou wander'st in his shade,
When in eternal lines to time thou grow'st.
   So long as men can breathe, or eyes can see,
   So long lives this, and this gives life to thee.

###148###
My love is like a rose, whose fragrant breath,
Doth fill the air with sweetness and delight,
But should it wither, facing certain death,
Then all my world would be plunged into night.
I cherish thee, as sailors prize the shore,
When tossed about by tempest's angry might,
And would not trade thy presence, evermore,
For all the treasures that the world can write.
But oh, what sorrow gnaws within my breast,
To think that time, the thief of all things fair,
May steal thee from me, putting love to test,
And leave me lost, in sorrow and despair.
   Yet still I cling to hope, though faint it seem,
   And live within this bright, beloved dream.

###149###
The moon, a pearl, doth hang in velvet skies,
And casts a silver glow on sleeping earth,
But in my heart, a different light now lies,
A burning passion, of celestial birth.
Thy beauty shines, a beacon in the dark,
A guiding star, to steer my errant soul,
And every glance thou giv'st, doth leave its mark,
And makes my wounded spirit once more whole.
I gaze upon thee, with a lover's eye,
And find within thy features, all I crave,
A perfect vision, that can never die,
A timeless beauty, that will e'er engrave.
   So let me worship thee, with fervent prayer,
   And in thy love, find solace past compare.

###150###
When absence doth the weary spirit seize,
And miles do stretch between what hearts desire,
Then memory, on whispers of the breeze,
Doth stir within my soul a living fire.
I see thy face, though leagues do intervene,
Thy voice I hear, though silence fills the air,
And in this dream, my joys are felt again,
A sweet relief from sorrow and from care.
But oh, the pain, when waking brings the truth,
That thou art gone, and I am left alone,
A barren land, devoid of joy and youth,
Where sorrow's seeds are plentifully sown.
   Yet still I dream, and find in dreams my all,
   Until reality doth sadly call.

###151###
The summer's heat doth make the world perspire,
And wilting flowers bow their weary heads,
But in my heart, a never-dying fire,
For thee, my love, eternally it spreads.
Thy presence is a balm to all my ills,
A cooling draught, when thirst doth paralyse,
And with thy smile, my anxious spirit stills,
And finds a haven in thy gentle eyes.
But shouldst thou leave, and wander far from me,
Then would this fire consume me with its rage,
And I, a cinder, lost eternally,
Would turn life's last and desolate, sad page.
   So let me hold thee close, and ne'er release,
   And in thy love, find everlasting peace.

###152###
My quill doth dance, with words of passion bold,
To paint the portrait of thy loveliness,
A tale of love, in verses to be told,
And banish from my soul all weariness.
Thy eyes, like jewels, that sparkle and do gleam,
Do capture all the light the sun can lend,
And in their depths, I see a waking dream,
A world of joy, on which I can depend.
Thy voice, a music, that doth charm my ear,
Doth banish sorrow, and all worldly strife,
And when thou speak'st, my spirit holds thee dear,
And finds in thee, the very breath of life.
   So let me write, till all my ink is spent,
   And with these lines, my true love be content.

###153###
The winter's frost doth bite with icy sting,
And strip the branches bare of leafy pride,
But in my heart, a constant warmth doth spring,
Wherein thy love doth evermore reside.
No chill can touch this fervent, inner flame,
No storm can quench its bright and steady glow,
For thou art all, and I do speak thy name,
As seeds in spring, that to the sunlight grow.
But oh, if fate should part us, far apart,
Then would this flame turn ashes, cold and grey,
And leave me frozen, with a broken heart,
To wander lost, and mourn the dying day.
   So let us cling, ere time doth us divide,
   And in our love, forevermore abide.

###154###
When worldly cares do press upon my mind,
And shadows lengthen, casting doubt and fear,
A solace in thy gentle love I find,
That makes the path ahead appear so clear.
Thy wisdom, like a beacon, shines so bright,
And guides my footsteps through the darkest night,
Dispelling gloom with rays of purest light,
And filling me with hope and sweet delight.
But shouldst thou falter, or thy counsel cease,
Then would I be adrift on stormy seas,
And lose the calm, and sweet, internal peace,
That only thy wise words can bring to ease.
   So let me heed thee, with a heart so true,
   And in thy guidance, find my strength anew.

###155###
The fleeting moments of this life do pass,
Like shadows fleeting on a sunlit wall,
And all our dreams, as fragile as spun glass,
Do shatter when the final moments call.
My youth, that once did bloom with vigour strong,
Now fades away, like mist before the sun,
And all the songs that I was wont to throng,
Are hushed, their vibrant melody outrun.
My face is lined, my hair is streaked with grey,
My strength doth dwindle, as the ebbing tide,
And soon I know, I'll pass from mortal day,
Where silent shades eternally do bide.
   Yet in thy love, a timeless joy I see,
   That shall outlive the frail mortality of me.

###156###
Thy laughter rings, a melody so sweet,
It doth outshine the lark's melodious tune,
And makes my very soul with joy replete,
Beneath the gaze of sun or shining moon.
Thy smile, a ray of sunshine, pure and warm,
Doth chase away the clouds that mar my day,
And shields my heart from every coming storm,
And lights my spirit on its onward way.
But should that laughter cease, that smile should fade,
Then would my world be plunged in deepest woe,
And I, a wretch, by sorrow would be swayed,
And watch my brightest, fairest prospects go.
   So let me cherish thee, and all thy grace,
   And in thy joy, find my appointed place.

###157###
The rose doth bloom, and then its petals fall,
The summer's glory fades to winter's chill,
And all things fair, obey time's urgent call,
And to its silent mandate must be still.
My love for thee, a passion fierce and deep,
Doth fear the hand of time, that steals away,
The youthful bloom, whilst we are fast asleep,
And turns our brightest moments into grey.
But though the seasons change, and years do fly,
My love for thee shall constant ever be,
A steadfast star, within the changing sky,
A truth eternal, for all eyes to see.
   So let us bind our hearts, and hold them fast,
   Against the ravages of time that blast.

###158###
When weary thoughts do throng my troubled mind,
And worries press, with burdens hard to bear,
A gentle solace in thy love I find,
A calming influence, beyond compare.
Thy voice, a balm, that soothes my anxious soul,
Thy presence, like a haven, safe and warm,
Doth make my fractured spirit once more whole,
And shields me from life's tempest and its storm.
But shouldst thou vanish, and thy light depart,
Then would I wander, lost in darkest night,
With shattered dreams, and a consuming smart,
Bereft of guidance, and of all delight.
   So let me cling to thee, my dearest friend,
   On whom my hopes and my best dreams depend.

###159###
The fleeting joy of youth doth quickly fly,
Like birds that wing their way to distant lands,
And leaves behind a tear within the eye,
And memories held within time's fading hands.
My strength declines, my vigour starts to wane,
My hair, once dark, is now of silver hue,
And all my former vigour I can't regain,
As morning mists are scattered by the dew.
But still my love for thee, it doth endure,
A constant flame, that burns with steady light,
And makes my passing days feel bright and pure,
And fills my fading vision with delight.
   So let me love thee, till my breath is done,
   My last, true heart's desire, my only one.

###160###
Thy gaze doth pierce my soul with tender light,
And makes my spirit soar on wings of joy,
Dispelling shadows of the darkest night,
And from my heart all worldly cares destroy.
Thy words, like music, sweet and soft they fall,
And fill my ears with melodies divine,
Responding to love's ever-urgent call,
And making all thy beauty wholly mine.
But ah, what if this vision should depart,
And thou shouldst turn thy lovely face away,
Then would a darkness seize my very heart,
And turn my brightest morning into grey.
   So let me hold thee close, and ne'er release,
   And in thy love, find everlasting peace.

###161###
The golden sun doth set with fiery grace,
And paints the western sky with hues of rose,
But in my heart, a deeper light doth trace,
The boundless love that ever truly grows.
Thy beauty shines, a star that doth not fade,
A timeless portrait, etched within my mind,
And in thy presence, all my fears are stayed,
And sweetest solace I am sure to find.
But should this light be veiled, this beauty dim,
Then would my world be plunged in dark despair,
And I, a wretch, upon a lonely whim,
Would wander lost, and breathing naught but air.
   So let me gaze upon thee, and adore,
   And love thee, now and for evermore.

###162###
When fickle fortune turns her fickle wheel,
And casts us down from heights of high estate,
The wounds of loss we deeply then do feel,
And curse the cruel and arbitrary fate.
But in thy heart, a constancy I find,
A steadfast truth, that time cannot assail,
A love so pure, it leaves all doubts behind,
And triumphs over every earthly gale.
Thy spirit, like a rock, doth stand so strong,
Against the battering of time and tide,
And to its strength, my weary soul doth long,
And in its sheltering arms, doth safely hide.
   So let me trust in thee, my constant star,
   No matter where our earthly fortunes are.

###163###
The blooming rose, that scents the summer air,
Doth fade and wither when the season turns,
And all things fair, their transient beauty share,
As life's bright candle briefly gleams and burns.
My youth, that once did boast of vigour bold,
Now yields to time, the thief of all that's fine,
And all my stories, destined to be told,
Grow faint and dim, like memories of wine.
But in thy love, a constant spring I see,
A living fountain, that shall never cease,
And by its grace, I am renewed in thee,
And find in thee, my everlasting peace.
   So let me love thee, till my last breath's drawn,
   My dearest treasure, from dusk until the dawn.###162###
When Fortune smiles and grants me fair estate,
My friends do flock and round about me throng,
They speak me fair, and whisper words of state,
And deem my worth beyond all earthly song.
But when the winds of adverse fortune blow,
And cast me down from heights of wealthy pride,
Then friends do vanish, like the winter snow,
And leave me naked, with no place to hide.
So true is this, that I have learned to know,
The hollow hearts that in fair seeming dwell,
And prize the few, whose love doth truly glow,
Against the tempest, they shall stand and tell.
  For in their souls, a nobler flame doth burn,
  Than fleeting favour, which doth swiftly turn.

###163###
My lady’s eyes, like stars that shine afar,
Do pierce my heart with shafts of sweet desire,
And every glance doth leave a shining scar,
Which burns within, with ever-feeding fire.
Her voice, a melody that doth enchant,
Doth steal away my reason and my sense,
And every word, a sacred, holy chant,
That holds my captive soul in sweet suspense.
Her lips, like roses, kissed by morning dew,
Do promise joys that mortal tongue can’t tell,
And in their touch, my spirit drinks anew,
The nectar’d draught, from which I cannot quell.
  O, let me ever in this thrall remain,
  And in her love, my true delight attain.

###164###
The fleeting hours, like thieves in silent night,
Do steal away the blossoms of my prime,
And leave behind a withered, somber sight,
Where once did bloom the fairest buds of time.
The raven locks, that graced my youthful brow,
Now turn to silver, touched by winter’s hand,
And strength doth wane, that I did boast ere now,
As sands run out upon a barren strand.
Yet in my heart, a younger spirit dwells,
That scorns the years, and yearns for joys of old,
And oft, when weary age my body quells,
My mind doth leap, with tales yet to be told.
  So let me live, whilst breath doth still remain,
  And chase the phantom joys that can’t be slain.

###165###
When contemplation doth my thoughts embrace,
And outward shows no longer hold me bound,
I seek within, a more celestial space,
Where truth and beauty ever can be found.
The world’s vain clamour then doth fade away,
And quiet contemplation holds its reign,
No fleeting passion doth my soul betray,
But reason’s light, that doth all error stain.
Here, in this sanctuary, I find my peace,
And gaze upon the stars with clearer eye,
Where earthly cares do swiftly find release,
And wisdom’s gentle currents softly fly.
  For in this realm, my truest self I see,
  And learn the secrets of eternity.

###166###
My love, that like a river, strong and deep,
Doth flow through all the valleys of my mind,
Doth banish cares, and secrets doth it keep,
The truest treasure that I e’er could find.
It knows no ebb, no shifting of the tide,
But constant as the sun, it doth impart,
A warmth that banishes all chill and pride,
And mends the broken pieces of my heart.
Let others seek their fortunes far and wide,
And chase the shadows that the world doth show,
My only wealth is in my love’s sweet side,
Where happiness and lasting joys do grow.
  So let me love, with all my soul’s desire,
  And feed my heart with this celestial fire.

###167###
The fleeting moments, like a hurried guest,
Do pass unheeded, ere we mark their flight,
And leave behind no comfort, nor no rest,
But hasten onward to eternal night.
The sun doth rise, and then doth sink to sleep,
The moon doth wax, and then doth softly wane,
And all that lives, its final course must keep,
And taste the bitter draught of earthly pain.
Yet in the face of this, I find a hope,
A lasting love, that time cannot destroy,
That through the trials, shall my spirit cope,
And find in sorrow, a most precious joy.
  For love endures, when all else turns to dust,
  A sacred flame, in which we place our trust.

###168###
When envy’s venom doth my spirit sting,
And jealous whispers poison all my days,
I turn my thoughts to what my muse doth sing,
And find a solace in her gentle praise.
She paints no colours of this mortal strife,
But sings of beauty, virtue, and of truth,
And fills my soul with a more vibrant life,
And brings me back the vigour of my youth.
Her melodies do soothe my troubled breast,
And chase away the shadows of despair,
And in her verse, I find a sweet release,
From worldly woes, and burdens I must bear.
  So let me write, whilst inspiration gleams,
  And weave my thoughts into immortal dreams.

###169###
My fairest youth, that like a summer’s day,
Did shine so bright, with promise and with bloom,
Hath felt the touch of time, and passed away,
And left me wrestling with impending doom.
The strength I knew, the vigour of my limb,
Now scarce suffice to bear my weary frame,
And all the joys that once did brightly swim,
Are but faint echoes of a dying flame.
Yet in my heart, a spark doth still remain,
A stubborn will, that will not yield to age,
And though my body suffereth from pain,
My spirit still doth turn a hopeful page.
  For in the soul, a power doth reside,
  That scorns the weakness of the outward tide.

###170###
The courtier’s smile, a mask of false delight,
Doth hide a heart of malice and of greed,
And gilded words, that glitter in the light,
Do sow the seeds of treachery and need.
They fawn and flatter, when the sun doth shine,
But turn their backs when clouds begin to form,
And seek their gain, with purposes malign,
And shelter safe within the passing storm.
I’ve seen their craft, their subtle, serpent’s art,
And learned to trust a simpler, honest soul,
Whose loyal heart doth play a truer part,
And seeks no glory, nor to take control.
  For in plain truth, a greater worth doth lie,
  Than all the falsehoods that the great ones ply.

###171###
When winter’s breath doth chill the very soul,
And frozen earth doth hold the world in thrall,
My thoughts do turn to where the seasons roll,
And dream of spring, that shall again enthrall.
The barren branches, stark against the sky,
Do promise life, though buried deep within,
And though the winds do mournfully do cry,
A brighter season shall ere long begin.
So too my heart, though now in sorrow bound,
Doth hold a hope, a seed of future joy,
That shall in time, its verdant beauty found,
And all my present grief shall then destroy.
  For after night, the dawn will surely break,
  And from the slumber, life shall then awake.

###172###
My dearest friend, whose presence is a balm,
To every sorrow that my soul doth know,
Whose counsel wise doth keep my spirit calm,
And helps my fragile inner self to grow.
When doubts do cloud my mind, and fears arise,
Your steadfast faith doth banish all dismay,
And in your truth, a guiding star applies,
To lead me safely on life’s winding way.
Your honest heart, a treasure to behold,
Doth scorn the petty squabbles of the crowd,
And in your friendship, richer far than gold,
My spirit finds a solace and a shroud.
  So let me hold you ever close to me,
  My truest comrade, till eternity.

###173###
The passing years, like swift-winged messengers,
Do bear away the bloom of youthful grace,
And leave behind the scars and dull censers,
Of time’s relentless, unforgiving pace.
The laughter sweet, that once did fill the air,
Is hushed to murmurs of a distant past,
And strength doth wane, replaced by weary care,
As shadows lengthen, and the die is cast.
Yet in my mind, the memories remain,
Of golden days, and joys that can’t be told,
And though the body suffers from the strain,
The spirit’s fire shall ne’er grow faint and cold.
  For what is lost, is gained in wisdom’s store,
  And richer for the trials gone before.

###174###
When musing deep, on life’s perplexing maze,
And seeking solace from the world’s harsh strife,
I find a comfort in the sun’s bright rays,
And in the gentle hum of humming life.
The robin’s song, that greets the morning light,
The babbling brook, that winds its silver way,
Do speak of peace, and banish anxious fright,
And bid my troubled spirit gently stay.
The scent of flowers, on the summer breeze,
Doth fill my senses with a sweet perfume,
And nature’s balm, beneath the leafy trees,
Doth chase away all traces of the gloom.
  For in her breast, true solace can be found,
  Where peace and beauty ever do abound.

###175###
The fleeting pleasures of this mortal stage,
Like painted scenes, do vanish from the sight,
And leave behind no lasting, printed page,
But fleeting phantoms in the fading light.
The lover’s kiss, the victor’s proud acclaim,
The miser’s hoard, the poet’s whispered fame,
Do all dissolve, like mist before the flame,
And leave no substance, but a hollow name.
Yet in my heart, a greater prize I hold,
A love that’s constant, and will ne’er decay,
More precious far than gems or finest gold,
That shall endure, and never pass away.
  For love’s true worth, no earthly power can steal,
  A lasting joy, that time shall e’er reveal.

###176###
When melancholy doth my spirit seize,
And dark despair doth cast its heavy shade,
I seek the solace of the whispering trees,
Where nature’s quiet beauty is displayed.
The gentle rustling of the verdant leaves,
Doth soothe my soul, and banish anxious thought,
And in the peace that woodland quiet weaves,
A greater strength and comfort I have sought.
The birds do sing, with voices clear and bright,
A symphony that bids my sorrow cease,
And fills my heart with pure and calm delight,
And grants my weary spirit sweet release.
  So let me walk where nature’s peace resides,
  And find the strength that in her soul abides.

###177###
The fickle crowd, with ever-changing mind,
Doth praise the brave, and then condemn their deed,
And truth itself, they scarcely seek to find,
But follow passions, planting bitter seed.
They cheer the victor, when the prize is won,
But scorn the vanquished, fallen in the dust,
And shift their gaze, when darker days have run,
And break their promises, and shed their trust.
I’ve learned to scorn their fickle, fleeting praise,
And seek a judgment from a nobler source,
That sees beyond the fleeting, outward phase,
And measures worth by virtue’s steady course.
  For in a heart that’s true, true worth doth dwell,
  Beyond the whisper and the passing bell.

###178###
My ink, a stream from sorrow’s deepest well,
Doth flow to paint the portrait of my pain,
Each word a tear, each phrase a mournful knell,
That echoes back the echoes of my strain.
The parchment pale, a witness to my woe,
Doth bear the imprint of a heavy heart,
And through the lines, my inner torments show,
A broken spirit, torn and rent apart.
Yet in this grief, a strange release I find,
A cleansing power in the act of writ,
And though the wounds remain, I leave behind,
A testament, where shadows softly flit.
  So let my tears, upon this page descend,
  And find in verse, a solace and a friend.

###179###
The mirror shows a face I scarce do know,
With lines of age, where youth did brightly bloom,
And silver threads, where raven locks did grow,
A silent harbinger of coming doom.
The strength I boasted, now doth much decline,
And weary limbs do ache with constant plea,
The days of revel, past their joyous prime,
Now but a whisper from eternity.
Yet in my soul, a younger spirit burns,
That scorns the weakness of the outward guise,
And though the body from its vigour turns,
The mind still dreams, and in its vision flies.
  So let me live whilst breath doth still remain,
  And find in spirit, what the flesh doth gain.

###180###
When worldly cares do press upon my soul,
And vexing doubts do cloud my weary mind,
I turn my gaze, beyond their harsh control,
To find a peace that’s true and undefiled.
The distant hills, in purple majesty,
Do stand serene, beneath the azure sky,
And speak of rest, and sweet serenity,
Where earthly troubles swiftly pass me by.
The clouds that drift, like ships upon the blue,
Do show a world where troubles have no sway,
And in this vastness, hopes again renew,
And chase the shadows of despair away.
  For in the grand design, a solace lies,
  That calms the storm within my troubled eyes.

###181###
The lover’s vow, a fragile, fleeting thing,
Doth often break, like glass upon the stone,
And vows of faith, like summer birds do sing,
Then fly away, and leave the heart alone.
The promises, that once did brightly gleam,
Do fade and tarnish, as the seasons turn,
And leave behind a hollow, bitter dream,
Where trust did dwell, now ashes dimly burn.
Yet there are souls, whose constancy doth shine,
A beacon bright, against the stormy sea,
Whose loyal hearts, in purpose so divine,
Do prove that lasting love can truly be.
  So let me cherish such a faithful band,
  And in their truth, forever take my stand.

###182###
My pen, a tool with which I do contend,
With fleeting thoughts that dance within my head,
And with each stroke, my passion doth extend,
And bring to light what words have left unsaid.
The ink doth flow, a dark and secret stream,
That paints the visions that my soul doth keep,
And turns to form a captivating dream,
Or wakes the sorrow from its slumber deep.
From silent thought, to lines of black and white,
My muse doth guide, with sure and steady hand,
And conjure worlds, of shadow and of light,
That shall forever in the pages stand.
  So let me write, whilst inspiration gleams,
  And capture life within these fleeting dreams.
###182###
Whenas the sun doth paint the eastern skies,
And bids the slumbering world awake from night,
My heart, with joyful expectation, flies
To seek thine image, bathed in morning light.
But lo, the shadows of my fear do creep,
And whisper tales of love's uncertain stay,
Lest beauty's bloom, ere it hath time to keep,
Should wither and from my fond sight away.
Yet hope, a fragile bird, doth build her nest
Within the chambers of my longing soul,
And there, with sweet assurance, takes her rest,
To make my troubled spirit sound and whole.
So trust I in thy faith, though storms may brew,
My constant love shall ever burn for you.

###183###
The world's a stage, and we but players here,
Each to our part assigned, for good or ill,
And fortunes shift, dispelling joy or fear,
As fate doth spin its ever-turning wheel.
The proudest king may fall from his high seat,
The beggar rise to wealth beyond his dream,
And all our striving, bitter and yet sweet,
Is but a passing, momentary gleam.
For what is power, or what is earthly store,
When dust shall claim us, and our name forgot?
We chase the wind, and ask for something more,
Than what this fleeting, transient life hath got.
Thus, let us live, with virtue as our guide,
And in true love, let all our cares subside.

###184###
Thy beauty's grace, a balm to sorrow's sting,
Doth shine upon me, like a guiding star,
And in its radiance, my spirits sing,
Dispelling shadows, though they linger far.
The gentle curve of thine enchanting smile,
The liquid depth of thine expressive eye,
Doth hold my captive heart, and thus beguile
Me into dreams, where naught but pleasures lie.
But oh, when absence doth my soul oppress,
And thou art distant, like the moon afar,
My heart doth ache with lonely helplessness,
And every moment seems a bitter scar.
Yet still I hope, that love will find its way,
And bring thee back, to brighten this my day.

###185###
The fickle wind, that doth the willow sway,
And whispers secrets through the leafy boughs,
Doth change its temper many times a day,
And seldom keeps the promises it vows.
So too, I find, do human hearts oft prove,
Inconstant in their feelings, warm and bright,
One moment fervent in their passionate love,
The next, estranged, and lost to fading light.
Beware then, friend, of pledges made in haste,
And trust not wholly to a fleeting word,
For love, like summer, may too quickly waste,
And leave behind a winter, stark and stirred.
Let actions speak, where eloquence doth fail,
And honest deeds, a truer love unveil.

###186###
When envious time, with fingers swift and keen,
Doth steal the rose's blush, and silver hair,
And leaves behind the lines, where youth hath been,
A mournful testament to life's despair.
Then shall my verse, with timeless magic wrought,
Preserve thy beauty, from oblivion's blight,
And in its lines, thy loveliness be caught,
To shine for ages, ever pure and bright.
Though seasons change, and empires rise and fall,
And generations pass like fleeting dreams,
Thy image shall endure, beyond them all,
And in my song, forever brightly gleam.
So fear not, love, the ravages of age,
For in my verse, thou'lt live on history's page.

###187###
My love is like a garden, fair and deep,
Where tender blossoms bloom in sweet array,
And hidden springs their crystal waters keep,
To quench the thirst that doth my spirit fray.
Each thought of thee, a fragrant bud unfurled,
Each whispered vow, a vine that climbs so high,
And in its beauty, doth my soul be whirled,
Beneath the azure of a summer sky.
But should a frost, with chilling breath descend,
And nip the tender leaves with icy hand,
Then would my garden's glory have an end,
And all its beauty vanish from the land.
So keep me warm, with love's enduring fire,
And quench the doubts that fill my soul's desire.

###188###
What is this passion that doth rage and burn,
And hold my senses captive in its sway?
To thee alone, my weary eyes do turn,
And in thy presence, all my troubles stray.
Thy voice, a melody that doth entrance,
Thy touch, a spark that sets my soul ablaze,
And in the rapture of our tender trance,
I lose myself, and wander through love's maze.
Yet, is this love, or but a fleeting whim,
A fevered dream, that shall too soon depart?
A painted bird, with plumage bright and trim,
Whose song is hollow, from an empty heart?
I pray it be true, this fire that I feel,
And that thy love, for me, is likewise real.

###189###
The moon, when hidden by a cloudy shroud,
Doth lose her luster, and her silvery gleam,
And earth is plunged in darkness, dark and proud,
As if to end the world, or spoil a dream.
So too, my spirit, when thou art not near,
Doth languish in a dim and mournful state,
And all the joys of life do disappear,
As if condemned by some unkindly fate.
But when thy smile, like sunlight, breaks anew,
And banishes the shadows from my sight,
My heart doth leap, and all the world seems true,
And bathed again in glorious, golden light.
Oh, let me never lose thy radiant face,
For in its light, I find my resting place.

###190###
My muse, thy subject is a noble theme,
A beauty that doth shame the morning star,
A grace that glides, as in a waking dream,
And heals the wounds that did my spirit mar.
Thy wit, as sharp as any polished blade,
Doth cut through folly, with a pleasing sound,
And in thy wisdom, I am not afraid,
To tread the paths where truth may yet be found.
Yet when I strive, with pen in hand to write,
The words do falter, and the lines are weak,
As if to dim thy pure and radiant light,
And fail the perfect praise thou dost bespeak.
But still I try, with all my humble art,
To capture thee, within my beating heart.

###191###
The serpent's coil, that doth with venom creep,
And strike its victim with a sudden sting,
Doth find its match in love's embrace so deep,
Where pleasure doth with sudden sorrow spring.
For who can trust, when beauty doth beguile,
And promises are whispered, soft and low,
That doth conceal a heart that waits a while,
To strike its blow, and make the spirit go?
Beware the glance, that seems so full of grace,
The tender sigh, that breathes of sweet desire,
For oft they mask a cold and cruel place,
That burns the heart with unrequited fire.
Let caution be thy shield, and wisdom guide,
Lest love's sharp dart doth pierce thee from inside.

###192###
When summer's heat doth bake the parched earth dry,
And all the streams have shrunk to trickling threads,
I long for rain, that falling from the sky,
May bring new life to slumbering flowerbeds.
So too, my soul, when love's refreshing stream,
Doth cease to flow, and leaves my spirit bare,
Doth crave thy presence, like a waking dream,
To banish forth this desolation there.
Thy gentle words, like raindrops, soft and mild,
Can quench the burning thirst that I do feel,
And make my barren heart, once more, run wild,
With joy that doth its deepest nature reveal.
So let thy love, like heaven's tears, descend,
And to my wilting spirit, solace lend.

###193###
The fleeting hour, that doth with silent pace,
Steal moments from our lives, and leave us old,
Doth urge us on, to seek love's sweet embrace,
Before our story can be fully told.
For youth, alas, is but a transient guest,
That lingers not, but flies on wings of air,
And leaves behind the wrinkles, and the rest,
Of years that bowed us down with heavy care.
So let us seize the day, and not delay,
The honest words that our true hearts do speak,
For time, the thief, will bear them all away,
And leave us with the memories, faint and weak.
Embrace me now, and let our passions twine,
Before the shadows of the grave are thine.

###194###
When storms do rage, and winds do loudly blow,
And threaten to o'erthrow the sturdy oak,
My steadfast love, no tempest shall o'erthrow,
Nor shall its strength, by any trial be broke.
Though clouds may gather, and the sky grow dark,
And thunder roll, with an alarming sound,
My heart, secure, shall bear love's burning spark,
And in its warmth, a constant solace found.
For true affection, like a rooted tree,
Doth stand unmoved, though tempests do assail,
And from its depths, its strength shall ever be,
A fortress strong, that never shall grow pale.
So let the world rage on, with all its might,
My love for thee shall be my guiding light.

###195###
The painted scene, though fair to outward eye,
Doth lack the breath of life, the living soul,
A hollow shell, beneath a painted sky,
That cannot make the wounded spirit whole.
So too, is love, when it is feigned and fake,
A shallow thing, that doth but mock the heart,
And leaves behind a grief, for sorrow's sake,
When its false colors finally depart.
But in thy gaze, a truth I plainly see,
A genuine warmth, that doth my soul embrace,
And in that truth, I find eternity,
And in thy love, I find my rightful place.
So let me not be fooled by outward show,
But in thy true affection, let me grow.

###196###
When in the night, the stars begin to gleam,
And fill the heavens with their radiant light,
My thoughts do wander, as in a waking dream,
And find their center in thy vision bright.
Each tiny star, a distant, shining soul,
Reflects the glory that doth in thee dwell,
And makes my longing spirit feel the whole
Of love's deep power, that doth me so compel.
Though galaxies may stretch, and worlds divide,
My heart shall find its constant guiding pole,
And in its stead, thy presence shall abide,
And make my fragmented spirit feel its whole.
So let the heavens turn, and ages fly,
My love for thee shall never, ever die.

###197###
The sweetest fruit, though ripened on the bough,
Can sour and fall, when time hath played its part,
And all its former sweetness, then, doth bow,
To worm and decay, and break the hopeful heart.
So too, the tender passion of our youth,
If not sustained by care, and constant thought,
May fade and wither, losing all its truth,
And leave behind the lessons dearly bought.
Let not our love become a fading bloom,
But let us tend it, with a watchful eye,
And chase away the shadows of its gloom,
With constant vows, beneath a faithful sky.
For love, like life, requires a constant toil,
To keep its beauty fresh, upon this soil.

###198###
The poet's ink, though dipped in deepest thought,
May fail to capture beauty's perfect grace,
And all his labours, though with striving wrought,
May leave its essence still in time and space.
For thine own charm, doth mock the poet's art,
And all the words that I can e'er devise,
Fall short of telling thee, from my poor heart,
The true extent of love that in me lies.
Thou art a wonder, past all mortal ken,
A living poem, writ in heaven's own hand,
And I, a humble scribe, can but pen,
The faintest echo, in this weary land.
So let my silence speak, where words do fail,
And tell my love, beyond all spoken tale.

###199###
When I behold the beauty of the rose,
Or mark the gentle dew upon the green,
A pang of sorrow through my spirit goes,
For what is fair, can never long be seen.
The bud that swells, with promise in the spring,
Shall soon unfold, and then begin to fade,
And all the joy that early blossoms bring,
Is but a prelude to the coming shade.
But in thy face, a fairer bloom I find,
That doth defy the cruel hand of time,
A beauty that shall ever be enshrined,
Beyond the reach of earthly, mortal crime.
So let me gaze, and in thy beauty's light,
Find solace from the ravages of night.

###200###
The world's a stage, and we but players here,
Each to our part assigned, for good or ill,
And fortunes shift, dispelling joy or fear,
As fate doth spin its ever-turning wheel.
The proudest king may fall from his high seat,
The beggar rise to wealth beyond his dream,
And all our striving, bitter and yet sweet,
Is but a passing, momentary gleam.
For what is power, or what is earthly store,
When dust shall claim us, and our name forgot?
We chase the wind, and ask for something more,
Than what this fleeting, transient life hath got.
Thus, let us live, with virtue as our guide,
And in true love, let all our cares subside.

###201###
The fleeting hour, that doth with silent pace,
Steal moments from our lives, and leave us old,
Doth urge us on, to seek love's sweet embrace,
Before our story can be fully told.
For youth, alas, is but a transient guest,
That lingers not, but flies on wings of air,
And leaves behind the wrinkles, and the rest,
Of years that bowed us down with heavy care.
So let us seize the day, and not delay,
The honest words that our true hearts do speak,
For time, the thief, will bear them all away,
And leave us with the memories, faint and weak.
Embrace me now, and let our passions twine,
Before the shadows of the grave are thine.

###202###
When gentle Spring doth shed her verdant hue,
And birds do tune their carols in the wood,
My heart, oppressed by Winter's chilly dew,
Doth yearn for solace, where it once had stood.
The sun, though bright, doth paint no cheerful scene,
For memories of thee do cloud my sight,
A phantom love, though absent, still is keen,
And steals away the pleasure of the light.
When shall I taste again that sweet embrace,
And feel the warmth that banished all my dread?
When shall my soul find comfort in thy face,
And rise like Phoenix from this lonely bed?
    Until that hour, my spirit shall remain,
    A captive soul, that longs to live again.

###203###
The moon, a pale disc in the velvet night,
Doth cast her beams upon my sleepless eye,
And whispers tales of what was once so bright,
As fleeting moments swiftly hasten by.
The stars do prick the darkness with their gleam,
But offer naught to mend this broken heart,
Lost in the shadows of a faded dream,
Where joy and sorrow play a bitter part.
I call thy name unto the silent air,
And echo answers with a mournful sound,
A testament to my profound despair,
On this cold, solitary, barren ground.
    Alas, my love, that I am left to mourn,
    A love that withered ere the day was born.

###204###
Thy laughter, like a melody so sweet,
Doth ring within the chambers of my mind,
A joyous sound my weary ears to greet,
A treasure rare, I thought I could not find.
Thy eyes, like stars that twinkle in the height,
Do pierce the gloom that doth my spirit bind,
And fill my soul with an effulgent light,
A balm for wounds of an ungentle kind.
When thou art near, the world seems fresh and new,
And every care doth vanish like the mist,
But when thou'rt gone, my world is cold and blue,
And all my hopes are dashed, and all are missed.
    So let me bask within thy radiant grace,
    And find my heaven in thy dear embrace.

###205###
The rose that blooms in summer's golden day,
Doth hold within its petals secrets deep,
Of beauty fleeting, destined to decay,
And promises that time itself doth keep.
So too thy beauty, though it shines so fair,
Is subject to the ravages of years,
And time, the thief, will steal with subtle care,
The bloom that now my loving heart endears.
Yet shall my verse, a more enduring thing,
Preserve thy grace for ages yet to see,
And to thy memory, my muse shall sing,
A testament to immortality.
    Though flesh may fade, and outward charms depart,
    Thy spirit's light shall linger in my heart.

###206###
The robin sings his matins at the dawn,
A cheerful sound to greet the rising sun,
But in my breast, no joyful song is born,
My sorrow's course has only just begun.
The dewdrop glistens on the spider's web,
A tiny jewel, soon to disappear,
And thus my hope, as if by fate's cold ebb,
Doth vanish, leaving naught but doubt and fear.
I sought a harbour from the stormy sea,
A haven where my weary soul might rest,
But found instead, a cruel deceit,
And now my spirit is by sorrow pressed.
    For love betrayed is a most bitter draught,
    And trust, once broken, cannot be re-graffed.

###207###
The ship that sails upon the ocean wide,
Doth brave the tempest and the raging gale,
And trusts in Providence to be its guide,
And hopes its efforts shall not be in vain.
So I, who venture on the seas of love,
Do face the storms of doubt and jealous ire,
And look to thee, my guiding star above,
To quench the flames of my consuming fire.
My heart, a vessel tossed on waves of woe,
Doth yearn for shore, a peaceful, calm retreat,
And where thy love its healing waters flow,
My weary journey shall at last be meet.
    Oh, be my compass, and my steady hand,
    And lead me safe unto the promised land.

###208###
When envious tongues do whisper words of blame,
And cast a shadow on my honest name,
My spirit shrinks, as if consumed by flame,
And feels the sting of undeserved shame.
The world's opinion is a fickle thing,
That shifts and turns with every passing breeze,
And often those who loudest virtue sing,
Are often caught in vice's dark unease.
But I, who know my own heart's true intent,
Will not be swayed by rumour's venomous dart,
My conscience clear, my purpose heaven-sent,
Shall shield me from the poisoned, cruel art.
    Let slander rage, and calumny assail,
    My truth shall stand, and never shall it fail.

###209###
The lute, when tuned to sweet and gentle note,
Doth charm the ear and soothe the troubled breast,
But when its strings are broken, it doth float,
A broken promise, bringing no true rest.
My soul, alas, is like that fractured lute,
Since thou, my muse, hath turned thy gaze away,
And left me with a silence, stark and mute,
Where once a symphony held happy sway.
I strike the chords of memory in vain,
And hear but echoes of a joyful sound,
A phantom music that doth cause me pain,
On this now desolated, barren ground.
    Oh, mend thy silence, and resume thy song,
    And make my wounded spirit whole and strong.

###210###
The winter's snow, that blankets all the land,
Doth chill the earth and freeze the flowing stream,
But deep within, a promise doth expand,
Of vernal warmth and a returning gleam.
So though thy absence chills my very soul,
And leaves me in a barren, frozen waste,
I hold a hope that makes my spirit whole,
That thy dear presence shall at length be placed.
The buried seed, though hidden from the eye,
Doth hold the power to burst forth anew,
And so my love, beneath this frozen sky,
Doth wait for thee, my sun, my spring, my dew.
    Then shall my heart, in joyous bloom arise,
    And find its summer in thy loving eyes.

###211###
The hurried clock, that measures out our days,
Doth steal our youth with every ticking sound,
And leads us through life's labyrinthine maze,
Until at last, in dust, we shall be found.
But in thy love, I find a timeless space,
Where moments linger and do never fade,
A sanctuary, filled with gentle grace,
Whereby my soul is evermore conveyed.
Let others fret about the passing hour,
And mourn the bloom that withers on the vine,
For in thy heart, I feel a deathless power,
A love that shall forever truly shine.
    So let the seasons turn, and years depart,
    Thy constant love remains within my heart.

###212###
The shepherd, tending to his woolly flock,
Doth watch the clouds that drift across the blue,
And shelters them from storm and thunder's shock,
His constant care, forever strong and true.
So I, thy shepherd, though my flock be small,
Doth guard thy heart from every lurking harm,
And answer ever to thy gentlest call,
And keep thee safe within my loving arm.
My devotion is a fortress strong and deep,
Wherein thy soul may find its sweet repose,
And from the world's rude tempest safely sleep,
Beneath the shelter that my true love knows.
    So rest thee here, my love, and fear no ill,
    My faithful heart shall keep thee safe and still.

###213###
The merchant counts his gold with eager hand,
And hoards his treasure from the envious eye,
But finds his riches cannot understand,
The worth of joy that money cannot buy.
So I, who deem thy love a richer prize,
Than all the wealth that kings can e'er possess,
Do guard it well, beneath these watchful skies,
And find in it my earthly happiness.
Thy smile, a jewel beyond all price and worth,
Thy voice, a melody that doth impart,
More true delight than all the gems of earth,
And stills the clamour of my troubled heart.
    Let others chase the fleeting, worldly gain,
    My truest wealth is found in thee, again.

###214###
The weary traveler, on dusty road,
Doth yearn for rest, and shade from sun's hot glare,
And dreams of home, to lift his heavy load,
And banish all his toil and anxious care.
So I, who've wandered in life's barren land,
And felt the sting of solitude and pain,
Have found at last, a place where I can stand,
And feel thy love like cool and welcome rain.
Thy heart, a haven from the world's harsh strife,
Thy presence, comfort to my aching breast,
Thou art the compass that directs my life,
And in thy love, I find my perfect rest.
    So let me dwell within thy gentle light,
    And banish from my soul eternal night.

###215###
The serpent, with its cunning, silent tread,
Doth strike the unsuspecting creature down,
And fills its heart with sudden, chilling dread,
And steals its life, and wears a victor's crown.
So doubt, a serpent in my loving mind,
Doth whisper falsehoods, venomous and sly,
And seeks my peace and happiness to bind,
And plant the seeds of darkness in my eye.
But I shall fight this foe with all my might,
And banish shadows with a steadfast will,
And hold my faith with all my soul's true light,
And trust that love shall conquer, by God's will.
    For truth and love shall evermore prevail,
    And banish sorrow, and all bitter wail.

###216###
The artist paints a portrait, fair to see,
And captures beauty with his skillful hand,
But still the image lacks the vibrancy,
Of life itself, throughout the living land.
So I, who strive to praise thy virtues rare,
And capture all thy grace within my rhyme,
Can only glimpse, and dimly do declare,
The perfect beauty that transcends all time.
My words are but a shadow of thy light,
My verse, a pale reflection of thy face,
And though I labor with my utmost might,
I cannot fully capture thy sweet grace.
    Yet shall my song, though faint, forever strive,
    To keep thy matchless beauty still alive.

###217###
The raging storm, that tears the sky apart,
Doth fill the stoutest heart with fearful awe,
And shakes the foundations of the very mart,
And bends the strongest oak with Nature's law.
So too, the passions that do rend my soul,
When thou art distant, and my hope doth wane,
Do leave me lost, beyond all self-control,
And wracked with sorrow, and with bitter pain.
But when thy gaze, like sun through clouds doth shine,
The tempest ceases, and the skies are clear,
And all my fears like phantoms do resign,
And peace returns, and all that I hold dear.
    Oh, be the sunshine that dispels my dread,
    And wake my spirit from this deathly bed.

###218###
The foolish child, who plays with fire's bright gleam,
Doth burn his hand, and learn a lesson hard,
And wakes at last from his delusive dream,
To find his folly has his flesh now scarred.
So I, who dallied with a fleeting joy,
And chased the phantom of a fickle love,
Did find my trusting heart at last destroy,
And learned the truth, from heavens high above.
The flame that promised warmth, did only sear,
The sweetness that I sought, was but a lie,
And now I weep, with sorrow and with fear,
Beneath a cold and unforgiving sky.
    Yet from this pain, a strength I shall attain,
    And rise again, and banish all this pain.

###219###
The king, who sits upon his lofty throne,
Doth wield the sceptre and the sword of might,
But cannot rule the heart, when love is sown,
Nor command feelings, shining ever bright.
So I, though humble, with no crown to wear,
Do hold dominion o'er a greater prize,
Thy love, a treasure beyond all compare,
That shines within thy captivating eyes.
No earthly power can command my will,
Nor sway the course of this devoted heart,
For in thy service, I am bound and still,
And from thy side, I never shall depart.
    So let me be thy loyal, faithful subject,
    And in thy love, find all I do expect.

###220###
The ancient ruins, standing proud and tall,
Though time has weathered their majestic stone,
Still whisper tales to those who heed their call,
Of glories past, and seeds that have been sown.
So shall my love, though years may intervene,
And outward forms may alter and decay,
Remain a constant, ever sharp and keen,
And shine with truth, in its own perfect way.
Let not the wrinkles that time doth impart,
Or fading bloom, thy loving gaze avert,
For in the depths of my devoted heart,
Thy beauty lives, and shall forever dart.
    And though my voice may falter and grow weak,
    My love for thee, my soul shall ever speak.

###221###
The fleeting dream, that visits in the night,
Doth fade with dawn, and leave no trace behind,
A phantom pleasure, bathed in ethereal light,
That vanishes, and can no more be find.
So too, my hopes, when thou art far away,
Do seem like phantoms, mocking my distress,
And leave me lost, at close of weary day,
In solitude, and utter loneliness.
I crave thy presence, as the parched earth craves,
The gentle rain to quench its burning thirst,
And long to swim in love's refreshing waves,
And from this arid desert be dispersed.
    Oh, let thy love, like dew, descend on me,
    And wake my spirit, and make me truly free.

###222###
The painter's brush, with colours rich and bold,
Doth bring to life a scene of grand design,
But cannot capture, as the stories told,
The inner spirit, and the spark divine.
So I, who praise thy outward comeliness,
Thy graceful form, thy beauty to behold,
Do know these charms are but a fainter guess,
Of that true worth, more precious than pure gold.
Thy gentle soul, thy kindness, and thy wit,
Are jewels that cannot be by mortal seen,
But in my heart, they brightly ever sit,
And make thee, fairest of all earthly queen.
    So let me love the virtues of thy mind,
    More than the fleeting graces I do find.###222###
When Phoebus doth his golden chariot guide
Across the heavens, making darkness flee,
My soul doth wake, and joy doth then preside,
And casts away all melancholy.
The birds do sing their carols to the morn,
Each flower doth ope its petals to the light,
A sweeter beauty never was so born,
As doth appear in nature's radiant sight.
But when I think on thee, my dearest friend,
These worldly glories do but fade and wane,
For in thine eyes, a greater joy I find,
That doth my restless, yearning spirit gain.
So let the sun rise, or the shadows fall,
Thy love alone doth hold me in its thrall.

###223###
The fleeting hours, like sand within the glass,
Do slip away and leave us to regret,
The golden moments that too quickly pass,
And in our memory, forever set.
The youthful bloom that graces every cheek,
Doth wither with the seasons as they turn,
And strength of limb, which once did make us meek,
Doth fade, and we to frailty then do learn.
So let us seize the day ere it be gone,
And plant our joys in fertile, present ground,
For tomorrow's sun may never shine upon
The hopes we build, nor the delights we've found.
Let not the past our future hours consume,
But live for now, and banish all dark gloom.

###224###
When I behold the beauty of thy face,
A fairer sight mine eyes did never see,
Thy gentle spirit, full of noble grace,
Doth captive make the very heart of me.
The raven locks that crown thy beauteous head,
The sparkling eyes that hold a starry gleam,
The rosy lips, where sweetest words are bred,
Do weave for me a most enchanting dream.
No sculptor's hand, nor painter's cunning art,
Could e'er portray such wonder to the eye,
As nature's self hath fashioned for my heart,
Beneath the vastness of the summer sky.
So may this beauty ever be preserved,
A lasting truth, by which my soul is served.

###225###
The cruel hand of time, which spares no soul,
Doth steal away the strength of youthful prime,
And makes the proudest spirit to grow old,
And leaves its mark with age and fading time.
The laughter bright, that once did fill the air,
Doth turn to sighs, and whispers of the past,
And vigour keen, that banished every care,
Doth yield to weakness, holding us at last.
Yet in the soul, a flame may still abide,
A nobler fire, that age cannot consume,
A wisdom deep, where truth doth sweetly guide,
And banish from our hearts all mortal gloom.
So let us live, with virtue as our guide,
And death itself shall then be cast aside.

###226###
My love for thee, a boundless, ocean deep,
Doth rise and fall with every passing tide,
No earthly force can its dominion keep,
Nor in its depths can any sorrow hide.
The stars above, that witness to my plight,
Do twinkle down with sympathetic gleam,
And whisper secrets through the silent night,
Of hopes that bloom within a lover's dream.
Should fortune frown, and cast me to the ground,
Or friends prove false, and leave me all alone,
Within thy heart, my solace shall be found,
A steadfast love, forever to be known.
So let the world its fickle courses run,
My heart with thine shall beat, till life is done.

###227###
The winter's blast, with icy breath so keen,
Doth strip the trees of verdant, leafy dress,
And paint the world in hues of white and green,
A barren scene of nature's loveliness.
The rivers freeze, and cease their merry flow,
The birds are hushed, their joyful songs are still,
And chilling winds do from the mountains blow,
And hold the land within their frozen will.
Yet in this gloom, a promise doth reside,
Of spring's return, and warmth's sweet, gentle reign,
When nature shall in fullest bloom abide,
And banish all the winter's cold disdain.
So shall my love, though trials may assail,
Endure and bloom, and never, ever fail.

###228###
When fortune smiles, and all the world is bright,
And joyous laughter echoes through the air,
My heart doth leap with gladness and delight,
And casts aside all doubt and every care.
The sun doth shine with beams of purest gold,
The gentle breeze doth whisper through the trees,
And tales of happiness are to be told,
As nature doth its fairest beauty please.
But should a cloud obscure the sunny sky,
And shadows fall where light did lately play,
Thy steadfast love doth then to me draw nigh,
And chase the gathering darkness far away.
So in good times, thy presence I embrace,
And in dark days, I find in thee my grace.

###229###
The painted hues that deck the fading rose,
Do speak of beauty that must soon depart,
And as the summer's golden season goes,
So too, alas, doth vanish from the heart.
The fleeting charms that hold the eye in thrall,
Are but a breath, a whisper in the wind,
And when they fade, we mourn their silent fall,
And leave their empty echoes far behind.
But in thy soul, a beauty doth reside,
That time and change shall never dispossess,
A inner light, where virtue doth abide,
And makes my loving heart forever bless.
So let the outward forms decay and cease,
Thy inward worth shall grant my soul its peace.

###230###
When envy's serpent, with its venomous hiss,
Doth seek to poison all that I hold dear,
And whispers tales that lead to deep abyss,
And fills my anxious heart with chilling fear.
The tongues of malice, sharp as any sword,
Do strike at honour, reputation, name,
And in their spite, do leave the truth abhorred,
And burn the soul with an unholy flame.
But let them rage, and let their venom spew,
My steadfast faith in thee shall never bend,
For in thine eyes, I find a virtue true,
That shall these wicked calumnies transcend.
So let the slanderers their falsehoods weave,
My heart in thine shall ever more believe.

###231###
The silent plea within thine eyes I see,
A tender yearning, spoken without sound,
And in that gaze, thou dost impart to me,
A deeper love, on consecrated ground.
No need for words, when souls can speak as one,
And understand each unspoken desire,
When in the light of love, our courses run,
And hearts are bound by passion's burning fire.
So let us build a world of our own making,
Where truth and trust shall be the guiding star,
And all the earthly worries we are shaking,
Shall find no purchase, no matter how far.
For in this bond, so pure and so sincere,
We banish doubt, and conquer every fear.

###232###
The fleeting shadow of a passing cloud,
Doth dim the sun, but cannot quench its fire,
And though the world may speak its praises loud,
My humble heart doth seek a higher hire.
The empty praise of fickle, common man,
Is but a breath, that vanishes from sight,
A transient glory, by no means can
Compare unto thy love, so pure and bright.
For in thy breast, a noble spirit dwells,
That scorns the show, and seeks the truth within,
And in its light, my truest virtue swells,
And helps my soul to conquer every sin.
So let the world its shallow favours lend,
Thy truer love is that which I commend.

###233###
When gentle sleep doth claim its rightful hold,
And weary eyes are closed against the night,
My dreams are filled with stories to be told,
Of thee, my love, a most enchanting sight.
I see thee walk in gardens, fair and green,
Thy laughter echoes through the moonlit air,
A vision of such beauty, rarely seen,
That doth my waking spirit gladly share.
But when I wake, and find the vision flown,
A pang of sorrow doth my heart possess,
And for thy presence, I do sadly moan,
And long to feel thy sweet, consoling press.
So dreams may cheat, and waking hours may sigh,
Yet still my heart doth for thy presence cry.

###234###
The painted blush that graces maiden's cheek,
Doth speak of youth, and beauty's tender bloom,
But age shall come, and strength begin to leak,
And cast its shadow, ushering in gloom.
The eyes that sparkle with a youthful fire,
Shall lose their lustre, as the years go by,
And passions strong, that once did them inspire,
Shall fade and dwindle, with a weary sigh.
Yet if within the soul, a virtue lies,
A steadfast goodness, that no time can stain,
Then beauty's charm forever shall arise,
And make the heart feel joy and not feel pain.
So let the outward form begin to fade,
Thy inward worth shall never be betrayed.

###235###
The distant shores that bound the restless sea,
Do beckon forth with promise of new lands,
And in my soul, a restless longing be,
To break the chains, and flee these weary sands.
The sails are set, the wind begins to blow,
A journey starts, with hopes that soar on high,
But ere I go, one truth I wish to know,
Will thy love follow, 'neath the foreign sky?
For though new worlds may greet my eager gaze,
And wonders rare my curious eye may meet,
If thou art not with me, in those far-off days,
My triumph then, would be but bitter-sweet.
So let me sail, with thee beside me still,
And conquer all, according to love's will.

###236###
The silent stars that gem the velvet night,
Do cast a glow upon the sleeping earth,
And whisper tales of universal light,
Of cosmic wonders, and of heaven's worth.
The moon, a pearl upon the heavens hung,
Doth shed its beams, a gentle, silver stream,
And ancient songs of creation are sung,
Woven into the fabric of a dream.
But when I turn my gaze to thee, my dear,
These heavenly glories do but fade and pale,
For in thine eyes, a brighter light is clear,
A love that doth all cosmic wonder hail.
So let the stars their silent vigils keep,
My heart finds heaven, when with thee I sleep.

###237###
The heavy chains of melancholy's hold,
Doth bind my spirit, and my joy doth seize,
And in its grip, my weary heart grows cold,
And finds no solace, and no sweet release.
The sun itself, that ought to bring me cheer,
Doth seem to mock my sorrow with its gleam,
And every sound doth fill my soul with fear,
As if I walk within a dreadful dream.
But then thy voice, like music, soft and low,
Doth break the spell, and chase the clouds away,
And in thy smile, the seeds of hope do grow,
And banish all the darkness of the day.
So let the shadows gather, if they must,
Thy presence is my solace, and my trust.

###238###
The fleeting whisper of a summer breeze,
Doth stir the leaves, and rustle through the grass,
And carries with it, on its wings, the ease
Of moments precious, that too swiftly pass.
The buzzing bee, that labours in the bloom,
Doth gather nectar, for its honeyed store,
And knows no fear of winter's chilling doom,
But lives for now, and asks for nothing more.
So let me learn from nature's simple way,
To seize the hour, and cherish every breath,
And banish all the worries of today,
And find true life, and conquer weary death.
For in this present joy, a power lies,
That shall outshine all future, sad surprise.

###239###
When absence doth thy presence steal from me,
And lonely nights do stretch with weary pace,
My heart doth ache with longing, and decree,
That time itself should quicken in its race.
The sun doth rise, but brings no warmth to me,
The stars do shine, but offer little light,
For all the world is robbed of gaiety,
When thou art far, and hidden from my sight.
Yet in my dreams, thy visage doth appear,
And in my thoughts, thy voice doth softly sound,
And though the miles may hold thee ever dear,
My love for thee on truest wings is bound.
So let the distance hold us for a while,
My heart shall beat for thee, with steadfast smile.

###240###
The ancient woods, where shadows softly creep,
And silent streams do murmur as they flow,
Hold secrets old, that nature doth to keep,
From mortal eyes, that cannot truly know.
The ancient stones, that time hath worn away,
Do speak of lives, and deeds long passed and gone,
And in their silence, they do bid us stay,
And ponder on the course that we have run.
But in thy love, a newer truth I find,
A present glory, brighter than the past,
A love that shall leave earthly cares behind,
And in its strength, forever shall it last.
So let the past its ancient tales unfold,
My future lies in love, more precious than gold.

###241###
When weary days do bring their heavy toll,
And toil and trouble dim the spirit's gleam,
A comfort deep doth enter in my soul,
And banish shadows, like a waking dream.
Thy gentle hand, that soothes my troubled brow,
Thy tender words, that whisper love's sweet plea,
Doth lift me up, and teach my heart to bow,
To that dear grace, that emanates from thee.
No earthly treasure, nor a kingly crown,
Can match the riches that thy love imparts,
For in its strength, all worldly cares are drowned,
And joy abides within our thankful hearts.
So let the world its fleeting pleasures send,
Thy love alone, my solace and my friend.

###242###
The fleeting joy that doth the senses seize,
Doth vanish swift, like dew before the sun,
And leaves behind a void, that doth not please,
When all its transient pleasure is outrun.
The sweet delight that kisses and doth clasp,
Is but a breath, that fades into the air,
And leaves the spirit with an empty gasp,
And all its promise turned to dark despair.
But in thy soul, a constant truth doth dwell,
A love that time and change can ne'er undo,
A deeper joy, whose virtues shall compel,
My heart to hold thee, ever, ever true.
So let the world its fickle favours show,
Thy steadfast love is all I need to know.


###242###
When Phoebus doth his golden chariot guide,
And casts his beams upon the sleeping earth,
My heart with sorrow doth to thee confide,
And mourns the absence of thy joyful mirth.
The birds do sing a sweet and lovely tune,
But to mine ears it sounds a doleful strain,
For thou art far beneath the argent moon,
And I do languish in a lonely pain.
The gentle breeze that whispers through the trees,
Doth bring no comfort to my weary soul,
But rather doth my pining spirit seize,
And makes my endless suffering take its toll.
So let me weep until the day is done,
And wait until thy longed-for face is won.

###243###
Thy beauty shines with such a radiant grace,
As doth outshine the stars in darkest night,
And in thy smile I find my rightful place,
A beacon guiding me with pure delight.
No earthly jewel can with thee compare,
Nor painter's skill thy likeness can impart,
Thou art a vision past all mortal care,
The living image of my beating heart.
The sweetest music that the ear can hear,
Is but a whisper when thy voice I gain,
And banishes all doubt and every fear,
And eases all my sorrow and my pain.
So shall my love for thee forever bloom,
Dispelling shadows, banishing all gloom.

###244###
When weary labour doth mine limbs embrace,
And bids me seek repose from worldly strife,
I turn my thoughts to thy beloved face,
And find new vigour to endure my life.
The sweet perfume that from thy presence streams,
Is as the essence of a summer's day,
And fills my waking thoughts and sleeping dreams,
And drives all lesser, earthly joys away.
Thy gentle touch, a balm to soothe my woe,
Thy loving gaze, a fire to warm my breast,
In thee, my truest happiness I know,
And in thy arms, I find my perfect rest.
So let me live and breathe thy very air,
And banish from my heart all worldly care.

###245###
The fleeting hours, like shadows, swiftly fly,
And steal away the bloom from every cheek,
And in their passage, bid the spirit sigh,
As youth and beauty grow so frail and weak.
Yet in thy eyes, a constant light doth dwell,
A fire that time itself cannot subdue,
A story that thy faithful heart doth tell,
Forever radiant, steadfast, and true.
Though winter's frost may touch the verdant land,
And strip the leaves from every naked tree,
Thy love, a summer's warmth, shall understand,
And shield my soul from all adversity.
So let us live, ere youth doth disappear,
And hold each other ever, ever dear.

###246###
My love for thee, a boundless ocean deep,
Whose surging waves do never cease to roll,
Doth in my inmost soul its vigil keep,
And holds dominion over heart and soul.
No earthly power can my passion quell,
Nor time's cruel hand my ardour can abate,
Within thy love, I find my earthly hell,
And yet a heaven, sealed by cruel fate.
The sun may set, and darkness claim the skies,
The moon may wane, and stars begin to fade,
But in thy breast, my constant hope still lies,
A love that never shall be disarrayed.
So let us pledge our vows and never stray,
But live in love unto our dying day.

###247###
When storms do rage and tempests loudly blow,
And all the world seems lost in darkest night,
I seek the solace that thy eyes bestow,
And find within their depths a guiding light.
The sweetest nectar that the gods do brew,
Could not compare with thy most precious kiss,
And every joy that mortal man can view,
Is but a shadow of thy perfect bliss.
Though fortune frown, and fickle fate may turn,
And cast me down to sorrow and despair,
My steadfast heart for thee alone shall burn,
And breathe thy name upon the very air.
So let me be thy servant and thy thrall,
And gladly give to thee my life and all.

###248###
The creeping vine that climbs the ancient wall,
Doth symbolize the growth of my desire,
And in its tendrils, I do stand or fall,
Consumed by love's all-wondering fire.
Each passing moment, as it takes its flight,
Doth but increase the passion in my breast,
And fills my being with a new delight,
And puts my restless, yearning soul to test.
Thy voice, a melody that doth enchant,
Thy smile, a sunbeam on a cloudy day,
My every thought and feeling dost thou grant,
And chase all worldly cares and doubts away.
So let me drown within thy loving grace,
And find my heaven in thy sweet embrace.

###249###
The fleeting shadow of a passing cloud,
