Doth often dim the brilliance of the sun,
And like a murmur from a distant crowd,
My hopes of joy are quickly overrun.
But then thy presence doth my spirit raise,
And like a Phoenix from the ashes sprung,
I find anew the ardour of my days,
And hear the praises that my heart hath sung.
Thy beauty doth my very senses thrill,
Thy gentle spirit doth my soul inspire,
And when thy will doth my own will fulfill,
I feel the burning of celestial fire.
So shall my love for thee forever gleam,
A waking truth within a happy dream.

###250###
The winter's chill, that bites with icy sting,
Doth freeze the blood and make the spirit quail,
And birds of passage their sad farewell sing,
As nature's colours sadly start to fail.
But in my heart, a spring doth ever bloom,
Where thy dear image doth forever stay,
Dispelling all the darkness and the gloom,
And bringing forth the brightness of the day.
Thy words, like dew upon a thirsty flower,
Do quench the arid longing of my soul,
And grant me strength in every trying hour,
And make my wounded spirit once more whole.
So let me bask within thy warming light,
And banish from my mind all thoughts of night.

###251###
When Fortune's wheel doth turn with cruelest spin,
And casts me down to depths of sheer despair,
I find a refuge from the woes within,
And breathe the sweetness of thy perfumed air.
Thy constancy, a star that guides my way,
Through stormy seas and tempests dark and wild,
Doth banish fear and chase all doubt away,
And makes me feel as if I were a child,
Secure and loved within a mother's arms,
Protected from the world's unkind decree,
Enfolded safe from all its harsh alarms,
And wholly given to thy love for me.
So let me ever cling to thee with might,
And find in thee my everlasting light.

###252###
The golden harvest that the fields do yield,
Doth speak of labours past and sweet reward,
And so my love, a treasure now revealed,
Is by thy grace eternally adored.
Each tender glance, each softly spoken word,
Doth weave a spell that holds my heart in thrall,
And in thy love, my spirit is upstirred,
And answers to thy most alluring call.
No summer's heat can with thy warmth compare,
Nor winter's frost thy constant flame subdue,
Thou art the object of my fervent prayer,
My fairest hope, my vision ever true.
So let our hearts in perfect union blend,
And love's sweet journey have no earthly end.

###253###
The fading rose, whose petals gently fall,
Doth mirror the decline of mortal years,
And whispers low a melancholy call,
Of vanished joys and unremembered tears.
But in thy breast, a beauty doth reside,
That time itself can never touch or stain,
A living monument, where love doth hide,
And from its fount, a ceaseless joy doth rain.
Thy wit, a spark that sets my soul aflame,
Thy kindness, balm to all my weary plight,
I speak with reverence thy cherished name,
And find in thee my solace and my light.
So let me drink from love's eternal spring,
And to thy praises everlasting sing.

###254###
When shadows lengthen and the day grows old,
And twilight hues do paint the western sky,
My thoughts return, as stories to be told,
To thee, my love, my joy, my reason why.
The fleeting pleasures that the world can give,
Are but as dust compared to thy sweet grace,
In thy dear presence, I alone do live,
And find my solace in thy warm embrace.
Thy whispered vows, like music to my ear,
Doth banish sorrow, quell all rising doubt,
And hold me ever, ever close and dear,
And cast all worldly cares and fears right out.
So let us walk where love's own pathway lies,
And gaze forever into loving eyes.

###255###
The murmuring stream that flows through verdant mead,
Doth carry whispers of a bygone dream,
And plants within my heart a longing seed,
That flourishes beneath love's radiant beam.
Thy voice, a siren's song that doth beguile,
Thy touch, a magic that doth set me free,
I languish fondly for thy loving smile,
And lose myself completely, dear, in thee.
Though fickle fortune may our paths divide,
And trials great may stand between us two,
My steadfast heart shall on thy love confide,
And find its strength and solace there anew.
So let us build a world of our own making,
Where love's bright dawn is ever fast awaking.

###256###
The gilded cage that holds a captive bird,
Doth symbolize the state of my own heart,
Until thy freedom from its bonds is heard,
And bids my lonely, yearning soul depart.
For thou art he who holds the master key,
To unlock passions long concealed from sight,
And set my captive spirit wild and free,
And fill my days with unalloyed delight.
Thy eyes, two stars that guide me through the night,
Thy lips, a promise of a sweeter kiss,
Thou art my dawn, my day, my guiding light,
My earthly heaven, my most perfect bliss.
So let me fly to thee on wings of love,
And find our nesting place in skies above.

###257###
When winter's breath doth chill the very soul,
And nature sleeps beneath a shroud of white,
My love for thee doth make my spirit whole,
And fills my heart with everlasting light.
Thy constancy, a beacon in the storm,
Thy gentle spirit, balm to all my pain,
Doth keep my weary, longing bosom warm,
And bids me hope for brighter days again.
The sweetest flower that the spring doth bear,
Could not with thy dear beauty then compare,
Nor rarest jewel that mortals hold so dear,
Could with thy worth and virtue e'er compare.
So let me pledge my heart to thee alone,
And make thy loving will my very own.

###258###
The shifting sands that greet the ocean's roar,
Doth change their form with every passing tide,
But my true love shall stand forevermore,
And in its strength, my very soul doth hide.
Thy beauty's bloom, though it may fade and wane,
Shall leave within my heart a lasting fire,
A memory that shall forever reign,
And fuel the flames of my intense desire.
No earthly joy can with thy love compete,
No fleeting pleasure can my heart appease,
For in thy gaze, my spirit finds its seat,
And sinks to rest on love's eternal seas.
So let us journey on, till life shall cease,
And in our love, find everlasting peace.

###259###
The fleeting moth, that dances near the flame,
Doth court destruction with a foolish haste,
And so my heart, when it doth speak thy name,
Doth venture forth, lest precious time be waste.
For in thy presence, all my fears depart,
And all my doubts are banished from my mind,
Thou art the compass that directs my heart,
The truest treasure I could ever find.
Thy gentle words, like music to my ears,
Thy loving smile, a balm that heals my woe,
Thou art the cure for all my earthly fears,
The seed from which my truest pleasures grow.
So let me live within thy loving sphere,
And hold thee ever, ever close and dear.

###260###
When shadows fall and evening calls to rest,
And weary minds from daily toils retreat,
My thoughts do fly to thee, supremely blest,
And find within thy love a solace sweet.
Thy voice, a melody that doth entrance,
Thy glance, a star that guides me through the night,
I yield my will to thee, at love's command,
And bask within thy ever-shining light.
Though worldly storms may beat with fiercest rage,
And fortune's favour may from me depart,
Thy love shall be my book, my life, my stage,
The constant subject of my beating heart.
So let us join our souls in sweet accord,
And in our love, be evermore adored.

###261###
The fleeting dream that vanishes with dawn,
Doth leave behind a whisper and a sigh,
But thy dear love, it never is withdrawn,
But shines with constant brilliance in mine eye.
Thy gentle spirit, like a summer breeze,
Doth stir the slumbering passions in my breast,
And brings my troubled, longing soul to ease,
And grants my weary, yearning heart its rest.
No earthly jewel can with thee compare,
Nor painter's skill thy likeness can impart,
Thou art a vision past all mortal care,
The living image of my beating heart.
So let me live and breathe thy very air,
And banish from my heart all worldly care.###262###
When gentle thought doth hold my mind in sway,
And conjures visions of a time long past,
My heart doth heave, and beauty fades away,
As shadows lengthen, and the joys do last.
The youthful bloom, that did my spirit grace,
Hath yielded to the winter's chilling hand,
And lines of care now mark my weary face,
A somber testament, I understand.
Yet in that time, a solace I did find,
A kindred soul, whose gaze was like the sun,
Whose loving words did ease my troubled mind,
And taught my hopeful heart how it had won.
Though years have flown, and changed what once I knew,
Her memory still makes my old heart new.

###263###
The golden sun, that climbs the eastern sky,
Doth chase the lingering shadows of the night,
And bids the weary world to wake and sigh,
And bathe itself in morning's glorious light.
So too my love, when she doth deign to smile,
Doth banish all the darkness from my soul,
And in her presence, for a little while,
I feel my fractured spirit made quite whole.
Her eyes, like stars, do pierce the deepest gloom,
Her voice, a melody to soothe my ear,
Dispelling doubt, and every lurking doom,
And drawing all my scattered senses near.
Oh, let her stay, and ne'er from me depart,
This radiant mistress of my captive heart.

###264###
When Fortune smiles, and all the world doth seem
A painted stage, where pleasures freely flow,
My joyful soul doth revel in the dream,
And earthly cares no longer vex me so.
The coffers full, the favour of the great,
The praise of crowds, that echo through the air,
These are the baubles of a fickle fate,
That swiftly vanish, leaving naught but care.
But when the tempest doth begin to blow,
And skies turn black, and all my hope is lost,
Then I do learn what true affections grow,
And count the gain, whatever be the cost.
For love alone, when riches take their flight,
Remains a beacon in the darkest night.

###265###
The silent hours, when weary mortals sleep,
And all the town is hushed in slumber deep,
My restless thoughts their mournful vigil keep,
And from my eyes the bitter teardrops leap.
I ponder on the follies of my youth,
The wasted days, the opportunities missed,
And curse the blindness that concealed the truth,
By fleeting pleasures falsely, fondly kissed.
Now wisdom's dawn doth break upon my mind,
Too late to mend what I have broken quite,
And yet, a solace I can still unbind,
In hoping for a future, more than right.
For though my past be stained with bitter rue,
My present thoughts are turned towards the true.

###266###
The changing seasons, as they onward pace,
Do bring their varied hues to field and wood,
From summer's heat to winter's frosty face,
Each hath its time, as nature understood.
So too my love, though constant in her heart,
Doth sometimes show a temper quick and wild,
A sudden storm, that tears my world apart,
And leaves me trembling, like a frightened child.
Yet, as the tempest doth at length subside,
And sunbeams pierce the clouds that veiled the day,
Her gentle spirit doth again preside,
And chase the lingering darkness far away.
So let me learn to bear her fleeting ire,
And cherish still the flame of her desire.

###267###
When I behold the moon, in fullness bright,
That casts her silver spell on silent streams,
I think of thee, and all my soul's delight,
And lose myself within a world of dreams.
Thy beauty, like that orb, doth shine afar,
A guiding light, to steer my errant bark,
A distant, yet a most enchanting star,
That pierces through the deep and lonely dark.
Thy voice, a music sweeter than the breeze,
That whispers through the leaves in summer's prime,
Doth lull my anxious, troubled soul at ease,
And makes me forget the heavy hand of time.
So let me gaze upon thy radiant face,
And find in thee my everlasting place.

###268###
The fleeting moments, as they swiftly flee,
Do steal away the bloom of youthful years,
And leave behind a withered, aged tree,
That stands alone, and sheds its silent tears.
I see the lines upon my brow increase,
The silver threads that mingle with my hair,
And crave the solace of a lasting peace,
That worldly honours can no more repair.
For what are riches, or a queenly crown,
When strength departs, and vigour takes its leave?
A hollow echo, in a fading town,
A garland that the passing winds do weave.
Yet, if thy love can still my spirit bind,
I shall find joy, and leave all care behind.

###269###
When I do ponder on the fate of man,
And see how quickly earthly glory dies,
How empires fall, and kingdoms have no span,
Beneath the gaze of ever-watching skies.
The mighty oak, that braved a hundred years,
Is felled by storm, or lightning's fiery brand,
The proudest king, with all his pomp and fears,
Is turned to dust, within a barren land.
So what is worth, this striving and this pain,
This anxious chase for that which cannot stay?
A fleeting shadow, borne upon the rain,
That vanishes, at the dawning of the day.
Yet in thy gaze, a truth I can behold,
More precious far than all the world's fine gold.

###270###
The gentle dew, that doth the morning grace,
And kisses soft the petals of the rose,
Doth bear the scent of some forgotten place,
Where beauty bloomed, and quiet pleasure grows.
So thy sweet breath, when it doth softly sigh,
Doth carry whispers of a love so deep,
That makes me wish to live and then to die,
Within the arms of promises to keep.
Thy touch, a balm, that soothes my aching breast,
Thy smile, a sunbeam, on a cloudy day,
Doth grant my weary spirit needed rest,
And chase all worldly troubles far away.
Oh, let me ever linger in thy light,
And find in thee my solace and my might.

###271###
The painted bird, that in the forest sings,
Doth warble notes of joy, a careless sound,
And flutters by on swift and airy wings,
Unburdened by the cares that here abound.
So too my heart, when thou art in my sight,
Doth cast aside its heavy, weary load,
And leaps and dances in a pure delight,
Upon life's bright and ever-verdant road.
Thy laughter, like the chime of silver bells,
Doth banish sorrow, and all shades of fear,
And in its music, true enchantment dwells,
That makes the distant future seem so near.
Oh, may this joy within my bosom rest,
And make me ever happy, ever blessed.

###272###
When envious tongues do speak of thy good name,
And cast dark shadows on thy virtues bright,
My loyal heart doth burn with righteous flame,
And champions thy cause with all its might.
Let slander rage, and malice spread its lies,
They cannot dim the lustre of thy soul,
Which shines above, to all discerning eyes,
And makes my spirit ever strong and whole.
For I have known thee, in thy purest guise,
And seen the goodness that doth dwell within,
And though the world may seek to compromise,
Thy truth shall triumph, and thy worth shall win.
So fear them not, those voices filled with gall,
My steadfast love shall stand and shield thee from them all.

###273###
The fleeting breath of summer now is gone,
And autumn winds begin to chill the air,
The golden leaves, that lately danced upon,
Now fall in heaps, a carpet of despair.
So too my youth, that once did brightly bloom,
Hath faded fast, like flowers in the frost,
And left me here, within a deepening gloom,
To reckon with the treasure I have lost.
The strength departs, the vigour starts to wane,
The years, like thieves, do pilfer all my store,
And leave me standing, battered by the rain,
And craving peace, that I can find no more.
Yet, if thy love can still my spirit mend,
My lingering days shall find a peaceful end.

###274###
When Cupid's dart hath pierced my foolish breast,
And left me wounded, by his fiery sting,
I find no comfort, and I find no rest,
But onward chase the joy his arrows bring.
Thy eyes, like beacons, draw me to thy shore,
Thy voice, a siren's call, I must obey,
And though I know the danger, I implore,
To be thy captive, till my dying day.
For in thy service, I have found a bliss,
That worldly treasures never could impart,
And seal my fate with every gentle kiss,
That binds my whole existence to thy heart.
So let me yield, and in thy love reside,
My guiding star, my passion, and my pride.

###275###
The silent stars, that in the heavens gleam,
Do witness tales of love, both lost and found,
And watch the lovers, in their waking dream,
Upon this weary, ever-turning ground.
So too thy gaze, when it doth rest on me,
Doth hold a universe of sweet desire,
And makes me feel eternally set free,
From earthly bonds, and every burning fire.
Thy lips, like roses, kissed by morning dew,
Doth promise joys I cannot yet define,
And in their softness, I find all things new,
A love that makes my very soul entwine.
Oh, let me then, in thy dear arms remain,
And banish all my solitary pain.

###276###
The hurried pace of life, it doth not cease,
But bears me onward, like a rushing stream,
And robs my weary soul of gentle peace,
And interrupts my most beloved dream.
I long to halt, and in some quiet nook,
To find a solace from the world's loud roar,
To read the wisdom in some ancient book,
And learn the lessons taught in days of yore.
But duty calls, and I must needs obey,
And strive and toil, though weary be my frame,
Until the setting of my final day,
And quench the last and fading vital flame.
Yet, in thy thought, a restful harbour lies,
A calm retreat, beneath all troubled skies.

###277###
When I do think upon the countless years,
That lie behind, a tapestry of pain,
And count the weight of all my silent fears,
That fall like drops of unrelenting rain.
I see how swift the bloom of youth hath fled,
How strength decayed, and beauty lost its gleam,
And how the hopes that I so fondly fed,
Have vanished like a half-forgotten dream.
Yet, in the twilight of my fading days,
Thy steadfast love doth shine, a guiding light,
And through the mist of memory's dark maze,
It leads me onward, to a future bright.
So let me cling to thee, my dearest friend,
And find with thee my journey's happy end.

###278###
The painted sails that catch the morning breeze,
And speed the vessels to some distant land,
Do fill my heart with longing, if you please,
To leave this shore, and follow their command.
For in this place, no solace can I find,
No joy to ease the burden of my soul,
But restless thoughts that trouble and do bind,
And leave me yearning for a distant goal.
Thy presence, though, doth make my spirit soar,
And paint the world with colours bright and new,
And bids my weary heart to ask for more,
Than I had dared to dream could e'er be true.
So let us flee, where fortune may us lead,
And plant together love's enduring seed.

###279###
When summer's heat doth scorch the thirsty ground,
And nature groans beneath the sun's bright fire,
I seek the shade, where cooling draughts are found,
And quench the burning of my soul's desire.
So too, when anger's blaze doth fill thy breast,
And bitter words like fiery arrows fly,
I seek to bring thy troubled spirit rest,
And soothe the tempest raging in thine eye.
For love's a balm, that heals the deepest wound,
A gentle hand, that calms the troubled sea,
And in its wisdom, solace can be found,
For thee, my love, and also, dear, for me.
So let us learn, when tempers start to fray,
To cool our passions, ere they lead astray.

###280###
The passing seasons, as they onward roll,
Do bring their changes to the world around,
And touch the deepest fibres of my soul,
And make my present joys seem less profound.
The days grow short, the nights begin to creep,
And winter's chill doth nip the tender bud,
And all the world seems lulled in slumber deep,
As if reborn from some primordial mud.
But when I think of thee, my dearest one,
All nature's gloom doth vanish from my sight,
And all my weary, lonely race is run,
And darkness yields to everlasting light.
So in thy love, eternity I find,
And leave the changing seasons far behind.

###281###
When I do gaze upon the ocean's might,
And watch the waves that crash upon the shore,
I feel a kinship with its endless plight,
And long for peace, that I can find no more.
The constant surge, the ebb and flow of tide,
Doth mirror well the turmoil in my breast,
Where hopes and fears do ceaselessly abide,
And grant my weary spirit little rest.
But then I see thy face, a tranquil scene,
A sunlit haven, in this stormy strife,
And all the turmoil that hath ever been,
Doth fade away, and give new strength to life.
So let me anchor in thy loving gaze,
And find repose through all my future days.

\
\###282###
When Phoebus doth his golden chariot guide,
And weary night her sable cloak doth cast,
My heart doth with a restless longing stride,
To know the moment that my joy shall last.
For beauty's bloom, though fair it doth appear,
Is but a fleeting shadow, soon to fade,
And time, the thief, doth steal it year by year,
Leaving behind a solitary glade.
Yet in thy eyes, a brighter sun I find,
Whose radiant beams do banish every shade,
A love that shall forever be enshrined,
By fickle fortune never to be swayed.
So let us seize the hour, ere it departs,
And bind our souls in everlasting hearts.

###283###
The murmuring brook, that doth through meadows creep,
Doth whisper tales of seasons past and gone,
And ancient trees, that silent vigil keep,
Have seen the rise and fall of many a dawn.
So I, a witness to thy wondrous grace,
Do marvel at the beauty thou dost bear,
A perfect form, no flaw can e'er efface,
A gentle spirit, beyond all compare.
But ah, the thought that thou art mortal, too,
Doth bring a chill that pierces to the bone,
And makes me fear what fate may have in view,
When thy sweet presence shall be overthrown.
Yet while thou liv'st, my love shall brightly burn,
And for thy sake, no earthly joy I'll spurn.

###284###
Hark, how the lark doth greet the rising day,
With jocund song, that doth the heavens fill,
And cheerful birds, that flit and wing their way,
Do chase the shadows from the silent hill.
So in my breast, a joyful spirit wakes,
Whene'er thy image doth before me gleam,
And all my earthly care it straight forsakes,
Lost in the rapture of a waking dream.
But dreams, alas, are shadows of the mind,
And often vanish with the morning's light,
And leave behind a sorrow, sharp and kind,
That lingers through the long and lonely night.
Therefore I pray, that this sweet dream remain,
And banish from my heart all sorrow's pain.

###285###
The summer's lease hath all too short a date,
And roses fair, though blushing, soon decay,
So is the bloom of youth, its destined fate,
To yield to age, and softly pass away.
Thy beauty, like a flower, doth so gleam,
A fragrant blossom, kissed by morning dew,
But ah, it is a transient, fleeting dream,
That time, the cruel spoiler, will pursue.
Yet can I not lament what cannot be,
Nor curse the hand that doth thy charms impart,
But in thy virtue, find my solace free,
And hold thy goodness ever in my heart.
For though thy outward form may lose its light,
Thy inner worth shall shine forever bright.

###286###
When envious eyes do gaze upon thy face,
And whisper tales of folly and of shame,
My soul doth burn with a protective grace,
And shields thy virtue from their bitter blame.
For in thy heart, a purity resides,
That no false tongue can ever mar or stain,
A constant flame, where truth and goodness guides,
And scorns the venom of malicious reign.
Let them who judge with hearts of leaden hue,
And mouths that spew forth naught but bitter gall,
Behold thy spirit, noble, strong, and true,
And learn that beauty is not all in all.
For though the world may cast a shadow dark,
Thy inner light shall leave its lasting mark.

###287###
The fickle wind, that doth the leaves displace,
And stirs the waters of the restless sea,
Doth bear no echo of thy lovely grace,
Nor can it steal the joy thou giv'st to me.
For though the world may shift and change its form,
And fortunes ebb and flow like ocean's tide,
My steadfast love shall weather every storm,
And in thy constancy, securely hide.
Let others chase the fleeting, transient gleam,
Of wealth and power, that doth quickly fade,
My greatest treasure is my waking dream,
Of thee, my love, in virtue's light arrayed.
So let us build our fortress strong and deep,
Where faithful hearts eternal vigil keep.

###288###
The silent moon, that doth the night adorn,
And casts a silver gleam on field and stream,
Doth witness vows that are by lovers sworn,
And sighs that mingle with a whispered dream.
So I, beneath thy gaze, do pledge my troth,
A vow more sacred than the oaths of kings,
To cherish thee, beyond all worldly sloth,
And sing the praise thy gentle spirit sings.
For in thy smile, a universe I find,
A realm of peace, where sorrows cannot tread,
And in thy voice, a music to my mind,
That fills my soul with joys that shall not shed.
So let us walk, hand clasped, through sun and shower,
And love each other in each passing hour.

###289###
When weary days have dimmed thy spirit's fire,
And heavy burdens press upon thy soul,
My love shall be thy comforting desire,
And make thy broken fragments once more whole.
For I have seen the tempest in thine eye,
And felt the chill that doth thy spirit seize,
And longed to whisper words that would not lie,
But bring thy troubled, anxious heart some ease.
Let not the shadows of despair prevail,
Nor let the whispers of the doubt take hold,
For love's bright banner shall again unfurl,
And make thy weary spirit strong and bold.
So lean on me, when strength doth start to wane,
And in my arms, find solace from thy pain.

###290###
The gilded cage, though rich it may appear,
Doth hold a bird that yearns for open sky,
So is my heart, when thou art not held dear,
And all its captive joys begin to die.
For thou art freedom's essence, pure and bright,
A soaring spirit, that doth touch the stars,
And in thy absence, darkness is my plight,
And all my being feels the bitter scars.
But when thy presence doth again impart,
The radiant sunshine of thy radiant smile,
My soul takes flight, and dances in my heart,
And banishes the loneliness awhile.
So let me ever dwell within thy sphere,
And hold thy precious presence ever near.

###291###
When envious Fortune doth her favours lend,
To those whose hearts are cold and base and vain,
My spirit doth with righteous anger rend,
And scorns the triumphs of their wicked reign.
For what is wealth, or power, or high estate,
When love's true substance is but held in scorn?
A hollow echo, sealed by cruel fate,
A joy that vanishes ere it is born.
But in thy gaze, a truer wealth I find,
A love that doth outshine all earthly gold,
A treasure rich, that time can never bind,
A story in our hearts to be untold.
So let us build our kingdom, strong and free,
Upon the rock of shared felicity.

###292###
The fleeting moments, like the river's flow,
Do bear our youthful vigour far away,
And leave us with the seeds of age to sow,
When summer's bloom hath yielded to decay.
Yet in thy memory, I shall retain,
The vibrant colours of our shared delight,
And though the winter winds may fiercely reign,
Thy warmth shall be my solace in the night.
For beauty fades, and strength doth start to wane,
But love, like wine, doth ripen with the years,
And in its depths, a steadfast joy remain,
That conquers all our doubts and all our fears.
So let us grow old, together, hand in hand,
And find our peace within love's fertile land.

###293###
When jealous thoughts like serpents do arise,
And whisper doubts into my trusting ear,
I look upon the truth within thine eyes,
And banish all suspicion and all fear.
For in thy gaze, a mirror I do see,
Reflecting back a love that knows no guise,
A loyal heart, that beats alone for me,
And scorns the falsehoods of deceitful lies.
Let slanderous tongues their venomous darts employ,
And seek to sow the seeds of discord deep,
My faith in thee shall be my constant joy,
And through all trials, its sacred vow shall keep.
So let us stand, united, strong, and true,
My love for thee, and thy dear love for you.

###294###
The fleeting bloom of youth, a summer's sigh,
Doth vanish swift, as morning's gentle dew,
And leaves behind the autumn of the eye,
When former glories fade from mortal view.
But though thy outward form may feel the sting,
Of passing years, and time's relentless hand,
My love for thee shall ever brightly spring,
And in thy heart, find its eternal stand.
For in thy soul, a beauty doth reside,
That ages cannot touch, nor can efface,
A gentle spirit, where true virtues hide,
And shed upon the world their purest grace.
So let us cherish what the years impart,
And hold each other close within our heart.

###295###
When fortune frowns, and clouds obscure the sun,
And all the world seems clad in somber grey,
My love for thee, a steadfast course hath run,
And lights the darkness of my weary way.
For in thy smile, a sunbeam I do find,
That chases shadows from my troubled breast,
And in thy voice, a music to my mind,
That brings my anxious, weary spirit rest.
Let others seek their solace in the gold,
That glitters bright, but hath no lasting worth,
My richer treasure is a love untold,
That binds my heart to thee, from heaven to earth.
So let us face the trials that may come,
And find our comfort in love's faithful sum.

###296###
The hurried step of time, that onward flies,
And bears our fleeting moments to the past,
Doth often bring a sorrow to our eyes,
As beauty's fragile flower fades too fast.
But in thy love, a constancy I see,
That mocks the ravages of passing years,
A steadfast anchor, holding firm to me,
And banishing all doubts and all my fears.
For though the world may shift and change its face,
And fortunes turn, and pleasures cease to be,
Our love shall find its everlasting place,
A timeless bond, for all eternity.
So let us hold each other, dear and true,
My love, my life, my all, my only you.

###297###
When cruel fate doth whisper words of dread,
And threatens all that we hold dear and bright,
My courage, by thy gentle spirit led,
Shall rise to meet the challenge with all might.
For in thy gaze, a strength I do perceive,
A noble heart, that will not bend nor break,
And in thy love, I truly do believe,
That we can conquer for our own dear sake.
Let not the shadows of despair descend,
Nor let the whispers of the doubt take hold,
Our faithful love shall evermore transcend,
The trials that the future may unfold.
So let us stand, united, strong, and bold,
A story of true love, forever told.

###298###
The passing summer, with its verdant hue,
Doth yield at last to autumn's golden reign,
And as the leaves of change do fall anew,
My love for thee shall evermore remain.
For beauty's bloom, though fair it doth appear,
Is but a fleeting shadow, soon to fade,
But in thy heart, a truth I hold so dear,
A constant flame, by time's harsh hand unswayed.
So let us find our solace in the years,
That bring us closer, day by passing day,
And banish all our doubts and all our fears,
As love's true light doth guide us on our way.
Thus hand in hand, till life's last breath we sigh,
Our faithful love shall never, ever die.

###299###
When envious tongues do seek to stain thy name,
And whisper tales of folly and of shame,
My heart doth burn with a protective flame,
And shields thy virtue from their bitter blame.
For in thy soul, a purity resides,
That no false tongue can ever mar or stain,
A constant light, where truth and goodness guides,
And scorns the venom of malicious reign.
Let them who judge with hearts of leaden hue,
And mouths that spew forth naught but bitter gall,
Behold thy spirit, noble, strong, and true,
And learn that beauty is not all in all.
For though the world may cast a shadow dark,
Thy inner light shall leave its lasting mark.

###300###
The fleeting moments, like the river's flow,
Do bear our youthful vigour far away,
And leave us with the seeds of age to sow,
When summer's bloom hath yielded to decay.
Yet in thy memory, I shall retain,
The vibrant colours of our shared delight,
And though the winter winds may fiercely reign,
Thy warmth shall be my solace in the night.
For beauty fades, and strength doth start to wane,
But love, like wine, doth ripen with the years,
And in its depths, a steadfast joy remain,
That conquers all our doubts and all our fears.
So let us grow old, together, hand in hand,
And find our peace within love's fertile land.

###301###
When weary days have dimmed thy spirit's fire,
And heavy burdens press upon thy soul,
My love shall be thy comforting desire,
And make thy broken fragments once more whole.
For I have seen the tempest in thine eye,
And felt the chill that doth thy spirit seize,
And longed to whisper words that would not lie,
But bring thy troubled, anxious heart some ease.
Let not the shadows of despair prevail,
Nor let the whispers of the doubt take hold,
For love's bright banner shall again unfurl,
And make thy weary spirit strong and bold.
So lean on me, when strength doth start to wane,
And in my arms, find solace from thy pain.

###302###
The silent moon, that doth the night adorn,
And casts a silver gleam on field and stream,
Doth witness vows that are by lovers sworn,
And sighs that mingle with a whispered dream.
So I, beneath thy gaze, do pledge my troth,
A vow more sacred than the oaths of kings,
To cherish thee, beyond all worldly sloth,
And sing the praise thy gentle spirit sings.
For in thy smile, a universe I find,
A realm of peace, where sorrows cannot tread,
And in thy voice, a music to my mind,
That fills my soul with joys that shall not shed.
So let us walk, hand clasped, through sun and shower,
And love each other in each passing hour.

###302###
Whenas the sun his golden course doth run,
And doth the weary world in slumber lay,
My troubled thoughts, their labour not yet done,
Do chase the fleeting shadows of the day.
The memory of thy face, a burning brand,
Doth scorch my soul with unfulfilled desire,
And in this lonely, melancholy land,
I feed the flames of my consuming fire.
My sighs do whisper tales of love's sweet pain,
My tears, like dew, do fall on barren ground,
And though I search, I seek thy form in vain,
Where only echoes of thy name are found.
  Yet in this woe, a strange delight I keep,
  For in thy absence, my true love doth sleep.

###303###
The raven hair that crowns thy beauteous head,
Doth shame the darkness of the deepest night,
And from thine eyes, where starry beauties bred,
There shines a beam of pure, celestial light.
Thy voice, a melody that doth enthrall,
Doth make the very birds to hold their tune,
Thy gentle spirit, answering nature's call,
Is fairer than the pale and silken moon.
If Cupid's dart hath struck my heart in twain,
'Tis by thy hand that I am thus undone,
And though I bear this sweet and welcome pain,
I count it gain, for thou art beauty's son.
  So let me languish in thy sweet embrace,
  And find my heaven in thy peerless grace.

###304###
When Fortune frowns and clouds obscure the sky,
And all the world seems cloaked in shades of grey,
My thoughts then turn to where my joys do lie,
And in thy memory I find my way.
Thy smile, a sunbeam on a wintry day,
Can banish all the cold and biting frost,
Thy kindly word can drive my fears away,
And make me count no seeming pleasure lost.
For though the world may offer wealth and fame,
These fleeting baubles cannot match thy worth,
My truest treasure is to speak thy name,
And find in thee my solace on this earth.
  So when the shadows lengthen and grow deep,
  'Tis in thy love my faithful heart I keep.

###305###
The rose doth bloom, its velvet petals spread,
A fleeting beauty, destined soon to fade,
The lily white, with innocence is bred,
But even it must wither and be made
A memory upon the summer breeze,
That whispers soft of days that are no more.
So too, the strength of ancient, mighty trees,
Must yield to time, and fall upon the shore.
But thy fair image, etched within my soul,
Doth mock the ruin that time seeks to wreak,
It stands unmoved, beyond his harsh control,
And bids my heart with constant passion speak.
  For whilst I live, and draw this mortal breath,
  Thy beauty conquers even cruelest death.

###306###
When jealous tongues do wag with venomous spite,
And whisper tales that mar thy noble name,
My spirit rises to defend thy right,
And quench the sparks of their consuming flame.
For I do know thy heart, so pure and true,
More constant than the stars that guide our way,
And though their slanders pierce me through and through,
They cannot dim the brightness of thy day.
Let them heap calumny and scornful lies,
Their petty malice shall not long endure,
For truth, like dawn, shall break upon their eyes,
And prove thy virtue, radiant and pure.
  So let them rail, their foolish words are vain,
  My love for thee no earthly storm can stain.

###307###
The fields are green, the birds do sweetly sing,
The gentle breeze doth stir the verdant leaves,
And nature's bounty doth her wonders bring,
As summer's warmth her golden harvest weaves.
But all these sights, and all these pleasant sounds,
Seem dull and lifeless when thou art not near,
My joy departs, my weary spirit bounds,
To seek the one who makes my life so dear.
Thy presence is the sun that lights my sky,
Thy laughter is the music of my soul,
Without thy grace, my hopes begin to die,
And life itself doth lose its cherished goal.
  So let me bask within thy radiant gleam,
  And live with thee, as in a waking dream.

###308###
When twilight falls, and shadows start to creep,
And weary mortals seek their nightly rest,
My restless mind doth vigil sadly keep,
And thoughts of thee do swell within my breast.
The moonbeams paint a silver on the stream,
The stars do twinkle in the velvet height,
But all their beauty fades into a dream,
When I recall thy more resplendent light.
My heart doth yearn, a constant, aching plea,
To feel thy hand, to hear thy gentle sigh,
And though I know it may not ever be,
I still must love, and for thy favour cry.
  So let me dream of thee, whilst darkness reigns,
  And find in sleep some solace for my pains.

###309###
The fleeting moments, like a hurried stream,
Do pass us by, and leave us here behind,
And what we deemed a bright and lasting dream,
Is but a shadow that we cannot find.
So let us seize the present hour with might,
And drink the nectar of its sweet delight,
Before it flees into the endless night,
And leaves us lost, with nothing left to light
Our darkened path, our lonely, weary way,
But memory of joys that are no more.
Then let us love, and make the most of day,
And treasure every moment that's in store.
  For time, the thief, will steal our youth away,
  And leave us but the dust of yesterday.

###310###
Thy constancy, a beacon in the storm,
Doth guide my bark when winds begin to blow,
And keeps my fragile spirit safe and warm,
From chilling doubts that threaten to o'erthrow.
For many hearts are fickle as the tide,
That ebbs and flows with every changing gust,
But in thy love, I can securely hide,
And place my faith, and my eternal trust.
Thou art the anchor that doth hold me fast,
When tossed about on life's tumultuous sea,
And by thy side, my doubts are overcast,
And all the world seems fair and bright to me.
  So let me cling to thee, my guiding star,
  And find my peace, no matter where we are.

###311###
When winter's frost doth bind the barren earth,
And all the world is cloaked in silent snow,
My thoughts then turn to thee, and to thy worth,
And in my heart, a warming passion glow.
The naked trees, with branches gaunt and bare,
Do stand as sentinels against the sky,
But in my mind, I see thee standing there,
And all the colours of the spring pass by.
Thy voice, a melody that doth recall
The birdsong sweet of summer's golden age,
Thy smile, a sunbeam that can conquer all
The frozen dread that hovers on life's stage.
  So let me dream of thee, when tempests blow,
  And find in love a warmth that banishes woe.

###312###
The fleeting shadows of the dying day,
Do lengthen now, and stretch across the land,
And as the light begins to steal away,
I feel the absence of thy gentle hand.
The stars appear, like diamonds in the deep,
And cast a faint and shimmering delight,
But still my lonely heart doth softly weep,
For thee, my love, throughout the silent night.
Thy memory, a phantom, close at hand,
Doth tease my senses, and my soul doth crave,
The sweet communion that I understand,
Is but a dream, beyond the earthly grave.
  Yet still I hope, and in that hope I find,
  A solace that transcends all earthly kind.

###313###
When lovers part, and distance doth divide,
Their souls may ache with unfulfilled desire,
But if true love doth in their bosoms ride,
No miles can quench its ever-burning fire.
Though oceans roll and continents do lie,
Between two hearts that beat as one, it seems,
Their spirits meet beneath the selfsame sky,
And walk together in their waking dreams.
So let us not lament the miles that stretch,
Nor mourn the days that keep us far apart,
For in our minds, our spirits we can fetch,
And bind them close within each beating heart.
  Our love, a bridge, no earthly force can sever,
  And thus we shall be joined, for all forever.

###314###
The bloom of youth, a precious, fragile thing,
Doth fade too soon, like dew upon the morn,
And all the joys that passing seasons bring,
Are lost to time, ere we are fully born
To wisdom's light, and deeper understanding.
So let us cherish every passing hour,
And make our lives with worthy deeds expanding,
Before we wither, like a scentless flower.
For what is beauty, if it lacks a soul?
Or strength of arm, if no good deed it claims?
Let virtue be the aim that makes us whole,
And light our path with everlasting flames.
  So let us strive, while life's brief candle burns,
  To gain the love that true affection earns.

###315###
When fickle Fortune turns her wheel about,
And casts us down from heights of sweet content,
My soul doth seek a shelter from the doubt,
And finds in thee my solace heaven-sent.
Thy steadfast love, a rock that will not sway,
Doth bear the brunt of all the storms that rage,
And lights with hope my solitary way,
When darkness threatens to engulf life's stage.
For though the world may offer gilded lies,
And flatterers may sing a pleasing tune,
Thy honest heart, before my very eyes,
Doth shine more brightly than the midday moon.
  So let me lean on thee, my strength, my guide,
  And in thy love, my truest joys abide.

###316###
The summer's lease, hath all too short a date,
And all that's fair must perish and decay,
The rose that blooms, by winter's chilling fate,
Must bow its head and wither and give way.
So too, the bloom of beauty, rich and deep,
Doth fade with years, and leave no trace behind,
And all the promises that lovers keep,
Are lost to time, and leave no joy to find.
But thy true worth, a jewel of purest gleam,
Doth mock the ruin that the years bestow,
It shines more brightly than a passing dream,
And shall endure, whate'er the seasons show.
  For in thy soul, a beauty doth reside,
  That time itself can never turn aside.

###317###
When thoughts of thee do fill my waking hours,
And chase the shadows from my troubled mind,
I feel the strength of nature's gentlest powers,
And all the world seems loving and so kind.
Thy voice, a balm unto my weary ear,
Doth soothe the aches that sorrow doth impart,
Thy smiling countenance doth banish fear,
And plant sweet hope within my longing heart.
Though fortune may bestow her fickle smile,
Or frowning fate may cast its darkest shade,
My love for thee shall conquer every trial,
And by thy side, my heart shall not be swayed.
  So let me dwell within thy loving gaze,
  And find my bliss throughout my earthly days.

###318###
The weary traveller, when far from home,
Doth seek a haven, peaceful and serene,
And gladly doth his wandering spirit roam,
To find a spot where comfort may be seen.
So I, who've strayed through life's tempestuous seas,
And faced the gales of doubt and bitter strife,
Do find in thee a spirit that doth please,
And bring new joy and meaning to my life.
Thy gentle presence, like a summer's breeze,
Doth calm the tempest raging in my breast,
And in thy love, my troubled soul finds ease,
And in thy arms, my weary heart finds rest.
  So let me linger here, and ne'er depart,
  And make thy love the harbour of my heart.

###319###
When I behold the heavens vast and deep,
And see the stars that twinkle, bright and far,
My thoughts then turn to secrets they do keep,
And wonder where my truest pleasures are.
But looking back, my soul doth clearly see,
That all the beauty of the firmament,
Doth pale beside the lovely face of thee,
On whom my deepest affections are bent.
Thy eyes, like stars, do shed a radiant light,
Thy smile, the sun that chases night away,
And in thy love, my spirit takes its flight,
And finds its heaven, brighter than the day.
  So let me gaze on thee, my guiding light,
  And banish all the darkness of the night.

###320###
The hurried world doth rush and seldom pause,
To mark the beauty of a simple flower,
Or heed the wisdom of nature's ancient laws,
That guide the seasons in their timely hour.
But I, who've learned from thee, my gentle muse,
To see the grace in all that doth appear,
Do find the time to banish all my blues,
And hold each fleeting moment ever dear.
Thy quiet strength, a lesson to my soul,
Doth teach me patience, and a gentle grace,
And makes my broken spirit once more whole,
And finds in thee my true and rightful place.
  So let me learn from thee, and ever be,
  A faithful student of thy virtue, free.

###321###
When doubts do rise, like spectres in the night,
And whisper fears that seek to make me quail,
I look to thee, my guiding, steady light,
And all my earthly troubles then grow frail.
Thy steadfast love, a fortress strong and true,
Doth shield my heart from every bitter blow,
And though the world may be of somber hue,
Thy radiant spirit makes my own soul glow.
For in thy gaze, I find a peace profound,
A haven safe from all the storms of life,
And in thy voice, a solace can be found,
That stills the clamour and the inner strife.
  So let me rest within thy loving care,
  And find my joy, beyond all earthly care.

###322###
The fleeting moments, like a swift-winged bird,
Do pass us by, and leave us here alone,
And all the joys that once our spirits stirred,
Are but as echoes, fainter than a moan.
So let us seize the present hour with zest,
And drink the nectar of its sweet delight,
Before it flies, and puts us to the test,
And leaves us waiting for the endless night.
For what is life, but but a transient gleam,
A flickering candle, destined soon to fade?
Then let us live, as in a waking dream,
And make our lives with noble purpose made.
  So let us love, while yet the sun doth shine,
  And make each precious moment truly mine.###322###
When golden Phoebus doth his beams impart,
And chase the shades of night from out the sky,
A gentle warmth doth stir within my heart,
And bids my sleepy senses wake and try.
The birds do carol with melodious sound,
Their joyful tunes upon the morning air,
And nature's beauty doth on every ground,
A tapestry of wonders doth prepare.
The blushing rose, with dew-drop on its cheek,
Doth open wide its petals to the light,
And fragrant breezes, passing, gently speak
Of pleasures past and glories yet in sight.
So let me greet this day with open soul,
And bid all worldly cares from me unroll.

###323###
My love, whose eyes do shine with brighter gleam
Than any star that graces heaven's height,
Doth fill my waking thoughts and in my dream,
A constant beacon, banishing the night.
Her voice, a melody that doth entrance,
More sweet than lark's song at the break of morn,
Doth hold me captive in a loving trance,
And makes my weary spirit to be born.
Her lips, like rubies, soft and dewy red,
Do promise kisses that can never cease,
And in her smile, all sorrow is outspread,
Replaced by joy and everlasting peace.
   So in her grace, my heart finds its true rest,
   And by her love, I am supremely blest.

###324###
When Fortune's wheel doth turn with cruelest spite,
And casts me down from heights of sweet content,
When clouds do gather, dimming all my light,
And all my hopes to sorrow are then bent.
When friends, like summer flies, do fade away,
And leave me lonely in the darkest hour,
When faith and hope do seem to go astray,
And leave me subject to despair's dark power.
Then do I turn my thoughts to thee, my dear,
And find a solace that doth never fail,
Thy constant love dispels each rising fear,
And in its strength, I shall again prevail.
   For though the world may frown and skies be grey,
   Thy radiant spirit lights my onward way.

###325###
The fleeting hours, like shadows, swiftly glide,
And steal away the bloom from beauty's face,
The sands of time, that none can turn aside,
Do mark the passage of our earthly race.
The youthful vigour, once so strong and bold,
Doth yield at length to age's chilling hand,
And tales of glory, once so brightly told,
Do fade like whispers on a lonely strand.
Yet in thy heart, a timeless beauty lies,
That mocks the passage of the passing years,
A gentle spirit, seen within thine eyes,
That conquers all our mortal doubts and fears.
   So let us cherish love that will not fade,
   A sanctuary from life's sharpest blade.

###326###
What art is there that can with truth portray
The subtle workings of a jealous mind?
That serpent's hiss, that poisons every day,
And leaves but bitter ashes far behind.
It breeds suspicion where no cause is found,
And twists kind actions into darkest plots,
It builds a prison on unhallowed ground,
And binds the soul with ever-tightening knots.
The loving glance, it sees as treachery,
The tender word, a falsehood meant to sting,
And in its grip, all joy doth cease to be,
And only restless, gnawing sorrows bring.
   Oh, curse of envy, banish from my breast,
   And grant my troubled spirit peaceful rest.

###327###
When absence doth my dearest love divide,
And leagues of land do stretch between us twain,
My lonely heart, where sorrow doth preside,
Doth yearn for thee and feel a gnawing pain.
The sun doth rise, but brings no warmth to me,
The moon doth shine, but casts a mournful gleam,
For all the world is void without thy plea,
And life itself doth seem a troubled dream.
I trace thy face upon the empty air,
And whisper words that no one else can hear,
And dream of moments when we again will share
A love that makes each passing moment dear.
   Until that day, my soul shall sigh and weep,
   And in my dreams, thy promised kiss I'll keep.

###328###
The fading light of day, when sun descends,
And paints the western sky with fiery hue,
A solemn peace upon the world extends,
And bids the restless soul to find anew.
The day's loud clamour, with its hurried pace,
Doth yield at last to evening's gentle calm,
And in this quiet, I can find a space,
To soothe my spirit with a peaceful balm.
The stars begin to prick the darkening veil,
And shine like diamonds on a velvet cloth,
And ancient legends that the night doth hail,
Awaken thoughts that banish sorrow's wrath.
   So let me rest, ere morning calls me forth,
   And find new strength to face the coming worth.

###329###
My muse, that art the fountain of my rhyme,
That doth inspire these verses from my soul,
Whence comes the power to conquer cruel time,
And make my humble thoughts of worth extol?
Is it the breath of heaven, gently blown,
That stirs the embers of a poet's fire,
Or is it seeds of beauty, deeply sown,
That blossom forth at thy divine desire?
Perchance it is the love I bear for thee,
That lends a wing to all my captive words,
And sets them soaring, wild and strong and free,
Like joyous, unchained, brightly singing birds.
   So guide my pen, and let thy grace impart,
   The truest feelings of a lover's heart.

###330###
When winter's frost doth grip the barren land,
And nature sleeps beneath a snowy shroud,
When bitter winds do blow at stern command,
And hide the sun behind a chilling cloud.
When all the world seems bleak and desolate,
And warmth and colour have entirely fled,
My heart finds solace, though it be by fate,
In memories of summer days instead.
Thy love, a sun that shines eternally,
Doth chase away the chill and darkest gloom,
And in its warmth, new life returns to me,
Dispelling shadows from my silent tomb.
   So though the season bids the world be bare,
   Thy love provides a comfort past compare.

###331###
What power hath the eye, that can impart
A thousand thoughts without a single sound?
That can arrest the motion of the heart,
And plant deep feelings in unlooked-for ground.
A fleeting glance, a sidelong, stolen look,
Can raise a tempest in a tranquil breast,
And write a chapter in love's mystic book,
That puts all reason to a sudden test.
The silent language of a tender gaze,
Doth speak of passions that no words can tell,
And lost in admiration's dizzy maze,
We fall beneath its captivating spell.
   So let my eyes convey what words can't show,
   The depths of love that in my spirit flow.

###332###
When folly doth my truer judgment blind,
And reason slumbers, leaving me astray,
When worldly cares do occupy my mind,
And lead my wandering footsteps far away.
When vanity doth whisper honeyed lies,
And pride erects a throne within my soul,
And earthly pleasures, with their sweet disguise,
Do tempt my spirit to a siren's shoal.
Then do I think of thee, my guiding star,
Whose wisdom shines with clear and steady ray,
And though I wander, ever near or far,
Thy counsel turns me to the righteous way.
   So blesséd be the one whose gentle plea,
   Doth draw my errant spirit back to thee.

###333###
The gentle dew, that falls in morning's hush,
Doth kiss the petals of the sleeping flower,
And wakes its beauty with a tender blush,
To greet the dawning of the early hour.
The lark ascends, with notes of pure delight,
And pours its melody upon the breeze,
While shadows vanish from the fading night,
And life awakens in the verdant trees.
So does thy presence, with its sweet repose,
Awaken joy where sorrow held its reign,
And beauty blossoms like a summer rose,
Dispelling darkness, easing every pain.
   For in thy love, a new dawn doth appear,
   And makes the world more beautiful and clear.

###334###
When time doth steal the roses from thy cheek,
And silver threads do mingle with thy hair,
When weary age doth make thy spirit weak,
And dims the lustre that was once so fair.
Let not despair thy gentle soul embrace,
Nor let the thought of fading beauty sting,
For in thy heart, a nobler, truer grace,
Doth bloom eternal, joy and comfort bring.
Thy wisdom, gained through many passing years,
Doth shine more brightly than youth's fleeting glow,
And in thy spirit, calm dispels all fears,
A timeless beauty, ever strong and slow.
   So let us age with dignity and pride,
   With love and wisdom walking side by side.

###335###
The busy bee, that toils with ceaseless might,
And gathers honey from the sweetest bloom,
Doth teach me lessons, shining ever bright,
To banish idleness and idle gloom.
It seeks its labour with a joyful hum,
And makes its purpose clear to all who see,
And though its task be arduous and numb,
It finds a sweetness in its industry.
So let me strive, with purpose in my heart,
To build a life that's worthy to be known,
And play with diligence my humble part,
Upon this earthly stage, where seeds are sown.
   For in our work, a noble strength we find,
   And leave a worthy legacy behind.

###336###
When envious tongues do wag with bitter spite,
And spread their calumnies like poisoned darts,
Assailing innocence with darkest might,
And piercing through the most devoted hearts.
When falsehood reigns, and truth is cast aside,
And reputation's honour is defiled,
When malice walks with impudent stride,
And innocence is cruelly reviled.
Then do I cling to truth, my steadfast guide,
And trust in justice, though the path be long,
For though the wicked may in triumph ride,
Their reign is fleeting, and their power not strong.
   So let them speak, their venom shall not last,
   While honest virtue holds its anchor fast.

###337###
The fading sun, that bids the day adieu,
And paints the heavens with a dying fire,
Doth whisper tales, forever old and new,
Of moments past, and visions that inspire.
The shadows lengthen, soft and dark and deep,
And weary nature settles down to rest,
While silent stars their vigil start to keep,
And twinkle brightly from the heavens blessed.
So let us find in evening's quiet grace,
A time for thought, for peace, and sweet release,
And in this stillness, find our rightful place,
Where weary souls may find a lasting peace.
   For though the day may end in fading light,
   The coming dawn shall banish darkest night.

###338###
When duty calls, with stern and solemn plea,
And bids me leave what makes my spirit glad,
When sacrifice is asked of humble me,
And all my pleasure must be rendered sad.
When worldly gain doth beckon from afar,
And whispers tales of riches to be won,
But honour bids me stay, where I now are,
And see my rightful obligation done.
Then do I choose the path of noble worth,
Though it be steep, and fraught with toil and pain,
For true reward resides not on this earth,
But in a conscience that is clear and plain.
   So let me serve with steadfast, honest will,
   And let my duty my whole being fill.

###339###
The silent stream, that through the meadow flows,
With gentle murmur, whispers soft and low,
Reflecting skies where beauty ever grows,
And carrying seeds of life where it doth go.
It asks no praise, nor seeks a loud acclaim,
But with its quiet presence, sweet and mild,
It nourishes the earth, and bears its name,
A simple blessing, wonderfully wild.
So let my actions, like this flowing stream,
Be humble, constant, and forever true,
And in their course, fulfill my deepest dream,
To bring some goodness, ever fresh and new.
   For in the quiet work, a strength we find,
   That leaves a lasting peace for all mankind.

###340###
When tempest winds do rage with furious might,
And shake the oak that stands against the blast,
When darkened clouds obscure the guiding light,
And fear within the soul is fiercely cast.
When waves do crash and threaten to o'erwhelm,
And all seems lost, and hope begins to flee,
Then do I hold to thee, my guiding helm,
My steadfast anchor in the stormy sea.
Thy love, a beacon, shining through the gloom,
Doth guide me safely to a peaceful shore,
And from despair's dark, all-consuming tomb,
Doth raise my spirit, wounded and so sore.
   So though the storms of life may fiercely blow,
   In thy dear love, a strength I ever know.

###341###
The bloom of youth, that fades as seasons turn,
And leaves behind the lines of passing years,
A lesson that all mortal hearts must learn,
And conquer vanity with wiser tears.
The fleeting beauty, that the world doth prize,
Is but a shadow of a deeper grace,
That shines eternally within our eyes,
And time itself can never quite erase.
Thy spirit's light, that burns with constant fire,
Doth far outshine the bloom of passing days,
And fills my soul with an untold desire,
To walk with thee in wisdom's gentler ways.
   So let us seek the beauty of the soul,
   That makes the fractured spirit truly whole.

###342###
When doubt doth whisper, with a chilling sound,
And casts a shadow on my trusting heart,
When faith and reason cannot here be found,
And all my surest purposes depart.
When fears like spectres do begin to creep,
And steal the courage that I held so dear,
And troubled thoughts do banish peaceful sleep,
And fill my waking hours with anxious fear.
Then do I turn my gaze to skies above,
And seek the solace of a power unseen,
And in the whisperings of endless love,
I find a peace, serene and ever keen.
   For though the world may press with heavy hand,
   My faith in heaven helps me understand.

###342###
Whenas the sun, with golden eye, doth gaze
Upon the world, and chases night away,
My heart doth burn with love's incessant blaze,
And all my thoughts on thee do brightly play.
The gentle breeze that whispers through the trees,
Doth speak thy name in every sigh it sends,
And birds do sing their sweetest melodies,
As if to praise the joy thy presence lends.
But ah, my soul is bound by bitter chain,
For thou art far, and I can but lament,
My love, a captive to this endless pain,
On dreams of thee my weary days are spent.
So let me hope that fate will soon conspire,
To bring us nigh, and quench this burning fire.

###343###
The fleeting years do steal our youth apace,
And furrow lines upon the fairest brow,
As time, that thief, doth leave his cruel trace,
And with his scythe doth mow our beauty now.
The rose that blooms with petals soft and deep,
Shall surely fade and wither to the ground,
And all the vows that lovers swore to keep,
In dust and ashes shall at last be found.
Yet, if thy love, like a celestial star,
Doth shine upon me with its steadfast light,
Then shall my heart find solace from afar,
And banish shadows of eternal night.
So let us cling to love, a treasure rare,
That conquers death, and time, and all despair.

###344###
When Fortune smiles, and all the world seems fair,
And every step is graced with sweet success,
Beware the serpent hiding in the lair,
Whose venomous sting brings sorrow and distress.
For gilded smiles may mask a heart of guile,
And honeyed words may hide a poisoned dart,
The fairest guise can oft conceal a vile
And treacherous purpose, tearing love apart.
My trusting soul, so eager to believe,
Hath learned a lesson, etched in bitter tears,
That beauty's face can truly and deceive,
And sow the seeds of all my future fears.
So let me learn to read each subtle sign,
And guard my heart from treachery divine.

###345###
The silent night, when stars begin to gleam,
Doth lend a canvas for my thoughts to stray,
And in the mirror of a waking dream,
I see thy face, and wish to greet the day.
Thy gentle voice, a music to mine ear,
Doth banish all the clamour of the town,
And in thy presence, banish is all fear,
As peace descends, and lays my burdens down.
But when thou art from me by distance torn,
A hollow ache resides within my breast,
My joyful spirit, utterly forlorn,
Doth yearn for thee, and cannot find its rest.
So guide my steps, thou beacon of my soul,
And make my fractured heart entirely whole.

###346###
The winter's chill doth bite with icy breath,
And nature sleeps, in slumber cold and deep,
As life itself seems vanquished unto death,
And chilling winds their mournful vigil keep.
The naked trees, with branches stark and bare,
Do reach towards the heavens, in their plea,
And frozen streams no longer flow with care,
Reflecting naught but bleakest misery.
Yet in this gloom, a tiny seed doth lie,
Beneath the snow, in hopeful slumber bound,
Awaiting spring, beneath a warmer sky,
To break its shell, and spring from out the ground.
So shall my love, though frozen now it seems,
Awake in time, and bloom in summer dreams.

###347###
When I behold thy countenance so bright,
More fair than Phoebus in his midday pride,
My spirit soars, and takes a joyous flight,
As all my earthly troubles do subside.
Thy eyes, like stars that pierce the darkest night,
Do fill my soul with an ethereal grace,
And in their depths, I find a pure delight,
Reflected in thy captivating face.
The rosy blush that paints thy cheeks so soft,
Doth shame the dawn, and make the roses pale,
And every word thy lovely lips do waft,
Is sweeter than the nightingale's own tale.
So let me dwell forever in thy sight,
And bask in love's all-conquering delight.

###348###
The fickle crowd, with ever-changing mind,
Doth praise today what they condemn tomorrow,
Their loyalty is not of any kind,
But shifts and turns, like wind, to joy or sorrow.
One hour they cheer, with voices loud and long,
The next they scorn, with curses and with hate,
Their fickle hearts, they follow every throng,
And blindly yield themselves to changing fate.
My constant love, however, shall remain,
A steadfast rock against the stormy sea,
Though tempests rage, and all else turn to pain,
My heart beats true, devoted all to thee.
So let the world its senseless whims pursue,
My love, my truth, shall ever be for you.

###349###
When gentle sleep doth steal my senses hence,
And all the cares of day begin to fade,
My dreams are filled with thy sweet innocence,
A perfect vision, in my slumber made.
We walk through fields where golden flowers bloom,
And hear the music of the whispering breeze,
Dispelling shadows of all earthly gloom,
And finding solace in such ecstasies.
But then I wake, and find myself alone,
The dream dispersed, the vision flown and gone,
My lonely heart, with silent grief doth moan,
And longs to greet the dawning of the sun.
So let me seek the slumber that I crave,
Wherein thy presence doth my spirit save.

###350###
The poet's quill, though dipped in ink so black,
Can never truly capture all thy grace,
Nor can the painter, on his canvas rack,
Portray the beauty of thy wondrous face.
For words are weak, and colours fade and die,
Compared to that which lives within my breast,
A fire burning, reaching to the sky,
A love that puts all mortal souls to test.
Thou art a masterpiece, by heaven wrought,
A symphony of beauty, pure and true,
A gift from realms that can alone be thought,
And all my being is enthralled by you.
So let me praise thee, though my voice be low,
For in thy light, my truest passions glow.

###351###
When I do gaze upon the fading light,
And see the sun descend behind the hills,
A melancholy creeps into the night,
And with a mournful dirge my spirit fills.
The shadows lengthen, and the day is done,
And all the joys that it did once possess,
Are gone, as if they never had begun,
Leaving behind a void of emptiness.
My heart, like twilight, holds a mingled hue,
Of joy for what hath been, and sorrow deep,
For in the coming darkness, I eschew,
The precious moments that I cannot keep.
So let me cherish what I hold so dear,
Before it vanishes, and disappears.

###352###
The world's a stage, and we are players all,
Who strut and fret our hour upon the scene,
And answer to the beck and call,
Of fates unseen, both cruel and ever keen.
We play our parts, with laughter and with tears,
And don our masks, to hide our inner strife,
And all our triumphs, all our deepest fears,
Are but a breath within this fleeting life.
Yet, in this play, one role I choose to own,
To love thee truly, with a heart sincere,
A part that shall forever be my throne,
And banish all that is of doubt and fear.
So let us act with love, our guiding star,
And play our roles, no matter where we are.

###353###
When bitter words like poisoned arrows fly,
And pierce the soul with keen and sharpest sting,
My wounded heart can only weep and sigh,
And find no balm that healing balm can bring.
The careless tongue, a weapon of the night,
Doth wound more deeply than a sharpened blade,
And leaves behind a never-ending blight,
Where trust and tenderness have been betrayed.
Yet, if thy voice, like music, soft and low,
Doth speak of peace, and banish all my pain,
Then shall my spirit find the strength to grow,
And rise again, from sorrow's weary reign.
So let thy gentleness my wounds repair,
And chase away the shadows of despair.

###354###
The summer's heat, with languid, golden ray,
Doth lull the world to slumber, sweet and deep,
And all the cares of life are chased away,
While lazy hours their silent vigil keep.
The scent of roses fills the perfumed air,
And birds do sing their carols, clear and bright,
A time for joy, and freedom from all care,
Bathed in the sun's all-conquering delight.
But even in this bliss, my thoughts do turn,
To thee, my love, who art my dearest prize,
And for thy presence, does my spirit yearn,
To share this joy beneath the summer skies.
So let us revel in this golden time,
And make our love the sweet, eternal rhyme.

###355###
When envy's eye doth cast a hateful glance,
And poisons all with its malignant fume,
My spirit trembles, caught within a trance,
And sees my fortune shrouded in the gloom.
The whispers dark, that spread like wildfire's spread,
Can mar the fairest name, and tarnish truth,
And fill the hearts with doubt and chilling dread,
Destroying joy, and stealing precious youth.
Yet, if thy faith, a shield against all harm,
Doth stand with me, and banish every foe,
Then shall my soul be safe from all alarm,
And in thy love, my inner strength shall grow.
So let us scorn the serpent's venomous hiss,
And find our refuge in a loving kiss.

###356###
The ocean deep, with its mysterious might,
Doth hold within its vast and boundless breast,
A thousand secrets, hidden from the light,
Where ancient wonders find their silent rest.
The rolling waves, that crash upon the shore,
Do sing a song of ages past and gone,
And echo tales of battles fought of yore,
And futures yet to break upon the dawn.
So too my love, a sea that knows no end,
Doth surge and swell with passion's endless tide,
And in its depths, my spirit doth transcend,
All earthly bounds, with nowhere left to hide.
So let us plunge within this loving sea,
And find our souls forever joined as we.

###357###
When sickness strikes, and brings the body low,
And all the strength doth drain from weary frame,
Then friendship's touch, a comfort sweet doth flow,
And whispers hope, and calls us by our name.
The kindly hand that smooths the fevered brow,
The gentle voice that speaks of sweet relief,
Doth make the darkest moments less somehow,
And banish swiftly all consuming grief.
But if thy love, like medicine so rare,
Doth pour its balm upon my ailing soul,
Then shall I rise, and cast away all care,
And be made whole, and truly be made whole.
So let thy love be that which heals my pain,
And makes me strong, and vigorous again.

###358###
The changing moon, that waxes and doth wane,
Doth mirror well the fickle human heart,
Which shifts and turns, and seeks its pleasure vain,
And plays with love, then tears the bonds apart.
One moment bright, with promise and with fire,
The next obscured, by clouds of doubt and fear,
Consumed by lust, or base and low desire,
And holding naught that is of spirit dear.
My steadfast heart, however, shall remain,
A constant orb, that shines for thee alone,
Unmoved by storms, or by the driving rain,
Upon this truth, my love is ever shown.
So let us be like sun and moon above,
United ever, in our faithful love.

###359###
When weary labours steal my strength away,
And all my efforts seem to be in vain,
I long to find a respite from the fray,
And rest my spirit from its constant strain.
The world demands, with never-ending plea,
That we should toil, and strive, and never cease,
But in that toil, we lose ourselves, and flee,
From all that brings us solace and true peace.
Yet, in thy smile, I find a sweet release,
A balm that soothes the weariness I bear,
And bids my troubled thoughts at last to cease,
And fill my soul with comfort beyond compare.
So let me find my solace in thy gaze,
And live anew, through all my coming days.

###360###
The fading bloom, that once did brightly shine,
Doth now decline, its beauty gone and past,
And all its glory, once so truly thine,
Is but a memory, too frail to last.
The withered leaf, that falls from autumn tree,
Doth speak of change, and seasons on the wing,
And all that seemed so permanent to me,
Doth fade away, as fleeting moments sing.
Yet in my heart, thy beauty shall endure,
A timeless grace, that never shall decay,
A love eternal, steadfast and secure,
That conquers time, and drives all fears away.
So let us cherish what we hold so true,
My love, my life, forever bound to you.

###361###
When sorrow's shadow falls upon my soul,
And all the world seems draped in deepest grey,
My spirits sink, beyond my own control,
And find no comfort in the light of day.
The tears do flow, unbidden and unseen,
And grief doth grip me with its icy hand,
As all my hopes, and all that might have been,
Dissolve to dust, across a barren land.
But if thy voice, a solace sweet and mild,
Doth whisper comfort, banishing my woe,
Then shall my heart, like a contented child,
Find peace and strength, and in thy love shall grow.
So let thy kindness be my guiding star,
And heal the wounds, no matter where they are.

###362###
The fleeting fame, that mortals strive to gain,
Is but a bubble, rising in the air,
Which bursts and vanishes, and leaves no stain,
A hollow prize, beyond all true repair.
The laurels won, by deeds of might and main,
Shall wither soon, and fade to naught but dust,
And all the praise, that men so strive to gain,
Is but a whisper, lost in time's cold gust.
But if my verse, though humble it may be,
Can capture some small echo of thy worth,
Then shall it live, eternally for thee,
And find a fame that spans the whole wide earth.
So let my rhyme, a monument of love,
Be praised by thee, and blessed by stars above.

###362###
When as the sun doth blaze with summer's heat,
And nature blooms in colours bright and bold,
My heart doth yearn for solace, calm and sweet,
A gentle breeze to make my spirit whole.
The buzzing bee doth flit from flower to flower,
And birds do sing with voices clear and strong,
But in my breast, I feel a lonely hour,
Wherein no joyful melody doth throng.
Oh, when shall love, like dew upon the rose,
My parched and weary soul refresh and cheer?
When shall my discontented spirit close
Its weary eyes and banish every fear?
   For in thy presence, all my ills do cease,
   And grant my troubled heart a blessed peace.

###363###
The fleeting moments, swift as winged time,
Doth steal away the blossoms of my youth,
And leave behind the winter's bitter rime,
And dim the glory of my summer's truth.
My locks, once black as midnight's darkest hue,
Are now bedewed with streaks of frosted white,
And in my face, the furrows deeper grew,
Betraying age with all its fading light.
Yet still within my soul, a spark remains,
A fire unquenched by years, however long,
That leaps and dances, breaking through the chains
Of weary flesh, and bids my spirit strong.
   So let me love, whilst life doth grant me breath,
   And scorn the cold embrace of coming death.

###364###
When Fortune smiles, and all the world doth seem
A painted stage, where joy doth freely flow,
And golden hopes do shimmer like a dream,
Then shall my heart with gratitude o'erflow.
But when the clouds do gather, dark and deep,
And all the light of happiness is gone,
And bitter tears do from my eyelids leap,
I find no solace, till the break of dawn.
So is it with the lover's fickle state,
One moment blest, the next in deep despair,
Tossed on the waves of an uncertain fate,
A fragile bark, exposed to every air.
   Yet love, though tempest-tossed, can still endure,
   And find its haven, steadfast and secure.

###365###
The silent night, with starry mantle spread,
Doth whisper secrets to the sleeping earth,
Whilst troubled thoughts within my weary head,
Do stir and wrestle, finding little mirth.
I gaze upon the moon, a pallid gleam,
And think of thee, my distant, cherished one,
And in my soul, a poignant, silent dream,
Of days we walked beneath the golden sun.
Doth absence dull the ardour of thy heart?
Or doth thy memory still hold me dear?
Alas, I fear our loves are torn apart,
And whisper'd words are lost to passing year.
   Yet hope doth cling, though faint and far away,
   That love shall triumph, and our hearts shall stay.

###366###
The ink doth flow, a river from my quill,
To paint the portrait of my lady's grace,
Her eyes, like stars that shine on midnight's hill,
Her smile, a dawn that lights her lovely face.
Her voice, a music that the Muses weave,
Her wit, a dart that pierces through the mind,
And when she speaks, I scarce can well believe,
Such perfect beauty I could ever find.
No painter's brush, nor sculptor's patient hand,
Could e'er immortalize her radiant charm,
She is the fairest creature in the land,
And holds my captive heart from any harm.
   So let me write, and praise her virtues still,
   And for her love, my very life I'll spill.

###367###
My heart doth beat a rhythm strange and new,
A pulse that quickens at thy gentle sigh,
And all the world appears in brighter hue,
When thy dear gaze doth softly meet my eye.
The common things, which once I held in scorn,
Now seem ennobled by thy passing touch,
And every breeze that blows on summer's morn,
Doth whisper of a love that means so much.
Oh, could I but enshrine this precious hour,
And hold it fast, against the coming years,
To banish doubt, and every bitter sour,
And drown the memory of all my fears.
   For in this love, a greater joy I find,
   Than all the fleeting pleasures of mankind.

###368###
When envy's viper, with its venomous sting,
Doth seek to poison all that I hold dear,
And whisper doubts that make my spirit sing,
A song of sorrow, mingled with great fear.
When petty minds, with malice in their gaze,
Do seek to mar the beauty I behold,
And cast a shadow on my sunniest days,
And truths I cherish, turn to lies and gold.
Then do I turn my thoughts to thee alone,
My constant star, my beacon in the night,
And in thy love, a strength is surely known,
That shields me from the envious and slight.
   For thou art pure, and free from all disdain,
   And in thy virtue, I shall e'er remain.

###369###
The fleeting rose, that blooms with summer's pride,
Doth shed its petals to the passing breeze,
And ere we know it, beauty doth subside,
And leave the boughs of barren, winter trees.
So is the bloom of youth, that fades so fast,
The strength of manhood, that begins to wane,
And all the glories that were meant to last,
Are swallowed by the unrelenting rain.
Yet in my verse, I strive to keep alive,
The memory of that which I adore,
That beauty's essence may forever thrive,
And live and breathe, when flesh shall be no more.
   So shall my lines, thy loveliness commend,
   And to all time, thy radiant charms extend.

###370###
When absence chills the spirit's warmest fire,
And days grow long, and nights seem dark and deep,
My soul doth yearn with unfulfilled desire,
And lonely vigil, restless, I do keep.
The birds still sing their customary tune,
The sun still rises, painting skies with gold,
But all is hollow, 'neath the distant moon,
A story of my sorrow to be told.
Oh, tell me, love, when shall we meet again?
When shall this painful separation cease?
And banish all this overwhelming pain,
And bring my weary heart a sweet release?
   For till that hour, my spirit shall not mend,
   Nor find true solace, till our loves transcend.

###371###
The tongue of rumour, with its babbling sound,
Doth spread false tales, and stain the purest name,
And whisper slanders on the common ground,
To set the world ablaze with idle flame.
The honest heart, that knows no guile nor art,
Is oft assailed by venomous report,
And torn asunder, rent with painful smart,
And made a target for the cruel sport.
But wisdom lies in knowing what is true,
And not in yielding to the common cry,
To judge with care, and see the matter through,
And let the false accuser pass thee by.
   For truth, though slow, shall conquer in the end,
   And virtue's shield, shall ever thee defend.

###372###
When I do gaze upon thy beauteous face,
And mark the lines of kindness in thine eyes,
I feel within my soul a sweet embrace,
A calm that stills the storm and dries my sighs.
Thy gentle spirit, like a summer's morn,
Doth chase away the shadows of my doubt,
And bids my weary spirit be reborn,
And banish all the fears that hover 'bout.
No other treasure, wealth can e'er bestow,
No worldly gain, can equal such delight,
As when I feel thy loving kindness flow,
And banish darkness with its radiant light.
   For in thy love, my truest joy I find,
   The rarest jewel of all humankind.

###373###
The fleeting joy, that dances in the air,
And makes the present moment seem so bright,
Doth vanish swift, and leave a soul's despair,
When shadows gather, and conceal the light.
The laughter fades, the happy song is done,
The gilded moment turns to bitter dust,
And all the triumphs that we thought were won,
Are swept away by time's relentless gust.
So let me build my joy on firmer ground,
On love that deepens with each passing year,
A lasting solace, ever to be found,
