And banish all that makes the spirit fear.
   For in a love that's constant and is true,
   My soul shall find its lasting joy in you.

###374###
When weary nature, 'neath the winter's snow,
Lies dormant, waiting for the spring's embrace,
And icy winds do through the branches blow,
And silence holds the solitary place.
My heart doth mirror this benumbed estate,
A frozen landscape, where no blossom grows,
And though I long for love, I must await,
The melting of these long and bitter woes.
But hope, a faint and distant star, doth gleam,
That spring shall come, and life shall rise anew,
And break the slumber of this frozen dream,
And bring my frozen heart its vital hue.
   So shall I wait, with patience, for that day,
   When love shall thaw and chase all grief away.

###375###
The world doth offer pleasures, sweet and vain,
That sparkle briefly, like a passing gleam,
And chase the spirit with a joyous strain,
Then vanish swift, as fades a waking dream.
The taste of wine, the touch of softest silk,
The thrill of conquest, and the lover's kiss,
Are transient joys, as fleeting as the milk,
That soon is curdled, bringing naught but miss.
But in thy presence, I a deeper bliss,
A joy that doth with every moment grow,
A love that never can I truly miss,
A constant stream, whose currents freely flow.
   For in thy love, my truest comfort lies,
   A lasting joy that never fades or dies.

###376###
When shadows lengthen, and the day doth wane,
And twilight whispers of the coming night,
My thoughts do turn to thee, and ease the pain,
Of separation, with a fond delight.
Though miles may stretch between us, far and wide,
And weary days may bring us little cheer,
My heart doth hold thee ever close inside,
And banishes all doubt and every fear.
For in the chambers of my memory,
Thy image shines, a beacon bright and bold,
And whispers to my soul, eternally,
A love that never can grow weak or old.
   So let us hold this love, however far,
   And guide our souls by its celestial star.

###377###
The fleeting bloom of youth, with rosy cheek,
Doth vanish fast, as doth the morning dew,
And age doth creep, with footsteps slow and meek,
And steal the vigour that was ever new.
The locks of raven, turn to silver white,
The eyes that sparkled, lose their fiery gleam,
And strength departs, with all its former might,
As shadows lengthen in a passing dream.
But though my outward form may fade and wane,
And time doth carve its furrows on my face,
My love for thee shall ever still remain,
And find within my heart its dearest place.
   So let us love, whilst life doth grant us days,
   And find our solace in each other's gaze.

###378###
When doubts do plague me, and the world seems dark,
And fortune's favour seems to turn away,
I find within thy love a guiding spark,
That leads me onward to a brighter day.
Thy gentle spirit, like a healing balm,
Doth soothe the wounds that life has dealt to me,
And in thy presence, I can find a calm,
A sweet release from all anxiety.
No earthly treasure, e'er could bring me peace,
Like that which flows from thy devoted heart,
A love that bids my troubled spirit cease,
And plays in life a sweet and vital part.
   For in thy love, my truest joy I find,
   The rarest solace of all humankind.

###379###
The summer's lease, too short and yet so sweet,
Doth hasten on, with ever-quickened pace,
And ere we know it, beauty doth retreat,
And leave behind a bare and empty space.
The verdant fields, that once did proudly bloom,
Are now laid low, by autumn's chilling hand,
And all the light of summer finds its tomb,
As winter's frost doth sweep across the land.
So is it with the fleeting joys of love,
That blossom brightly, for a little while,
Then fade and wither, sent from high above,
To leave the heart in sorrow and in trial.
   Yet true affection, shall outlast the frost,
   And bloom anew, when all seems truly lost.

###380###
When envious tongues do speak with bitter gall,
And malice seeks to stain the purest name,
And cause the bravest spirit e'en to fall,
Beneath the burden of their hateful blame.
When slanders fly, like poisoned arrows cast,
To pierce the heart, and leave it bleeding sore,
And reputations, built to ever last,
Are shattered, scattered, and are seen no more.
Then do I turn to thee, my steadfast friend,
Whose honest judgment, never goes astray,
And in thy wisdom, all my fears do end,
And chase the shadows of the doubt away.
   For thou art just, and true in all thy ways,
   And guide my heart through all my darkest days.

###381###
The fleeting hour, that brings us joy and mirth,
Doth vanish swift, as doth the morning mist,
And leaves behind no lasting trace on earth,
But memories that our hearts have kissed.
The laughter fades, the happy song is done,
The gilded moment turns to bitter dust,
And all the triumphs that we thought were won,
Are swept away by time's relentless gust.
So let me build my joy on firmer ground,
On love that deepens with each passing year,
A lasting solace, ever to be found,
And banish all that makes the spirit fear.
   For in a love that's constant and is true,
   My soul shall find its lasting joy in you.

###382###
When I do think upon thy absent face,
And feel the void that absence leaves behind,
My heart doth long to find its rightful place,
And leave these lonely, troubled thoughts confined.
The days are long, the nights are dark and deep,
And in my breast, a constant ache I bear,
Whilst weary eyes their silent vigil keep,
And whisper prayers upon the empty air.
Oh, when shall Cupid, with his arrow keen,
Reunite our souls, and end this painful strife?
And grant us bliss, where sorrow hath not been,
And fill our hearts with everlasting life?
   For till that hour, my spirit shall not mend,
   Nor find true solace, till our loves transcend.
   
###382###
When thou dost smile, the very sun doth hide,
And shadows creep where brighter beams should play;
Thy laughter, like a tempest on the tide,
Doth steal the calm and chase the light away.
Thy brow, a field where noble thoughts do dwell,
Doth knit itself in seeming discontent;
Yet in thy gaze, a softer story tell,
Of love that burns, though to itself be lent.
If outward frowns do mask an inward grace,
And silence speak what words cannot convey,
Then let me read the spirit of thy face,
And find the truth that doth my soul obey.
So shall I know, though tempest may abound,
That in thy heart, true constancy is found.

###383###
The fleeting moments, like swift birds in flight,
Do bear away the hours of my delight;
And when I seek to hold them, with all might,
They vanish fast, beyond my keenest sight.
The roseate morn, that paints the eastern sky,
Doth fade ere noon, and yields to evening's shade;
So youth's fair bloom doth wither and doth die,
And all its pomp and glory is decayed.
Yet if my love, like some enduring star,
Can pierce the gloom and banish all my fear,
Then shall this passing world seem not so far,
And in thy presence, joy shall be held dear.
For though time's hand doth work its cruelest art,
Thy steadfast love shall keep my hopeful heart.

###384###
My muse, which erst did soar on wings so bold,
And sing of glories that would ne'er grow old,
Now lags behind, its fervent tale untold,
As if by icy winter's grasp controlled.
The spring of youth, with all its verdant hue,
Hath passed me by, and left but withered leaves;
My wit, once sharp, now dull and scarce anew,
A barren ground where nothing fruitful weaves.
Yet when I look upon thy beauteous eye,
A spark of fire doth rekindle in my breast;
And though my verse may fainter seem to fly,
Thy matchless worth shall put it to the test.
So let me strive, though feeble be my quill,
To praise thy name, and show my loving will.

###385###
The babbling brook, that winds through meadows green,
Doth murmur secrets to the listening ear;
A gentle sound, of sights that can be seen,
And tales of nature, banishing all fear.
But in my breast, a deeper current flows,
A hidden stream of passion, fierce and deep;
Whose silent surge no outward tempest shows,
While secret fires within my bosom sleep.
If thou couldst know the ocean of my soul,
And chart the depths where hidden treasures lie,
Then wouldst thou see what joys my heart control,
And understand the reason of my sigh.
For though my words be few, and softly said,
My love for thee hath no appointed stead.

###386###
When envious tongues do whisper of my fault,
And seek to stain the honor of my name,
My steadfast heart doth stand as on a vault,
Unmoved by slander's fire, or malice' flame.
For in thy sight, I find a truer judge,
Whose keenest eye doth pierce the specious show;
And though the world may whisper, snarl, and nudge,
Thy pure regard doth make my spirit glow.
Let them decry, and weave their tangled lies,
Their venom spent, their malice turned to dust;
For in the mirror of thy honest eyes,
I see my worth, and in thy love I trust.
So let them rage, and spew their bitter gall,
Thy faithful love shall be my shield for all.

###387###
The painted scenes that grace a theatre's stage,
With gilded frames and colors bright and bold,
Do tell a tale upon a fleeting page,
That by the morrow shall be bought and sold.
But thy true beauty, etched within my mind,
No artist's hand can truly replicate;
A living portrait, of a nobler kind,
Whose lasting grace doth hold me in its state.
Though pigments fade, and colours lose their gleam,
Thy inner worth shall ever shine anew;
A constant sun, a bright and hopeful beam,
Whose radiant light shall ever see me through.
So let the world admire what art can trace,
My heart shall hold the truth of thy dear face.

###388###
The winter's frost, that binds the earth in chains,
And stills the pulse of nature's vibrant song,
Doth mock the warmth that in my spirit reigns,
And seeks to prove my loving heart is wrong.
But like the seed that, buried deep below,
Doth wait for spring to break its icy tomb,
My passion waits, and shall in season grow,
To banish from my soul all winter's gloom.
Thy absence, like a barren, frozen land,
Doth chill my hopes, and make my spirit ache;
Yet in the thought of thy most gentle hand,
A thawing warmth doth make my courage wake.
So let the snows descend, and winds blow cold,
My love for thee shall never be controlled.

###389###
The busy bee, that toils from flower to flower,
And gathers nectar for its winter store,
Doth spend its strength throughout the summer hour,
And asks no more than nature doth implore.
So I do labour in the field of love,
And gather moments of thy sweet embrace;
A precious hoard, sent down from skies above,
To cheer my heart and light my lonely place.
But oh, the season turns, and days grow short,
And soon the frost shall claim the fading bloom;
And I shall mourn the days of sweet resort,
And sit alone within my silent room.
Yet if thy love, like sunshine, doth remain,
My heart shall bloom, and banish all my pain.

###390###
When I do muse upon the days gone by,
And all the joys that youth did freely lend,
I see the shadows lengthen in mine eye,
And know that all bright pleasures have an end.
The mirthful song, the dance with nimble feet,
The hopeful gaze towards the dawning year,
All pass away, and leave a solace sweet,
Of mem'ries held, and pleasures once held dear.
But in thy presence, all the past doth fade,
And present bliss doth make my spirit soar;
A newer world, by thy dear grace is made,
And I desire no other joy, nor more.
So let the past retreat, and time fly on,
With thee, my love, my brightest day is born.

###391###
The merchant sails upon the briny deep,
And ventures forth for fortune and for gain;
While I, like some poor shepherd, guard my sheep,
And find my wealth in love's enduring reign.
No earthly gold can match the treasure found
Within the chambers of thy loving heart;
No spice from Indies, nor from foreign ground,
Can with thy virtue and thy grace impart.
Let others chase the fleeting, worldly prize,
And stake their all upon a gambler's throw;
My richest bounty lies within thine eyes,
And in thy love, my truest riches grow.
So let them sail, and seek their distant shore,
My soul finds rest in thee, and asks no more.

###392###
When Fortune frowns, and clouds obscure the sky,
And all the world seems clad in somber grey,
My spirit droops, and fain would cease to try,
And yield itself to sorrow's bitter sway.
But then I think upon thy smiling face,
And all the warmth thy gentle spirit lends;
And in that thought, I find a saving grace,
A strength that rises, and my soul defends.
Though winds may howl, and tempests rage around,
Thy steadfast love shall be my sheltering tower;
Upon that rock, my faith is firmly bound,
And shall endure each dark and trying hour.
So let the storm descend, and skies be black,
Thy love, my sun, shall bring my spirit back.

###393###
The careless tongue, that speaks with thoughtless ease,
Doth wound the soul with words that cannot mend;
Like jagged stones, cast forth upon the seas,
Whose cruel impact doth no comfort send.
So have I erred, and spoken words unkind,
That pierced thy heart, and brought thee bitter pain;
And now I seek forgiveness I may find,
And wash away the sorrow and the stain.
My deepest wish, my soul's most fervent plea,
Is that thy pardon, like a balm, may flow;
And that thy grace shall once again find me,
And help my wounded spirit live and grow.
Forgive the fault, and let the past depart,
And keep me ever throned within thy heart.

###394###
The learned man, who pores o'er ancient lore,
And seeks the wisdom of the ages past,
May find much truth, and knowledge to explore,
But deeper truths are in thy presence cast.
For though the scrolls may hold a scholar's prize,
And dusty tomes may wisdom to them give,
The truest lessons lie within thine eyes,
And in thy presence, I do truly live.
Let them debate the meanings of the stars,
And seek for knowledge in the written word;
My understanding breaks down all their bars,
When thy dear voice is all that I have heard.
So let them read, and ponder, and inquire,
My soul finds truth in thee, my sole desire.

###395###
When weary nights do steal the precious day,
And slumber's balm doth banish weary thought,
My restless mind doth wander far away,
And in thy absence, battles must be fought.
The dreams that haunt me are of thee alone,
A phantom fair, that will not let me rest;
And though I seek a peace I have not known,
Thy image lingers, and doth fill my breast.
But when the dawn doth break the hold of night,
And morning's light doth chase the shades afar,
I wake to hope, and bathed in morning's light,
I long to see thee, my most guiding star.
So let me dream, and wake to thee anew,
My waking joy, my slumber's comfort too.

###396###
The shifting sands, that on the seashore lie,
Are borne away by every passing breeze;
And so it is with moments of my sigh,
That fade and vanish, lost among the trees.
But in my heart, a firmer place is kept,
A sanctuary where thy love doth reign;
Where all my hopes and fondest dreams are swept,
And banished are all sorrow and all pain.
Let other hearts be swayed by every gust,
And change their course with every turning tide;
My constant love, like solid, ancient dust,
Shall ever with thy noble spirit bide.
So though the world may change, and seasons fly,
My love for thee shall never fade nor die.

###397###
The summer's heat, that makes the spirit faint,
Doth test the strength of all that seeks to bloom;
And like a flower, weary of complaint,
My soul doth wither in this passing gloom.
But then I think upon thy cooling shade,
A gentle respite from the fiery sun;
And in thy love, my weary strength is made,
And all my trials seem to be undone.
So let the sun beat down with fiercest ray,
And parch the earth with unrelenting fire;
Thy presence, like a cool and welcome spray,
Doth quench my thirst, and lift my spirit higher.
For in thy love, a balm I always find,
That stills the heat, and soothes my troubled mind.

###398###
When I do see thee walk, with measured pace,
And hear the music of thy gentle voice,
A wondrous beauty doth my soul embrace,
And bids my captive heart to then rejoice.
The pearls that grace the ocean's deepest bed,
Or diamonds that the mountain's heart doth keep,
Can not compare to what is here instead,
The treasures that thy very being heap.
So let the world its glittering stones display,
And boast of riches that will fade and rust;
My richer prize is found within thy way,
And in thy love, my spirit puts its trust.
For though all earthly wealth may turn to dust,
Thy noble heart shall ever be my must.

###399###
The silent stars, that in the heavens gleam,
Do tell a tale of ages long since past;
A silent watch, a never-ending dream,
Whose distant light forevermore shall last.
So shall my love, though silent it may seem,
Endure beyond the turning of the sphere;
A constant flame, a never-fading beam,
That shines for thee, and holds thy presence dear.
Though spoken words may falter and decay,
And promises like morning mist depart,
My hidden love shall light thee on thy way,
And dwell forever in thy loving heart.
So let them fade, these fleeting, earthly things,
My love for thee, eternal solace brings.

###400###
The busy ant, that toils with ceaseless might,
Doth gather stores against the coming storm;
And plans ahead, with foresight clear and bright,
To keep its humble dwelling safe and warm.
So I do labour in the field of love,
And gather moments of thy sweet regard;
A precious hoard, sent down from skies above,
To be my shield, and keep my spirit hard.
Against the days when absence makes me weep,
And lonely nights do bring me bitter pain,
Thy memory shall my faithful promise keep,
And make my hopeful spirit live again.
So let the storms descend, and winds blow cold,
Thy love's true worth, more precious than all gold.

###401###
When I do gaze upon thy countenance fair,
And see the light that doth within it shine,
I feel a joy beyond all earthly care,
A blessed moment, truly felt as mine.
The purest gold, that from the mine is drawn,
Doth seem but dross compared to thy bright grace;
The rosy blush that greets the early dawn,
Is pale beside the beauty of thy face.
So let the world admire what it can see,
And praise the outward show, the painted art;
My soul doth find its truest ecstasy,
Within the chambers of thy loving heart.
For though the eye may marvel and may praise,
My love looks deeper, through all passing days.

###402###
The fleeting breath, that doth our life sustain,
Is but a moment in eternity;
And all our toil, our pleasure, and our pain,
Shall vanish hence, for all the world to see.
Yet in the realm of love, a truth I find,
That doth transcend the reach of mortal years;
A bond of souls, forever intertwined,
That conquers all our doubts, and all our fears.
So let the world pass by, with all its might,
And time consume the works that men have wrought;
Our love shall stand, a beacon shining bright,
A lasting flame, with endless beauty fraught.
For though our days on earth be but a span,
Our love shall live, beyond the life of man.

###402###
When winter's breath doth chill the verdant scene,
And nature sleeps beneath a snowy shroud,
My heart doth yearn for joys that once had been,
A fleeting dream, now lost within the cloud.
The sun, though pale, doth promise milder days,
And buried seeds await the vernal rain,
So shall my spirit rise from sorrow's maze,
And cast aside this melancholic pain.
For though the frost doth bind the earthly ground,
A hidden strength within doth lie concealed,
And when the warmth of spring shall eke be found,
New blossoms shall their fragrant hues revealed.
   Thus hope shall bloom, though seasons may depart,
   And mend the broken fragments of my heart.

###403###
Thy beauty shines, a star in darkest night,
Whose radiant gleam doth guide my wandering soul,
And banish shadows with its glorious light,
And make my wounded spirit once again whole.
Thy voice, a melody of sweetest sound,
Doth charm my ears and lift my heavy mood,
And in thy presence, solace can be found,
A gentle balm, most wondrous, pure, and good.
If thou art absent, then my world turns grey,
And all delight doth vanish from my view,
But when thou dost return, the gloom gives way,
And life itself doth seem to bloom anew.
   So let me gaze upon thy lovely face,
   And dwell forever in thy sweet embrace.

###404###
The fleeting hours, like sand through fingers glide,
And steal away the moments that we hold,
No matter how we strive, or how we hide,
Their hasty passage never can be told.
The bloom of youth, so fair and bright to see,
Doth fade and wither with the passing years,
And strength and vigor, once possessed by me,
Are claimed by time, and drowned in bitter tears.
Yet in thy love, a constancy I find,
A steadfast beacon in this shifting tide,
A bond that shall not be by time resigned,
Wherein my faithful heart may safe abide.
   So let us cherish what we have this day,
   Before it too shall vanish and decay.

###405###
When Fortune smiles and grants a golden hour,
The world doth flock with friends and flattery,
Each eager soul doth seek to gain thy power,
And whisper praises with a sycophant's glee.
But when misfortune casts its doleful shade,
And clouds of sorrow gather o'er thy head,
Then shall these fair-weather friends begin to fade,
And leave thee lonely, with no word of dread.
True amity is rarer than fine gold,
A precious gem that doth not lose its worth,
A story that shall never be grown old,
A guiding star upon this weary earth.
   So count thy friends, and number them with care,
   For few are true, and fewer still will share.

###406###
My love for thee, a flame that doth not cease,
Though trials may assail and tempests roar,
It burns with fervor, bringing sweet release,
And yearns to find its haven on thy shore.
The world may judge, and whisper words of doubt,
And seek to dim the brilliance of our flame,
But still my heart shall sing its joyful shout,
And call thy cherished and beloved name.
Let envious tongues their bitter venom spill,
And carping critics their dark censures lend,
My steadfast love shall never cease to thrill,
Nor shall its fervent passion ever end.
   For in thy breast, my truest home I see,
   And there I'll dwell, for all eternity.

###407###
The ink doth flow, and words begin to form,
To capture thee within this humble verse,
A fragile shelter from the passing storm,
A whispered truth, a blessing, or a curse.
Thy grace, thy wit, thy spirit, pure and bright,
Are treasures that my memory doth keep,
A constant source of wonder and delight,
While all the world doth slumber in its sleep.
If time should steal the beauty from thy brow,
And silver threads adorn thy raven hair,
My love shall be as steadfast, even now,
And banish sorrow, every worldly care.
   For in my heart, thy image shall remain,
   A timeless treasure, free from mortal stain.

###408###
The fickle moon doth wax and wane anew,
And tides do ebb and flow upon the sand,
So do my thoughts, both false and also true,
And shift and change, at fickle fate's command.
One moment I do vow eternal love,
The next, despair doth seize my troubled mind,
And doubt descends, sent from the heavens above,
Leaving my weary spirit far behind.
But then thy face, a vision clear and fair,
Doth break the clouds and banish all my fear,
And banishes the shadows of despair,
And makes thy cherished presence ever dear.
   So trust my love, though it may seem to stray,
   For thee it waits, at close of every day.

###409###
The painted scenes that grace the artist's hand,
May capture likeness, yet not life's true fire,
A lifeless form, across the barren land,
That cannot stir the soul with its desire.
So too, the lover's vows, if spoken light,
Without the depth of feeling, pure and deep,
Are but a fleeting shadow in the night,
That wakes to find itself where sorrows sleep.
But when the heart doth truly feel the sting,
Of absence, or of unrequited plea,
Then doth the spirit learn to truly sing,
And find its solace, in sincerity.
   So let thy love be real, and not a show,
   That from the heart's true fount doth freely flow.

###410###
The golden fields, that once with plenty gleamed,
Are now laid bare, beneath the autumn's blight,
And all the joys that in my youth I dreamed,
Have vanished now, and left me in the night.
The laughter rings, but not for me it sounds,
The revelers dance, but not for me they move,
My lonely spirit, on forbidden grounds,
Doth yearn for solace, and for gentle love.
Yet in thy smile, a flicker I can see,
A distant sun, that promises to shine,
A tender hope, that whispers just to me,
That joy may yet again again be mine.
   So let me cling to this, my dearest friend,
   And hope our shadowed days will have an end.

###411###
The fleeting scent of summer's sweet perfume,
Doth linger still, though winter now is here,
A tender echo, banishing the gloom,
And bringing memories that I hold dear.
The songs of birds, though silenced by the frost,
Still warble in the chambers of my mind,
A precious solace, never to be lost,
A treasure that no earthly care can bind.
So let me hold these visions in my breast,
When storms do rage and chilling winds do blow,
And find within them comfort and sweet rest,
And let my grateful spirit gently glow.
   For in these echoes, love and beauty lie,
   Beneath the coldness of a winter sky.

###412###
When absence doth my weary spirit seize,
And thou art far from where my heart doth dwell,
I conjure thee upon the gentle breeze,
And in my dreams, thy dear voice I can tell.
Thy image fair, I paint upon the air,
And speak thy name, with reverence and awe,
And banish all my sorrow and my care,
By nature's sweet, and unsubverted law.
For love, though bound by distance, can remain,
A steadfast flame that burns with ardent might,
And conquers all the emptiness and pain,
And fills the darkness with its glorious light.
   So though we part, our souls shall still be one,
   Until our joyful reunion has begun.

###413###
The jester's wit, though sharp and often keen,
Doth serve to mask a sorrow deep within,
And all the smiles that in his face are seen,
May hide the pangs of failure and of sin.
So too, my heart, though it doth play the part,
Of one content, with outward show of glee,
Doth bear a wound, a deep and silent smart,
That none but thou, my dearest, canst decree.
But in thy gaze, a balm I find, a cure,
A gentle healing for my wounded soul,
A love so potent, and so ever pure,
That makes my broken spirit once again whole.
   So let me trust in thee, and thee alone,
   My dearest love, upon thy sacred throne.

###414###
The fleeting shadow of a passing cloud,
Doth briefly dim the sun's resplendent ray,
But still the light, though hidden from the crowd,
Doth wait to shine upon a brighter day.
So too, my hopes, though buried deep in night,
And overwhelmed by sorrow's cruel decree,
Shall rise again, with renewed strength and might,
And burst forth into glorious liberty.
For in thy promise, solace I do find,
A whispered word, that banishes my fear,
A faithful anchor, for my troubled mind,
That makes thy presence ever doubly dear.
   So let me wait, and trust in thee, my love,
   Until our happy dawn arrives above.

###415###
The changing seasons, as they onward roll,
Do bring new beauty to the waiting earth,
And banish winter from the weary soul,
And give to life a fresh and joyful birth.
So shall my love, though tested by the years,
Remain as constant as the steady tide,
And banish all my doubts and all my fears,
And in thy steadfast heart shall e'er abide.
Let time's swift current bear away the past,
And change the outward semblance of our days,
Our bond of love shall ever, ever last,
And shine through all of life's bewildering maze.
   For thou art mine, and I am thine, my dear,
   And naught can part us, banishing all fear.

###416###
The rose that blooms, with beauty and with grace,
Doth bear a thorn, that pricks the careless hand,
So beauty's touch, in this terrestrial place,
Doth often bring a hurt we understand.
Thy outward form, so pleasing to the eye,
May hide a temper, or a fickle mind,
A subtle venom, that doth pass us by,
And leave our trusting hearts in grief confined.
But in thy soul, a gentleness I find,
A spirit pure, untouched by earthly stain,
A love so true, that leaves all doubt behind,
And heals the wounds of sorrow and of pain.
   So let me love thy substance, not thy show,
   And in thy heart, my truest solace know.

###417###
When fickle Fortune turns her wheel around,
And casts me down from heights I once did gain,
And all my hopes lie buried in the ground,
And naught but sorrow doth my spirit reign,
Then shall I seek thy comfort and thy grace,
Thy steadfast love, a beacon in the storm,
And find within thy kind and gentle face,
A shelter from misfortune's chilling form.
For though the world may prove a faithless friend,
And leave me stranded on life's barren shore,
Thy faithful heart, on which I can depend,
Shall be my solace, now and evermore.
   So let me cling to thee, and thee alone,
   My dearest love, my solace and my throne.

###418###
The summer's heat, though fierce it may appear,
Doth yield at last to autumn's gentle cool,
And all the joys that held our spirits dear,
Do fade and vanish, like a passing fool.
So too, the passion that did burn so bright,
May cool and dim, with seasons passing by,
And leave behind a shadow of its light,
Beneath a pale and ever-watching sky.
But in our hearts, a deeper love doth lie,
A steadfast flame, that time cannot consume,
A bond of souls, that shall not ever die,
And banish all the melancholy gloom.
   So let our love, though changed, endure and grow,
   A timeless flame, that we shall ever know.

###419###
The fleeting dream, that vanishes with dawn,
And leaves behind a sense of vacant space,
So do my thoughts, when thou art lost and gone,
And leave my spirit in a lonely place.
I search for thee, in every passing face,
And listen for thy voice, in every sound,
And long to find again thy dear embrace,
On this too-empty and unhallowed ground.
But when thou dost return, the world is bright,
And all the shadows of my soul take flight,
And all is bathed in beauty and in light,
And life itself seems wonderfully right.
   So let me hold thee close, and ne'er depart,
   Thou art the beating of my very heart.

###420###
The stars above, though distant and so cold,
Do guide the sailor on the trackless sea,
A constant light, a story to be told,
Of hope and promise, for eternity.
So is thy love, a star within my soul,
That guides me through the darkness and the strife,
And makes my wounded spirit once again whole,
And fills with meaning all the breadth of life.
Let others seek their fortunes, high and low,
And chase the phantom of a fleeting gain,
My dearest love, it is enough to know,
Thy faithful heart shall ease my every pain.
   So let me gaze upon thee, and be blest,
   My guiding star, my haven and my rest.

###421###
The painted mask, that hides a mournful guise,
May fool the eye, but not the discerning soul,
And all the mirth that in a smile arises,
May not conceal a spirit far from whole.
So too, the vows that lovers often speak,
May hold no truth, no substance, and no might,
And leave the trusting heart to weep and shriek,
When shadows gather, and conceal the light.
But in thy gaze, a truth I clearly see,
A love that burns with an unswerving fire,
A steadfast faith, that sets my spirit free,
And satisfies my deepest soul's desire.
   So let us pledge our hearts, both pure and true,
   And find our heaven, in the love of you.

###422###
The fragile bloom, that courts the morning dew,
Doth ope its petals to the warming sun,
And drinks the light, in hues both fresh and new,
Before its brief and lovely race is run.
So too, my love, though delicate and fair,
Doth bloom within the garden of my breast,
And draws its life from thy most tender care,
And finds in thee its solace and its rest.
Let envy's frost attempt to blight its gleam,
Or absence dim the brightness of its hue,
Our love shall be a strong and constant dream,
Forever faithful, and forever true.
   So let us tend this blossom, day by day,
   And watch its beauty never fade away.

###462###
Whenas the sun doth hide his golden face,
And weary day doth yield to darkest night,
My troubled soul finds solace in this place,
Where shadows dance and banish all my light.
The moon, a pearl upon a velvet sea,
Doth cast a beam, a pale and fragile gleam,
And whispers secrets meant for only me,
A fleeting comfort in a waking dream.
But dawn shall break, and with it shall return,
The weary world, with all its toil and strife,
And in my heart, a lonely fire shall burn,
For solitude, the balm of all my life.
So let me dwell in this my silent hour,
Ere day's harsh light doth steal its gentle power.

###463###
The bloom of youth, that fair and blushing rose,
Doth fade and wither ere the summer's end,
And all the beauty that the season shows,
To winter's icy touch, must needs descend.
So too my love, a flower bright and bold,
Hath felt the frost of time's relentless hand,
And stories that were once so bravely told,
Now lie like dust upon a barren land.
Yet in my breast, a spark doth still remain,
A hidden ember of a former fire,
That though it cannot banish all the pain,
Doth whisper still of a lost, sweet desire.
Alas, that beauty, transient as a sigh,
Must bid farewell to all beneath the sky.

###464###
My muse, once swift, now lags with heavy tread,
Her once-bright quill doth falter and grow cold,
The vibrant hues that filled my youthful head,
Now muted shades, a story to be told.
The ink that flowed with passion, strong and deep,
Now stains the page with a reluctant tear,
As slumbering thoughts within my spirit sleep,
And banish all that once I held so dear.
Yet still I strive, though labour be my lot,
To wake the echoes of a vanished song,
To find the words that I have long forgot,
And prove my weary spirit is not wrong.
For in the depths of silence, truth may lie,
And beauty waiteth for a poet's eye.

###465###
When cruel Fortune doth her favour turn,
And smiles of joy are lost in clouds of woe,
My soul doth feel a bitter lesson learn,
And bitter seeds of discontent do grow.
The sun that warmed my days with golden ray,
Now casts a shadow, chilling to the bone,
And all the laughter of a brighter day,
Is silenced by a solitary groan.
Yet in this darkness, where all hope seems fled,
A flicker bright, a steadfast star I see,
The love that lives, though by the world unsaid,
A constant beacon, shining back to me.
So let me brave the tempest and the gale,
For love's true strength shall never, ever fail.

###466###
The fleeting moment, like a whispered breath,
Doth vanish ere we scarce have felt its grace,
And life, a journey leading unto death,
Doth onward press with unrelenting pace.
The blossoms bloom, and then they swiftly fall,
The summer's heat gives way to winter's chill,
And human hearts, responding to the call,
Must learn to bow to nature's steadfast will.
Yet in this change, a constancy I find,
A deeper truth that time cannot erase,
The lasting love that binds my heart and mind,
And holds within its sweet and warm embrace.
So let us cherish every passing hour,
And find our strength within love's gentle power.

###467###
When envious tongues do whisper calumny,
And slanders fly with venom in their sting,
My weary spirit seeks felicity,
Where truth and justice their fair tribute bring.
The fair report that malice seeks to stain,
Doth rise anew, though tempests rage and roar,
And innocence, though battered by the rain,
Shall stand unblemished, stronger than before.
Let not the wicked triumph in their lies,
Nor let the slanderer his foul work pursue,
For righteous judgment from the heavens flies,
And sets the honest heart forever true.
So I shall trust in fate's impartial hand,
And know my innocence shall understand.

###468###
The beauty of a maiden's blushing cheek,
Doth hold a power that no man can withstand,
Her gentle smile, her voice, so soft and meek,
Doth hold my captive heart within her hand.
Her eyes, like stars that sparkle in the night,
Do shed a radiance, pure and undefiled,
And fill my soul with wonder and delight,
As though by Cupid's sweetest arrow styled.
But beauty fades, as flowers do in frost,
And youth's bright bloom doth wither and decay,
And all the charms that I have held so cost,
May vanish in the passing of a day.
Yet still I love, though time its course doth run,
My dearest lady, fairest of the sun.

###469###
The world, a stage where we do play our part,
Doth hold us captive in its busy scene,
And busy hands do labour with their art,
To build up fortunes, or to live serene.
But what is all the toil, the gain, the strife,
If in our hearts, no true contentment lies?
We chase the shadows, and we mock at life,
And gaze with longing at the distant skies.
Let us not chase the baubles of the great,
Nor envy those who seem to climb so high,
But seek instead a more enduring state,
Where peace and love shall never, ever die.
For true content, a treasure rich and rare,
Doth bloom within, beyond all worldly care.

###470###
When absence doth my dearest love remove,
And miles between us stretch in mournful length,
My lonely spirit, robbed of all its love,
Doth pine and wither, lacking all its strength.
The sun seems dull, the stars do shed no gleam,
And every sound doth grate upon my ear,
Lost in the echoes of a waking dream,
Where she, my soul's delight, is no more near.
But hope, a flicker in the darkest hour,
Doth whisper solace to my aching breast,
That soon again, with love's renewing power,
She shall return, and bring my heart its rest.
So I shall wait, though sorrow fills my day,
Until she comes, and drives all grief away.

###471###
The winter's chill hath bound the barren earth,
And nature sleeps beneath a snowy shroud,
No sign of life, no hint of joyful mirth,
But silent stillness, speaking not aloud.
The trees stand bare, their branches stark and gaunt,
The fields lie frozen, hard and cold and deep,
And all the world, in mournful, weary chant,
Doth seem in slumber, buried in its sleep.
Yet deep within, a promise doth reside,
Of spring's return, when warmth shall stir the air,
And life's sweet essence, long cast to the side,
Shall rise again, beyond all earthly care.
So let us trust, though darkness may prevail,
That spring shall come, and banish winter's wail.

###472###
The weight of years, a burden hard to bear,
Doth press upon my soul with heavy hand,
And silver threads do mingle with my hair,
As time doth march across this mortal land.
The vigor of my youth hath long since fled,
My strength doth wane, my sight begins to dim,
And all the joys that once my spirit fed,
Now seem like phantoms, distant, faint, and grim.
But in my heart, a flicker still doth glow,
A memory of days when I was bold,
And though the swift-winged years do onward flow,
My spirit clings to stories yet untold.
So let me face the ending with good grace,
And find in age, a solace and a place.

###473###
When flattery doth fill a lover's ear,
And honeyed words do weave a subtle snare,
The honest heart should hold that poison dear,
And flee from vows that are beyond compare.
For those who speak with tongues of silver bright,
And promise realms of everlasting bliss,
Do often hide a darkness from the light,
And seek to take advantage of a kiss.
Let truth and trust be anchors to the soul,
And let sincerity guide every deed,
For hollow praise can never make us whole,
But plant within our hearts a bitter seed.
So judge not by the sweetness of the sound,
But by the love that in the action's found.

###474###
The silent night, when stars begin to gleam,
And all the world doth sink in slumber deep,
Doth whisper softly of a waking dream,
Where hidden thoughts their secret vigil keep.
My restless mind doth wander to and fro,
And conjures visions of a time gone by,
Where joys and sorrows ebb and softly flow,
Beneath the gaze of heaven's watchful eye.
The silent moon, a sentinel on high,
Doth cast a beam upon my lonely face,
And in its light, I find a reason why,
My heart still beats with love's enduring grace.
So let me muse, until the morning light,
And find my solace in the silent night.

###475###
The storm doth rage, the winds do fiercely blow,
And dark clouds gather, hiding sun from view,
The sea doth toss with fierce and angry flow,
And threatens all that earthly man holds true.
My heart doth quail, my spirit feels the sting,
Of tempests that do lash with mighty force,
And fear doth rise, on swift and raven wing,
And pulls my soul from its accustomed course.
Yet when the tempest shall at last subside,
And calm returns, with skies of azure hue,
My strength shall rise, and with a hopeful stride,
I shall embrace the world, both fresh and new.
For after rain, the sun doth ever shine,
And peace shall come, a gift to thee and mine.

###476###
The passing days, like rivers to the sea,
Doth bear us onward to an unknown shore,
And time, the thief, doth steal relentlessly,
The moments that we shall possess no more.
The bloom of youth, the vigour of the prime,
Doth fade and vanish, leaving naught behind,
But withered leaves, a testament to time,
And memories that linger in the mind.
Yet in this fleetingness, a truth I find,
That love endures, beyond the touch of years,
A bond that time itself cannot unbind,
And dries the fount of all our mortal tears.
So let us hold this precious treasure fast,
For love's true light forever shall outlast.

###477###
When folly doth with youthful spirit play,
And heedless hearts do leap before they look,
The path of wisdom seems a weary way,
And pleasure's siren call doth them ensnook.
The rash pursuit of fleeting, vain desire,
Doth lead to ruin, with its bitter end,
And quenched the flames of reason's steady fire,
That caution doth to foolish souls extend.
Let sober thought preside, and judgment guide,
The actions of the young and eager mind,
Lest they with naught but sharp regret abide,
And sorrow's tangled web themselves do find.
For haste doth breed a harvest of despair,
And leaves but ashes, when the joy was there.

###478###
The gentle breeze that stirs the summer leaves,
Doth whisper secrets of a love so true,
And in its sigh, my longing spirit grieves,
For one whose absence makes my world feel blue.
Her voice, a melody, so sweet and clear,
Doth echo still within my memory's halls,
And banishes all doubt, and conquers fear,
As tender love my captive spirit calls.
Though leagues may part, and absence doth still sting,
My heart beats only for her, it is known,
And to her name, my deepest vows I sing,
A love that time and distance can't disown.
So let me dream, until our paths entwine,
And once again, her loving hand in mine.

###479###
The fickle crowd, with ever-changing mind,
Doth praise today what it will scorn tomorrow,
And honours given, they do seldom find,
When fortune turns, and brings them naught but sorrow.
The fickle favour, like a summer's cloud,
Doth drift and vanish, leaving skies of grey,
And voices that were once so bright and loud,
Do turn to whispers, or do fade away.
Let not the judgment of the common throng,
Doth sway the purpose of a noble soul,
But let integrity, both deep and strong,
Be guide and compass, to achieve the goal.
For true renown, a virtue earned with care,
Doth stand unshaken, banishing all despair.

###480###
When shadows lengthen, and the day grows old,
And weary limbs begin to feel the strain,
The stories of my youth, so bravely told,
Return to me, a solace from the pain.
The triumphs past, the battles bravely won,
The friendships forged, the love that did inspire,
All these return, beneath the setting sun,
And fill my soul with a renewed desire.
For though the body may begin to fade,
The spirit's strength can never be undone,
And in the memories that time hath made,
A lasting legacy hath been begun.
So let me live, though twilight doth descend,
And find my peace, until the very end.

###481###
The lark ascends on wings of morning light,
And sings a carol to the dawning day,
Dispelling shadows of the fading night,
And chasing all the weary dark away.
So too my love, a beacon bright and bold,
Doth rise within my heart, a joyful sound,
A story that can never be too old,
On consecrated, consecrated ground.
Her smile, a sunbeam on a frosty morn,
Her laughter, music to my listening ear,
She is the joy for which my soul was born,
And drives away all doubt, and conquers fear.
So let me praise her, with a heart aflame,
And ever whisper her beloved name.

###482###
When outward show doth mask a hollow core,
And gilded words conceal a heart of stone,
True worth resides within, and asks no more,
Than honesty, on which true love is grown.
Let not the gaudy dress, the painted face,
Doth lure the eye with false and fleeting art,
But seek the soul, the spirit's gentle grace,
The humble virtue of a loving heart.
For beauty fades, and fortunes turn to dust,
But goodness shines, a star that lights the way,
And in the pure affections we can trust,
Doth lie the solace of a brighter day.
So let us judge, not by the outward gleam,
But by the truth that lives within a dream.

###482###
When first mine eyes did gaze upon thy face,
A sudden warmth did steal into my soul,
And banished hence all doubt and lonely space,
As if a greater destiny made whole.
Thy laughter, like a bird on summer's wing,
Did charm my ear and set my spirit free,
And in thy voice, a joyful song did sing,
That whispered tales of sweet felicity.
No earthly treasure can with thee compare,
Nor all the gems that ocean's depths do hide,
For thou art fairer than the morning air,
And in thy grace, my truest joys reside.
    So let me live, my love, for thee alone,
    And make thy heart my everlasting throne.

###483###
The fleeting hours, like shadows, onward creep,
And steal away the bloom from beauty's cheek,
While mortal cares do banish joyful sleep,
And make the stoutest, weariest spirit meek.
But in thy gaze, a timeless truth I find,
A constant star that guides my wandering way,
A gentle balm to ease my troubled mind,
And chase the gloom of melancholic day.
Though winter winds may strip the branches bare,
And frost may bite with sharp and chilling sting,
Thy love, a summer sun, doth still repair
The wounded heart that doth to thee still cling.
    So let us cherish what the gods have sent,
    And in our love, find sweet contentment.

###484###
My heart, a vessel tossed on stormy seas,
Did founder 'neath the weight of worldly strife,
And sought in vain a shore of gentle ease,
To find repose and solace for my life.
But then didst thou, a beacon in the night,
Appear to guide my vessel to the land,
And fill my darkened soul with glorious light,
And offer me thy soft and loving hand.
Thy smile, a sunbeam on a frosty morn,
Doth melt the ice that held my spirit bound,
And in thy presence, I am newly born,
On consecrated and on joyful ground.
    So let me pledge my troth and faith to thee,
    And in thy love, forever happy be.

###485###
The world doth boast of riches, grand and rare,
Of gilded halls and jewels beyond all price,
But these are naught, when weighed against the share
Of love that mak'st my weary heart suffice.
For what is gold, or silver, or the gleam
Of diamonds bright, or pearls from distant shore,
Compared to one sweet look, a whispered dream,
That bids my soul forever to adore?
Thy beauty is a garden, rich and deep,
Where flowers of virtue bloom in sweet array,
And in its soil, my loyal love I keep,
And nurture it with each returning day.
    So let me be thy servant, true and bold,
    And in thy gaze, my truest wealth unfold.

###486###
When absence doth my weary spirit seize,
And thou art far from my adoring sight,
My soul doth pine, and finds no gentle ease,
But wanders lost within the darkest night.
Each passing hour doth seem an age to stray,
And every dawn, a pale and mournful hue,
Until thy presence doth my fears allay,
And make the world seem wondrous, fresh, and new.
The memory of thy voice, a sweet refrain,
Doth echo in the chambers of my mind,
And chases hence the lingering, bitter pain,
And leaves but hopeful ecstasies behind.
    So let us meet, and banish every fear,
    And hold each other ever, ever near.

###487###
The fickle tongue of rumour, sharp and keen,
Doth strive to wound thy fair and noble name,
And paint thee black, where all is white and clean,
And cast on thee a shadow, and a blame.
But I, who know thy heart, so pure and true,
Do scorn the venom that these tongues do spill,
And see the sun that shines in all thou doest,
And love thee more, and serve thee with my will.
Let envious souls their poisoned arrows dart,
They cannot pierce the shield of my belief,
For thou art etched within my inmost heart,
And shall remain, beyond all worldly grief.
    So let them rage, and let their curses fly,
    My love for thee shall never, never die.

###488###
This fragile life, a candle in the breeze,
Doth flicker low, and soon will cease to burn,
And all our joys and sorrows, if you please,
To silent dust, the earth shall then return.
But in thy love, a lasting grace I find,
A flame that time itself cannot subdue,
A bond that shall eternally be twined,
And keep our spirits ever fresh and new.
Though flesh may wither, and though youth may fade,
And silver hairs the brow of age shall crown,
The vows of love, once truly, deeply made,
Shall never from our steadfast hearts be thrown.
    So let us build our lasting edifice,
    Upon the rock of love's true happiness.

###489###
The world's a stage, where all men play their part,
And fortune's smiles and frowns do ebb and flow,
But in thy love, I've found a work of art,
That makes my barren spirit brightly glow.
Thou art the muse that doth my verses guide,
The inspiration that my quill doth chase,
And in thy beauty, all my hopes abide,
And find their solace in thy gentle grace.
No tyrant's decree, nor envious decree,
Can alter what my heart doth truly feel,
My soul is bound, my dearest love, to thee,
And all my future joys, to thee reveal.
    So let me write, with passion's ardent fire,
    Of thee, my goddess, and my heart's desire.

###490###
When doubts like shadows gather in my mind,
And whisper fears of loss and swift decay,
Thy constant truth, so steadfast and so kind,
Doth chase the lingering darkness far away.
For in thy faith, a fortress I possess,
Against the slings and arrows of the world,
And in thy love, a sweet and sure redress,
Where all my anxious banners are unfurled.
No storm can shake the roots of this firm bond,
No earthly tempest shall our union mar,
For we are joined, and shall be ever fond,
Beneath the watchful eye of evening star.
    So let us stand, united, strong, and bold,
    A story of true love, forever told.

###491###
The painted hues of nature, rich and deep,
The emerald fields, the skies of azure hue,
The mountains high, where ancient secrets sleep,
All pale and dim, when measured next to you.
Thy laughter is the music of the spheres,
Thy voice, a melody both sweet and clear,
Thy eyes, like stars, that banish all my fears,
And draw my longing, captive spirit near.
What need have I of outward, worldly show,
When such a treasure I within my sight
Do hold and cherish, and forever know,
To be my joy, my solace, and my light?
    So let me dwell, within this blessed space,
    And lose myself within thy sweet embrace.

###492###
My foolish heart, that once did wildly roam,
And sought for bliss in pleasures false and vain,
Hath found at last its true and happy home,
And cast aside all former, useless pain.
For in thy presence, peace I do attain,
A quiet joy that cannot be destroyed,
And from thy love, I drink, and drink again,
And find my spirit utterly employed.
The passing years, with all their varied chance,
Shall find me constant, and forever true,
And in thy fond and loving, gentle glance,
My endless happiness shall bloom anew.
    So let me live, and serve thee till I die,
    Beneath the favour of thy loving eye.

###493###
This outward form, that time doth seek to mar,
And wrinkle deep, and steal its youthful bloom,
Is but a shell, beneath a brighter star,
That shines within, and conquers every gloom.
For though thy hair may turn to silver thread,
And feeble age may dim thy vision's light,
The spirit's grace, on which my love is fed,
Shall shine with ever-increasing might.
Thy wisdom, like a well that never dries,
Doth quench the thirst of my inquiring soul,
And in thy gentle, understanding eyes,
I find the peace that makes my spirit whole.
    So let us grow, in virtue, day by day,
    And let true love forever lead the way.

###494###
The flatterer's tongue, with honeyed words so sweet,
Doth oft deceive the unsuspecting ear,
And promises of joy, however fleet,
Do vanish swift, and leave behind but fear.
But thou, my love, art honest, plain, and true,
Thy words are balm, and thy affections deep,
And in the vows and promises of you,
My steadfast trust I can forever keep.
No painted smile, no false and hollow grace,
Can tempt me from the path where thou dost tread,
For in thy heart, I find my resting place,
And on thy truth, my very soul is fed.
    So let us walk, with purpose, hand in hand,
    And build our love upon this solid land.

###495###
When weary of the world's discordant sound,
And all the noise that doth my senses fray,
I seek a refuge, where true peace is found,
And where my troubled spirit can hold sway.
And that is found, my dearest, in thine arms,
A sanctuary from all worldly care,
Protected from the world's insidious harms,
And breathing in a sweet and loving air.
Thy gentle touch, a balm to soothe my soul,
Thy tender kiss, a pledge of faith so pure,
Doth make my broken spirit once more whole,
And promise joys that ever shall endure.
    So let us dwell, within this tender space,
    And find in love our everlasting grace.

###496###
The rose doth bloom, and then it fades away,
The summer's sun, that warms the verdant field,
Doth yield at last to winter's chill array,
And all its vibrant beauty is concealed.
But love like ours, though outward forms may cease,
And beauty's bloom be destined to decay,
Doth find within itself a lasting peace,
And shall not wither, nor be swept away.
For in the heart, where true affection lies,
A fire burns, that time cannot extinguish,
And it shall shine, beneath all mortal skies,
A constant flame, that naught can ever vanquish.
    So let our love, like stars, forever gleam,
    And be the subject of our waking dream.

###497###
When age doth creep with slow and silent tread,
And steal the vigour from my youthful frame,
And all my former strength be rendered dead,
And memory doth whisper forth my name,
Still shall thy love, a constant, burning light,
Illumine all my days with radiant glow,
And banish hence the shadows of the night,
And make my fading spirit truly grow.
For in the depth of thy devoted heart,
A spring of joy doth ever brightly flow,
And plays a never-ending, healing part,
In easing all the pains that mortals know.
    So let us find, in age, a deeper grace,
    And see the love that shines upon thy face.

###498###
The envious eye doth see with warped design,
And twists the truth to suit its bitter aim,
And deems my love, a thing of base incline,
And seeks to tarnish thy most honoured name.
But they who judge with hearts devoid of light,
And understand not love's true, potent spell,
Can never pierce the veil of day and night,
Nor know the secrets that our spirits tell.
My love for thee, a fortress strong and high,
Defies all slander, and all spoken scorn,
And in its strength, I find my reason why,
And greet each new and hopeful, blessed morn.
    So let them speak, and let their whispers fly,
    Our steadfast love shall conquer and defy.

###499###
This earthly house, this fragile, mortal shell,
That bears my soul through seasons, fair and foul,
Shall one day break, and bid its guest farewell,
And join the dust, beneath the silent cowl.
But in thy love, a greater home I've made,
A lasting dwelling, built on truth and trust,
Wherein my spirit shall not be afraid,
But find its peace, beyond the turning dust.
Thy heart, a haven, safe from every storm,
Thy constant faith, a shelter from the cold,
Doth keep my loving spirit ever warm,
And richer than all earthly, treasured gold.
    So let us live, in love's enduring light,
    And banish hence all shadows of the night.

###500###
The fickle winds of fortune, swift and keen,
Do blow and change, and leave us in despair,
And joy that seemed so bright and so serene,
Doth vanish fast, and leave our spirits bare.
But in thy love, a constancy I find,
A steadfast shore, where my poor barque can rest,
A gentle balm to soothe my troubled mind,
And make me feel divinely, truly blessed.
No worldly loss, nor sorrow's bitter sting,
Can dim the light that in thy presence shines,
For thou dost make my weary spirit sing,
And bind my heart with everlasting lines.
    So let us hold, this treasure we possess,
    And find in love our endless happiness.

###501###
When shadows lengthen, and the day grows old,
And weary nature seeks its sweet repose,
My thoughts return, as stories to be told,
To thee, the one who maketh my heart glow.
Thy image, fair, doth grace my waking thought,
And in my dreams, thy beauty doth appear,
A gentle vision, by the Muses wrought,
To banish doubt, and conquer every fear.
The stars above, though bright and far they seem,
Reflect the lustre of thine eyes so true,
And in their light, I find my waking dream,
And know my love shall ever be with you.
    So let me gaze, until the morn doth break,
    And for thy love, my very soul I'll stake.

###502###
The world doth laud the brave, the strong, the bold,
Who conquer realms, and gain a victor's crown,
But in thy love, a greater worth I hold,
Than all the honours of a kingly town.
For in thy gaze, a gentleness I find,
A quiet strength that doth my spirit heal,
And in thy heart, so tender and so kind,
The truest solace that my soul can feel.
Let others strive for glory, power, fame,
And chase the phantom of a fleeting day,
My sole ambition is to speak thy name,
And in thy love, forever find my way.
    So let me be, thy servant, loyal, true,
    And dedicate my humble life to you.
    
###502###
When gentle zephyrs whisper through the trees,
And Phoebus gilds the world with golden light,
My heart doth pine for joys that cannot ease,
And wander lost within the darkest night.
For thou, my love, art distant from my gaze,
A star that shines beyond my earthly sphere,
And all my days are spent in mournful haze,
Replete with sighs and unavailing tear.
Oh, would that fortune might my suit attend,
And bring thee back unto my longing sight,
My faithful love, my life, my dearest friend,
And banish hence this everlasting blight.
Then shall my soul with sweetest music sing,
And all my sorrows take their rapid wing.

###503###
The painted bloom that doth the summer grace,
And scents the air with perfume passing sweet,
Shall wither soon and lose its lovely face,
As winter’s chill doth make its conquest meet.
So too, alas, doth beauty fade away,
The flush of youth, the eye of sparkling fire,
Consumed by time, that doth all things betray,
And leave behind a heap of spent desire.
Yet, if thy virtue doth thy form transcend,
And grace of spirit doth thy soul adorn,
Then shall thy worth for ever have no end,
Nor be by cruelest passing years outworn.
For outward show is but a fleeting dream,
Whilst inner worth doth ever brightly gleam.

###504###
My pen doth falter, and my ink doth dry,
When I do strive thy praises to impart,
For such a beauty doth enchant mine eye,
It doth o'erwhelm the craftsman of my art.
No earthly hue can match thy cheek so fair,
No silken thread thy tresses can outshine,
And in thy voice, a melody beyond compare,
Doth make the very heavens feel divine.
Yet, lest this praise should puff thee up with pride,
And make thee deem thyself beyond all fault,
Remember, love, that frailties do abide,
And mortal coil doth make the stoutest halt.
So temper now thy pride with humble grace,
And let true worth shine forth from thy dear face.

###505###
When I behold thy countenance so mild,
A gentler dawn doth break upon my soul,
And all the cares that made me feel exiled,
Do vanish quite, and lose their harsh control.
Thy voice, a balm to soothe my troubled breast,
Thy smile, a sun that banishes the shade,
Doth bring my weary spirit perfect rest,
And makes me feel as though I were new made.
Let others chase the phantoms of renown,
Or hoard their gold with avaricious hand,
My greatest treasure I in thee have found,
The fairest jewel in this earthly land.
So let us live, united, ever so,
And from our love eternal rivers flow.

###506###
The fleeting hours, like swift-winged messengers,
Do steal away the substance of our prime,
And leave behind but withered, aged sufferers,
To mourn the loss of youth and early time.
The strongest oak, that doth the tempests brave,
At length succumbs to age’s slow decay,
And even kings, who hold a sovereign wave,
Must yield their crowns to death’s impartial sway.
So let us seize the moments as they fly,
And drink the nectar of this present day,
For what is gone, we never can descry,
And what’s to come, doth often go astray.
Let love’s bright flame, therefore, our spirits fill,
And burn with ardour, constant and still.

###507###
When Fortune smiles, and all the world doth seem
A garden rich with blossoms newly sprung,
We deem our joy a never-ending dream,
And on the lute of happiness are sung.
But ah, how quickly doth the tempest blow,
And scatter all our pleasant hopes like dust,
The sun retreats, and chilling shadows grow,
And all our fondest dreams dissolve to rust.
So learn, my friend, to temper thy delight,
And build not castles on so frail a shore,
For what seems firm may vanish in the night,
And leave thee weeping, wanting evermore.
Let wisdom guide thy steps, and judgment true,
And thus shall Fortune never quite undo.

###508###
The moon, that doth the starry vault adorn,
And casts a silver gleam on slumbering lands,
Doth wax and wane, from darkness newly born,
And follow still the heaven’s stern commands.
So too, my love, thy favour I do seek,
And find it sometimes bright, and sometimes dim,
And though my heart doth ardently bespeak,
Thy moods do oft me o'er the ocean swim.
Yet, when thy sun doth shine with kindly ray,
My world is filled with beauty and with grace,
And all my doubts and fears do melt away,
And leave no trace within this happy place.
So grant me, love, a steady, constant beam,
And banish hence this intermittent dream.

###509###
When winter’s frost doth bite the barren ground,
And naked branches shiver in the breeze,
No cheerful song of feathered joy is found,
But silence reigns amongst the leafless trees.
So when my heart is chilled by thy disdain,
And all my hopes are buried in the snow,
My spirit droops beneath this icy rain,
And cannot find a warmth wherein to grow.
Yet, wouldst thou thaw this winter of my soul,
And grant me but a glance of tender care,
My frozen veins would feel a quick control,
And life’s sweet current would again repair.
Then would I bloom, like spring’s returning flower,
And bless thee in that life-restoring hour.

###510###
The fleeting shadow that the swift cloud makes,
Doth dance upon the meadow green and wide,
And ere it’s seen, its transient form it shakes,
And in the sun’s bright beams it doth abide.
So is it with the joys of mortal kind,
A moment’s pleasure, then it disappears,
And leaves the soul with memories to find,
And fills the heart with unavailing tears.
For nothing here on earth can long endure,
The fairest face, the richest, proudest king,
All must at last their final doom secure,
And to the dust their earthly substance bring.
So let us love, whilst love doth yet remain,
And ease thereby our transient mortal pain.

###511###
My love for thee, a flame that doth not cease,
Nor quivers when the roughest tempests blow,
Doth burn within, and grant my soul release,
From all the worldly cares that vex me so.
The stars above may alter in their course,
The solid earth may crumble and decay,
But still my heart shall hold its steadfast force,
And love thee truly, till my dying day.
Let envious tongues their venomous darts unleash,
And speak of scorn where only truth doth lie,
My constant faith no falsehood can impeach,
Nor dim the lustre of thine ever eye.
So rest assured, my dearest, in my troth,
Thou hast my heart, and all I have is thine, both.

###512###
The eye that gazes on the distant hill,
Doth see the shape, but not the substance there,
And though the outward form may please it still,
The inner truth it cannot well declare.
So is it oft with lovers’ ardent vows,
They speak of passion, fervent and profound,
But when misfortune on their spirit bows,
Their promises on barren ground are found.
Yet mine, dear love, is built on firmer stone,
A love that shall not falter or grow weak,
A steady fire, eternally my own,
And from this truth, my constant spirit speak.
Let time and trial prove the worth of me,
And find my love eternally decree.

###513###
When I do think upon the time to be,
And picture us in years yet to unfold,
My heart doth leap with fondest ecstasy,
A tale of love that never can grow old.
For though our brows with silver shall be crowned,
And steps grow slow, and senses waxen dim,
The same affection shall be ever found,
And fill our hearts unto the very brim.
Thy gentle hand shall guide my failing sight,
Thy voice shall be the music of my ear,
And in thy presence, shall my soul find light,
Dispelling all that once did cause me fear.
So let us age, with love our constant guide,
And in each other’s arms, serenely bide.

###514###
The bird that sings at dawn’s first breaking light,
Doth greet the sun with melody so clear,
And banishes the remnants of the night,
And fills the waking world with joyful cheer.
So didst thou come, and chase away my gloom,
And with thy presence make my spirit soar,
Dispelling shadows from my lonely room,
And opening wide love’s ever-bolted door.
No richer music can my ear embrace,
Than thy sweet words, that fall like summer rain,
And in thy smile, I find my truest grace,
And from my heart, all sorrow doth abstain.
So let us join, in love’s eternal art,
And make of our two souls a single heart.

###515###
When outward show doth captivate the eye,
And gilded pomp doth dazzle and allure,
The shallow mind doth often fall thereby,
And deems that fleeting beauty shall endure.
But substance true lies hidden from the gaze,
A gem unseen, that gleams with inner light,
And though it shun the sun’s more common rays,
Its worth is constant, shining ever bright.
So let us seek that virtue, pure and deep,
That time nor fortune can consume or fade,
A treasure that the soul shall safely keep,
And by its radiance, our lives be swayed.
For outward gloss is but a passing show,
Whilst inner worth shall ever brightly glow.

###516###
The ship that braves the ocean’s angry roar,
And battles with the tempest’s furious blast,
Doth seek at length a safe and welcome shore,
And finds its harbour, till the storm be past.
So have I sailed upon life’s troubled sea,
And faced the waves of sorrow and of doubt,
But in thy love, I found my anchorage,
And all my fears were banished and cast out.
Thou art my haven, where my soul may rest,
My guiding star, that points me to the true,
And in thy gentle arms, I feel most blessed,
And all my world is made anew with you.
So let us anchor here, and never roam,
And find within each other’s heart our home.

###517###
The rose that blooms with petals soft and red,
Doth draw the bee with perfume rich and sweet,
And though its beauty doth the sense o'er-spread,
 Its life is brief, its blooming soon complete.
So, my dear love, thy beauty doth enthrall,
And hold me captive with its sweet embrace,
But fear I lest it should too quickly fall,
And leave behind no vestige of its grace.
Yet, if thy spirit, like a hidden spring,
Doth bubble forth with kindness and with truth,
Then shall thy charm, a lasting joy still bring,
And bloom with grace throughout thy precious youth.
So let thy virtues be thy lasting dower,
And shine forth ever, in thy sweetest hour.

###518###
When I do read the tales of ages past,
Of heroes bold, and lovers true and brave,
My heart doth yearn for glories that did last,
And souls that could their fervent passion save.
But in this age, where fickle fortunes sway,
And constancy is deemed a childish dream,
True love doth seem to wander far away,
And vanish like a momentary gleam.
Yet, in thy eyes, I see a spark so bright,
A flame that whispers of a truer fire,
And in thy faith, I find a guiding light,
To lead me on, to my heart’s deep desire.
So let us build, upon this noble ground,
A love that shall eternally be found.

###519###
The fleeting moments, like a hurried guest,
Do pass so swiftly, leaving scarce a trace,
And steal away the joy we hold possessed,
And leave behind no comforting embrace.
So let us not delay, but seize the hour,
And fill our lives with pleasures, rich and deep,
For time, the master, holds us in its power,
And soon will call us to eternal sleep.
Let laughter ring, and let our spirits blend,
In sweet communion, banishing all woe,
And on love’s wings, our joyful thoughts shall send,
A message that shall eternally glow.
So let us live, with passion and with glee,
And find our solace, you and I, and me.

###520###
When I do gaze upon the starry night,
And contemplate the heavens, vast and deep,
My soul doth yearn to take its upward flight,
And leave behind the earthly cares that creep.
But then I think of thee, and all is well,
Thy presence is a heaven here below,
And in thy love, a magic doth compel,
My earthly spirit, evermore to glow.
Let others seek the heavens, far and high,
And dream of realms beyond the mortal ken,
My paradise is found when thou art nigh,
And in thine arms, I’m happier than when
I dreamt of stars, or wished for wings to flee,
For all my heaven rests, dear love, with thee.

###521###
The winter’s snow, that doth the landscape white,
Shall melt away when spring’s warm breath returns,
And frozen streams shall gleam with liquid light,
As nature’s gentle, verdant life re-burns.
So too, my sorrow, though it chills my breast,
Shall yield at length unto thy loving gaze,
And bring my weary spirit sweetest rest,
And fill my darkened soul with golden rays.
Let not thy absence be a source of pain,
But trust that love, like spring, will find its way,
And banish hence this cold and dreary reign,
And bring a brighter, more auspicious day.
For in thy heart, I find a sun so true,
That melts all ice, and makes my world anew.

###522###
The tapestry that doth a story weave,
With threads of colour, delicate and fine,
Doth please the eye, and doth the heart relieve,
With beauty wrought by patient, skilled design.
So is thy spirit, woven with such care,
With threads of kindness, loyalty, and grace,
A masterpiece beyond all else compare,
That time itself can never quite efface.
Let outward show be judged by fleeting glance,
And vanity may hold its hollow sway,
But true worth lies within, beyond mere chance,
And shines eternally, come what may.
So let us praise that beauty, pure and deep,
That in the heart of worth, doth safely keep.

###522###
When that my heart with sorrow is o'erpressed,
And heavy thoughts do cloud my weary mind,
I turn my gaze unto the heavens blessed,
Where solace pure and true I often find.
The stars above, with ancient, steady gleam,
Do whisper tales of ages long since past,
And banish hence the trouble of my dream,
A balm to wounds that seemed too deep to last.
Though earthly cares may vex and wound me sore,
And fortune's wheel doth spin with cruelest might,
The firmament, I know, will evermore
Shine down upon me with its constant light.
So shall I bear what trials life may send,
With hope renewed, until my journey's end.

###523###
My love, whose eyes do hold the morning's dew,
And smile that doth the darkest winter chase,
Hath wrought a spell, both potent and so true,
That holds my soul within its tender grace.
No fairer sight the sun hath e'er beheld,
Than is her form, in loveliness arrayed,
By earthly standards, she hath long excelled,
A queenly grace, by no decree unmade.
Her voice, a lute, doth sweetly tune my ear,
And banish hence the discord of the day,
Dispelling shadows, conquering all fear,
And leading me upon a brighter way.
So shall I sing her praises, day by day,
And worship her, whilst breath within me lay.

###524###
The winter's breath, with icy hand doth seize
The verdant fields, and all their beauty steal,
And bare-branched trees do shiver in the breeze,
As nature's bloom doth mournfully congeal.
The sun, though high, doth grant but feeble heat,
And lengthens not the hours of morning's rise,
The world lies hushed, a silence bittersweet,
Beneath the gaze of grey and cloudy skies.
Yet in my breast, a warmth doth still remain,
A hidden fire, that winter cannot quell,
A love that blooms, and conquers wind and rain,
A secret joy, no season can dispel.
So let the frost its chilling power show,
My love for thee, like summer, still shall grow.

###525###
When envious tongues do speak in sland'rous tone,
And cast their venom on my honest name,
I find my strength, and stand myself alone,
Against the darkness and the burning shame.
For truth, like steel, doth bear a tempered gleam,
And though it may be dimmed by specious lies,
It shall endure, a bright and constant beam,
That pierces through the falsity that flies.
Let rumour rage, and wicked whispers fly,
They cannot touch the substance of my soul,
Which rests secure, beneath the watchful eye
Of justice, that doth make the broken whole.
So let them carp, and let their malice spread,
My conscience clear, no fear shall fill my head.

###526###
The fleeting hours, like shadows, haste away,
And youth's fair bloom doth wither on the vine,
Each moment lost, cannot be brought to stay,
But joins the past, in realms no longer mine.
The mirror shows a face that time hath lined,
And silver threads do mingle with the gold,
The strength of youth, no longer can I find,
As tales of bygone years are now unfold.
Yet though the body may grow weak and frail,
And outward grace begin its slow decay,
My spirit's fire shall never, ever fail,
But burn more brightly as I pass away.
For inner worth, no outward change can mar,
And love's true light shall guide me from afar.

###527###
My dearest friend, whose counsel wise and deep,
Hath been a balm unto my troubled soul,
When doubts and fears do cause my heart to weep,
And dark despair doth take its heavy toll.
Thy steady hand, hath pulled me from the brink,
Of ruin's edge, and showed me clearer skies,
Thy gentle words, do make my spirit think,
And banish hence the sorrow and the lies.
Through tempest's rage, and fortune's cruelest blow,
Thy constant faith hath been my guiding star,
And taught me truths that I did scarce yet know,
And healed the wounds that left my spirit raw.
So let me pledge, with all my heart and might,
To cherish thee, my beacon, shining bright.

###528###
The sun descends, and paints the western sky,
With hues of gold, and crimson, fiery red,
As weary day prepares itself to die,
And twilight's gentle mantle is outspread.
The birds do cease their sweet and joyful song,
And silence falls, upon the sleeping land,
The world grows still, where shadows stretch out long,
And nature rests, at slumber's soft command.
Yet in my heart, a waking thought doth dwell,
A longing deep, for one who holds my love,
Whose absence makes the present moments hell,
And sends my prayers to gentle heavens above.
Oh, hasten, night, and bring her to my sight,
Or banish sleep, and grant me sweet delight.

###529###
When fickle Fortune smiles with treacherous face,
And showers down her gifts with lavish hand,
'Tis then I fear her swift and swift embrace,
And learn to build my hopes on firmer sand.
For she, that goddess, fickle and untrue,
Doth raise men high, but then doth cast them down,
Her favour gained, doth vanish like the dew,
And leaves them stripped of honour and renown.
So I shall build my fortune on my deed,
And find my wealth within my honest toil,
And plant the seeds of virtue, as my creed,
And trust the fruits of this my native soil.
For what I earn, by labour of my hand,
Shall last beyond the reach of her command.

###530###
The summer's heat, doth parch the thirsty ground,
And weary folk do seek the cooling shade,
Where gentle breezes softly play around,
And nature's bounty is in full parade.
The leaves do rustle with a whispering sound,
And blossoms bloom, in colours bright and bold,
The world is filled with beauty all around,
A tapestry, in summer's warmth unrolled.
Yet in this warmth, a chilling thought I find,
That all this beauty is but for a day,
And soon will fade, and leave no trace behind,
As autumn's touch doth steal its charm away.
So let me seize the moments as they fly,
And cherish beauty, ere it bids goodbye.

###531###
When in the night, and all the world doth sleep,
My restless thoughts do pace within my brain,
And ancient sorrows, that the heart doth keep,
Do rise again, and bring their bitter pain.
I think of vows, that were so lightly made,
And promises, that vanished in the air,
Of friendships lost, and trust that was betrayed,
And all the burdens that my soul doth bear.
Yet in this darkness, a faint light I see,
A hope that whispers of a brighter dawn,
That even past misfortunes shall agree,
To make me stronger, when the night is gone.
So shall I wake, with spirit undismayed,
And face the day, by virtue unafraid.

###532###
Thy beauty, dear, doth shame the blushing rose,
And steal the stars from their celestial height,
Thy gentle voice, a melody that flows,
Doth fill my soul with wonder and delight.
No earthly gem, nor treasure, can compare,
Unto the grace that doth adorn thy face,
A gift from heaven, beyond all mortal prayer,
That holds my heart in its enchanting chase.
Though seasons turn, and outward forms may fade,
Thy spirit's light shall ever shine anew,
A steadfast star, by no decay betrayed,
Forever shining, beautiful and true.
So shall I pledge my love, eternally,
And worship thee, my dearest, only she.

###533###
The fleeting moments, like a river's flow,
Do carry onward all that we hold dear,
And youth's bright flame, that burns with ardent glow,
Must dim and fade, as passing years appear.
The bloom of cheek, and vigour of the limb,
Shall yield at last, to age's heavy hand,
And memory's light, though once so strong and firm,
May falter now, and slip beyond command.
Yet in the heart, a deeper wisdom lies,
A knowing gaze, that pierces through the veil,
And sees the truth, beneath the outward guise,
A richer spirit, that shall never fail.
So let us greet the twilight with a smile,
And find our peace, for one more precious while.

###534###
When worldly cares do press with heavy weight,
And burdens seem too great for me to bear,
I turn my thoughts unto a higher state,
And cast my troubles on the passing air.
For in the realm of dreams, where fancy reigns,
And thoughts take wing, on swift and airy steed,
I find a solace that my soul sustains,
And plant the seeds of future hopeful deed.
The mind, unbound by earthly, harsh decree,
Can soar to heights, where no man can deny,
And build new worlds, for all eternity,
Beneath the gaze of an approving sky.
So let me dream, and let my spirit roam,
And find within my thoughts a peaceful home.

###535###
The robin's song, doth greet the morning's rise,
And herald forth the dawn with cheerful note,
Dispelling shadows from the sleeping skies,
And on the air, its joyful tidings float.
The dew-kissed grass, doth sparkle in the light,
And flowers bloom, in colours pure and deep,
The world awakens, banishing the night,
While gentle breezes through the meadows sweep.
My heart, though oft with worldly sorrow fraught,
Doth feel a stirring, at this sweet rebirth,
And learns anew the lessons nature taught,
