Of simple joy, and beauty of the earth.
So let me learn from this inspiring scene,
To find true happiness, and live serene.

###536###
When envy's sharp and poisoned dart doth fly,
And seeks to wound with malice and with hate,
I lift my head, and meet it with mine eye,
And stand unmoved, against its cruel fate.
For what is built on lies, shall surely fall,
And what is gained by treachery and strife,
Can never stand, nor answer virtue's call,
But wilts and fades, and forfeits all its life.
My worth, I know, is not in outward show,
Nor in the praise that fickle crowds bestow,
But in the truth, that deep within doth grow,
And in the deeds that from my heart do flow.
So let them speak, their venom to impart,
It cannot touch the fortress of my heart.

###537###
The stars above, in vast and silent throng,
Do watch the earth with ever-steady gaze,
Their ancient light, hath shone for ages long,
And guides the mariner through stormy haze.
They speak of realms, beyond our mortal ken,
Of endless space, and time that knows no end,
A mystery, that doth entrance all men,
On whom our earthly hopes and fears depend.
And when I feel the weight of worldly strife,
And human frailty makes my spirit quail,
I look to them, the constant lights of life,
And find a strength that never seems to fail.
So shall I trust, in their celestial might,
And find my solace in their guiding light.

###538###
When thou art near, the world doth seem to bloom,
And sorrow's veil is lifted from mine eyes,
Dispelling shadows, conquering all gloom,
And filling me with wondrous, sweet surprise.
Thy presence is as sunshine after rain,
A gentle balm unto my weary soul,
That banishes all doubt and worldly pain,
And makes me whole, and renders me control.
No fairer sight, the heavens e'er did grant,
Than is thy smile, that doth my heart enthrall,
A perfect beauty, that doth ever chant,
A melody that captivates us all.
So let me linger, in thy radiant light,
And find my heaven, in thy presence bright.

###539###
The fleeting years, do steal our precious youth,
And leave their mark upon the furrowed brow,
The rosy cheek, the vigour and the truth,
Are lost to time, as we must learn somehow.
The strength of limb, the sharpness of the mind,
Do yield at last, to age's cold decree,
And memories, that once were clear and kind,
May dim and fade, for all the world to see.
Yet in the heart, a deeper love may dwell,
A wisdom gained, through trials bravely faced,
A spirit's grace, that time can never quell,
A lasting worth, by no decay effaced.
So let us cherish, what the soul hath won,
And find true beauty, when the race is run.

###540###
When discord reigns, and angry voices rise,
And hearts are filled with envy and with spite,
I seek the calm, beneath the peaceful skies,
And find a solace in the fading light.
For anger's flame, doth burn and then consume,
The very soul that harbors it within,
And leaves behind naught but a hollow room,
Where joy and peace can never more begin.
But gentle words, like dew upon the grass,
Do soothe the spirit, and restore the soul,
And teach the heart, that transient troubles pass,
And make the broken spirit once more whole.
So let me choose, the path of love and peace,
And find within my heart, a sweet release.

###541###
The moon ascends, in majesty and grace,
And casts her silver glow upon the land,
A silent watch, within her ethereal space,
A guiding beacon, by night's dark command.
The stars do twinkle, with a distant gleam,
As constellations, in their silent dance,
Do weave a tapestry, as in a dream,
That holds the world within their mystic trance.
And in this hush, when all the world doth sleep,
My thoughts take wing, and soar to realms afar,
Where ancient secrets, doth the darkness keep,
And dreams unfold, beneath the evening star.
So let me gaze, and let my spirit fly,
Beneath the wonder of the midnight sky.

###542###
When that my love doth cast her gentle eyes,
Upon the page where my poor thoughts are writ,
A sudden joy within my bosom lies,
And all my doubts do swiftly take their quit.
Her grace doth shine, a beacon in the night,
Dispelling shadows that my heart would keep,
And paints my world with colours ever bright,
As from a slumber, I do wake from sleep.
No muse hath ever touched so sweet a chord,
No bird hath sung so fair a melody,
As what her presence to my soul hath poured,
A symphony of perfect ecstasy.
  So let my quill for ever sing her praise,
  And live immortal in her loving gaze.

###543###
The fleeting hours, like shadows, steal away,
And leave behind the traces of their flight,
As summer's bloom doth yield to winter's sway,
And day gives place to the encroaching night.
So too my youth, a blossom rich and fair,
Doth feel the touch of time's relentless hand,
And beauty fades, a whisper on the air,
As sands slip through the hourglass on the strand.
Yet in my heart, a treasure I do keep,
A love more constant than the moon above,
That shall through all the weary seasons sleep,
And wake renewed, a testament of love.
  For though my form may wither and grow old,
  My soul's devotion never can be sold.

###544###
When Fortune smiles, her favour doth appear,
A golden sun that warms my earthly face,
And banishes all doubt and lurking fear,
And fills my days with bounty and with grace.
But when she frowns, her tempers quickly turn,
And all her gifts are snatched with cruel disdain,
Leaving me where the bitter lessons burn,
And naught remains but sorrow and sharp pain.
I am a bark upon a stormy sea,
Tossed by the waves of her capricious will,
No chart to guide, no compass to set me,
But to the winds my fragile hopes are still.
  Yet, if thy love, my star, doth shine so clear,
  I fear no tempest, nor shall shed a tear.

###545###
The subtle serpent of despair doth creep,
Within the garden of my troubled mind,
And with its venom, bids my spirit weep,
Leaving all hope and solace far behind.
The joyous bird that once did sweetly sing,
Now sits in silence, with a drooping head,
And all the pleasures that the seasons bring,
Are turned to ashes, and to sorrow fled.
My strength doth fail, my courage doth decay,
As though a blight had fallen on my soul,
And from my heart, all happiness doth stray,
Leaving me lost, beyond all self-control.
  But if thy hand, a healing balm, I find,
  I may yet rise, and leave despair behind.

###546###
My love, when thou dost speak, the heavens bend,
To lend an ear to thy melodious sound,
And every word, a message doth portend,
That on my soul, a blessedness hath found.
Thy laughter rings, a chime of purest gold,
That echoes through the chambers of my heart,
A story that can never be told,
Of beauty that doth set my soul apart.
Thy eyes, like stars that twinkle in the dark,
Do guide my steps, and light my weary way,
And leave upon my spirit, their bright mark,
To chase the gloom of every passing day.
  So let me listen, and for ever stay,
  Within the sunshine of thy gentle ray.

###547###
When I behold the grandeur of the sky,
And mark the courses of the planets bold,
Or watch the feathered creatures as they fly,
And hear the stories that the winds have told,
I marvel at the power that hath wrought,
Such wonders in this vast and boundless space,
And ponder on the wisdom that hath taught,
Each living thing its proper time and place.
Yet, more I marvel at the love I see,
Reflected in the mirror of thine eyes,
A greater miracle, it seems to me,
Than all the starry host that fills the skies.
  For in thy soul, a universe I find,
  That doth surpass all nature, and mankind.

###548###
The silent night, with velvet mantle spread,
Doth hush the world to slumber, soft and deep,
And over all, her gentle peace is shed,
While weary mortals in their slumber sleep.
But in my breast, no rest can I procure,
My thoughts do wander, restless and alone,
And seek a solace that may long endure,
A comfort that I have not yet made known.
I think of thee, my fairest, and my dear,
And to thy image, all my hopes I turn,
And banish every doubt and creeping fear,
As in thy love, my spirit starts to burn.
  So in this quiet hour, my heart takes wing,
  And to thy distant shore, its praises bring.

###549###
The painted rose, though fair to outward sight,
Doth hold within its petals, thorns unseen,
That prick the hand that seeks to grasp it tight,
And wound the soul, where beauty should have been.
So many smiles, that mask a heart of guile,
And honeyed words, that whisper sweet deceit,
Do lure the unwary to their bitter trial,
And make their passage through life bittersweet.
But in thy truth, I find a steadfast rock,
A haven from the storms that rage and blow,
Where I may safely anchor and not mock,
The treacherous currents that do ebb and flow.
  Thy honest heart, a jewel beyond all price,
  Doth save me from the world's cold artifice.

###550###
When I do gaze upon thy lovely face,
My soul is filled with wonder and with awe,
And in thy presence, I do find my place,
Obeying love's immutable, sweet law.
Thy voice, a music that doth charm my ear,
Doth banish all the troubles of my mind,
And makes the path of life appear so clear,
That all my former sorrows are resigned.
Thy touch, a flame that sets my blood afire,
Doth kindle passions I had not known,
And lifts my spirit to a higher,
A joy that earthly pleasures have not shown.
  So let me ever dwell within thy light,
  And banish from my soul the shades of night.

###551###
The winter's frost, that chills the very bone,
Doth strip the trees of all their leafy pride,
And leaves them bare, to stand in silence lone,
As though all life had from their branches died.
Yet, when the spring doth come with gentle hand,
New leaves do sprout, and blossoms start to bloom,
And life returns, to grace the verdant land,
Dispelling shadows, and the winter's gloom.
So too my heart, though once in winter's thrall,
Doth feel the warmth of thy returning grace,
And from despair's cold grip, it doth recall,
A spring of hope, within this barren place.
  For in thy love, new life I do embrace,
  And find again my joy, and my true space.

###552###
The fickle crowd, that doth with praises roar,
When fortune smiles, and all doth go their way,
Will turn their backs, and heed their cries no more,
When shadows gather, and the skies are gray.
Their loyalty, a whisper on the breeze,
Doth vanish swift, when trials do appear,
And leave the heart, that once did find its ease,
To face the storm, with nothing but its fear.
But thy true heart, a constant, steady flame,
Doth shine unwavering, in darkest hour,
And whispers low, and speaks my dearest name,
A comforting and ever-present power.
  So let them judge, and let them turn aside,
  Thy steadfast love, my solace and my guide.

###553###
When absence doth my love from me divide,
And weary miles between us lie so deep,
My spirit aches, with naught where it can hide,
And lonely vigils through the night I keep.
The sun doth shine, but brings no warmth to me,
The birds do sing, but their sweet tunes are vain,
For all my joy doth rest on thee, and thee,
And without thee, my heart doth feel the pain.
Each passing hour, a torture to endure,
Each waking moment, a protracted sigh,
And hope alone, a thing that can secure,
 A future meeting, 'neath a happier sky.
  So hasten, love, and bridge this cruel divide,
  And in thy arms, let all my sorrows hide.

###554###
The world doth judge by what the eyes behold,
By outward show, and by the minted gold,
And little heed they to the stories told,
Within the heart, that's brave and strong and bold.
They see the rags, and scorn the noble soul,
They hear the voice, and doubt the truth it speaks,
And set their limits, and their strict control,
Upon the worth that humble virtue seeks.
But thou, my love, dost pierce this shallow guise,
And see the treasure hidden from the view,
And in thy favour, I find my true prize,
A love that's honest, and forever true.
  So let them look, and let them turn away,
  Thy gentle judgment lights my darkest day.

###555###
The ancient oak, that hath so long withstood,
The buffetings of wind and driving rain,
Doth stand a testament, in field and wood,
Of strength and patience, that doth long sustain.
Its roots run deep, its branches spread so wide,
A shelter from the sun, a shield from storm,
And in its presence, weary souls confide,
And find a solace, in its ancient form.
So is my love, a growth of many years,
Deep-rooted now, in soil of honest care,
And though it faces storms and bitter tears,
Its strength shall hold, and for thy sake, I swear.
  For as the oak, my love shall still remain,
  Through passing seasons, and through joy and pain.

###556###
When I do dream, thy image doth appear,
A vision fair, that fills my sleeping sight,
And banishes all worldly doubt and fear,
And bathes my soul in pure and sweet delight.
We walk in gardens, where the roses bloom,
And gentle breezes whisper through the trees,
And in that realm, beyond all earthly gloom,
Our hearts are joined, in perfect, loving ease.
But then the dawn, with rude and jarring ray,
Doth break the spell, and bid the vision cease,
And I am left, to greet the waking day,
With naught but memory, and a longing peace.
  Yet in that dream, a truth I still do keep,
  That in thy love, my truest joys do sleep.

###557###
The buzzing fly, that doth with ceaseless hum,
Disturb the peace, and vex the weary ear,
Doth seek its food, and where the sweet drops come,
With wanton disregard, and naught to fear.
So too the fool, with uninvited word,
Doth interrupt the thought, and break the spell,
And makes his presence often to be heard,
When wiser silence would have served him well.
But thou, my love, dost know when to be still,
And when to speak, with wisdom and with grace,
And with thy presence, thou dost gently fill,
My heart with comfort, in this hurried place.
  So let the triflers buzz, and prate, and stray,
  Thy quiet wisdom guides me on my way.

###558###
When I do think of all the love I bear,
A vastness that no measure can contain,
It doth a fearful burden seem to share,
And makes me doubt if love itself be sane.
For what if thou shouldst prove untrue and cold,
And all my passion be bestowed in vain,
A story that can never be retold,
But leaves behind a bitter, burning stain.
Yet, in thy eyes, I see a mirrored truth,
A loyalty that shall not turn aside,
And in that sight, I find my loving youth,
And cast away all doubt, and foolish pride.
  For in thy faith, my own doth find its rest,
  And all my fears are banished from my breast.

###559###
The changing moon, that waxes and that wanes,
Doth mark the passage of the passing time,
And in its cycle, nature still remains,
A perfect rhythm, a celestial chime.
So too my love, though seasons may depart,
And worldly changes alter and decay,
Shall hold its course within my steadfast heart,
And shine the same, at close of every day.
Let tempests rage, let fortunes ebb and flow,
Let empires fall, and kingdoms turn to dust,
My love for thee, no earthly power can know,
Or shake the anchor of my ardent trust.
  For in this truth, my spirit finds its might,
  And burns with passion, ever pure and bright.

###560###
The fading light, that paints the western sky,
With hues of orange, purple, and of gold,
Doth bid the weary day prepare to die,
And stories of its passing to unfold.
So too my life, doth feel the gentle call,
Of time's slow march, that leads to setting sun,
And though I strive, I know I must let fall,
The race I've run, ere my short course is done.
But if thy love, a lasting legacy,
Doth grace my memory, when I am gone,
Then shall my soul find sweet eternity,
And live immortal, in thy heart, anon.
  So let the shadows lengthen, and grow deep,
  Thy love's bright echo shall my spirit keep.

###561###
When I do read the lines that thou hast writ,
My heart doth leap, and all my senses wake,
And in each phrase, a deeper meaning lit,
That doth my very being gently shake.
Thy thoughts do flow, like streams of purest water,
Reflecting truths, that common eyes do miss,
And in thy words, I find a loving daughter,
Of wisdom's bounteous and enduring kiss.
No learned sage, nor poet of renown,
Hath ever penned such beauty, clear and bold,
As that which from thy gifted hand is thrown,
A treasure richer than all gems and gold.
  So let me pore, and drink thy wisdom deep,
  And in its truth, my truest self shall keep.

###562###
The gentle rain, that falls with softest sound,
Doth kiss the earth, and make the flowers grow,
And life abundant, shall on all be found,
Where'er its cleansing, nurturing waters flow.
So too thy love, a blessing from above,
Doth fall upon my soul, and make it bloom,
And fill my spirit with a soaring love,
Dispelling darkness, and the deepest gloom.
It doth revive the hopes that once did fade,
And paints my world with colours bright and new,
And in its light, all weary fears are stayed,
And all my dreams at last are brought to view.
  For in thy love, my life finds its true quest,
  And in its warmth, my weary heart finds rest.

###562###
When Phoebus doth his golden chariot guide,
And bids the weary world to wake from sleep,
My heart doth stir, no longer can it hide,
The secret hopes that in its bosom keep.
The lark ascends with melody so sweet,
And chases shadows from the dawning skies,
My thoughts, like birds, on airy currents meet,
And sing of joys that in thy presence rise.
But when thy brow is clouded by some frown,
Or silence doth thy loving voice estrange,
My spirits sink, my hopeful blossoms drown,
And all my comfort doth to sorrow change.
    Yet still I trust thy heart will prove more true,
    Than fleeting clouds that obscure skies of blue.

###563###
The winter's chill doth bite with frosty teeth,
And naked trees do stand in solemn state,
As if they mourn the verdure lost beneath,
And bow their heads to an unkindly fate.
So doth my soul, when absence doth me seize,
And all the warmth of thy sweet presence fade,
I feel a winter that doth bring no ease,
A barren land where joy hath been betrayed.
No sun of comfort doth my spirit find,
No vernal breeze to stir my heavy heart,
But chilling thoughts that whisper to my mind,
And tear my hopeful, fragile soul apart.
    Yet wait I for the thaw that spring shall bring,
    When thou return'st, and all my joys shall sing.

###564###
I saw thee walk amidst a verdant mead,
Where summer's blush did paint the blushing rose,
And Nature's bounty did its beauty breed,
As gentle zephyrs kissed thy tender nose.
Thy grace did outshine all the blooms so fair,
Thy voice, a music to the list'ning air,
And in thy smile, I found beyond compare,
A heaven sent to banish all despair.
But like a dream, the vision passed away,
And left me standing in the common light,
Where beauty's power hath no longer sway,
And all my world is cloaked in darkest night.
    Yet in my mind thy image I do keep,
    A treasure stolen from my waking sleep.

###565###
My pen doth falter, and my ink doth stain,
The parchment white, with tearful, salty dew,
For thoughts of thee do bring a gentle pain,
A bittersweet remembrance, ever new.
Thy beauty shines, a beacon in the gloom,
Thy wit, a dart that pierces through my heart,
And in thy love, I find my destined doom,
A willing captive, playing out my part.
But cruel fortune doth our paths divide,
And envious distance doth our souls estrange,
And though my longing cannot be denied,
It must endure this sorrow and this change.
    Yet in my dreams, thy face I still embrace,
    And find some solace in that phantom space.

###566###
The busy world doth rush with hurried stride,
And minds are bent on gain and worldly care,
But in thy presence, all such thoughts subside,
And leave my soul with naught but love to bear.
Thy gentle hand doth soothe my troubled breast,
Thy loving gaze doth banish every fear,
And in thy arms, I find my sweetest rest,
A haven true, forever to be near.
But shadows fall, and jealous doubts arise,
And whisper tales of falsehood and of strife,
And dim the brightness of thy loving eyes,
And threaten to extinguish all my life.
    Yet still I cling to hopes that thee I'll find,
    The truest solace for my weary mind.

###567###
When envy's serpent whispers in my ear,
And plants a seed of doubt within my soul,
I banish thence the venom and the fear,
And bid my loyal heart to take control.
For what is truth, if not a steadfast flame,
That burns more bright when tested by the blast,
And what is love, if not a constant name,
That holds through time, and shall forever last?
Let others speak with tongues of bitter gall,
And paint the world with hues of discontent,
My faith in thee shall stand above it all,
A fortress strong, on solid virtue bent.
    So let them rail, and let their malice spread,
    My love for thee shall never be unsaid.

###568###
The fleeting hours, like shadows, steal away,
And leave behind a melancholy trace,
As youth's bright dawn gives way to sober day,
And time doth etch its lines upon my face.
So too, thy beauty, though it doth still gleam,
Must yield at last to winter's frosty reign,
And all the splendours of a summer's dream,
Must fade and vanish, leaving naught but pain.
Yet in thy spirit, I do find a light,
That ages cannot quench nor time decay,
A constant star that shines in darkest night,
And guides my soul upon its lonely way.
    So let us cherish what we hold so dear,
    Before the final twilight draweth near.

###569###
My dearest friend, whose absence doth me rend,
And leaves my heart in solitary woe,
My thoughts to thee, on wings of longing, send,
And pray for joys that we again may know.
The days are long, the weary nights are deep,
And silent tears do fall upon my cheek,
While waking dreams and slumbering visions keep,
The sweet remembrance of the words you speak.
If fate should grant a merciful decree,
And bring us back to where we were before,
Then shall my soul rejoice eternally,
And love thee more than ever I have swore.
    Until that hour, I'll bear this heavy cross,
    And count each moment as a bitter loss.

###570###
The world's applause, a fickle, fleeting sound,
That lifts men high, then casts them to the dust,
On shifting sands, their glories are unbound,
And turn to naught, betrayed by faithless trust.
But true renown, that which is earned and deep,
Doth spring from deeds of worth and noble heart,
And in the minds of honest men doth keep,
A lasting praise that time cannot depart.
So let them chase the favour of the crowd,
And seek their fame in vanity's bright show,
My humble quest, though spoken not aloud,
Is in thy favour, where true merits grow.
    For thy good word, more precious than all gold,
    A richer story shall my life unfold.

###571###
When tempest's rage doth shake the ocean wide,
And mighty waves do crash with fearsome roar,
My spirit trembles, and I seek to hide,
From nature's wrath that batters at the shore.
So do I feel, when jealous whispers sting,
And doubts do rise like breakers from the deep,
My troubled soul no solace can it bring,
But fears that endless sorrows it must reap.
Yet like a ship that rides the stormy main,
And finds its harbour in a calmer bay,
My love for thee shall conquer every pain,
And guide me safely to a brighter day.
    So let the winds of discord fiercely blow,
    My heart to thee shall steadfastly still go.

###572###
The sun doth climb, and chase the night afar,
And banish shades with beams of radiant gold,
But in my heart, there shines a brighter star,
A love for thee, more precious than untold.
Thy gentle smile, a balm to soothe my woes,
Thy tender voice, a melody so sweet,
And in thy gaze, my dearest comfort grows,
A joy that makes my weary heart complete.
But when thou art from my embrace removed,
The world is cloaked in darkness and in grey,
And every happy moment is reproved,
And all my cheerful spirits fly away.
    Yet still I hope, and for thy return I wait,
    To mend my soul and seal my loving fate.

###573###
This world's a stage, where actors play their part,
With masks of joy, or sorrow's painted frown,
And each doth strive to capture every heart,
And win the plaudits of the fleeting town.
But I, dear friend, do find my truest scene,
Within the compass of thy loving eye,
Where all the artifice doth intervene,
And I may stand beneath a truthful sky.
Let others strut and fret their little hour,
And speak their lines with passion and with art,
My silent love shall wield a greater power,
And speak the honest language of my heart.
    For in thy sight, my true self I may find,
    The purest comfort for my searching mind.

###574###
The blooming rose, though fair it doth appear,
Must shed its petals to the chilling breeze,
And summer's warmth, though held so very dear,
Must yield to frost that strips the naked trees.
So too, thy beauty, though it doth now shine,
Must fade at last, as all things mortal do,
And though thy grace be ever so divine,
Time's cruel hand will change its aspect true.
But in thy virtue, I do see a bloom,
That season's change can never mar nor stain,
A steadfast light that conquers every gloom,
And shall eternal admiration gain.
    So let the outward form to dust return,
    Thy inward worth shall ever brightly burn.

###575###
My dearest love, whose absence makes me pine,
And leaves my soul in melancholy's shade,
I send to thee this humble, heartfelt line,
A token true, of vows that ne'er shall fade.
The sun doth shine, the birds do sweetly sing,
But all the joy seems wanting to my sight,
For without thee, no happiness they bring,
And all the world is draped in endless night.
I count the hours, and long for thy return,
To fill my breast with solace and with peace,
And in thy arms, my weary heart shall learn,
That all my former sorrows shall surcease.
    Until that day, I'll keep thy memory bright,
    And live in hope of future, sweet delight.

###576###
When Fortune smiles, and worldly goods abound,
And friends do flock with flattery and praise,
It is a time when truth can scarce be found,
And hearts are swayed by shallow, gilded ways.
But when the skies do darken, and the storm,
Doth strip away the comforts we possess,
Then shall we see the true and honest form,
Of those who stand with us in our distress.
So thank I thee, for showing in my need,
A loyalty that time cannot erase,
A helping hand, a comforting indeed,
A steadfast soul, in this uncertain race.
    For in the trial, true affection lies,
    A treasure found beneath the weeping skies.

###577###
The moon doth wax and wane, a changing face,
And tides do ebb and flow with constant might,
So too, my mood doth shift with time and place,
From darkest gloom to morning's hopeful light.
But through the changes, one desire remains,
A constant star that guides my wandering way,
To be with thee, and break these earthly chains,
And in thy love, forever to hold sway.
Let others seek for riches, fame, and power,
My greatest wealth is in thy loving gaze,
And every moment, every passing hour,
Is brighter when it's spent in thy sweet praise.
    So let us bind our souls with chains of love,
    And find our heaven in each other's love.

###578###
This mortal coil, where fleeting pleasures gleam,
And transient joys do dance before our eyes,
Doth often lead us from the nobler dream,
And fill our hearts with false and vain disguise.
But thou, dear friend, art free from such alloy,
Thy spirit shines with pure and steady light,
And in thy presence, I do find my joy,
A beacon burning in the darkest night.
Let fools pursue the phantom of desire,
And chase the shadows that will fade and die,
My heart is set on thee, a constant fire,
Beneath the vast and ever-watching sky.
    For in thy virtue, I do see the best,
    And in thy love, my soul shall find its rest.

###579###
The fleeting moments, like swift birds, do fly,
And bear away the treasures of our days,
And leave us weeping neath a mournful sky,
Lost in the sorrow of forgotten ways.
But in thy memory, a treasure lies,
More precious far than gems or earthly gold,
A constant joy that in my spirit cries,
A story that shall never be untold.
Though absence doth our outward paths divide,
And miles may stretch between our loving hearts,
Thy image in my soul doth still reside,
And in my dreams, thy gentle presence starts.
    So let us meet again, and banish pain,
    And in each other's arms, find joy again.

###580###
When I behold the stars in heaven's vault,
And mark their courses, distant and serene,
I wonder at the wisdom, free from fault,
That guides their journey, though unseen.
So too, thy mind, with wisdom doth abound,
And sheds a light upon my darkened way,
A deeper truth within thy words is found,
Than all the shallow wisdom of the day.
Let others boast of learning, vast and wide,
And fill their heads with trifles, light and vain,
Thy thoughtful grace doth with my soul preside,
And ease my troubles and my worldly pain.
    For in thy counsel, I do find my guide,
    And in thy truth, my spirit can confide.

###581###
The winter's hand doth grip the frozen land,
And strips the trees of all their summer's pride,
And icy winds do blow with bitter strand,
Where once the verdant leaves did softly hide.
So too, my heart, when thou art far from sight,
Doth feel a chill that numbs its vital glow,
And all the world seems void of joy and light,
As barren fields where frozen rivers flow.
But spring shall come, and chase the frost away,
And life shall stir, and verdure shall appear,
So too, thy presence shall restore the day,
And banish hence all doubt and chilling fear.
    When thou return'st, my heart shall brightly bloom,
    And banish hence all lingering winter's gloom.

###582###
When envious tongues do speak of thee with spite,
And paint thy name with shadows and with lies,
My heart doth burn with anger and with might,
And seeketh truth beneath those false disguise.
For I have known thy worth, both deep and true,
Thy noble spirit, and thy gentle mind,
And all the calumnies that they pursue,
Are but the venom of a poisoned kind.
Let them cast stones, and let their malice fly,
My faith in thee shall stand against their scorn,
For in thy soul, a brighter light doth lie,
Than all the darkness that their words have borne.
    So let them speak, and let their rumours spread,
    My love for thee shall never be unsaid.
    
###581###
When that my muse doth paint the summer's bloom,
And with sweet words the fleeting hours embrace,
I fear lest winter steal away its room,
And leave behind no vestige, nor no trace.
So too thy beauty, like a flower bright,
Doth hold my heart in thrall with gentle grace,
But age, a thief, doth creep with silent might,
And mar the fairness of thy lovely face.
Yet in these lines, thy virtue shall reside,
Beyond the reach of time, or envious fate,
And all thy virtues shall in verse abide,
To be admired, though years may come too late.
So let not fear thy joyful spirit blight,
For love eternal shines with truest light.

###582###
The sun, that doth the darkest shadows chase,
And wakes the world from slumber's drowsy hold,
Is but a pale reflection of thy face,
A story of thy virtues to be told.
When gentle breezes through the green leaves sigh,
And nature's choir doth sweet notes unfold,
My spirit soars, as if it learned to fly,
And finds in thee a treasure, more than gold.
But ah, the cruel hand of passing time,
Doth steal away the moments, one by one,
And leaves but echoes of a sweeter clime,
When all our golden days are overrun.
Yet though the fleeting seasons ebb and flow,
My love for thee shall ever steadfast grow.

###583###
My heart, a ship upon a stormy sea,
Doth toss and turn, with tempest's angry roar,
And finds no harbour, nor no certainty,
Until thy loving gaze it doth explore.
For in thine eyes, a compass I do find,
That guides me onward to a peaceful shore,
And leaves the troubled, weary world behind,
Where peace and true content I do adore.
But doubt, a serpent, whispers in mine ear,
Of fickle fortune, and of love's decay,
And fills my soul with apprehension's fear,
That thou wilt turn and cast my hope away.
Yet trust I in thy truth, with all my might,
And banish thence all shadows of the night.

###584###
When first I saw thee, in thy youthful prime,
My soul was captured, held in tender sway,
And felt the stirrings of a love sublime,
That would not from my yearning heart give way.
Thy laughter, like the chime of silver bells,
Did banish all the cares of yesterday,
And in thy gaze, a thousand magic spells,
Did bid my lonely spirit to obey.
But seasons turn, and beauty doth depart,
As summer's green gives way to autumn's gold,
And winter's frost doth pierce the aching heart,
When youthful charms no longer can be sold.
Yet in my memory, thy grace shall live,
A constant joy, that time can never give.

###585###
The subtle ink, that doth my thoughts express,
And builds a castle of my fondest dreams,
Doth strive to capture thy true loveliness,
And paint it fair, as through my spirit gleams.
But human art, though fervent it may be,
Falls short of nature's all-pervading schemes,
And cannot hold the essence of thee,
As in my waking hours, or slumbering streams.
So let this humble verse my passion show,
A testament to love's enduring flame,
Though words may falter, and though feelings grow,
My heart shall ever whisper thy dear name.
For in this world, no greater joy I find,
Than to be loved, and to be truly kind.

###586###
When envious tongues do speak of absent friends,
And weave their slanders with a subtle art,
My loyal heart its steadfastness transcends,
And holds their virtues deeply in my heart.
So thou, dear friend, though miles between us lie,
And circumstance doth bid us play our part,
Dost dwell within my thoughts, beneath the sky,
And find a lodging in my truest heart.
Let not the whispers of the world deceive,
Nor distance breed a chasm in our bond,
For in thy spirit, I do still believe,
And in our friendship, I do much respond.
So let us keep our promises so true,
And prove our faith, in all we say and do.

###587###
The fleeting moment, like a butterfly,
Doth dance and flutter, in the sunlit air,
And then it vanishes before mine eye,
And leaves behind no token, nor no snare.
So too thy presence, though it brings delight,
Is but a passing charm, beyond compare,
And fades away, with morning's early light,
Leaving my lonely spirit to despair.
Yet in the memory of thy gentle smile,
I find a solace, sweet and true and deep,
And dwell upon thy grace a little while,
Before the restless hours my vigil keep.
So let me hold thee in my mind so dear,
Until again thy radiant self is near.

###588###
When fortune smiles, and all the world doth praise,
And worldly goods do fill our coffers high,
We strut and preen in life's delusive maze,
And think our happiness shall never die.
But ah, the fickle wheel doth turn apace,
And sends our riches fleeting to the sky,
Leaving us bare, with sorrow in our face,
And causes us to heave a mournful sigh.
So let us build our joy on surer ground,
Than transient wealth, or fame's ephemeral gleam,
And in the love of hearts, let us be found,
A lasting joy, a never-ending dream.
For what is gold, or silver's shining hue,
Compared to love, so faithful and so true?

###589###
The cruel hand of absence doth impart
A bitter pang, a void within my breast,
And steals the comfort from my aching heart,
And robs my weary spirit of its rest.
When I recall the moments we did share,
Thy gentle words, thy presence, heaven-blessed,
A phantom touch doth linger in the air,
And leaves me longing, put to sorest test.
Yet in the hope of our reunion bright,
I find a solace, though the darkness press,
And dream of seeing thee, a glorious sight,
To banish thence all sorrow and distress.
So let us pray for days of coming joy,
When love's embrace shall all our fears destroy.

###590###
When summer's lease hath all too short a date,
And autumn's chill doth creep upon the scene,
I mourn the loss of pleasures, soon abate,
And all the joys that summer held within.
So too thy youth, though radiant it doth seem,
Is but a moment, vibrant and serene,
And soon shall fade, like some forgotten dream,
And leave behind what might have ever been.
But in the strength of love, I find a way,
To hold thy beauty, though the seasons change,
And in my verse, thy memory shall stay,
Beyond the reach of time's relentless range.
So let this tribute be thy lasting prize,
Reflected in my ever-loving eyes.

###591###
The painted rose, that doth the garden grace,
With crimson hue, and fragrance sweet and rare,
Doth hold within its captivating space,
A fleeting beauty, held in summer's air.
So is thy charm, a blossom fair to see,
That doth my captivated spirit ensnare,
But time, the gardener, with stern decree,
Shall pluck it hence, and leave the branches bare.
Yet though the petals fall, and scent takes flight,
The root remains, in earth so firm and deep,
And in my heart, thy memory shines bright,
A constant flame, that slumber cannot keep.
So let not fear thy joyous spirit bind,
For love eternal, I shall ever find.

###592###
When busy hands do fashion works of art,
And skilled design doth grace the craftsman's toil,
I oft do marvel at the patient heart,
That doth with tireless effort break the soil.
But all their labours, though they strive so well,
Can ne'er compare to nature's wondrous coil,
Nor can their finest efforts e'er excel,
The art that doth the living flesh embroil.
For in thy form, a masterpiece I see,
More rare than gold, more precious than the gem,
A living sculpture, wrought by destiny,
Whose matchless beauty none can e'er condemn.
So let me gaze upon thy wondrous frame,
And whisper low, thy ever-honoured name.

###593###
The fleeting whisper of a summer breeze,
That stirs the leaves and dances through the trees,
Doth bring a joy that doth my spirit please,
And calms the tempest of my own unease.
So too thy voice, a melody so sweet,
Doth chase away all melancholy seas,
And makes my troubled, weary heart complete,
And sets my anxious, roving mind at ease.
But oh, when silence falls, and thou art gone,
The world grows dim, and shadows start to creep,
And I am left to face the lonely dawn,
While all the promises I made to keep,
Seem hollow now, and filled with deep despair,
Until again I hear thy voice so fair.

###594###
The golden coin, that doth the merchant prize,
And hoards with care, lest fortune prove unkind,
Doth fade and tarnish in his eager eyes,
And leaves no lasting pleasure for his mind.
So is it with the fleeting joys of earth,
That glitter brightly, but are left behind,
And cannot give a true, eternal worth,
To souls that worldly riches seek to find.
But in the richness of a loving heart,
A treasure lies, that time cannot destroy,
A bond of truth, that never shall depart,
A pure and everlasting, sweet employ.
So let us seek this wealth, beyond compare,
And find our solace in its tender care.

###595###
When envious thoughts do cloud the mind of man,
And bid him scorn what he cannot possess,
He sees but faults, since first his course began,
And magnifies each imperfection's stress.
So let me cast such petty cares aside,
And love thee purely, with no thought of less,
For in thy virtues, I do much confide,
And find a comfort in thy tenderness.
Let not the world with its discerning gaze,
Find cause to question what my heart doth hold,
For in thy spirit, through all passing days,
A truer beauty doth itself unfold.
So let us walk this path, with steadfast troth,
And shield our love from any cruel uncouth.

###596###
The soaring hawk, that circles in the height,
And views the world with keen and piercing eye,
Doth spy its prey, and stoops with all its might,
Beneath the vast and all-observing sky.
So my desire, when it doth see thee near,
Doth fix its gaze, and bids my spirit fly,
And conquer all that whispers of old fear,
To win thy favour, ere the moments die.
But ah, the chase is perilous and long,
And many a snare doth lie within the way,
And fickle fortune may prove weak or strong,
And steal the prize from out my grasp this day.
Yet still I strive, with ardour unconfined,
To make thy love the treasure I shall find.

###597###
When winter's frost doth hold the world in thrall,
And biting winds do through the branches blow,
My thoughts do turn to thee, beyond the wall
Of frozen nature, where no blossoms grow.
For in thy warmth, a summer I do find,
A gentle sun, that makes my spirit glow,
And leaves the bleakness of the world behind,
And bids a sweet and happy feeling flow.
So art thou to my soul, a haven bright,
A refuge from the storms that rage and roar,
And in thy presence, all is calm and light,
And I am happy, needing nothing more.
So let me bask within thy loving ray,
And chase the chill of winter far away.

###598###
The fleeting shadow, cast by passing cloud,
Doth briefly dim the sun's celestial fire,
And leaves the world in darkness, though endowed
With light that soon shall re-inspire.
So is thy absence, though it brings me pain,
A temporary state, to soon retire,
For like the sun, thou shalt return again,
And fill my heart with long-desired fire.
Let not despair thy noble spirit sway,
Nor let the darkness dim thy hopeful eye,
For brighter dawns shall herald a new day,
When reunited, we shall joyful cry.
So hold thou fast, and banish every fear,
For soon, my dearest love, I shall be near.

###599###
When solemn oaths are sworn, and vows are made,
To keep a faith that shall not know decay,
The heart feels strong, and is no more afraid,
But walks with courage on its chosen way.
So hath my love for thee been sworn and sealed,
A sacred bond, that shall not fade away,
And in its strength, my spirit is revealed,
And finds a solace for the passing day.
Let rumour whisper, and let slander strive,
To dim the lustre of our honest love,
Our steadfast hearts shall keep its flame alive,
And prove its truth, as sent from realms above.
So let us stand as one, in faith so deep,
While all the world its watchful vigil keep.

###600###
The painter's brush, that doth with skill impart
The hue of cheek, the sparkle of the eye,
Can scarce portray the workings of the heart,
Nor capture all that makes the spirit sigh.
So though I strive with words to paint thy worth,
And tell the tales of glories passing by,
I find my language falters from its birth,
And cannot reach the heights where virtues lie.
Yet this I know, with certainty so sure,
Thy inner beauty doth outshine the rest,
A flame of goodness, destined to endure,
And put all outward charms unto the test.
So let my verse, though simple it may be,
Declare the wonder that resides in thee.

###600###
When Fortune frowns and smiles no more on me,
And chilling doubts do whisper in my ear,
My weary heart, a ship upon the sea,
Doth founder 'neath the weight of doubt and fear.
The sun, that once did gleam with golden light,
Now hides its face behind a shroud of gray,
And shadows deep do steal away the bright,
Where erst my hopes did dance in joyful play.
Alas, that fickle dame, with moods so strange,
Should toss me thus on waves of discontent,
And all my worldly treasures rearrange,
My former joys now sadly backward sent.
Yet in this storm, a quiet strength I find,
To wait the dawn, and leave the past behind.

###601###
My muse, though slow to stir, and prone to sleep,
Hath found a theme, a blossom fresh and fair,
Whose gentle beauty doth my spirit keep,
And banishes all sorrow and all care.
Her eyes, like stars that pierce the darkest night,
Do hold a gleam that bids my soul to rise,
Her voice, a melody of sweet delight,
Doth charm the very heavens with its sighs.
The rose that blushes on her tender cheek,
Doth shame the dawn, with colours rich and deep,
And all her graces, none can ever speak,
For secrets in her silent heart do sleep.
So let my verse her loveliness embrace,
And consecrate her virtue and her grace.

###602###
When thou dost speak, the very air doth swoon,
And silence waits thy pleasing voice to hear,
As if the sun should yield unto the moon,
And earthly sounds to thy sweet strains appear.
Thy laughter rings, a silver, chiming bell,
That chases all the mournful thoughts away,
And in its music, doth a magic dwell,
That turns the darkest midnight into day.
Thy gentle hand, when it doth rest on mine,
Doth send a tremor through my very frame,
A touch more precious than the purest wine,
That sets my loyal, loving heart aflame.
So let me live, and breathe thy very air,
And in thy presence find my solace there.

###603###
The painted scene, though skilfully it's wrought,
Can ne'er compare to Nature's vibrant hue,
Nor idle words, by practised cunning taught,
Express the truth that in my heart rings true.
For artifice, though pleasing to the eye,
Is but a shadow of the thing it seems,
While genuine affection, by and by,
Doth shine more brightly than the poet's dreams.
Let flatterers their honeyed phrases spend,
And praise the false, with tongue of silver gleam,
My honest love, I shall to thee extend,
A constant, flowing, ever-moving stream.
So judge me not by gaudy outward show,
But by the love that in my bosom grow.

###604###
The fleeting hours, like swift-winged birds do fly,
And steal away the bloom of youth and prime,
Leaving behind a melancholy sigh,
And counting down the weary steps of time.
The raven locks, that once did grace my head,
Now streaked with silver, tell a mournful tale,
Of days long past, and joys now lost and fled,
And strength that doth begin to wax and fail.
Yet in thine eyes, a youthful spark I see,
That mocks the ravages of passing years,
And wakes within my heart a memory,
Of love that conquers all our earthly fears.
So let us seize the moments ere they cease,
And find in shared affection lasting peace.

###605###
When envious tongues do spread their venomous lies,
And whisper slanders to my lady's ear,
I pray she sees the falsehood in their eyes,
And holds my steadfast, faithful love more dear.
For malice oft doth wear a friendly face,
And smiles conceal a heart of bitter gall,
They seek to dim thy bright and noble grace,
And cast a shadow over thee and all.
But let them rave, and let them spread their hate,
Their wicked plots shall come to naught at last,
For truth and love shall triumph over fate,
And every envious dart shall be out-cast.
So turn thy gaze from their deceitful art,
And find sure comfort in my loyal heart.

###606###
The summer's day, though warm and bright it seems,
Must yield at length unto the chilling frost,
And lovers' vows, like fading, idle dreams,
Are by the touch of harsher trials lost.
The rose that blossoms in the morning light,
By evening's chill is withered and undone,
So too, the fire that burns with passion's might,
May fade and die, when harder tasks are spun.
But though the seasons change, and nature wanes,
And earthly beauty cannot long endure,
My love for thee, it evermore remains,
A constant flame, steadfast and ever pure.
So let us build our house on solid ground,
Where faith and constancy shall e'er be found.

###607###
When thoughts of thee do fill my waking mind,
And in my dreams thy image doth appear,
A sweeter solace I can never find,
Than that which from thy gentle presence dear.
The bustling world, with all its toil and strife,
Doth fade away, when I recall thy face,
And in the quiet chambers of my life,
Thy memory doth hold its rightful place.
The stars that twinkle in the vaulted sky,
Do seem but dim, compared unto thine eyes,
And all the joys that earthly men can buy,
Are worth to me far less than thy soft sighs.
So let me dwell, in contemplation deep,
And in thy love, my cherished vigil keep.

###608###
My ink doth falter, and my quill doth pause,
When I would sing thy beauty and thy worth,
For human words are subject to life's laws,
And cannot capture wonders of thy birth.
The finest gems, the rarest, richest gold,
Could ne'er adorn thy virtue and thy grace,
A tale more precious than hath e'er been told,
Is writ upon thy fair and lovely face.
The poet's art, though striving to be grand,
Doth fall so short of what my heart doth feel,
For no mere verse can truly understand,
The heavenly truths that thy sweet presence seal.
So let my silence speak, where words must fail,
And in my heart, thy lasting praise prevail.

###609###
The fleeting smile that dances on thy lip,
Doth banish all the shadows from my soul,
And from thy gaze, my spirit doth not slip,
But yields itself unto thy sweet control.
Thy gentle touch, a balm to every pain,
Doth soothe the wound that sorrow left behind,
And makes my weary, burdened heart again,
With light and joyous gratitude to bind.
The sun itself, though king of all the day,
Doth seem less radiant than thy beaming brow,
And all the world's applause I would not stay,
If I could win thy favour here and now.
So let me bask within thy loving light,
And banish all the darkness from my sight.

###610###
When winter's breath doth chill the very ground,
And barren trees do shiver in the gale,
No comfort in the frozen earth is found,
And all the living world seems faint and pale.
But in my breast, a different season reigns,
A warmth that scorns the sharpest, biting wind,
A love that breaks the icy, winter chains,
And leaves the frost of loneliness behind.
For thou art summer to my frozen heart,
A constant spring, where verdant life doth grow,
And from thy grace, I never shall depart,
As long as in this mortal sphere I go.
So let the world grow cold, and storms may rave,
Thy love shall be the warmth that I do crave.

###611###
The whispered vow, that in the moonlight past,
Was sworn with fervor, strong and true and deep,
Is by the harsh realities out-cast,
When daily cares begin their watch to keep.
For love that blooms in sunshine, fair and bright,
May wither fast when clouds begin to loom,
And passion's fire, that burned with all its might,
May fade and leave behind an empty room.
But ours, my love, is built on firmer stone,
Than shifting sands of passion's fickle tide,
A bond of souls, that shall be ever known,
Where truth and steadfast loyalty do ride.
So let the world test us with storm and strife,
Our love shall be the anchor of our life.

###612###
When time doth steal the colour from thy hair,
And lines of age do furrow thy fair brow,
I shall not find thee changed beyond compare,
But lovelier still, than I do find thee now.
For beauty's bloom is but a fleeting thing,
That fades with years, and cannot long remain,
But true affection, on immortal wing,
Doth grow and deepen, banishing all pain.
The outward show, though pleasing to the eye,
Is but a shell, that time doth soon consume,
While inner worth, that shall not ever die,
Doth shine more brightly, chasing every gloom.
So let us age, and let the years fly past,
My love for thee, eternally shall last.

###613###
The hollow praise, that flatterers do bestow,
Doth ring with falsehood, empty and untrue,
A gilded bait, that doth the unwary know,
And leads them to a doom they can't eschew.
They speak of virtue, when their hearts are base,
And sing of honour, while they plot and scheme,
Their smiles conceal a cold and heartless space,
And all their words are but a waking dream.
But in thy gaze, a honest truth I find,
A gentle soul, that scorns all false pretence,
Thy open heart, to all the world is kind,
And shines with virtue's radiant eloquence.
So let me trust thy pure and noble mind,
And leave the hollow flatterers behind.

###614###
The sun descends, and twilight veils the sky,
And weary mortals seek their welcome rest,
But in my heart, no slumber can I spy,
When thoughts of thee do fill my wakeful breast.
The silent stars, that spangle heaven's dome,
Do witness to the passion I confess,
And in this quiet, I am overcome,
By longing for thy sweet and soft caress.
My soul doth yearn, with ardour ever strong,
To find its haven in thy loving arms,
Where all my worldly troubles shall be gone,
And I be safe from all external harms.
So let me dream of thee, till morning light,
And banish all the shadows of the night.

###615###
When I do gaze upon thy features fair,
And mark the grace that doth thy form adorn,
I feel a sweetness banishing all care,
As if from earthly troubles I were torn.
Thy gentle voice, a melody so sweet,
Doth charm the very air with its soft sound,
And when our eyes in silent converse meet,
A deeper, truer happiness is found.
The rarest flower, that in the garden grows,
Doth not possess such beauty to behold,
Nor doth the richest perfume that it throws,
Compare unto thy spirit, brave and bold.
So let me sing thy praises, day by day,
And chase all lesser, worldly cares away.

###616###
The fleeting moment, swift as summer breeze,
Doth pass us by, and leaves no trace behind,
Unless we hold it fast amongst the trees,
And in our hearts, its precious essence bind.
So too, thy love, a treasure beyond price,
If left to wander, might at last depart,
But I shall guard it with a sacrifice,
And keep it ever fastened to my heart.
Let others chase the phantom of desire,
That burns so bright, and then is quenched and dead,
My steadfast love, a never-dying fire,
Shall warm thee still, when all is cold and dread.
So let us pledge our faith, and hold it fast,
A love that shall forever truly last.

###617###
When in my grief, I feel my spirit sink,
And shadows gather, dark and deep and cold,
Thy gentle presence stands upon the brink,
And makes my weary, trembling heart grow bold.
Thy loving words, like sunbeams, pierce the gloom,
And chase away the spectres of despair,
They light the path, and lead me from the tomb,
And breathe a hope into the heavy air.
The trials that assail me, fierce and strong,
Do seem to lessen, when thou art beside,
And all my burdens that did seem so long,
Are lifted by the turning of the tide.
So let me lean on thee, when woes do press,
And find in thy embrace my happiness.

###618###
The painted sky, though grand its hues may seem,
Is but a canvas, touched by mortal hand,
And all the beauty of a waking dream,
Is transient, fading, built on shifting sand.
But in thine eyes, a truth that shall not fade,
A depth of feeling, honest and sincere,
A love that shall not by the years be swayed,
Nor by the passing moments disappear.
Let worldly praise their empty echoes raise,
And seek the favour of the fickle crowd,
My heart is fixed upon thy nobler ways,
And speaks thy virtues, silently and proud.
So let us shun the false, and hold the true,
My love shall ever be renewed in you.

###619###
The rose doth bloom, and then its petals fall,
The summer's warmth doth yield to winter's chill,
And earthly beauty answers Nature's call,
And beauty's reign must cease, against our will.
But in thy soul, a beauty shall endure,
That time nor season ever can deface,
A gentle spirit, constant, strong, and pure,
That shines with everlasting, heavenly grace.
So let the outward form begin to fade,
And wrinkles trace the story of the years,
My love for thee, shall never be betrayed,
But grow more deep, and banish all my fears.
For in thy heart, a treasure I do find,
That leaves all fleeting, earthly charms behind.

###620###
When silent thoughts of thee do fill my head,
And in my heart a tender warmth doth grow,
I feel the bonds of worldly cares are shed,
And in thy love, a sweeter solace know.
The bustling world, with all its vain pursuit,
Doth seem a distant, unsubstantial thing,
When I recall thy voice, thy gentle root,
From which my happiness doth ever spring.
Thy very presence is a gift divine,
A star that guides me through the darkest night,
And in thy love, my truest joy doth shine,
A beacon burning, ever strong and bright.
So let me dwell, within thy loving gaze,
And spend with thee, my consecrated days.

###621###
When that the sun doth hide his golden face,
And shadows stretch to claim the fading light,
My heart, once filled with joy and sweet embrace,
Now sinks into a melancholy night.
The birds no longer sing their cheerful tune,
But mournful sighs upon the breeze do creep,
As I lament beneath the silent moon,
The promises that you could never keep.
My love, a garden once with blossoms crowned,
Now lies in ruin, withered and forlorn,
Upon this barren and forsaken ground,
Where hope hath perished ere the break of morn.
  So must I weep, until my tears are dry,
  And bid farewell unto my love and I.

###622###
The rose, though fair, doth bear a thorny sting,
And beauty's bloom may quickly fade away,
As summer's warmth gives place to winter's wing,
And all its vibrant colours turn to grey.
So is my love, a fire bright and bold,
That burns with passion, fierce and yet so deep,
But lest it cool, and turn both dead and cold,
I must with constant care its embers keep.
For fickle fortune, with its shifting hand,
Doth oft conspire to blast the fairest flower,
And scatter seeds of sorrow through the land,
To dim the glory of our brightest hour.
  So guard this flame, lest chilling winds descend,
  And bring our loving union to an end.

###623###
When weary thoughts do crowd my troubled mind,
And sleep, that knits the ravished sense to rest,
Doth flee afar, leaving my soul unkind,
To wander lost, with sorrow in my breast.
I turn my gaze unto the starry height,
Where constellations weave a silent tale,
And seek therein a solace in the night,
That may my heavy spirit to thee hail.
For in thy presence, all my woes do cease,
Thy gentle voice, a balm unto my soul,
Doth bring my restless heart a perfect peace,
And makes my fractured spirit once again feel whole.
  So let me dream of thee, till dawn doth break,
  And for thy sweet return, my heart shall ache.

###624###
The fickle world, with all its vain pursuit,
Doth chase after the shadows of desire,
And plucks the tempting, yet the hollow fruit,
And feeds the fleeting, unconsuming fire.
But I, content with what thy love doth give,
Do find a treasure far beyond all price,
And in this simple joy, I truly live,
And scorn the world's deceitful artifice.
Let others hoard their gold and gems untold,
And build their castles on a sandy shore,
My richer mine is in thy heart, I hold,
And ask for nothing, wishing for no more.
  For thee alone, my loyal heart doth beat,
  And finds in thee, its haven, safe and sweet.

###625###
When time, the thief, doth steal our youthful prime,
And furrowed brows and silver hairs do show,
And all our strength doth yield to age and slime,
And from our lips the vibrant colours go.
Yet shall my love, a monument of truth,
Endure the ravages of passing years,
And stand unbent, defying age and ruth,
And banish all our hesitations and our fears.
For though our outward forms may shrink and fade,
And outward beauty take its silent flight,
Within our souls, a lasting love is made,
That shines with ever-constant, brilliant light.
  So let us age, with this our bond so strong,
  And prove that true love lasts, and shall endure long.

###626###
The gentle rain, that falls upon the ground,
Doth feed the earth, and make the flowers grow,
And life renewed, doth everywhere abound,
Where once lay barrenness, and seeds of woe.
So is thy love, a nurturing embrace,
That doth revive my spirit, long since dry,
And brings a smile unto my pallid face,
And bids my weeping, troubled spirit fly.
For in thy kindness, I have found a spring,
Of sweet compassion, pure and ever true,
And from this source, my hopeful heart doth sing,
And renders thanks, my dearest love, to you.
  So let thy grace upon my soul descend,
  And be my constant, ever-faithful friend.

###627###
When envy's serpent doth its poison shed,
And whispers tales of doubt and cruel disdain,
And friendship's bonds are broken, and lie dead,
And trust is lost, and all our hopes are slain.
Then do I find, within thy steadfast gaze,
A shield against the arrows of the foe,
A beacon bright, through life's uncertain maze,
That guides my steps, and bids my courage grow.
For in thy loyalty, I find my strength,
A rock on which my fragile bark can rest,
And though the storm may rage at any length,
Thy faithful heart doth put me to the test.
  So let them rage, their wicked words they fling,
  Thy truth alone, is all my heart doth sing.

###628###
The artist's brush, that daubs with colours bright,
May capture forms, and make the vision real,
But cannot paint the spirit's inner light,
Nor touch the secret thoughts the heart doth feel.
But thou, my love, with eyes that speak so clear,
Dost read my soul, and know its every thought,
Dispelling shadows, chasing every fear,
With understanding, dearly, truly bought.
No artist's hand, though skilled and much admired,
Can sketch the depth of feeling I possess,
For it by thy sweet nature is inspired,
And finds its truth in thy true tenderness.
  So let the world admire what they can see,
  My truest art resides, dear love, in thee.

###629###
The lute doth sing, with music sweet and low,
And stirs the soul, with melodies refined,
But cannot match the joy thy words bestow,
Nor speak the feelings of my loving mind.
For when thou speakest, all the world is hushed,
And in thy voice, a symphony I find,
My weary spirit, by thy words is brushed,
And leaves all earthly cares and woes behind.
Let others seek their pleasure in the sound
Of hollow praise, or fleeting, vain delight,
My dearest music, in thy voice is found,
And banishes the darkness of the night.
  So speak to me, and let thy sweet words flow,
  And in their harmony, my soul shall glow.

###630###
When weary travels bid me seek my rest,
And far from home, my lonely spirit pines,
I dream of thee, and hold thee to my breast,
And trace again thy love's familiar lines.
The foreign lands may hold a passing grace,
And novel sights may for a moment please,
But none can fill thy true and rightful place,
Nor offer comfort, nor my spirit ease.
For thou art home, my harbour, safe and dear,
Where all my longings find their sweet release,
And banish every doubt and every fear,
And grant my troubled, wandering soul its peace.
  So let me journey, though the miles be long,
  My heart's true compass leads me back to thee, where I belong.

###631###
The fleeting moment, like a hurried guest,
Doth scarce arrive, ere it doth take its leave,
And all our present joys are put to test,
As future sorrows we begin to weave.
But in thy love, a constant joy I find,
That doth defy the passage of the years,
A treasure of a rare and precious kind,
That stills my doubts and dries my falling tears.
For though the world may change, and seasons turn,
And fortunes shift, and friends may prove untrue,
Thy constant heart, with steady passion burns,
And shines a guiding star, forever new.
  So let us cling unto this love we share,
  And find eternal solace in its care.

###632###
The subtle poison, of a rumour spread,
May taint the air, and spread a dark mistrust,
And turn the living unto weary dead,
And lay their honest reputations in the dust.
But I have learned, through trials of the past,
To trust the truth, that in thy heart doth lie,
And know thy virtue, destined e'er to last,
And scorn the falsehoods whispered passing by.
Let slanderers their wicked venom vent,
And weave their webs of malice and of spite,
Thy steadfast soul, shall never be thus rent,
But shine with truth, a pure and guiding light.
  So let them speak, their empty words are vain,
  Thy loyal truth shall evermore remain.

###633###
When storms do rage, and winds begin to blow,
And nature's fury shakes the very ground,
And all the world seems filled with fear and woe,
And safety's solace cannot then be found.
Then do I turn unto thy gentle hand,
A steadfast anchor in the raging sea,
And in thy presence, I can bravely stand,
And face the tempest, confident and free.
For thou art strength, when I am weak and frail,
And courage, when my spirit starts to quail,
Thy loving counsel shall for me prevail,
And turn the tide, and make my efforts avail.
  So let the tempest howl, and thunder roar,
  Thy love shall guide me to a peaceful shore.

###634###
The captive bird, within its gilded cage,
Doth beat its wings, and longs for skies so wide,
And reads of freedom on life's written page,
But finds no egress, though it seeks to hide.
So was my soul, ere thou didst set it free,
Confined by doubt, and sorrow's heavy chain,
But thy sweet presence brought a liberty,
And broke the bonds of all my former pain.
Now do I soar, upon the wings of love,
And taste the air of freedom, pure and bright,
Sent from the heavens, from realms above,
And bathed within thy spirit's glorious light.
  So let me fly, and sing thy praises high,
  Beneath the bounty of thy loving sky.

###635###
The miser's hoard, though vast, can bring no ease,
Nor fill the void that hollow riches make,
But leaves him longing, craving more to please,
And for his wealth, his very soul doth shake.
But I have found, a treasure far more grand,
A wealth of love, that cannot be outdone,
Held in the hollow of thy gentle hand,
A boundless fortune, second unto none.
Let others count their ducats, bright and bold,
And hoard their silver, shining in the sun,
My richer store is in thy heart, I hold,
And with thy love, my victory is won.
  So let them hoard, their emptiness they keep,
  My heart's true riches in thy love do sleep.

###636###
When duty calls, and honour bids me go,
To distant lands, or battles to be fought,
My heart doth yearn, and feels a pang of woe,
For absence from the love that I have sought.
But though my feet may tread on foreign soil,
And skies above may wear a different hue,
My steadfast thoughts shall ease the weary toil,
And turn to thee, my dearest love, anew.
For in my mind, thy image shall remain,
A guiding star, to lead me on my way,
And banish all the loneliness and pain,
And bring me back to thee, at close of day.
  So let me strive, and labour, and endure,
  Thy love shall be my solace, ever sure.

###637###
The flickering lamp, that burns with fading light,
Doth cast a shadow, dancing on the wall,
And whispers tales of darkness and of night,
As weary hours do slowly rise and fall.
But thou, my love, art like the steadfast sun,
Whose constant rays do banish every gloom,
And when thy presence is by me outrun,
My spirit sinks, and hastens to its tomb.
So let me bask within thy golden gleam,
And draw my strength from thy effulgent fire,
And live within this sweet and waking dream,
And feed the flames of my intense desire.
  So let thy light upon my soul descend,
  And be my life, my purpose, and my end.

###638###
The painted idol, of a false renown,
May draw the crowds, and win a passing praise,
But crumbles swift, when truth doth cast it down,
And all its hollow glory swiftly decays.
But in thy virtue, I have found a truth,
That stands unwavering, firm, and ever bright,
A genuine love, that knows no age nor youth,
And shines with everlasting, pure delight.
Let others chase the shadows of deceit,
And bow before the idols of their whim,
My worship lies where true affections meet,
And finds its solace, steadfast to the brim.
  So let them bow, their fleeting gods they serve,
  Thy honest heart is all that I preserve.

###639###
When winter's frost doth bind the barren earth,
And naked branches reach towards the sky,
And nature sleeps, devoid of joy and mirth,
And life itself seems destined but to die.
Then doth my love, a spring within my breast,
Begin to bloom, with promise warm and deep,
And in its verdure, I find sweetest rest,
And wake my spirit from its frozen sleep.
For though the outward world may bear a chill,
And outward beauty seem to disappear,
Thy constant love, doth make my spirit thrill,
And banish all the winter's icy fear.
  So let the frost descend, and tempests blow,
  Thy love's warm sun shall make my spirit grow.

###640###
The fleeting dream, that vanishes with dawn,
And leaves the soul with longing and with pain,
A memory of joys that now are gone,
And whispers of what will not come again.
But in thy love, no dream I find, but truth,
A waking reality, so fair and deep,
That doth outshine the fancies of my youth,
And promises that thou alone wilt keep.
For what the dream doth falter and forsake,
Thy constant heart doth steadfastly embrace,
And for thy sweet and everlasting sake,
I find my heaven in this earthly place.
  So let me wake, and live this joy with thee,
  For in thy love, I find true ecstasy.

###641###
Whence comes this shadow that doth chill my soul,
And steal the colour from my summer's day?
No outward cause doth make my spirit roll,
Nor outward foe that I can chase away.
It is a guest within, a subtle blight,
That feeds upon the substance of my peace,
And turns the clearest noon to darkest night,
And grants my troubled thoughts no sweet release.
This inward strife, a war I cannot name,
Doth leave me weary, spent, and much undone,
And mocks my strength with its relentless flame,
Until my very will hath scarce begun.
    Alas, this tempest in a breast so small,
    Doth threaten wholly to consume my all.

###642###
The rose, though fair, must yield unto the frost,
Its blushing beauty wither and decline.
So too, the bloom of youth is often lost,
And leaves behind a wrinkled, faded sign.
The summer's heat, though fervent and so bright,
Will fade to autumn's cool and gentle breeze,
And day must give its place unto the night,
And ancient oaks must fall from mighty trees.
Yet in this flux, this constant ebb and flow,
I find a solace, though it may seem strange,
That change itself doth teach what we should know,
And wisdom grows by every bitter change.
    For in the passing of each fleeting hour,
    We learn the measure of our earthly power.

###643###
Thy gaze, a sun that warms my winter's heart,
Doth chase the lingering shadows from my mind.
With every glance, new joys begin to start,
And all my former griefs I leave behind.
Thy voice, a music sweeter than the lute,
Doth fill my ears with melody and grace,
And makes my sad and weary spirit hoot
With gladness, in this solitary place.
No earthly treasure can with thee compare,
Nor gems that glitter in a king's domain,
For thou art fairer than the morning air,
And brighter than the stars that wax and wane.
    So let me gaze, and let me listen still,
    And drink this nectar, to my spirit's fill.

###644###
What art thou, Love, that holds me in thy sway,
And makes me thine, though reason bids me flee?
Thou art a storm that will not go away,
A sweet delirium that conquers me.
I know thy power, and thy potent dart,
That strikes the soul and leaves it much undone,
And makes a prisoner of a willing heart,
And bids the noblest courage to be run.
Yet in this bondage, I find liberty,
And in this pain, a pleasure I embrace,
For thou art all the world that I can see,
And in thy presence, I find my true place.
    So let me burn, and let me suffer still,
    For in thy flames, my soul doth find its will.

###645###
The fickle moon, that doth reflect the sun,
Doth change her face with every passing phase.
And so, my love, thy constancy is run,
And thou art lost within a misty haze.
One day thou art my sun, my guiding star,
The next, a cloud that hides thee from my sight.
And though I seek thee, near and yet afar,
Thy promise fades into the fading light.
I know not where thy wandering foot may stray,
Nor what new fancy doth thy heart beguile,
But this I know, thou lead'st me far astray,
And mock'st my faith with every fickle smile.
    So fare thee well, thou ever-changing one,
    My weary race with thee is now undone.

###646###
When envious Time, with his destructive hand,
Shall steal the bloom from out thy youthful cheek,
And leave thee bare upon this barren land,
And all thy former glories thou shalt seek,
Then wilt thou know the worth of loyal love,
That stood beside thee in thy brightest hour,
And did not flee, as doth the timid dove,
When tempests rage and show their fearful power.
My love for thee, no season can decay,
No winter chill can make its warmth grow less,
But like the sun, it shines both night and day,
And doth thy future happiness confess.
    So fear not Time, nor all his bitter sting,
    For in my heart, eternal spring I bring.

###647###
The fool doth prate of wisdom, bold and loud,
And thinks his babbling doth the world enlighten.
He stands within the ignorant, proud crowd,
And seeks his own false glory to heighten.
He knows not depth, nor yet the subtle art
Of understanding what is truly wise,
But judges all with a deluded heart,
And sees but shadows with his clouded eyes.
I pity him, this creature of the day,
Who treads the path of vanity and pride,
And cannot see the truth that lights the way,
Nor where his errant footsteps truly guide.
    For wisdom's seed in humble soil is sown,
    And by the quiet heart it is made known.

###648###
This earthly life, a stage where all do play,
A fleeting show, a shadow of the real.
We strut and fret our hour, then pass away,
And leave no trace of what we truly feel.
The joy we chase, the sorrows that we bear,
Are but illusions in this mortal dream.
The sun that shines, the rain that fills the air,
Are but a part of Nature's passing stream.
Yet in this dream, I find a deeper truth,
A love that binds, a spirit that transcends,
And though I fade, as doth the bloom of youth,
My soul's true essence never truly ends.
    For in the fleetingness of all we see,
    A spark of God resides eternally.

###649###
My pen, though tasked to sing thy wondrous praise,
Doth falter, finding words too weak to tell
The heaven's light that beams from thy dear gaze,
Or all the magic that within thee dwell.
The sweetest muse, the one that doth inspire,
Could not with all her skill achieve this feat,
To capture flames of such intense desire,
Or paint a portrait that is truly sweet.
Thou art a vision, beyond mortal ken,
A perfect form, a soul of purest gold,
And more divine than any work of men,
A story that can never be outtold.
    So let me fail, and let my verse be poor,
    If it but whispers what I do adore.

###650###
The bitter draught of parting I must take,
And bid farewell to thee, my dearest friend.
My heart doth ache, and for thy absence quake,
As summer's glory finds its sudden end.
No longer shall we walk in sunlit fields,
Or share our thoughts beneath the moon's soft gleam,
But silence now my lonely spirit wields,
And waking hours are but a mournful dream.
Yet in my breast, thy memory shall reside,
A shining beacon in the darkest night,
And though the miles may cruelly divide,
Our souls remain united, pure and bright.
    So go in peace, and know my love runs deep,
    A constant vow that I shall ever keep.

###651###
When fortune smiles, and all the world seems fair,
And golden joys do fill my waking hours,
I cast aside all doubt and every care,
And bask beneath the sun's most radiant powers.
But when the clouds do gather, dark and grim,
And tempests rage, and fortune turns her face,
Then doth despair my weary spirit dim,
And leave me lost in sorrow's bleak embrace.
I know this change, this turning of the tide,
Is but the way of all that doth exist,
And yet I find no solace deep inside,
When fate's cold hand doth give me such a twist.
    For though I strive, and though I play my part,
    I am a vessel, tossed by wind and art.

###652###
The silent night, a cloak of deepest black,
Doth hide the world from my discerning eye.
No star doth guide me on my lonely track,
No moonbeam shows me where my footsteps lie.
Yet in this dark, I feel a presence near,
A whispered comfort, though no voice I hear.
It is thy spirit, banishing all fear,
And drawing me to thee, my love so dear.
Though absent now, thy essence fills the air,
A scent of roses, delicate and sweet.
And though I cannot see thee standing there,
I feel thy presence, making life complete.
    So let the darkness hold me in its keep,
    While in thy love, my faithful heart doth sleep.

###653###
What madness drives me, that I chase a shade,
And build my hopes on futures yet unseen?
My fondest dreams, like morning mist, do fade,
And leave me longing for what might have been.
I waste my days in fruitless, vain pursuit,
And chase a phantom that I cannot grasp.
The bitter fruit of failure is my fruit,
And sorrow's chains do hold me in their clasp.
Yet still I strive, with spirit undeterred,
And though I fall, I rise to try again,
For in my heart, a whisper can be heard,
That whispers hope, and bids me not complain.
    So let me chase, though loss may be my gain,
    And find my strength within this constant pain.

###654###
Thy beauty shines, a beacon in the night,
And guides my soul unto a safer shore.
No earthly lamp can match its radiant light,
Nor can my weary spirit ask for more.
The roses blush, and lilies pale in shame,
When set against the glories of thy face.
And all the stars do seem a lesser flame,
Compared to thy celestial, winning grace.
I gaze upon thee, lost in sweet amaze,
And feel my heart with adoration swell.
And in the rapture of these passing days,
I find a heaven where my spirit dwell.
    So let me worship, and let me adore,
    This perfect vision, now and evermore.

###655###
The fleeting hours, like sand within the glass,
Do slip away, and leave no trace behind.
So too, our youth, it doth too quickly pass,
And leaves but memories for us to find.
The bloom of cheek, the vigour of the limb,
The eager spirit, quick to laugh and play,
All fade and wither, growing faint and dim,
And turn to dust upon a future day.
Yet in this passing, I find solace deep,
That age doth bring a wisdom hard to gain,
And though the joys of youth I cannot keep,
A quieter peace doth in my spirit reign.
    For in the fading, we do learn to see,
    The timeless truth of what we truly be.

###656###
When slander's tongue doth wag with venomous spite,
And whispers falsehoods in the public ear,
It strikes the soul with an unholy blight,
And fills the honest heart with bitter fear.
The innocent man, though pure in all his ways,
May fall a victim to the serpent's hiss,
And lose the favour of his former days,
And suffer shame for deeds he did not kiss.
No shield can guard against this poisoned dart,
No plea can turn the tide of wicked tongues.
It festers deep within the wounded heart,
And breeds a sorrow that forever stings.
    Alas, that malice should so strongly reign,
    And innocent worth be sullied by such stain.

###657###
My love for thee, a river strong and deep,
Doth flow with passion, constant and so true.
No drought can dry the vows that I do keep,
No winter chill can make its warmth untrue.
It was not born of fleeting, outward show,
Nor of a fancy, that doth quickly fade,
But from a root that doth securely grow,
Within the soul, where true affections made.
And though the world may seek to tear us hence,
Or envious stars conspire to make us part,
My steadfast love shall be thy strong defence,
And hold thee ever in my faithful heart.
    So let the years their onward course pursue,
    My love for thee shall ever be anew.

###658###
The mimic's art, that doth with skill portray
The passions that within the human breast
Do burn and rage, then slowly die away,
And leave the actors weary and at rest.
He wears the mask, and speaks the borrowed word,
And feigns a joy, or sorrow, deep and keen.
His very soul by artifice is stirred,
And what he shows is but a painted scene.
Yet in this play, I see a truth unfold,
That life itself is but a fleeting stage,
And all our acts, however brave and bold,
Are writ upon a transient, mortal page.
    So let us play, with all our might and main,
    And find our meaning in the joy and pain.

###659###
When I behold thy face, so fair and bright,
A heavenly vision, sent from realms above,
My mortal senses are o'ercome with light,
And all my soul doth melt in purest love.
No earthly gem, nor treasure of the mine,
Can match the lustre of thine eyes so clear,
Nor can the sun itself with thee combine,
To cast a radiance that is half so dear.
Thou art the star that guides my wandering way,
The sweetest music that my ear doth hear,
And in thy presence, darkness turns to day,
And all my earthly troubles disappear.
    So let me gaze, and let my spirit fly,
    And find my solace in the light of thine eye.

###660###
The cruel hand of Time, that doth command
All mortal things to wither and decay,
