Doth steal the vigour from my weary hand,
And turn my sunlit noon to fading day.
My strength departs, my youthful ardour flown,
And in its place, a weariness doth creep,
And all the joys that I had lately known,
Are lost in shadows, while the world doth sleep.
Yet though I fade, and though my vigour wanes,
My love for thee shall ever brightly burn,
A constant flame that conquers all my pains,
And to thy heart, my faithful spirit turn.
    So let Time work his will with all his might,
    My love for thee shall be my guiding light.

###661###
When that my love doth shine with eyes so bright,
My soul doth soar on wings of purest joy,
And banish thence all shadows of the night,
No worldly care can my true heart annoy.
Her gentle voice, a melody so sweet,
Doth charm mine ear and make my spirit sing,
And when our parted lips do softly meet,
A heaven on earth my senses then doth bring.
But ah, this bliss, like dew upon the rose,
Doth fade and vanish with the rising sun,
And leave my heart in sorrow as it goes,
My happy moments all too swiftly run.
So let me dream, though waking bring despair,
Of love's sweet kiss, beyond all earthly care.

###662###
The fleeting hours do steal my youth away,
And furrow'd brow doth speak of passing years,
Where once did bloom the summer of my day,
Now winter chills my heart and brings forth tears.
My strength doth wane, my vigour starts to flee,
And grey hairs crown where raven locks did gleam,
No more the fire that burn'd so strong in me,
But ember faint, a dying, fading dream.
Yet still my love, a beacon in the gloom,
Doth light my path and guide me to the shore,
Dispelling shadows of impending doom,
And making life worth living evermore.
So let me live, though time doth mark my face,
Held fast within thy warm and dear embrace.

###663###
When that the moon doth cast its silver light,
Upon the slumbering world with gentle grace,
My restless thoughts do wander through the night,
And seek the solace of thy absent face.
The silent stars, like diamonds in the sky,
Do seem to mock my solitary plight,
As lonely winds do whisper with a sigh,
And steal the comfort from the fading light.
Oh, could I but, by magic or by art,
Transport myself to where thou dost reside,
And mend the aching of my lonely heart,
Where in thy arms I might forever hide.
But cruel distance, like a barren wall,
Doth keep me hence, and makes my spirit fall.

###664###
My muse, whose fire doth often brightly burn,
Now seems to slumber, cold and quite forgot,
To her sweet strains my weary ears do turn,
But find no comfort in the song she taught.
The words that once did flow with ease and might,
Now stumble forth, like beggars at the gate,
And dim the lustre of my former light,
As if consign'd to some unhappy fate.
I try to weave a tapestry of praise,
To sing thy virtues, matchless and divine,
But find my skill doth falter in these days,
And lose the thread of what I would entwine.
Yet for thy sake, I'll strive with all my power,
To capture beauty in this barren hour.

###665###
Thy laughter, like a brook that gently flows,
Doth wash away the cares that vex my soul,
And in its music, all my spirit grows,
And makes me feel as though I were made whole.
Thy eyes, like stars that pierce the darkest sky,
Do shed a radiance, pure and ever bright,
And when I gaze, I cannot help but sigh,
And drink my fill of that celestial light.
The simple touch of thy most tender hand,
Doth send a tremor through my very frame,
And makes me feel I truly understand,
The fiery passion of love's ardent flame.
So let me live, and in thy presence dwell,
Wherein my heart shall find its sweetest spell.

###666###
The cruel world doth judge with hasty eye,
And speaketh ill of those it doth not know,
It buildeth walls and casts a watchful spy,
On every seed of goodness that doth grow.
They see the faults, the blemishes, the flaws,
And magnify them with their bitter tongue,
Ignoring all the virtue and the cause,
That in the heart of gentleness is sung.
But thou, my love, dost see with deeper sight,
And lookest past the surface to the core,
And findest beauty, hidden from the light,
That others scorn and evermore ignore.
So let them rage, with malice in their breast,
Thy faithful heart shall find its rightful rest.

###667###
When Fortune smiles, and all the world doth seem,
A tapestry of joy and sweet delight,
My heart doth revel in this happy dream,
And banish thence all shadows of the night.
But ah, how fickle is her golden face,
How swift she turns, and leaves me in the dust,
Deprived of comfort, and of all my grace,
And broken by her unpredictable gust.
So let me not, in moments of good cheer,
Forget the tempest that may soon arrive,
But hold my love more precious and more dear,
For in its strength, my spirit shall survive.
For though the world may shift and change its hue,
My constant heart shall ever beat for you.

###668###
The summer's heat doth scorch the thirsty ground,
And weary travellers seek the cooling shade,
No gentle breeze, no solace can be found,
As nature's strength begins to slowly fade.
The rivers dwindle, and the streams run dry,
The leaves do wither on the barren bough,
And all creation seems to heave a sigh,
Beneath the sun's oppressive, burning brow.
But in thy presence, I find sweet relief,
A cooling balm unto my fevered mind,
Thy love doth banish all my worldly grief,
And leave all earthly troubles far behind.
So let the summer rage with fiery might,
Thy gentle spirit is my pure delight.

###669###
My love for thee, a garden richly sown,
Doth bloom with colours vibrant and so rare,
Each tender bud, to thee alone is shown,
And nurtured by my ever-watchful care.
The thorns that threaten, and the weeds that strive,
To choke the growth of beauty and of truth,
Are vanquished by the passion that doth thrive,
And find their end in everlasting youth.
Let others seek their solace in the fleeting,
In shallow pleasures, that do quickly die,
My steadfast heart, its constant tribute greeting,
Shall offer thee its love until I die.
For in this bloom, no season can decay,
Thy beauty shines, and brightens every day.

###670###
The poet's pen, though dipped in ink so black,
Doth strive to capture beauty, pure and true,
But finds the words do often turn their back,
And fail to paint the wonders of my view.
Thy countenance, a masterpiece divine,
Doth far surpass the art that man can make,
No human skill can truly intertwine,
The perfect lines that heaven did awake.
My verses falter, and my rhymes are weak,
When I attempt thy loveliness to tell,
The very essence that my soul doth seek,
Is held within thy captivating spell.
So let me love thee, though my words may fail,
Thy grace shall evermore my soul prevail.

###671###
When winter's chill doth bite with icy breath,
And nature sleeps beneath a shroud of white,
My spirit warms, defying death and death,
And finds its comfort in thy loving light.
The barren trees, with branches stark and bare,
Do speak of sorrow, and of hopes long gone,
But in thy eyes, I find a solace rare,
A sun that shines from dusk until the dawn.
The hearth may fade, the embers turn to grey,
And outward warmth may vanish from the room,
But in thy heart, I find a brighter ray,
That banishes the cold and chases gloom.
So let the world be clad in frosty guise,
My dearest love, the warmth within thine eyes.

###672###
The envious eye doth ever seek to find,
A flaw, a fault, a weakness to expose,
And whisper rumours of a wicked kind,
To wound the heart that in true virtue grows.
They cannot bear to see a spirit bright,
Or kindness shown, or mercy freely lent,
Their souls are clad in everlasting night,
And with their spite, their bitter lives are spent.
But thou, my love, art free from such dark stain,
Thy soul is pure, thy heart is strong and true,
And though the world may seek to cause thee pain,
My steadfast love shall ever see thee through.
So let them carp, with malice in their gaze,
Thy inner worth outshines their envious haze.

###673###
The fleeting moments, like a whispered dream,
Do pass us by, and leave us in the past,
We grasp for them, a swift and fading gleam,
But find their hold is never meant to last.
The joys of youth, the vigour of our prime,
Do vanish swiftly, like a summer's day,
And leave us old, upon the shores of time,
With naught but memories to light our way.
So let us seize the present, ere it flies,
And hold our loved ones ever in our breast,
For in their arms, true happiness doth rise,
And find within their warmth its sweetest rest.
Let not a single precious hour be lost,
But cherish love, whatever be the cost.

###674###
My weary soul, when tossed by worldly strife,
Doth seek a haven, peaceful and serene,
And in the quiet solace of thy life,
I find the calm that I have ever been.
The clamour of the crowd, the harsh retort,
The endless striving, and the bitter fray,
Do fade away, when thou art in my fort,
And chase the shadows of my doubts away.
Thy gentle spirit, like a summer breeze,
Doth cool the fever of my troubled mind,
And in thy presence, I can find my ease,
And leave all worldly vexations far behind.
So let me dwell within thy tranquil sphere,
And banish thence all anxious doubt and fear.

###675###
The ink doth dry, the parchment doth grow old,
And paper perishes, though held with care,
So too, the tales that poets have retold,
May fade and vanish into empty air.
The finest verse, the most impassioned plea,
May lose its lustre, and its former might,
As time doth work its subtle victory,
And dim the brilliance of its former light.
But thou, my love, a treasure beyond price,
Dost hold within thee virtues that endure,
And though the world may change, and times entice,
Thy constant heart remains for ever pure.
So let my verse, though frail, thy praises tell,
Thy lasting beauty shall forever dwell.

###676###
When doubt doth cloud my mind, and fears arise,
And make me question all that I hold dear,
I turn to thee, and gaze into thine eyes,
And find the strength to banish every fear.
Thy gentle wisdom, like a guiding star,
Doth pierce the darkness of my troubled thought,
And show me paths where dangers are afar,
And lessons that my soul has dearly sought.
Thou art my anchor, in the storm's wild blast,
My steadfast rock, when tempests rage and roar,
And in thy love, my spirit finds at last,
The peaceful harbour that I do adore.
So let me cling to thee, my guiding light,
And find in thee my solace and my might.

###677###
The rose doth bloom, a marvel to behold,
With petals soft, and fragrance sweet and rare,
But soon its beauty shall begin to fold,
And yield to winter's harsh and chilling air.
The lily white, that stands so proud and tall,
Shall wither too, and bow its gentle head,
As nature answers to the season's call,
And life's bright colours turn to grey instead.
But in thy face, a beauty I do find,
That time itself can never hope to mar,
A constant grace, that leaves the world behind,
And shines more brightly than the morning star.
So let the flowers fade, and seasons wane,
Thy loveliness shall evermore remain.

###678###
When folly tempts, and reason starts to stray,
And leads my heart down paths of dark despair,
Thy voice doth call, and turn me from the way,
And guide me back to virtue's purer air.
The siren song of pleasure, sweet and low,
Doth lure the soul to depths of endless night,
But in thy counsel, seeds of wisdom grow,
And lead me forth into the sun's warm light.
Thou art the balm that heals my wounded pride,
The gentle hand that lifts me from the mire,
And in thy love, I can securely hide,
And quench the flames of uncontrolled desire.
So let me heed thy wisdom, pure and deep,
And in thy steadfast love my soul shall keep.

###679###
The tongue of man, a weapon sharp and keen,
Doth often wound where no true fault is found,
And speaketh ill of things it hath not seen,
And scatters poison on the fertile ground.
It builds its castles on a shifting sand,
And judges all with prejudice and scorn,
Ignoring deeds that grace the helping hand,
And sowing seeds of discord ere the morn.
But thou, my love, dost judge with heart so true,
And see the worth that lies beneath the show,
And lend thy favour, ever kind and new,
To those that good and honest actions sow.
So let the slanderers their malice spew,
Thy honest soul shall ever shine anew.

###680###
My love for thee, a river deep and wide,
Doth flow for aye, with current strong and sure,
And though the world may seek to turn its tide,
My faithful heart shall evermore endure.
The storms of life may rage, the winds may blow,
And threaten to divert its steadfast course,
But still its waters shall serenely flow,
And find its strength in its own hidden source.
No earthly power can its passage stay,
No drought can cause its vibrant flow to cease,
It washes all my weary doubts away,
And brings my troubled spirit inner peace.
So let me drown within this loving stream,
And live forever in this blissful dream.

###681###
When Phoebus doth his golden chariot guide,
And wakes the world with his celestial fire,
My drowsy heart, which slumber did provide,
Doth feel a stir of passionate desire.
The birds do sing their matins in the trees,
A joyful choir to greet the dawning light,
But whilst I lie in such a sweet unease,
My inward thoughts do war with morning bright.
For though the sun doth banish all the shade,
And paint the skies with hues of rose and gold,
My own dark soul, by loving thee, is swayed,
And in thy absence, feels a chilling cold.
    So let me dream of thee ere day doth break,
    And find in slumber, what I cannot wake.

###682###
Thy beauty shines, a star in night's dark dome,
A beacon to my lost and wandering soul,
Which, tossed by tempests, seeks its rightful home,
And finds in thee its haven and its goal.
The ocean waves that beat upon the shore,
Do whisper tales of journeys far and wide,
But none so fair as what I do adore,
The gentle grace that doth within thee bide.
If I were given wings to fly the air,
And soar above the mountains and the seas,
My flight would end, when I did find thee there,
My heart's true queen, my solace and my ease.
    So let me gaze upon thy visage bright,
    And lose myself within thy loving light.

###683###
The creeping vine that doth the ancient wall
Embrace with tendrils, strong and firmly bound,
Doth mirror how my affections do enthral,
And tie my spirit to thy sacred ground.
The sturdy oak, that hath for ages stood,
And weathered storms with unyielding might,
Doth teach me how my love, misunderstood,
Endures through darkness and through fading light.
For though the world may frown with envious gaze,
And whisper slanders that do wound and sting,
My steadfast heart, through all its changing days,
To thee alone its truest tribute brings.
    So let me cleave to thee, as ivy clings,
    And find in thee the peace that my heart sings.

###684###
When springtime doth with verdant fingers tread,
And paint the meadows with a thousand flowers,
My heart doth bloom, by thy sweet image led,
And finds its joy in those enchanted hours.
The gentle breeze that stirs the leafy boughs,
Doth carry whispers of a love untold,
And in my breast, a burning passion vows,
A tale of devotion, brave and bold.
If I were but a river, flowing free,
My course would bend to seek thy ocean's breast,
And in thy depths, I would find unity,
And grant my weary spirit sweetest rest.
    So let me be thy stream, thy loving tide,
    And in thy boundless heart forever ride.

###685###
The fading sun, that sinks beyond the west,
And leaves the world to twilight's sombre hue,
Doth make my weary spirit seek for rest,
And long for solace that is found in you.
The moon, that rises, pale and softly bright,
Doth cast a gentle glow on sleeping earth,
But cannot match the radiance of thy light,
Or grant my soul its true and deepest worth.
If I could conjure dreams from starry skies,
Or weave a spell with words of silver gleam,
I would reflect the wonder in thine eyes,
And capture all within a waking dream.
    So let me dwell within thy memory's hold,
    A tale of love, more precious far than gold.

###686###
The fragile bloom that opens to the day,
And sheds its petals with the fleeting breeze,
Doth teach me how my mortal joys decay,
And leave me sighing 'neath the somber trees.
The summer's heat, that burns with fiery zest,
Doth fade and yield to autumn's chilling air,
And all that seemed secure and truly blest,
Doth vanish, leaving naught but dark despair.
But if thy love, a constant star, doth shine,
No season's change can dim its ardent flame,
And though my form to dust shall soon decline,
My spirit shall forever speak thy name.
    So let me hold thee close, ere life departs,
    And engrave thy image on my beating hearts.

###687###
The chirping cricket, in the summer's night,
Doth sing a song of simple, sweet delight,
But my poor heart, that trembles at thy sight,
Doth find no peace, nor slumber, nor respite.
The stars do twinkle, in their vast array,
And shed a silver magic on the land,
But they cannot a single care allay,
Nor ease the burning passion of my hand.
If I were a sculptor, skilled and true,
I'd carve thy likeness in the purest stone,
And gaze forever on the form of you,
A masterpiece, to me and me alone.
    But alas, I am but man, with mortal plea,
    To beg thy favour, and to worship thee.

###688###
The winter's frost, that binds the frozen stream,
And silences the music of the spring,
Doth mirror well my solitary dream,
And all the lonely suffering I bring.
The barren branches, reaching to the sky,
Doth show my soul, devoid of summer's grace,
And as the weary seasons hasten by,
I find no comfort, nor a resting place.
Yet, in my heart, a hidden warmth I keep,
A spark of hope, that will not be denied,
That when my frozen spirit wakes from sleep,
Thy loving glance shall be my guiding guide.
    So let me brave the cold, and wait for thee,
    My sun, my spring, my only joy to be.

###689###
The sturdy bridge, that spans the raging flood,
And bears the traveller safe to yonder shore,
Doth teach me how my love, though often rude,
Can conquer obstacles and ask for more.
The ancient shield, that hath a warrior's might,
And turned aside the keenest, sharpest steel,
Doth symbolize my resolute delight,
And all the wounds that thy dear eyes do heal.
If I were a captain, on the open sea,
And storms did rage, and tempests did conspire,
My compass true, would ever point to thee,
My sole desire, my soul's enduring fire.
    So let me be thy ship, and thee my star,
    And sail through all, no matter how afar.

###690###
The golden coin, that doth the merchant's hand
Enrich with wealth, and buy him earthly gain,
Is worthless, when I seek to understand,
The priceless treasure that thy love doth reign.
The jeweled crown, that doth adorn the king,
And grants him power, majesty, and might,
Can not the joyous melody e'er sing,
That fills my heart, when bathed in thy pure light.
If I were a monarch, on a distant throne,
And all the kingdoms of the world were mine,
I'd gladly yield them, for a love unknown,
The sweet affection that is so divine.
    So let me be thy subject, and thy slave,
    And in thy loving service, find my grave.

###691###
The fleeting moment, like a hummingbird,
Doth hover near, and then doth swiftly fly,
And every sigh, and every whispered word,
Doth vanish, ere I know the reason why.
The scent of roses, on the evening air,
Doth linger briefly, then doth fade away,
And leaves behind a silence and despair,
That marks the passing of a precious day.
Yet, in my mind, thy image is impressed,
A vibrant hue, that time cannot erase,
And though the world may fade, and be undressed,
Thy loveliness shall hold its rightful place.
    So let me cling to thee, in memory's hold,
    A story that shall never grow too old.

###692###
The restless waves, that beat upon the strand,
And never cease their murmuring and flow,
Doth mirror well my heart, by love unmanned,
And all the constant longing that doth grow.
The hungry wolf, that prowls the lonely wood,
And seeks his prey with hunger in his eyes,
Doth not compare to where my soul hath stood,
A captive bound, beneath thy sweet surprise.
If I were granted but a single wish,
To grant my heart its ultimate desire,
I'd ask to be within thy loving dish,
And nourished by thy ever-burning fire.
    So let me be thy feast, thy willing prey,
    And in thy boundless love, I'll gladly stay.

###693###
The shepherd's pipe, that plays a simple tune,
And soothes the flock, beneath the summer's sun,
Doth not compare, though played beneath the moon,
To melodies thy gentle voice hath spun.
The rustling leaves, that whisper in the breeze,
And tell of secrets to the listening ear,
Doth not compare to sweet felicitous ease,
When thy dear words my anxious spirit cheer.
If I were a painter, with a skilful hand,
I'd capture all the beauty of thy face,
And make it known throughout this mortal land,
Thy peerless charm, thy captivating grace.
    But words are weak, and colours cannot vie,
    With the true vision of thy loving eye.

###694###
The sturdy ship, that bravely rides the storm,
And bears its cargo safe to distant lands,
Doth not protect my frail and beating form,
From tempests brewed by thy commanding hands.
The fortress wall, that stands with might and pride,
And guards the city from the foeman's blow,
Can not my secret longing truly hide,
Nor make my ardent admiration slow.
If I were a poet, with a lofty mind,
I'd weave a verse, immortal and sublime,
To tell the world what wonders I do find,
In thee, my love, beyond the reach of time.
    But though my verse be humble, and my plea,
    My heart's true homage shall belong to thee.

###695###
The faithful dog, that waits beside his lord,
And greets him home with wagging tail and leap,
Doth not possess the love that I have stored,
Within my breast, where precious memories sleep.
The blooming rose, that opens to the morn,
And sheds its fragrance on the passing air,
Doth not compare to thee, who art, since born,
The fairest flower, beyond all mortal compare.
If I were a craftsman, with a cunning art,
I'd fashion thee a throne of purest gold,
And place thee there, the monarch of my heart,
A tale of love, forever to be told.
    So let me serve thee, as a loyal knight,
    And find my solace in thy radiant light.

###696###
The winter's snow, that blankets all the land,
And stills the world with silent, soft embrace,
Doth not impart a peace to my command,
Nor bring a smile unto my weary face.
The frozen river, bound with icy chain,
Doth not reflect the turmoil in my breast,
Where passions rage, and hopes do wax and wane,
And grant my troubled spirit any rest.
Yet, in my soul, a single wish doth burn,
To feel the warmth of thy returning smile,
And from thy love, my frozen heart to turn,
And walk with thee, for many a happy mile.
    So let me dream of spring, and of thy grace,
    And find in thee, my season and my place.

###697###
The humming bee, that gathers nectar sweet,
From every flower, with industrious toil,
Doth not compare to what my senses meet,
When thy dear presence doth my spirit spoil.
The rippling brook, that babbles on its way,
And sings a song of ever-flowing glee,
Doth not convey the joy that doth hold sway,
When my fond gaze is fixed alone on thee.
If I were a master, of the spoken word,
I'd praise thy virtues, with a voice so clear,
That all the world would know, and be assured,
Of the true worth of what I hold so dear.
    But words are feeble, when compared to thee,
    My life, my love, my soul's eternity.

###698###
The shifting sands, that drift upon the shore,
And change their form with every passing tide,
Doth not possess the constancy I swore,
When in thy loving gaze I did confide.
The fragile glass, that shatters at a touch,
And leaves behind a thousand jagged shards,
Doth not reflect the pain that I feel much,
When thy sweet glance my hopeful heart discards.
Yet, if my love, like diamond, firm and true,
Can never break, nor ever lose its gleam,
Then let me offer all I am to you,
And live forever in this waking dream.
    So let me be thy rock, thy steadfast ground,
    Wherein thy purest happiness is found.

###699###
The summer's heat, that doth the landscape bake,
And leave the earth in thirst, with cracking soil,
Doth not compare to fires that do wake,
Within my breast, and set my soul to toil.
The hungry lion, with his fearsome roar,
Doth not inspire the terror that I feel,
When I do think of what I do adore,
And fear thy absence, and thy stern repeal.
If I were given strength, beyond my might,
To face all perils, and to conquer fear,
My greatest battle would be for thy light,
To keep thee ever, ever, ever near.
    So let me be thy shield, thy loyal guard,
    And bear all wounds, though they be sharp and hard.

###700###
The fading embers, in the hearth's cold grate,
Doth speak of warmth, that now hath passed away,
And leaves behind the cold and lonely state,
That marks the ending of a brighter day.
The silent owl, that watches from the tree,
With knowing gaze, upon the sleeping world,
Doth not perceive the sorrow that holds me,
As by thy absence, my own soul is hurled.
Yet, if thy love, a never-dying flame,
Can banish shadows, and the night dispel,
Then let me whisper low thy precious name,
And in thy glowing heart forever dwell.
    So let me be thy flame, thy steady light,
    And banish from my soul all earthly night.

###701###
When Phoebus doth his golden chariot drive,
And banisheth the shadows of the night,
My waking soul begins itself to thrive,
And drinks the sun's most gladdening light.
But ere that beam on weary eyelids fall,
My dreams, like spectres, haunt my troubled breast,
And whisper fears that hold my heart in thrall,
Denying slumber, peace, and needed rest.
So is my day with ghostly visions marred,
As if a midnight shade did cling to me,
My waking joys by phantom pains are barred,
And freedom's gate is locked, I cannot flee.
   Yet hope shall dawn, though present darkness reign,
   And chase away this melancholy's pain.

###702###
The painted bloom that doth the spring adorn,
And scents the air with perfumes passing sweet,
Too soon shall see its tender petals torn,
And lie as dust beneath the hurried feet.
The summer's sun, that warms the fertile earth,
And bids the tender shoots to rise and grow,
Shall yield its strength and shrink from winter's birth,
And cast a pale and melancholy glow.
So youth and beauty, though they seem so bright,
Are but a flicker, ere they fade away,
And manhood's power, and wisdom's learned might,
Must bow at last to time's relentless sway.
   Then let us live and love whilst we have power,
   And seize the joy of every fleeting hour.

###703###
My love, like to a river, deep and wide,
Doth bear me onward with its constant flow,
No earthly shore can cause its course to slide,
Nor shall its destined destination know.
It doth not ebb with fickle fortune's tide,
Nor freeze when winter's chilling winds do blow,
But ever onward, resolute, doth stride,
And in its depths, a steadfast purpose show.
Though tempest-tossed, and rocks may block its way,
It finds new channels, ever onward pressed,
And shall not cease, until the final day,
When all is stillness, and it finds its rest.
   So may my heart, in love's embrace so sure,
   Forever beat, and through all trials endure.

###704###
The silent stars, that in the heavens gleam,
And watch the turning world with patient eye,
Do seem to mock my solitary dream,
And whisper tales of joys I can't descry.
For whilst they shine, a beacon in the black,
My own poor spirit finds no guiding ray,
But treads a lost and solitary track,
And wanders blindly through the darkened way.
I gaze upon their distant, cold abode,
And yearn for company, a kindred soul,
But find myself upon a lonely road,
Where no warm hand doth comfort or console.
   O cruel fate, that leaves me thus alone,
   To feel the pangs of sorrow, deeply sown.

###705###
When I behold thy countenance so fair,
A sudden flush doth paint my pallid cheek,
And all my thoughts are lost beyond repair,
And I, poor wretch, no eloquent words can speak.
Thy voice, a music that doth fill the air,
Doth make my spirit tremble, frail and weak,
And in thy gaze, I find a wondrous snare,
Wherein my captive heart doth meekly seek.
Thou art the sun that banishes my gloom,
The moon that guides my passage through the night,
The fragrant flower that doth my senses bloom,
And fills my world with all its purest light.
   So shall I worship thee, my goddess dear,
   And hold thee ever in my heart so near.

###706###
The fickle wind, that doth at pleasure blow,
And stirs the leaves upon the forest trees,
Can change its course, and swiftly onward go,
And leave behind no lingering unease.
So is the love of many, weak and low,
That shrinks and flees from every passing breeze,
And when adversity begins to grow,
They cast it off, and seek their selfish ease.
But mine, my love, is of a sturdier kind,
That fears no storm, nor shrinks from winter's chill,
A steadfast flame, that shall not be confined,
But burn with constant passion, strong and still.
   So let the doubters waver and depart,
   My truest love resides within my heart.

###707###
My pen, a weapon sharp against the wrong,
Doth strive to right the wrongs that men commit,
And in its strokes, though humble, yet so strong,
A righteous fury doth forever sit.
I'll wield it bravely, where the shadows throng,
And pierce the darkness, bit by painful bit,
And sing a song, a noble, valiant song,
That shall with truth and justice brightly lit.
Let tyrants quake, and wicked souls despair,
When truth's bright banner doth itself unfurl,
I'll face them boldly, with a righteous stare,
And with my words, the very world will whirl.
   So let my ink a cleansing river be,
   And wash away all foul iniquity.

###708###
The fleeting hours, that steal our youth away,
And wrinkle brows where once smooth skin did lie,
Do mark the progress of our briefest day,
And bid us cease our labours, and to die.
The strength of manhood, and the bright display
Of beauty's bloom, do vanish by and by,
And leave us old and withered, in decay,
Beneath the gaze of an indifferent sky.
Then let us not our precious moments waste,
In idle dreams or foolish, vain regret,
But let our lives be with true purpose graced,
And sow the seeds of deeds we won't forget.
   For time, though swift, shall leave a lasting name,
   For those who live with honour and with fame.

###709###
Thy gentle hand, that doth my spirit mend,
And banisheth the shadows of despair,
Is like a balm, on which I can depend,
A precious treasure, beyond all compare.
Thy whispered words, that softly do transcend,
The noise and clamour of this worldly care,
Do teach my wounded soul to comprehend,
A peace that worldly goods can ne'er declare.
Thou art the haven, where my ship may rest,
When tempests rage and billows rise so high,
The guiding star, that leads me to the best,
And wipes the tear from my most weary eye.
   So let me ever in thy love abide,
   And feel thy presence ever at my side.

###710###
The golden coin, that doth the miser's hand
Enslave with greed, and hold him in its thrall,
Can buy no joy, nor happiness command,
But builds a lonely, self-created wall.
The jewels bright, that sparkle through the land,
And tempt the covetous, to risk their all,
Bring naught but sorrow, when they understand,
Their true worth is not in such things to call.
For wealth of spirit, and a heart sincere,
Outshine the brightest diamond's fiery gleam,
And love's true bond, that holds us ever dear,
Is richer far than any waking dream.
   Then let us seek what truly makes us blest,
   And find in virtue, everlasting rest.

###711###
The changing seasons, in their ordered round,
Do teach us lessons, of a profound might,
How death doth yield to life, on hallowed ground,
And darkness flees before the morning light.
The winter's snow, that doth the earth surround,
Gives way to spring, with verdant, fresh delight,
And barren fields, where naught could then be found,
Are clothed anew in nature's glorious sight.
So shall my soul, though plunged in deepest woe,
Find solace, and its former strength regain,
And like the seed, that deep within doth grow,
Break forth anew, and banish every pain.
   For e'en in loss, a deeper strength is found,
   When hope's fair blossoms rise from sorrow's ground.

###712###
My muse, O art thou fled, and left me thus,
Without thy grace, my verse doth seem to die,
My feeble efforts, prove of little use,
And all my thoughts beneath a vacant sky.
I seek thy aid, with desperate, earnest fuss,
And scan the heavens with a longing eye,
But find no spark, no inspiration, thus,
To lift my spirit, and to make it fly.
The words, like barren stones, lie at my feet,
No rhythm flows, no melody takes wing,
My labored lines, imperfect and unmeet,
No joy to thee, or to my soul can bring.
   Yet still I strive, though effort be in vain,
   To woo thee back, and ease this aching pain.

###713###
The rose, that opens to the sun's warm kiss,
And showers forth its fragrance on the breeze,
Must yield at last, to time's unkind abyss,
And fall in fragments 'mongst the fallen leaves.
So beauty's bloom, that we so dearly miss,
When faded, then the weary spirit grieves,
And youthful vigour, that we held in bliss,
Is stolen hence, as time itself deceives.
But though the outward form may lose its grace,
And outward charms like fleeting shadows flee,
The inner light, that time cannot efface,
Shall shine eternal, for the world to see.
   Then let us nurture what can never fade,
   The soul's true worth, by lasting virtue made.

###714###
When Fortune smiles, and all doth seem to go
As we have wished, and all our hopes succeed,
Then many friends do round our bounty flow,
And offer solace in our every need.
But when the clouds of trouble start to show,
And fortune's favour doth itself recede,
These fickle friends, like summer birds, do go,
And leave us to our solitary creed.
True friendship's worth, in trials it is known,
When darkest hours do press with heavy hand,
A loyal heart, on which we can be thrown,
A steadfast rock, on which we firm can stand.
   So let us cherish bonds that will not break,
   For true friends' love, our weary souls will make.

###715###
The ocean vast, that stretches far and wide,
And holds within its depths a mystic might,
Doth whisper secrets, on the turning tide,
Of ages past, and futures burning bright.
I gaze upon its power, where dreams collide,
And feel a wonder, mingled with affright,
As waves do crash, and surge, and then subside,
Beneath the moon's soft, pale, ethereal light.
So is my love, a boundless, deep expanse,
That knows no limit, and no earthly shore,
It drowns all doubt, and bids my spirit dance,
And asks for naught, but to be loved the more.
   For in its depths, my soul finds sweet release,
   And in its calm, a everlasting peace.

###716###
The written word, that doth the ages span,
And brings to life the wisdom of the past,
Doth hold the power to inspire the man,
And make his understanding ever last.
From ancient scrolls, to tales that now began,
The thoughts of thinkers, steadfast and so fast,
Do guide our steps, and shape the mortal plan,
And sow the seeds of knowledge, to be cast.
So let us read, and let our minds expand,
And drink the wisdom from each treasured page,
For in these lines, a greater truth is scanned,
That lifts us up, and sets our souls engage.
   So in these books, true immortality we find,
   And leave behind a legacy for humankind.

###717###
My heart, a fortress, built of stone so deep,
Doth stand against the siege of worldly woe,
And guards its treasures, whilst the world doth weep,
And makes no sign, to let its feelings show.
But thou, my love, with tender grace dost creep,
And find the path, where secret currents flow,
And waken feelings that have long did sleep,
And melt the ice, that I did hide below.
Thy gentle touch, a key of purest gold,
Doth ope the gates, that I so closely barred,
And in thy gaze, a story to be told,
Of love's sweet power, that never can be marred.
   So let me yield, and let my heart be thine,
   For in thy love, true happiness I find.

###718###
The fleeting moment, that doth swiftly fly,
And leaves no trace upon the sands of time,
Doth hold a power, that we can't deny,
To shape our lives, and make our purpose climb.
A word, a glance, a sigh, a tear, a cry,
Can change the course of destiny sublime,
And elevate us to a higher sky,
Or cast us down to depths of deepest slime.
So let us seize each breath, and every day,
With fervent spirit, and with purpose true,
And cast aside the things that lead astray,
And live a life that's ever fresh and new.
   For in these moments, futures are designed,
   And lasting joy, for all of humankind.

###719###
The silent tears, that from mine eyes do stream,
Are testament to sorrows I conceal,
A hidden pain, that haunts my waking dream,
And makes my wounded spirit sadly reel.
I wear a mask, to hide the inner gleam,
Of anguish deep, that time cannot unseal,
And play a part, as in a tragic theme,
While secret wounds my weary body feel.
But thou, my love, with understanding bright,
Dost see the truth, behind the outward show,
And with thy comfort, banish all the night,
And help my troubled, broken spirit grow.
   So in thy love, a healing balm I find,
   And leave the shadows of my past behind.

###720###
When I behold thy form, divinely wrought,
And mark the grace that doth thy beauty hold,
My very soul is with new rapture caught,
A tale of wonder, silently unfolds.
Thy eyes, like stars, with purest light are fraught,
Thy lips, like roses, stories can be told,
Thy gentle voice, more precious than all thought,
Doth turn my base metal into finest gold.
Thou art the sun that warms my frozen heart,
The moon that guides me through the darkest night,
The very essence, of celestial art,
And fills my world with pure, unending light.
   So let me love thee, till my breath shall cease,
   And in thy presence, find eternal peace.

###721###
When Phoebus doth his golden chariot guide,
And sheds his light upon the waking earth,
My weary soul, which in the darkness sighed,
Doth find again a cause for joyful mirth.
The birds do sing their carols in the trees,
A melody that doth my spirit lift,
And gentle whispers borne upon the breeze,
A welcome, sweet, and unlooked-for gift.
The flowers bloom with colours bright and bold,
And chase away the shadows of the night,
A fairer prospect than was ever told,
That fills my heavy heart with pure delight.
So let me greet the dawning of the day,
And cast my former sorrows far away.

###722###
My love, whose beauty doth outshine the stars,
And doth command my ever-constant gaze,
Hath wrought my heart with such a wound as mars
The quiet passage of my lonely days.
Her eyes, like sapphires, pierce me to the core,
Her voice, a music that doth charm the ear,
Her grace, a virtue I do much adore,
Dispelling all my doubt and every fear.
But ah, alas, she knows not of my plight,
Nor of the burning passion in my breast,
And so I languish in perpetual night,
And find within her presence little rest.
Yet still I love, though hope be but a dream,
And burn within this unrequited gleam.

###723###
The fleeting hours, that steal our youth away,
And carve their furrows deep upon the brow,
Do mock our efforts to prolong our stay,
And make us slaves to time's relentless vow.
The bloom of beauty, like a summer's rose,
Doth fade and wither ere the autumn's chill,
And strength, which in our vigorous youth it shows,
Doth wane and leave us feeble and quite still.
Yet in the mirror of thy comely face,
I see a beauty that doth time defy,
A lasting charm, a never-ending grace,
That shall not with the passing seasons die.
So let us cherish what we hold so dear,
And banish from our hearts all mortal fear.

###724###
When envious Fortune frowns and doth withdraw
Her fickle favour from my humble state,
And I am left to battle 'gainst her law,
And bear the heavy burden of my fate.
When friends, who once did pledge their loyalty,
Now turn their backs and mock my sad distress,
And I am left alone with misery,
And clad in rags of wretched emptiness.
Then do I turn my thoughts to thee, my queen,
Whose kindness shines a beacon in the gloom,
And in thy gentle spirit, I have seen
A solace that doth banish every doom.
So though the world with scorn may me assail,
Thy love alone shall evermore prevail.

###725###
The winter's blast, that chills the very bone,
And strips the branches bare of leafy green,
Doth find my spirit feeling quite alone,
And in the darkness, where no joy is seen.
The frozen earth, that yields no fertile seed,
Reflects the barrenness within my soul,
And every waking thought doth intercede,
To make my weary spirit once more whole.
But when thy smile doth break the icy air,
And thy sweet words do fall upon my ear,
A sudden warmth doth banish all despair,
And springtime blossoms, chasing away fear.
So art thou to my frozen heart the sun,
Whose radiant beams have made my winter done.

###726###
My ink doth flow, but finds no worthy theme,
To sing the praises of thy peerless worth,
My muse doth slumber, lost in idle dream,
And gives no tribute to thy beauty's birth.
My verse doth falter, weak and lacking might,
To capture half the splendour of thy face,
My tongue is tied, though I desire to write,
The wondrous virtues of thy gentle grace.
Yet still I strive, with labour and with pain,
To weave a rhyme that may thy favour find,
And though my efforts prove to be in vain,
My constant love shall ever be enshrined.
So take these words, though they be poor and few,
And know my heart beats only, love, for you.

###727###
The painted scenes that fleetingly do pass,
Upon the stage of this dramatic world,
Are but reflections in a looking-glass,
Where truth and falsehood are in chaos hurled.
The smiles of kings, the tears of common man,
The lover's vow, the traitor's whispered lie,
All are but parts within a greater plan,
That shift and change beneath the watchful sky.
But thy true heart, a treasure to behold,
Doth stand apart from all this fleeting show,
A story in itself, more prized than gold,
Whose constant virtue doth forever glow.
So let the actors play their hollow parts,
Thou art the truth that occupies my heart.

###728###
When slumber's hand doth close my weary eyes,
And dreams do conjure visions fair and bright,
My soul takes flight to where my true love lies,
And basks within her ever-shining light.
I walk with her through fields of purest gold,
And hear her laughter, like the sweetest chime,
A story in my dreaming to be told,
That doth transcend the bounds of earthly time.
But when the dawn doth break and I awake,
And find myself alone in waking hours,
My heavy heart begins again to ache,
And longs again for sleep's enchanted bowers.
So let me dream, though waking bringeth pain,
And in thy presence, find my bliss again.

###729###
The babbling brook, that winds its gentle way,
Through verdant meadows, kissed by summer's sun,
Doth sing a song throughout the livelong day,
Until its joyful course is fully run.
The whispering wind, that stirs the rustling leaves,
Doth carry secrets on its airy breath,
And Nature's symphony, that so deceives,
Doth speak of life, and hints of coming death.
But in thy voice, a deeper melody,
A sweeter cadence than the stream or breeze,
Doth find its echo in the heart of me,
And brings my troubled spirit unto ease.
So let the world its lesser tunes impart,
Thy voice alone doth captivate my heart.

###730###
When shadows lengthen and the day grows old,
And weary mortals seek their nightly rest,
My thoughts do turn to tales that must be told,
And ardour burns within my fevered breast.
The tales of valiant knights and ladies fair,
Of battles fought and victories hard-won,
Of lovers bound by an eternal prayer,
Beneath the gaze of moon and setting sun.
But chief among them all, thy image stands,
A paragon of beauty and of truth,
Whose virtues shine across these barren lands,
And breathe new life into my fading youth.
So let me write, though words be weak and frail,
Thy matchless worth shall evermore prevail.

###731###
The fickle crowds, that throng the city's street,
Do ebb and flow like tides upon the shore,
Their fickle favour, transient and fleet,
Is sought by many, yet desired by few for more.
They cheer the victor, then with scorn they frown,
Upon the loser, fallen from his height,
And build up heroes, only to cast down,
Their fleeting idols, in the fading light.
But thou, dear friend, whose steadfast heart I know,
Dost stand apart from this capricious throng,
Thy constancy doth ever brightly glow,
And makes my spirit feel profoundly strong.
So let the multitude their favour lend,
Thou art the truest, most beloved friend.

###732###
The deepest night, though cloaked in darkest hue,
Doth hold within its breast a secret gleam,
Of distant stars, whose light doth pierce anew,
And paint the heavens with a silver dream.
The darkest clouds, that shroud the sun from sight,
Do promise rain to quench the thirsty land,
And in their gloom, a hope for coming light,
A brighter future, close at Nature's hand.
So though my heart be plunged in sorrow's shade,
And all my prospects seem to fade and die,
Thy love, a star that never can be swayed,
Doth shine upon me from the highest sky.
So let the darkness gather all around,
In thy dear light, my solace can be found.

###733###
My quill doth hesitate, my pen doth pause,
To trace the line that might thy beauty seize,
For what can match great Nature's wondrous laws,
Or paint perfection with such perfect ease?
The sculptor's hand, though skilled and finely wrought,
Can ne'er impart the breath of living grace,
The painter's brush, though with great labour taught,
Can scarce portray the radiance of thy face.
So I, a humble bard, with naught to boast,
But love for thee, shall strive to sing thy praise,
And though my efforts may be counted least,
My heartfelt tribute shall endure all days.
So let me try, though failure I may meet,
My love for thee is ever true and sweet.

###734###
The fleeting joys that earthly pleasures bring,
Are like the dew that vanishes with sun,
A momentary bliss, a passing thing,
Whose fragile substance is too quickly done.
The sweetest wine, that doth the palate please,
Doth leave a thirst that cannot be appeased,
The finest silk, that doth the body ease,
Is but a garment, by the worm appeased.
But thy dear love, a constant, flowing spring,
Doth nourish all the parchedness of my soul,
A lasting comfort that doth comfort bring,
And makes my wounded spirit ever whole.
So let the world its fleeting pleasures chase,
Thy love alone doth hold my heart in place.

###735###
When illness grips my frame and strength doth flee,
And fever's fire consumes my fading might,
I turn my thoughts to thy dear face, and see
A solace shining, banishing the night.
The weary hours, that crawl with leaden pace,
Are softened by the memory of thy smile,
And though I suffer in this lonely place,
Thy whispered promise doth my pain beguile.
So though my body languish and grow weak,
And all the world seems clad in somber hue,
Thy steadfast love, the solace that I seek,
Doth grant me courage to endure it through.
For in thy presence, strength doth reappear,
And banish all my doubt and every fear.

###736###
The seasons change, the winter yields to spring,
And summer's heat doth give way to the fall,
Each turning year doth new delights to bring,
And Nature answers to the primal call.
The leaves that bud, then bloom in emerald bright,
Do fade and fall, then rise again in green,
A constant cycle, bathed in changing light,
A wondrous, never-ending, vibrant scene.
But thy dear love, a season of its own,
Doth know no winter, nor a fading leaf,
Its verdant beauty ever brightly shown,
A joy that brings my spirit sweet relief.
So let the world its seasons ebb and flow,
Thy love's a summer that shall ever grow.

###737###
My tongue doth falter, and my thoughts do stray,
When I endeavour to describe thy worth,
For words are weak, and words will oft betray,
The true magnificence of Nature's birth.
The stars above, that spangle heaven's dome,
The ocean's depth, where hidden treasures lie,
The fragrant fields, where gentle breezes roam,
All fail to capture thy bright majesty.
Yet still I strive, with ardour in my breast,
To weave a rhyme that may thy spirit please,
And in this labour, find my soul's true rest,
And win from thee a moment of sweet ease.
So take these lines, though fashioned with such care,
As humble tribute to thy beauty rare.

###738###
The fleeting shadows of this mortal life,
Do mock our plans and scatter our desires,
And leave us wounded by relentless strife,
And quenched by sorrow's cold and bitter fires.
The dreams we build, so fragile and so grand,
Do crumble swift before the winds of fate,
And leave us standing in a barren land,
Where naught remains but sorrow and its weight.
But thy true heart, a fortress strong and deep,
Doth offer refuge from the world's harsh storm,
And in its shelter, quiet I can keep,
And find a solace, safe and ever warm.
So let the world its changing fortunes cast,
Thy constant love shall evermore outlast.

###739###
When envious tongues do whisper tales of woe,
And spread their poison with malicious art,
And seek to strike where wounds do deeply grow,
And plant their seeds of discord in the heart.
When slander's breath doth chill the very soul,
And malice seeks to mar a spotless name,
And strive to drag us down into its hole,
And feed itself upon another's shame.
Then do I think upon thy honest mind,
Whose virtues shine with such a radiant glow,
That no false rumour can my spirit bind,
Nor make my loyal sentiments to go.
So let them speak their venom, sharp and keen,
Thy truth protects me, fairest, noblest queen.

###740###
The sweetest song, that doth the ear delight,
And makes the weary spirit lift and soar,
Is but a fleeting sound, and then takes flight,
And leaves the silence knocking at the door.
The richest feast, that doth the palate bless,
Doth vanish quick, and leaves a hunger keen,
And all the joys that earthly lives possess,
Are but a moment, then they are unseen.
But thy dear love, a never-ending tune,
Doth echo ever in my grateful breast,
A constant balm beneath the sun and moon,
That grants my longing spirit perfect rest.
So let the world its passing pleasures boast,
Thy love's the treasure that I cherish most.

###741###
When I do count the clock that tells the time,
And see the brave day sunk in hideous night;
When I behold the violet past prime,
And sable night o'ertakes the day's delight;
When I perceive the warlike Gentry's pride,
And all the glory of the world decay;
When I do see them whom we most confide,
Like shadows from the sunbeams steal away;
Then of thy beauty do I question make,
That thou among the wastes of time must go,
Since sweets and beauties do themselves forsake,
And die in themselves, to live and fresh grow.
   But thy eternal summer shall not fade,
   Nor lose possession of that fair thou ow'st.

###742###
My mistress' eyes are nothing like the sun;
Coral is far more red than her lips' red;
If snow be white, why then her breasts are dun;
If hairs be wires, black wires grow on her head.
I have seen roses damask'd, red and white,
But no such roses see I in her cheeks;
And in some perfumes is there more delight
Than in the breath that from my mistress reeks.
I love to hear her speak, yet well I know
That music hath a far more pleasing sound;
I grant I never saw a goddess go;
She treads upon the ground.
   And yet, by heaven, I think my love as rare
   As any she belied with false compare.

###743###
When forty winters shall besiege thy brow,
And dig deep trenches in thy beauty's field,
Thy youth's proud livery, so gazed on now,
Will be a tatter'd weed, of small worth held:
Then being ask'd where all thy beauty lies,
Where all the treasure of thy lusty days,
To say, within thine own deep sunken eyes,
Were an all-eating shame and thriftless praise.
How much more doth beauty, now in height,
Live treasure in a glass, and not in gold,
Whose date is
  the time of night,
And who with youthful lungs
  to us is told;
   But if this
    be the doom of youth
   Then would I give my
    to thee, in truth.

###744###
The expense of spirit in a waste of shame
Is lust in action; and till action, lust
Is perjured, mad, blind, halt,        disgraced,
         Enrag'd, and sunk, and lost in the dust.
       All this the world well knows, yet none knows well
To shun the  that makes many run.
The conclusion
    of our best is to be lost,
And
        that our wills do most abhor.
For all the best is in the action
    of lust,
And
        in it, we are most undone.
Yet, by all means, we do it,
        for what we lust,
And in this
        we are as undone.
     So are we undone, by this,
     And
        all our reason is undone.

###745###
When in disgrace with fortune and men's eyes,
I all alone beweep my outcast state,
And trouble deaf heaven with my bootless cries,
And look upon myself and curse my fate,
Wishing me like to one more rich in hope,
Featured like him, like him with friends possessed,
Desiring this man's art and that man's scope,
With what I most enjoy contented least;
Yet in these thoughts myself almost despising,
Haply I think on thee, and then my state,
Like to the lark at break of day arising
From sullen earth, sings hymns at heaven's gate;
   For thy sweet love remembered such wealth brings
   That then I scorn to change my state with kings.

###746###
Fear no more the heat o' the sun,
Nor the furious winter's rages;
Thou thy worldly task hast done,
Home art gone, and ta'en thy wages.
Golden lads and girls all must,
As chimney-sweepers, come to dust.
Fie, fie, fie, fie!
Thou art gone.
Fair and foul are soon forgot,
When the grave's dark mouth is shut.
Mermaids and nymphs are all forgot,
When the grave's dark mouth is shut.
   Witches and goblins all do fly,
   When the grave's dark mouth is shut.

###747###
No longer mourn for me when I am dead
Than you shall hear the surly bell give warning
Of that lame progress to your own death's bed;
And no more do I question you of warning.
That you on the top of me will be,
And no more do I question you of this;
That you in the grave will be,
And no more do I question you of this;
That you on the top of me will be,
And no more do I question you of this;
That you in the grave will be,
And no more do I question you of this;
   For, if you cannot be with me,
   Then no more do I question you of this.

###748###
My love is as a fever, longing still
For that which longer nurseth the disease;
Feeding on that which doth preserve the ill,
The uncertain sickly appetite to please.
My reason, the physician to my love,
Angry that his prescriptions are not kept,
Hath left me, and I desperate now approve
Desire is death, which physic did except.
Flesh stays my tooth, and love makes me to keep
My whole flesh, as I was once before,
And by this means my love doth grow and leap,
And doth my reason now abhor.
   But in this fever I do languish still,
   And for this fever I do long until.

###749###
Let me not to the marriage of true minds
Admit impediments. Love is not love
Which alters when it alteration finds,
Or bends with the remover to remove.
O no! it is an ever-fixed mark
That looks on tempests and is never shaken;
It is the star to every wand'ring bark,
Whose worth's unknown, although his height be taken.
Love's not Time's fool, though rosy lips and cheeks
Within his bending sickle's compass come;
Love alters not with his brief hours and weeks,
But bears it out even to the edge of doom.
   If this be error and upon me proved,
   I never writ, nor no man ever loved.

###750###
When I do count the cost of our delight,
And see how swiftly pleasure takes its flight;
When I behold the bloom of beauty's might,
And know it fades into the endless night;
When I perceive how riches turn to dust,
And all the pomp of worldly power decays;
When I do see them whom we put our trust,
Like fleeting shadows from the sunbeams stray;
Then of thy constancy I question make,
That thou among the ruins must remain,
Since all that's fair doth beauty undertake,
And dies in losing that it did attain.
   But thy true love shall not then decay,
   Nor lose the worth it holds this very day.

###751###
My lady's gaze doth shame the morning sun,
Her cheeks with rose and lily are not blent;
If coral be her lips, their race is run,
Her breath a sweeter perfume heaven hath sent.
I have seen gardens where the roses thrive,
But no such garden in her visage lies;
And in her voice, a melody alive,
Doth banish all the world's discordant cries.
I grant I never saw a shape so fine,
She walks with grace that angels might admire;
A mortal form, yet heavenly design,
That sets my very soul and heart afire.
   And though no goddess she, nor angel bright,
   My love for her doth burn with endless light.

###752###
When fifty winters furrow deep thy face,
And steal the vigour from thy youthful hand;
Thy present beauty, that doth time efface,
Shall be a tale that few can understand.
Then if you ask where all thy grace hath fled,
Where vanished all thy laughter and thy glee;
To say, within thine own heart, cold and dead,
Would be a cruel truth, a misery.
How much more doth beauty, now at its height,
Reside in glass, a treasure to behold,
Whose lease is short, ere comes the endless night,
And tales of youth are seldom to be told;
   But if this fate for beauty doth decree,
   Then would I gladly give my days to thee.

###753###
The wasting of our strength in fruitless quest,
Is lust's pursuit, and ere it finds its aim,
Is mad, and blind, and wholly dispossessed,
Enrag'd, and drown'd in an eternal shame.
All this the common eye doth plainly see,
Yet none can shun the lure that doth entice;
The end of all our striving is to be,
Lost in the toils of passion's subtle vice.
For all that seems most worthy to be sought,
Is but the fleeting pleasure we embrace,
And in its chase, our reason comes to naught,
And we are ruin'd in that sinful space.
   So are we lost, by this desire we hold,
   And all our better selves remain untold.

###754###
When fortune frowns and men do turn away,
I sit alone and weep my sorry plight,
And send to heaven my unheeded plea,
And curse my star that dims my inward light.
I wish myself like one with hope adorned,
With friends as many as the sand grains are,
Desiring gifts that I have not suborned,
And finding joy in naught, however rare.
Yet, while I dwell on thoughts that bring me low,
And my own worth I scarcely can esteem,
My mind turns to thee, and my spirits glow,
Like larks that rise from earth in morning's gleam;
   For thy dear memory such solace lends,
   That kings' estate I'd gladly make amends.

###755###
My love is like a fever, burning bright,
That craves the cure which feeds the very ill;
It doth consume me with a fierce delight,
And mocks my reason with a wicked will.
My sober sense, that would my course amend,
Doth leave me, and I, desperate, now embrace
The sweet damnation I cannot transcend,
The pleasing poison that doth seal my race.
My flesh doth hold me captive to its sway,
And love doth bind me with a silken chain,
And by this means my passion holds its day,
And reason doth my pleas forbear in vain.
   Yet in this fever I do languish still,
   And for this fever I do crave my fill.

###756###
Let not my absence dim thy loving thought,
Nor absence make thee find another's grace;
True constancy is dearly to be bought,
And time itself can not its strength displace.
Love is no fleeting passion of the eye,
That shifts and changes with the passing hour;
It is a star that watches from on high,
Whose steadfast beam doth hold eternal power.
No outward show can make true love depart,
Though beauty fade and youth begin to wane;
It dwells within the chambers of the heart,
And through all storms, its constancy doth reign.
   So let thy love be fixed, and ever true,
   As mine shall be, my dearest, unto you.

###757###
My mistress' eyes are not the sun's bright gleam,
Nor coral redder than her lips can show;
If snow be white, her skin, it doth but seem,
Black wires of hair upon her head do grow.
I have seen roses of a lovely hue,
But none so bright as in her cheeks I find;
And in her breath, a fragrance ever new,
A sweeter scent than perfumes of mankind.
I love to hear her speak, though common sound,
Her voice doth hold a music all its own;
I grant she treads upon the earthly ground,
Yet in her step, a queenly grace is shown.
   And though she boast no godhead's faultless art,
   She hath ensnared my true and loving heart.

###758###
When twenty summers have left their mark,
And sown deep furrows in thy brow so fair,
Thy youthful bloom, a momentary spark,
Shall be a memory, held beyond compare.
Then if you ask where all thy beauty lies,
Where all thy laughter and thy joyful days,
To say, within thy own forgetful eyes,
Would be a sorrow past all human praise.
How much more doth beauty, now in prime,
Lie treasured in a glass, and not in gold,
Whose brief existence yields to passing time,
And tales of youth are seldom to be told;
   But if such fate on beauty must befall,
   Then let me love thee, giving thee my all.

###759###
The time will come when thou shalt cease to sigh,
And find no solace in the lengthening day;
Thy weary limbs shall rest beneath the sky,
And all thy earthly cares be put away.
The songs of birds, the flowers of the field,
The summer's warmth, the winter's chilling blast,
Shall fade from memory, their power concealed,
When life's brief lease is finally recast.
No more shall love thy heart with passion fill,
Nor beauty hold thee captive to its sway;
Thy earthly race is run, thy soul is still,
And all thy striving hath passed away.
   Then shall I mourn thee, with a heavy heart,
   And all my dreams with thee shall now depart.

###760###
My love is like a sickness, deep and strong,
That feeds upon itself and grows more keen;
It doth preserve the ill, and doth prolong,
The endless yearning that remains unseen.
My reason, that the cure would fain impart,
Doth find its counsel wilfully ignored;
It leaves me to the passions of the heart,
And by desire, my better sense is gored.
The flesh doth hold me in its firm embrace,
And love doth bind me with a subtle thread;
And by this means my passion finds its place,
And reason's voice remains forever dead.
   Yet in this sickness I do find my bliss,
   And for this fever, I would gladly kiss.

###761###
When that the sun doth cast his golden ray,
Upon the fields where weary plowman toils,
And chases all the chilly night away,
As nature doth her verdant self uncoils,
So doth my love, a beacon burning bright,
Dispel the shadows of my darkest fears,
And fill my soul with pure and sweet delight,
That dries the source of all my bitter tears.
Yet doth this joy, like fleeting summer's bloom,
Too soon depart, and leave me in the shade,
Consumed by sorrow and a heavy gloom,
As youthful bloom doth wither and doth fade.
   But hope remains, though trials do abound,
   That in thy love, true solace shall be found.

###762###
The busy bee, with purpose in its flight,
Doth gather nectar from each fragrant flower,
And works with ardour from the morn till night,
To store its treasure for a future hour.
So do I labour, with a heart afire,
To build a monument of lasting praise,
To feed the flame of my intense desire,
And sing thy virtues through my fleeting days.
But ah, my verse, though writ with honest care,
Doth seem a shadow of thy worth so grand,
A humble echo, lighter than the air,
Unfit to capture what I understand.
   Yet shall I strive, till breath doth leave my frame,
   To glorify thy ever-honoured name.

###763###
When that the moon, with silver, gentle grace,
Doth light the path where lovers softly tread,
And shadows dance within that silent place,
Where whispered vows are tenderly outspread,
My thoughts do wander to thy visage fair,
And in my dreams, thy presence I embrace,
A balm of comfort banishing despair,
And bringing solace to this lonely space.
But when the dawn doth break, and light appears,
Thy form doth vanish, like a morning mist,
And leaves me drowned in unavailing tears,
By cruel reality and sorrow kissed.
   Yet in my heart, thy image shall reside,
   My guiding star, where truth and beauty bide.

###764###
The raging storm, with thunder's awful sound,
Doth shake the heavens and the trembling earth,
And tempests howl, with fury all around,
Destruction spreading in their fearful birth.
So do my passions, like a tempest tossed,
Assail my spirit with a wild desire,
And leave me shipwrecked, utterly lost,
Consumed by flames of an unquenchable fire.
But through the chaos, a calm voice I hear,
That whispers solace to my troubled soul,
Dispelling doubt and banishing all fear,
And making my fractured spirit whole.
   This voice is thine, a melody so sweet,
   That bids my warring, weary heart complete.

###765###
When winter's breath, with chilling hand so cold,
Doth strip the branches bare and leave them stark,
And nature's vibrant colours turn to old,
As darkness settles, leaving its bleak mark,
So doth my spirit, when thou art afar,
Feel empty, barren, and devoid of cheer,
As if beneath a dim and fading star,
My life's true purpose doth begin to disappear.
But spring shall come, with blossoms fresh and new,
And life shall stir where slumber held its sway,
And all the world be painted in a hue
Of verdant hope, to greet the brighter day.
   So shall thy love, with warmth it doth impart,
   Revive the winter of my frozen heart.

###766###
The fleeting hours, like sand that slips away,
Through open fingers, never to return,
Doth steal the moments of each precious day,
And lessons that we never seem to learn.
So do I waste my youth in idle dreams,
And let the opportunities take flight,
Unheeding of the swift, departing streams,
That bear away my unillumined light.
But if thy love, a tutor wise and true,
Should guide my steps and point a better way,
Then might my life begin its task anew,
And chase the shadows of my past astray.
   For in thy counsel, wisdom I can find,
   To mend the errors of my erring mind.

###767###
When I behold the beauty of the skies,
With stars like diamonds scattered through the night,
And wonder fills my ever-watching eyes,
At cosmic wonders, bathed in pale moonlight,
My thoughts do turn to thee, whose loveliness,
Outshines the radiance of all that's seen,
A queen of beauty, none can e'er possess,
A vision bright, a most enchanting queen.
Yet, alas, this beauty, held so dear,
Doth cause my heart a pang of secret dread,
For mortal charms must vanish, year by year,
And life's sweet tapestry be finally shed.
   But if thy soul, with virtue doth it shine,
   Then shall thy lasting beauty e'er be mine.

###768###
The gentle stream, that murmurs through the dale,
Doth find its course, though stones may lie in way,
And ever onward, doth its journey trail,
Until it joins the ocean, far away.
So do I strive, with purpose in my breast,
To reach the haven where my heart finds rest,
To overcome each trial, put to test,
And give my all, with courage I am blessed.
But oft discouragement doth hold me bound,
And whisper doubts that sap my vital strength,
As if no solace ever can be found,
Nor journey's end, whatever be its length.
   Yet if thy hand, doth offer me support,
   I shall endure, and stand within my fort.

###769###
When golden Phoebus, from his lofty throne,
Doth cast his warmth upon the weary ground,
And bids the seeds that slumber to be sown,
Where life and verdure shall at last be found,
So doth thy presence, like a summer's sun,
Revive my spirit, heavy and downcast,
And make me feel my race is newly run,
With hope renewed, and shadows of the past.
But should thy light withdraw, and skies grow grey,
My heart doth shrink, and all my joy doth cease,
As if the blossoms withered on the spray,
And left no promise of returning peace.
   So am I bound, unto thy beaming eye,
   Without its light, I surely droop and die.

###770###
The tapestry that art hath wrought with skill,
Doth show forth scenes of grandeur and of might,
Where heroes strive, and conquer with good will,
And beauty shines with ever-constant light.
But when I seek to capture thee in rhyme,
My humble quill doth falter and doth fail,
To paint the portrait worthy of thy prime,
And tell a story that shall e'er prevail.
For human skill, however finely spun,
Can ne'er achieve what nature hath designed,
Thy grace and beauty, none hath e'er outrun,
A perfect marvel, of a wondrous kind.
   So shall my praise, though lacking in its art,
   Still speak the truth that dwells within my heart.

###771###
The brittle glass, that falls from height so tall,
Doth shatter into fragments, sharp and keen,
And leaves behind no semblance of its thrall,
But scattered ruins, where it once had been.
So do my hopes, when dashed by cruel decree,
Lie broken, scattered, on life's stony shore,
And leave me weeping, in my misery,
And longing for what I can have no more.
But if thy pity, like a gentle hand,
Should gather up these shards with tender care,
And mend the pieces, as thou canst command,
Then might my spirit rise beyond despair.
   For in thy kindness, solace I shall find,
   To heal the wounds that pierce my troubled mind.

###772###
When summer's warmth doth fade, and autumn's chill,
Begins to bite, and leaves begin to fall,
And nature's colours, once so bright and still,
Are dulled and muted, answering winter's call,
So do I fear, that time, with cruelest pace,
Will steal the bloom from thy most lovely face,
And leave behind a wrinkle and a trace
Of seasons past, in this world's fleeting race.
Yet, if thy virtue, like a hidden gem,
Doth sparkle brighter as the years go by,
Then shall thy beauty, a diadem,
Outshine the fading of the earth and sky.
   For outward grace, though pleasing to the eye,
   Is naught compared to goodness that doth lie.

###773###
The silent owl, that through the darkness flies,
With watchful gaze and feathers soft and deep,
 doth spy its prey with keen and piercing eyes,
While all the weary, slumbering world doth sleep.
So do I watch thee, in my lonely hours,
And learn thy ways, with ardour in my soul,
As if to plunder nature's fairest flowers,
And make thy perfect beauty my sole goal.
But though I strive with all my might and main,
To capture essence of thy matchless grace,
My efforts prove but labour spent in vain,
Thou art a marvel that no words can trace.
   Yet still I gaze, with wonder and with awe,
   Subjected to thy captivating law.

###774###
When jealous envy doth with venom's sting,
Assail the heart and whisper words of spite,
And dark suspicion on its wicked wing,
Doth dim the day and banish all delight,
So do I feel, when rumours fly abroad,
And speak of falsehoods that do wound my name,
As if by falsehoods I am overthrown and awed,
And cast into a pit of burning shame.
But if thy trust, a shield of purest gold,
Doth guard my honour from each poisoned dart,
Then shall the truth, more precious than untold,
Prevail and mend my bruised and wounded heart.
   For in thy faith, my strength I do regain,
   And banish all the sland'rous, cruel pain.

###775###
The sturdy oak, that hath withstood the blast,
Of tempest's fury and of winter's snow,
Doth stand unbent, its roots hold firm and fast,
And sees the fleeting seasons come and go.
So do I wish my love for thee to be,
A steadfast anchor in life's stormy sea,
Unchanging, firm, for all eternity,
A constant flame, a sweet felicity.
But ah, the heart of man is frail and weak,
And prone to wander from its promised vow,
The words we speak, we may not always keep,
And change doth stalk us, even here and now.
   Yet in thy constancy, I place my trust,
   That our true love shall never turn to dust.

###776###
When weary travelers, with thirst oppressed,
Do seek a spring, to slake their burning need,
And find sweet water, bringing them to rest,
A welcome solace, planting a hopeful seed,
So do I seek thy love, a fountain pure,
To quench the fever of my deep desire,
A balm that can my aching spirit cure,
And fan the embers of my soul's true fire.
But should this fount of kindness be denied,
Or turned to bitter waters, cold and strange,
Then shall my heart, with sorrow sorely tried,
Be left to wander, in a barren range.
   So grant me, love, thy ever-flowing grace,
   And find in me a loving, resting place.

###777###
The silent tomb, where noble spirits sleep,
Doth hold their dust, their earthly journey done,
And secrets buried, that the ages keep,
Beneath the pallor of the setting sun.
So do my thoughts, when I do ponder death,
And all the stillness of that solemn place,
Do turn to thee, and with my parting breath,
I wish thy memory to time's embrace.
For though my life may fade and turn to naught,
And all my deeds be lost in dark oblivion,
Thy grace and beauty, lovingly I've sought,
Shall live within the verse I have now spun.
   So let me die, with thy dear name in store,
   My cherished love, forever and evermore.

###778###
The fleeting moment, ere the die is cast,
Doth hold a future, hidden from our sight,
A path unknown, where fortunes may be amassed,
Or plunged to darkness, in eternal night.
So do I stand, upon this precipice,
And gaze upon the unknown years to be,
With hope for joy, and dread of sorrow's kiss,
And pray that fate may smile propitiously.
But if thy love, a compass true and bold,
Doth guide my vessel through the ocean's foam,
Then shall my journey, worth more than fine gold,
Lead me at last to happiness and home.
   So be my guide, my constant, guiding star,
   And banish fears, whate'er the trials are.

###779###
When envious tongues do wag with malice keen,
And cast their shadows on the pure and good,
And paint a falsehood where truth should have been,
Misunderstood, or wrongly understood,
So do I feel, when rumours do arise,
And stain the honour that I hold so dear,
As if a veil is cast before mine eyes,
And all my honest purpose turned to fear.
But if thy judgment, fair and free from stain,
Doth see the truth that lies within my soul,
Then shall I rise above the bitter pain,
And make my wounded spirit once more whole.
   For in thy wisdom, justice I can find,
   To set my troubled, slandered heart to mind.

###780###
The painted rose, though fair to outward view,
Doth lack the scent that makes the living bloom,
And though its colours may be bright and new,
It holds no fragrance to dispel the gloom.
So do I fear, lest my affections prove,
A hollow shell, a beauty but skin-deep,
A superficial and a fleeting love,
That cannot truly promises to keep.
But if thy heart, with passion doth it burn,
And holds a love that's honest, true, and deep,
Then shall my soul, to thee it shall return,
And in thy faithful keeping, safely sleep.
   For in thy breast, my truest home I find,
   A love that's constant, steadfast, and refined.

###781###
When I do view the fading summer's light,
And feel the chill that heralds autumn's reign,
My soul doth shrink and tremble at the sight,
As all my former joys begin to wane.
The golden hues that kissed the verdant field,
Now turn to brown and dust, a sorry show,
And Nature's bounty, that was once revealed,
Doth yield to frost and winds that fiercely blow.
So too my love, though once it burned so bright,
Now flickers low, and seems to lose its flame,
And I am left to face the coming night,
With naught but sorrow whispered by my name.
   Yet even so, I pray this love endure,
   Though seasons change, my heart shall be most sure.

###782###
My dearest friend, whose worth I cannot tell,
Thou art the sun that doth my darkness chase,
And in thy presence, all my fears do quell,
And joy doth blossom in this barren place.
Thy voice, a melody that soothes my soul,
Thy smile, a beacon in the stormy sea,
Thou dost my weary spirit make me whole,
And set my captive heart and fancy free.
If ever fortune shall thy favour scorn,
And cast thee down from heights of sweet content,
Then know that I, though utterly forlorn,
Will share thy grief, on thee my heart is bent.
   For in this world, so fraught with toil and pain,
   True fellowship doth make our burdens vain.

###783###
The tyrant Time, with ever-hungry maw,
Doth gnaw upon the fairest of the fair,
And makes of beauty but a fleeting law,
A phantom shape that vanishes in air.
The rose that blooms with velvet, blushing cheek,
Shall soon be withered, pale, and cast aside,
And laughter's echo, once so loud and sleek,
Shall fade and die, where sorrow doth preside.
So must I fear that all that I hold dear,
Shall fall victim to this ceaseless decay,
And love itself, that conquers every fear,
Shall yield at last unto the ending day.
   Yet if thy love in constancy doth stay,
   Time's cruelest hand shall steal it not away.

###784###
When I behold the stars that dot the night,
And ponder on their courses, vast and deep,
I wonder if there shines a greater light,
Wherein the secrets of the heavens sleep.
Do kindred souls in distant spheres reside,
Who feel the pangs of absence, sharp and keen,
And for their absent loves do softly chide
The cruelest fate that keeps them from their queen?
Or art thou, lady, but a single star,
Whose beauty outshines all the host above,
And drew me hence, from where my true joys are,
To worship at the shrine of thy sweet love?
   If so, then let me gaze and ever burn,
   Until the day my loving suit doth earn.

###785###
My muse, alas, doth languish and grow weak,
Her former fire, now but a dying ember,
And when I strive her potent aid to seek,
No worthy thought her vacant mind doth remember.
The quill lies idle, and the ink is dry,
My heart is heavy, and my spirit low,
And all the verses that I fain would cry,
Are lost within the stream of endless woe.
Perhaps my passion doth begin to fade,
Or love's sweet sting hath lost its former power,
And in this barren land, by Fortune made,
I cannot pluck a single, blooming flower.
   Yet still I hope, with lingering despair,
   To find again the verses that I swear.

###786###
Thy face, a mirror to my soul's desire,
Doth hold a beauty that doth shame the dawn,
And sets my ardent, beating heart afire,
As I, thy humble thrall, do gaze upon.
The ruby lips, that promise sweet delight,
The gentle eyes, that hold a world of grace,
The silken hair, that catches sunbeams bright,
All conspire to make this happy place.
Should I then dare to breathe a whispered plea,
And offer up my heart, so true and bold,
Wouldst thou consent to grant thy love to me,
A treasure richer far than gems or gold?
   Oh, speak the word that shall my spirit lift,
   And seal our fate, a most eternal gift.

###787###
The world doth rush, with hurried, restless pace,
And men do chase their fortunes, far and wide,
Each seeking for a better, nobler place,
Wherein their vain ambitions may preside.
But I, content with this my humble state,
And blessed with thy companionship so sweet,
Do find my joy, and laugh at cruelest fate,
As hand in hand, our happy spirits meet.
Let others toil and strive for empty fame,
And gain the world, yet lose their precious souls,
My only treasure is thy whispered name,
And thy dear love, that evermore consoles.
   For in thy eyes, a universe I find,
   A haven for my ever-wandering mind.

###788###
I swore to thee, my love, my life, my all,
That ne'er would absence dim my steadfast flame,
And though the winds of fortune fiercely call,
My heart would e'er repeat thy cherished name.
But cruel is absence, and the miles between,
Do cast a shadow o'er my brightest day,
And in the silence, what was once unseen,
Doth whisper doubts and lead my thoughts astray.
I see thy face in every passing cloud,
I hear thy voice in every rustling breeze,
And still I yearn, though I am forced to shroud
My lonely grief, and seek for sweet unease.
   Yet trust I thee, as I trust sun and moon,
