   That we shall meet again, and that full soon.

###789###
When envy gnaws with sharp and bitter tooth,
And whispers slanders in the public ear,
It seeks to wound with venom and with ruth,
And plant suspicion, breeding doubt and fear.
So too they speak of thee, with jealous tongue,
And paint thy virtues in a shade of blame,
As if thy very excellence were wrong,
And sought to tarnish thy most noble name.
But I, who know thy heart, so pure and true,
And see the goodness that doth dwell within,
Can only pity those who speak anew,
And know their malice is a fruitless sin.
   For lies like shadows, though they fill the air,
   Are vanquished by the sun, beyond compare.

###790###
The golden sun, that climbs the eastern sky,
Doth shed its warmth upon the sleeping earth,
And bids the flowers with bright colours vie,
And nature celebrates a new rebirth.
So too thy presence, when it doth appear,
Doth banish all the shadows from my breast,
And makes my weary, burdened soul feel clear,
And puts my troubled, anxious heart to rest.
Thy smile, a sunrise, chasing night away,
Thy voice, a music, sweet and soft and low,
Doth make me wish that I could ever stay,
And in thy radiant company bestow
   My grateful heart, to thee forever bound,
   Wherein my truest happiness is found.

###791###
The fleeting years, like phantom ships at sea,
Do sail away, and leave no trace behind,
And steal our youth, and mock our vanity,
And leave but wrinkles for us all to find.
The hair that once was dark as raven's wing,
Now turns to silver, bleached by passing time,
And strength doth fail, and spirits cease to sing,
As we approach our final, silent clime.
But though my outward form doth fade and wane,
And strength departs, and beauty takes its flight,
My love for thee shall ever still remain,
A constant flame, a clear and steady light.
   For this true love, no season can decay,
   It lives and thrives, until the judgment day.

###792###
When love doth strike, it knows no gentle hand,
But bursts upon us with a sudden force,
And sweeps us off, to some enchanted land,
Where reason bows and yields to passion's course.
So was it with my heart, when first I saw
Thy beauteous face, so fair and passing rare,
I yielded to love's irresistible law,
And found myself ensnared within thy snare.
No more my own, my will is bent to thee,
My thoughts, my dreams, my very breath I give,
And in this sweet and willing captivity,
I find the truest way for me to live.
   For thou art all that I could e'er desire,
   My soul's true home, my everlasting fire.

###793###
The foolish poet, with his pen and ink,
Doth strive to capture beauty, swift and brief,
And on the page, doth make his fancies blink,
A fleeting solace for his inner grief.
He sings of eyes, like stars in midnight's deep,
Of lips, like roses, kissed by morning dew,
Of hearts that vow their faithful love to keep,
And souls entwined, forever fresh and new.
But all these words, though fairly spun and bright,
Can ne'er portray the wonder that I see,
When in thy presence, bathed in purest light,
All other loveliness seems naught to me.
   For thy true worth, no verse can e'er express,
   It shines supreme, beyond all loveliness.

###794###
When Fortune smiles, and all our hopes are met,
And joy doth overflow our happy cup,
We think this bliss will never know regret,
And raise our thankful voices, lifting up
Our souls to heaven, in a grateful prayer,
For all the blessings that we freely gain,
And cast aside all sorrow and all care,
Believing happiness shall still remain.
But ah, how fickle is this earthly state,
How swift the turn of Fortune's wheel doth go,
And plunges us from joy to darkest fate,
And leaves us weeping in the bitter woe.
   So let us hold our present pleasure fast,
   For earthly joys are never made to last.

###795###
My heart doth ache with unrequited love,
A bitter draught, that I am forced to drink,
And though I gaze at thee, as doth a dove
At cruelest hawk, my spirit starts to sink.
I offer up my soul, my fondest vow,
My truest faith, my every passing sigh,
But thou art cold, and dost not heed me now,
And turnest from my love with heedless eye.
Perhaps I am too bold, too plain, too rude,
And lack the grace that doth thy favour win,
Or else my passion is but misconstrued,
And thou dost think me but a foolish kin.
   Yet still I hope, though hope be thin and frail,
   That someday soon thy stony heart will quail.

###796###
The winter's grip, so icy and so cold,
Doth hold the land in its severe embrace,
And all the world, in white and stark unfold,
Doth seem to wear a melancholy face.
The trees stand bare, their branches gaunt and stark,
The rivers freeze, and flow no longer free,
And darkness reigns, from morn till falling dark,
A somber hue, for all the world to see.
Yet even in this season, chill and drear,
I find a warmth within my loving breast,
For thoughts of thee do banish doubt and fear,
And grant my weary spirit perfect rest.
   So let the winter rage, and storms descend,
   My love for thee shall know no earthly end.

###797###
When I do read the lines that poets write,
Of ancient loves, and battles fought and won,
I marvel at the power of their might,
To stir the soul, till day is done.
They speak of heroes, bold and strong and true,
Of ladies fair, with eyes that shone like stars,
And tales of passion, ever fresh and new,
That break down all of sorrow's bitter bars.
And though I cannot boast of deeds so grand,
Nor claim a fame that echoes through the age,
I still do hold my love within my hand,
And write it here, upon this humble page.
   For in this verse, my heart's true truth is shown,
   A love for thee, that stands to thee alone.

###798###
My dearest love, whose absence pains me sore,
And makes the days seem tedious and long,
I yearn to feel thy presence as before,
And hear again thy sweet and lovely song.
The world seems dull, without thy cheerful light,
The fairest scene doth lose its vibrant hue,
And in the lonely silence of the night,
My dreams are filled with visions of but you.
Oh, when shall fate permit our paths to meet,
And banish all these weary miles between,
To once again our joyous souls entreat,
And make our love eternally serene?
   Until that day, my heart shall ever pine,
   And send its tenderest affections thine.

###799###
The fleeting moment, like a butterfly,
Doth flit and flutter, then it disappears,
And though we seek to hold it, by and by,
It vanishes, and leaves us with our fears.
So too our youth, that bloomed so bright and fair,
Doth fade and wither, ere we are aware,
And leaves us with the burdens that we bear,
And wrinkles etched by time and by despair.
But in thy love, I find a lasting spring,
A beauty that no season can destroy,
And in my heart, thy praises ever sing,
A constant source of everlasting joy.
   For this true love, no earthly power can steal,
   It shall endure, and ever shall it heal.

###800###
The sun descends, and paints the western sky
With hues of crimson, gold, and burning red,
A glorious sight, that doth command the eye,
As day doth yield, and darkness starts to spread.
So too, my love, thy beauty doth unfold,
And fills my soul with wonder and delight,
A story richer far than tales of old,
A radiant vision, shining ever bright.
Though seasons change, and empires rise and fall,
And mortal things are subject to decay,
Thy loveliness shall conquer over all,
And chase the darkest shadows far away.
   So let me gaze, and in thy beauty find,
   A joy eternal, for my loving mind.

###801###
When Fortune frowns and casts a doleful shade,
And hopes, like summer blossoms, start to fade,
My weary spirit, by the tempest swayed,
Laments the joy that hath so long delayed.
The sun, though bright, doth mock my inner night,
And cheerful songs do grate upon mine ear,
For sorrow hath usurped its rightful might,
And whispers doubts, and breeds a chilling fear.
Yet will I strive, though darkness doth surround,
To find some gleam of comfort in the gloom,
And on the ashes of my hopes profound,
A fragile seedling may again find room.
    Though storms may rage, a stronger heart shall be,
    And rise anon, more resolute and free.

###802###
The fleeting hours, like nimble steeds, do fly,
And bear away the bloom of youth so fair,
While seasons change beneath the changing sky,
And leave behind a visage etched with care.
The rosy cheek, where once true beauty dwelt,
Now shows the lines that time hath carved so deep,
And ardent fires, where passion brightly felt,
Do dwindle low, and in their embers sleep.
Yet in the soul, a light may still reside,
A wisdom gained from trials understood,
A calm repose, where gentler thoughts do guide,
And find in age a greater, truer good.
    So let us greet the years that onward haste,
    With memories of love, that cannot waste.

###803###
My lady's eyes, like stars that grace the night,
Do cast a beam that pierces through my soul,
And fill my breast with wonder and delight,
And make my heart obey their sweet control.
Her voice, a melody of sweetest sound,
Doth charm the air and banish all my woe,
And in her smile, a paradise is found,
Where all my joys and fondest wishes grow.
Her gentle touch, a balm to all my pain,
Doth soothe my fears and bid my doubts depart,
And in her presence, I am born again,
A captive made, with all my willing heart.
    So let me live within her loving gaze,
    And spend with her my bright and happy days.

###804###
The world's applause, a fickle, gusty breeze,
Doth puff men up and then doth cast them down,
And fortune's wheel, that spins with such unease,
Doth make a king, and then a beggar crown.
The praise of crowds, a shallow, empty thing,
Doth fade away when trials do draw nigh,
And flatterers, with honeyed words do sing,
But flee like shadows when the storm is high.
I seek no fame, nor wealth beyond my need,
But in a friend, a truth that shall endure,
A loyal heart, that plants a constant seed,
And offers solace, steadfast, firm, and pure.
    For in such bonds, true riches I do find,
    A lasting treasure, to my heart and mind.

###805###
When envious tongues do whisper slanders low,
And malice aims its venom at my name,
My spirit sinks, my inner strength doth go,
And I am lost in sorrow's burning flame.
The poisoned dart, though unseen, doth strike deep,
And leaves a wound that time cannot erase,
While watchful fears their anxious vigil keep,
And steal the smile from off my pallid face.
Yet if a truth within my breast doth lie,
And innocence my constant shield shall be,
Then shall these calumnies like shadows fly,
And leave my honour whole, unblemished, free.
    For what is said by spiteful, lying tongue,
    Is but a passing echo, briefly sung.

###806###
The gentle rain, that nourishes the earth,
Doth bring forth life where barrenness did reign,
And bids the seeds to rise, and prove their worth,
And banish sorrow, and relieve all pain.
So may thy love, a sweet and vital shower,
Descend upon my soul, so parched and dry,
And wake within me a forgotten power,
And chase the clouds from off my weary sky.
Let kindness fall, like dew upon the land,
And banish doubt, and conquer all my dread,
And take my trembling, supplicating hand,
And lead me forth, where brighter days are spread.
    For in thy grace, my spirit finds its zest,
    And in thy favour, I shall be most blest.

###807###
When absence doth my loving heart embrace,
And miles between us keep our souls apart,
I long to see again thy beauteous face,
And feel the beating of thy kindred heart.
The days do crawl, and nights do seem to stay,
And all the world appears a barren place,
For thou art gone, and taken with thee,
The sun that shone upon my earthly space.
Yet in my dreams, I hold thee ever near,
And whisper words of love, though none can hear,
And banish doubt, and conquer every fear,
Until the time when thou again art here.
    So let me wait, with patience strong and true,
    For that sweet hour when I again see you.

###808###
The written word, a fragile, fleeting thing,
Doth carry thoughts across the passing years,
And tales of love, and battles, it doth bring,
And shed the light that conquers all our fears.
Though ink may fade, and paper turn to dust,
The spirit of the thought shall still remain,
And keep alive the memory and trust,
And ease the burden of our earthly pain.
So let me write, with ardour and with care,
My heart's true feelings, and my soul's deep plea,
And leave behind a testament to share,
Of love and truth, for all eternity.
    For in these lines, my very being lives,
    And to the ages, what I have, it gives.

###809###
The fleeting smile that graces thy dear face,
Doth banish shadows from my troubled sight,
And in its warmth, I find a resting place,
And all the world is bathed in golden light.
Thy laughter rings, a music to mine ear,
That soothes the soul and bids all sorrows cease,
And drives away the lingering, chilling fear,
And fills my heart with unalloyed peace.
So let me gaze, and drink thy beauty in,
And hold this moment, precious and so rare,
Before the fleeting hours shall begin,
To steal away this joy beyond compare.
    For in thy presence, life is truly sweet,
    And all my hopes and fondest wishes meet.

###810###
When envy's sting doth pierce my gentle breast,
And malice whispers falsehoods in the air,
My spirit falters, robbed of peaceful rest,
And I am lost in shadows of despair.
The whispered lie, a serpent in the grass,
Doth wound the soul with venom sharp and deep,
And as the envious moments onward pass,
My troubled heart its silent sorrow keeps.
Yet if my conscience doth remain so clear,
And truth and honour be my steadfast guide,
Then shall these slanders vanish, and with cheer,
My name shall stand, unblemished, by their side.
    For what is built on hatred's rotten ground,
    Shall surely fall, with not a single sound.

###811###
The changing moon, that waxes and that wanes,
Doth mirror well the fortunes of mankind,
Now bright with hope, now shadowed by our pains,
And leaving traces of what's left behind.
The fleeting tide, that ebbs and then doth flow,
Doth speak of change, that all things must embrace,
And in its rise, and in its gentle low,
We see the passing of time and space.
So let us learn, from nature's constant art,
To bear the storms, and hail the coming sun,
And in each change, to play a nobler part,
Until our earthly course is fairly run.
    For life itself, a river, onward flows,
    And finds its end, where sweet oblivion grows.

###812###
Thy gentle hand, that strokes my weary brow,
Doth banish all the troubles of the day,
And bids the restless spirit to allow,
The passing cares to softly drift away.
Thy whispered words, like music to mine ear,
Do calm the storm that rages in my breast,
And banish doubt, and conquer every fear,
And bring my troubled soul a welcome rest.
So let me linger, in thy sweet embrace,
And hold this moment, precious and so dear,
And feel the warmth that time cannot erase,
And banish all that brings a falling tear.
    For in thy love, my truest solace lies,
    Reflected bright within thy loving eyes.

###813###
When fortune smiles, and all the world is fair,
And joys abound, like blossoms in the spring,
We apt to think that sorrow is not there,
And cease our watch, and cease our anxious wing.
But clouds do gather, swift and unannounced,
And tempests rise, to mar the fairest day,
And all our hopes, by sudden storms are trounced,
And pleasures fade, and swiftly fly away.
So let us stand, with courage strong and bold,
Prepared to face the trials that may come,
And in our hearts, a steadfast story told,
Of strength renewed, and battles overcome.
    For only through adversity we learn,
    The lessons that shall make our spirits burn.

###814###
The silent stars, that watch from realms on high,
Do speak of peace, and secrets they do keep,
And in their gaze, beneath the midnight sky,
Our earthly woes do seem to fall asleep.
The gentle moon, a beacon in the dark,
Doth cast its beam, a comfort to the soul,
And leaves upon the world its silver mark,
And makes our weary spirits feel quite whole.
So let me gaze, and find a sweet repose,
In nature's calm, and beauty so profound,
And feel the peace that from the heavens flows,
And on this hallowed, silent ground.
    For in this quiet, where no sounds are heard,
    My heart finds solace, and my soul is stirred.

###815###
When absence doth thy presence steal from me,
And miles do stretch between our yearning hearts,
I find no solace, and no joy can see,
As sorrow plays its ever-bitter parts.
The world is dim, and colours lose their hue,
And music sounds a melancholy strain,
And every hour doth seem to bid adieu,
To joys I knew, and shall not know again.
Yet still I hope, with faith that will not bend,
That soon the distance shall no more divide,
And in thy arms, my journey finds its end,
And by thy side, my spirit shall abide.
    So let me wait, with longing deep and true,
    Until the joyful hour I meet with you.

###816###
The golden sun, that climbs the eastern sky,
Doth chase away the shadows of the night,
And bids the weary world awake and fly,
To greet the dawn with gladness and with light.
The birds do sing, their joyous carols loud,
And nature smiles, in beauty newly dressed,
And banish darkness from the lifting cloud,
And bring the weary soul a welcome rest.
So let us rise, and greet the morning bright,
With hopeful hearts, and spirits strong and bold,
And banish fears, and put our doubts to flight,
And let our stories bravely be untold.
    For in this dawn, a promise we can find,
    Of brighter days, for all of humankind.

###817###
When storms do rage, and thunder shakes the sky,
And lightning's flash doth cleave the darkened air,
My spirit trembles, and my hopes do fly,
And I am lost in shadows of despair.
The wind doth howl, a mournful, angry sound,
And rain doth beat upon the fragile earth,
And all the world seems broken and unbound,
And lost to sorrow, from its very birth.
Yet even in the tempest's fiercest roar,
A hidden strength within my soul doth lie,
And I shall rise, and stand as I did before,
Beneath the clearing of the angry sky.
    For storms do pass, and leave a calmer scene,
    And nature heals, and what hath been, hath been.

###818###
Thy tender gaze, that meets my own with grace,
Doth fill my heart with comfort and with ease,
And in its depths, I find a resting place,
And banish all my troubles and my unease.
Thy gentle touch, a balm to all my pain,
Doth soothe my soul and bid my fears depart,
And in thy smile, my spirit lives again,
And finds its joy, and plays its happy part.
So let me dwell, within thy loving light,
And hold this moment, precious and so dear,
And banish shadows from my inner sight,
And keep thy memory ever ever near.
    For in thy love, my truest strength I find,
    A steadfast beacon, for my soul and mind.

###819###
The fleeting moments, like a passing dream,
Do steal away the bloom of youth so fair,
And leave us standing, by life's troubled stream,
With lines of age etched deeply in our hair.
The fires of passion, once so bright and bold,
Do dwindle low, and in their embers sleep,
And stories that were meant to be untold,
Are whispered low, where silent sorrows creep.
Yet in the heart, a wisdom may reside,
A gentler flame, that burns with steady light,
And in its glow, our calmer thoughts do guide,
And find in age a beauty, pure and bright.
    So let us greet the years that onward press,
    With quiet grace, and mindful tenderness.

###820###
When flattery doth whisper in mine ear,
With honeyed words, and promises so sweet,
I know its purpose, and I hold it dear,
As false a coin, that never will be meet.
The sycophant, with smiling, painted face,
Doth seek to gain, and to himself to bend,
And in his praise, no true affection's trace,
But hollow sound, that soon shall have its end.
I seek no praise, from those who speak for gain,
But in a friend, a truth that shall endure,
A loyal heart, that banishes all pain,
And offers solace, steadfast, firm, and pure.
    For honest words, though sometimes sharp they be,
    Are truer far, than false sincerity.

###821###
When youthful ardour doth my senses seize,
And passion's fire doth burn with eager haste,
I oft do court the gentle, passing breeze,
And dream of pleasures that are held in taste.
But reason whispers with a sober sound,
That fleeting joys are but a transient shade,
And when the bloom of summer is unbound,
The frost of age shall leave the spirit frayed.
So let me temper this impetuous soul,
And seek a love that time cannot decay,
A steady flame to make my being whole,
And banish winter with its brighter ray.
    For beauty fades, though youth may brightly gleam,
    But constant truth shall ever be my dream.

###822###
My dearest friend, whose worth I hold so high,
Whose faithful heart is like a steadfast star,
When clouds of sorrow dim the hopeful sky,
Thy solace doth my wounded spirit mar.
Thou art a balm to ease the aching smart,
A gentle hand to dry the falling tear,
And in thy presence, I do find my heart
Restored from doubt and freed from every fear.
Let Fortune frown, let worldly cares abound,
Thy constant love shall be my surest guide,
On this firm ground, my spirit shall be bound,
And in thy faith, my truest joys reside.
    So long as breath doth in my bosom lie,
    My loyal love shall ever be thine by.

###823###
The fleeting moments of this mortal span,
Like shadows dance and vanish in the light,
And all our dreams, since first the race began,
Are swept away upon the wings of night.
The mighty king, who rules with iron sway,
Must yield at last to death's impartial hand,
The wisest sage, who charts the starry way,
Shall find his knowledge cannot understand
The final summons, when the bell doth toll,
And earthly glories fade to dust and grey,
No wealth nor power can reclaim the soul,
Nor bribe the grim collector of the day.
    Thus, let us live, ere life itself doth cease,
    And find in virtue our eternal peace.

###824###
When winter's breath doth chill the verdant earth,
And frosty skies do banish summer's grace,
My thoughts do turn to seasons of my birth,
And seek the sun in some forgotten place.
The barren trees, that stand in naked pride,
Do mock the hues that once adorned their boughs,
And in their starkness, I do clearly spied
The passing years that furrow up our brows.
Yet hope doth whisper of the coming spring,
When life anew shall stir in dormant seed,
And joyful birds their cheerful anthems sing,
Dispelling gloom and satisfying need.
    So shall my spirit, though now cold and bare,
    Revive again, and banish all despair.

###825###
Thy beauteous face, a marvel to behold,
Doth shine with light, as doth the morning star,
More precious far than silver or than gold,
Whose radiant charms no earthly blight can mar.
Thy gentle eyes, like pools of deepest blue,
Do hold a spell that captures every gaze,
And in their depths, my truest thoughts do view,
And find themselves within their loving maze.
The rose's blush, the lily's snowy white,
Do pale and fade when set beside thy cheek,
And all the world doth seem a lesser sight,
When in thy presence, my poor words do speak.
    So let me live, and worship at thy shrine,
    And deem my life most wonderfully divine.

###826###
When fickle fortune turns her wheel around,
And smiles no more upon my humble state,
When bitter winds do howl with mournful sound,
And press me down beneath the heavy weight
Of worldly cares, that press upon my soul,
And dim the light that once did brightly burn,
I seek a refuge, to make my spirit whole,
Where true affection doth forever turn
To ease the burden, and to soothe the sting,
A steady hand to guide me through the storm,
A faithful breast, where comfort I may bring,
And find a shelter, safe and ever warm.
    For in such love, a treasure I do find,
    That far outweighs all riches of mankind.

###827###
The passing time, that steals our youthful bloom,
Doth leave its trace upon the fairest face,
And ushers in a melancholy gloom,
As years advance with unrelenting pace.
The laughter bright, the spirit free and bold,
Are tempered down by wisdom's solemn art,
And stories of the past are to be told,
With memories etched within the aging heart.
Yet in that wisdom, solace may be found,
A deeper knowing, and a clearer sight,
And on this ground, a truer joy is crowned,
That burns with steady, everlasting light.
    So let us age, with grace and quiet mind,
    And leave the fleeting follies far behind.

###828###
When envy's serpent, with its venomous tongue,
Doth whisper slanders, vile and full of spite,
And cruel words, like poisoned arrows flung,
Do seek to wound and dim my inner light,
I turn my gaze to virtue's steady beam,
And know my worth, unblemished and sincere,
And drown the poison in a hopeful dream,
And banish doubt, and conquer every fear.
For deeds well done, and honesty's pure flame,
Are shields against the malice of the crowd,
And though they speak and mock my humble name,
My conscience stands, unbent, and yet unbowed.
    So let them rail, their empty threats I scorn,
    My spirit's peace shall never be outworn.

###829###
The summer's sun, that warms the fertile land,
Doth call forth life from slumber, deep and long,
And nature's bounty, spread on every hand,
Doth sing to us a joyful, vibrant song.
The fields of green, with flowers newly sprung,
Do greet the eye with colours rich and rare,
And busy bees, with nectar sweetly strung,
Do flit and hum upon the balmy air.
The birds do trill their melodies so sweet,
And chase the shadows with their joyful flight,
And all the world seems perfect and complete,
Bathed in the glory of the golden light.
    So let us live, and taste this sweet delight,
    And hold this beauty, precious, day and night.

###830###
When absence doth the lover's heart possess,
And miles divide the souls that yearn to meet,
A silent ache, a poignant tenderness,
Doth make the waiting bitter, not so sweet.
The spoken word, the touch of gentle hand,
The shared glance, that speaks what lips can't say,
Are memories that in the heart do stand,
And brighten still the solitary day.
Yet hope doth whisper of a swift return,
When parted lovers shall embrace once more,
And kindred spirits, reunited, learn
The depth of love that absence did explore.
    So let us wait, though sorrow may increase,
    For reunion brings our hearts sweet peace.

###831###
The stars above, that twinkle in the night,
Do speak of realms beyond our mortal ken,
And in their vastness, and their silent light,
We glimpse a power far beyond all men.
The moon, that sheds her soft and silver gleam,
Doth cast a magic on the sleeping world,
And in its radiance, we often dream
Of wonders that are yet to be unfurled.
The changing seasons, and the ocean's roar,
The mighty mountains, reaching for the sky,
All speak of forces that we can't ignore,
And bid our humble, mortal spirits fly.
    So let us gaze, and wonder at the sight,
    And find in nature, truth and pure delight.

###832###
When fickle fate doth cruelly depart,
And leaves me stranded on a barren shore,
A hollow ache doth fill my weary heart,
And hope departs, to be seen nevermore.
The winds of change, that blow with bitter blast,
Do tear the sails of my once steady ship,
And cast me down, my dreams forever past,
With naught but dust upon my trembling lip.
Yet in this void, a strength I must command,
A will to rise, though fallen to the ground,
And with a steady, unresisting hand,
To build anew, where ruin can be found.
    For even storms, when they have done their worst,
    Leave fertile soil, from which new life is nursed.

###833###
Thy gentle voice, a melody so rare,
Doth soothe my soul and banish all my strife,
And in its music, I do find my share
Of earthly joy, and promise of new life.
Each tender word, a balm to heal the wound,
Each whispered phrase, a comfort to my ear,
On sacred ground, my truest hopes are found,
Dispelling shadows, and removing fear.
The nightingale, that sings in leafy bowers,
Doth envy thee, thy sweet and dulcet tone,
And all the earth, through fleeting, passing hours,
Doth find its peace when thy soft voice is known.
    So let me listen, till my days are done,
    And in thy song, my heart shall be outrun.

###834###
The poet's art, a mirror to the soul,
Doth capture truths that human hearts do feel,
And from its depths, doth stories oft unroll,
Of love and loss, and wounds that never heal.
The measured rhyme, the rhythm of the verse,
Doth lend a beauty to the darkest plight,
And in its power, we can oft rehearse
The human drama, bathed in purest light.
Though words may fade, and paper turn to dust,
The sentiment, it shall forever live,
A testament to love, and faith, and trust,
The deepest treasures that the heart can give.
    So let us write, ere inspiration cease,
    And find in verse, our everlasting peace.

###835###
When winter's frost doth bind the frozen stream,
And chilling winds do whistle through the trees,
My spirit longs for summer's golden dream,
And gentle warmth, and soft, caressing breeze.
The naked branches, reaching for the sky,
Do seem to mourn the verdant leaves now gone,
And in their starkness, I can well descry
The passing of each bright and hopeful dawn.
Yet deep within, a promise doth reside,
That spring will come, and banish winter's reign,
And life renewed, will banish all that died,
And bloom again, with beauty free from pain.
    So let me wait, with patience and with grace,
    For warmer days, and nature's sweet embrace.

###836###
Thy constancy, a rock against the tide,
Doth hold me fast when storms begin to brew,
And in thy strength, I safely may abide,
My trusted friend, forever firm and true.
When fickle hearts do waver and do stray,
And promises are broken and forgot,
Thy faithful spirit shines a brighter way,
And anchors me, where others may be not.
The shifting sands, the waters that do churn,
Cannot affect thy purpose, pure and deep,
To thee, my loyalty shall ever turn,
And in thy care, my weary soul shall sleep.
    So let us stand, through all the coming years,
    United firm, dispelling all our fears.

###837###
The fleeting shadow of a passing cloud,
Doth scarce compare to moments of despair,
When sorrow's voice, so mournful and so loud,
Doth fill the soul with burdens hard to bear.
The weight of grief, a heavy, crushing chain,
Doth bind the spirit, and impede its flight,
And in its grip, we feel a piercing pain,
That robs the world of all its hopeful light.
Yet even darkness cannot last for aye,
And morning dawns, though night may seem so long,
And from the depths, a strength shall find its way,
To lift us up, and make our spirits strong.
    So let us weep, and let our tears then flow,
    For after sorrow, brighter joys shall grow.

###838###
The blush of dawn, that paints the eastern sky,
Doth herald forth a new and hopeful day,
And chases night, and bids the shadows fly,
And chase the lingering darkness far away.
The birds awake, and trill their morning song,
A joyful chorus, rising in the air,
And all the world, where shadows lingered long,
Doth greet the light, and cast away all care.
The dewdrop gleams, upon the grassy blade,
Reflecting heaven, in its tiny sphere,
And nature's beauty, perfectly displayed,
Doth banish doubt, and conquer every fear.
    So let us rise, and greet the sun's warm ray,
    And live with purpose, till the close of day.

###839###
When age doth steal the vigour of my youth,
And time's decree doth furrow up my brow,
I'll cling to virtue, and I'll seek for truth,
And find my solace in the here and now.
The fleeting joys that once did light my way,
May dim and fade, as seasons come and go,
But in the heart, a steady, inward ray,
Of understanding, shall continue to glow.
The wisdom gained, through trials and through tears,
Shall be my guide, my comfort, and my friend,
And in its light, I'll conquer all my fears,
And find a peace that shall endure to end.
    So let me age, with dignity and grace,
    And wear the years, upon my smiling face.

###840###
Thy love, a treasure, richer than all gold,
Doth fill my heart with an unceasing fire,
A story sweet, that never shall grow old,
The very essence of my soul's desire.
Each tender glance, each softly spoken word,
Doth weave a spell, that holds me in its thrall,
And in thy presence, I am truly stirred,
And gladly yield my spirit, giving all.
The world may rage, and fortunes may depart,
But this true bond, shall never be undone,
A sacred flame, imprinted on my heart,
A love that shines, like never setting sun.
    So let us cherish, this our perfect state,
    And find in love, our everlasting fate.

###841###
When as the sun doth cast his golden beam,
And chase the lingering shadows of the night,
My heart doth stir as from a troubled dream,
Awakened by thy beauty, clear and bright.
The birds do sing their sweetest melodies,
A testament to nature's joyful art,
But all their song doth seem but faint unease,
Compared to music playing in my heart.
For when I gaze upon thy wondrous face,
A thousand joys within my spirit bloom,
And time itself doth lose its measured pace,
Dispelling sorrow and all shades of gloom.
So let me drown in thy delightful sight,
And live forever in this blessed light.

###842###
The fleeting hours, like pilfering thieves, do steal,
The bloom of youth that once adorned my brow,
And leave behind the truths that age reveal,
A wrinkled map of all I was ere now.
My strength doth wane, my vigour starts to fade,
And nimble feet grow slow and prone to rest,
Where once with eager steps I was arrayed,
Now weariness doth hold me in its nest.
Yet in thy love, a fountain fresh I find,
That washes clean the dust of passing years,
And stills the anxious murmurings of my mind,
And dries the well of unavailing tears.
So in thy grace, I find a second spring,
And though I age, thy love makes young my soul sing.

###843###
When envious Fortune doth her wheel avert,
And casts me down from heights of sweet content,
My soul doth bleed, my spirit is expert,
In bearing burdens that the heavens have sent.
The world doth seem a stage of bitter woe,
Where fortune's smile is but a fleeting guest,
And every joy doth swiftly ebb and flow,
Leaving behind a heart that finds no rest.
But then thy presence, like a guiding star,
Doth pierce the gloom and show a brighter way,
And though the trials of my life be far,
Thy constancy doth banish disarray.
So in thy steadfast love, my anchor lies,
A haven sure beneath tempestuous skies.

###844###
The roseate dawn, with gentle hand, doth paint,
The eastern sky with hues of rose and gold,
Dispelling darkness, making shadows faint,
A lovely story waiting to unfold.
The dewdrop gleams upon the verdant blade,
A tiny jewel, reflecting morning's light,
And nature wakes, in beauty unafraid,
To greet the day and banish shades of night.
So too, my love, when first thy spirit shone,
Upon my soul, a darkness deep and vast,
Thy gentle presence, like a dawn, was known,
A ray of hope, a die forever cast.
And in that light, my heart began to mend,
A love eternal, without earthly end.

###845###
The swift-winged hours in hurried sequence fly,
And bear away the moments we hold dear,
As clouds do scud across the summer sky,
And leave behind a void, a silent fear.
The bloom of life, that once did brightly shine,
Now fades and wilts, its former glory past,
And wrinkles tell of seasons that decline,
A legacy of moments that did last.
But in thy gaze, I find a timeless grace,
A beauty that no earthly force can mar,
And in thy love, a safe and dwelling place,
That shines more brightly than the morning star.
So let us seize each moment as it flies,
And build a love that never truly dies.

###846###
When stormy winds do rage and skies are grey,
And tempests threaten to our fragile bark,
My spirit quails and longs to fly away,
To find a haven from the chilling dark.
The world's a stage where sorrows often play,
And fortune's frown doth cast a heavy pall,
And hope's faint lamp doth flicker and decay,
As shadows lengthen and as spirits fall.
But then thy voice, a soothing, gentle sound,
Doth whisper courage to my trembling soul,
And in thy strength, a steadfast truth is found,
That makes my shattered spirit once more whole.
So let us face the trials side by side,
With love our shield, and truth our constant guide.

###847###
The subtle poison of unkindly words,
Can wound the soul more deeply than a blade,
And break the spirit, like a flock of birds,
That scatter, frightened, from a sudden raid.
A careless jest, a scornful, bitter tone,
Can leave a scar that time can scarce efface,
And sow the seeds of discord, deeply sown,
That choke the tender blooms of loving grace.
But thy sweet counsel, like a gentle balm,
Doth heal the wounds that lesser words impart,
And brings my troubled spirit to a calm,
And stills the tempest raging in my heart.
So let thy kindness be my constant guide,
And let my tongue with gentle truth abide.

###848###
The fleeting fancy of a summer's day,
Doth vanish swift, when autumn winds begin,
And beauty's blush doth quickly fade away,
As chilling frosts their icy reign do win.
The transient joys that mortals chase and hold,
Are like the dew that vanishes with sun,
A tale too briefly, and too loosely told,
Whose fragile thread is swiftly overwon.
But thy affection, steadfast and sincere,
Doth mock the changing seasons and their power,
And in its truth, I banish every fear,
And find my comfort in each passing hour.
So let this love, like ancient oaks, endure,
And in its strength, my spirit be secure.

###849###
When jealous thoughts like serpents do arise,
And whisper doubts within my troubled mind,
They cloud my vision and they dim my eyes,
And leave my loving heart in chains confined.
The fair reports of others, falsely told,
Can poison trust and breed a bitter strife,
And turn a heart of purest, honest gold,
To dross and ruin, and a troubled life.
But thy true faith, a beacon strong and bright,
Doth pierce the fog of falsehood and of lies,
And guides me safely through the darkest night,
And shows the truth that in thy spirit lies.
So let suspicion vanish with the dawn,
And let our trust be ever newly born.

###850###
The babbling brook, that skips o'er mossy stone,
Doth sing a song of innocence and glee,
A joyful sound, to nature's music known,
That dances onward to the boundless sea.
The gentle breeze that stirs the leafy bough,
Doth whisper secrets to the listening wood,
And life's sweet symphony doth flow,
In harmonies divinely understood.
So when I hear the music of thy voice,
My soul doth echo with a kindred sound,
And in that harmony, I do rejoice,
As peace and perfect happiness are found.
For in thy love, a sweeter song I hear,
Than any sung by brook or breeze so clear.

###851###
The painted mask that worldly men do wear,
Doth hide the truth of their most secret heart,
And hides their malice and their dark despair,
And plays a false and captivating part.
They smile and flatter, with a cunning art,
And promise comfort, though their aim is gain,
And play the player, to a bitter start,
And leave their victims in a sea of pain.
But thy sincere and open, honest gaze,
Doth hold no guile, no artifice, no show,
And in its truth, my spirit finds its ways,
And in thy virtue, I do truly grow.
So let me shun the false, the painted face,
And find my solace in thy honest grace.

###852###
The fading embers of a dying fire,
Doth cast a glow, both feeble and so faint,
Reflecting thoughts of lost and vain desire,
And painting shadows, like a weary saint.
The warmth departs, and leaves a chilling air,
Where once the flames did leap with vibrant might,
A silent testament to all despair,
And dimming embers in the coming night.
So too my love, when absent from thy sight,
My spirit chills, and comfort starts to flee,
And all the world is cloaked in darkest night,
Until thy presence brings its warmth to me.
So let us ever be in close embrace,
And keep the fire of love in its true place.

###853###
When Cupid's dart doth pierce the unsuspecting soul,
And lodge itself within the tender breast,
A fevered longing takes its wild control,
And grants the heart no moment's ease or rest.
The world is changed, and painted in new hues,
Where common sights are filled with strange delight,
And every thought, the lover oft pursues,
Is bent upon the object of his might.
So have I learned this passion's fierce decree,
When first thy beauty struck me with its dart,
And now my spirit longs eternally,
To dwell within the chambers of thy heart.
So let me be by thy sweet love possessed,
And find in thy dear presence all my rest.

###854###
The sturdy oak that braves the winter's blast,
And stands unmoved by winds that fiercely blow,
Doth show a strength that shall forever last,
And mock the frailness of the passing snow.
The ancient rocks that face the ocean's roar,
And bear the brunt of every crashing wave,
Stand firm and constant on the shifting shore,
And from the tide, their very being save.
So is thy love, a bastion strong and deep,
Against the storms of life that rage and swell,
A promise that my heart shall ever keep,
And in its truth, a heaven I can tell.
So let us be like these, in strength aligned,
A love that time and tempest leaves behind.

###855###
The fleeting shadow of a passing cloud,
Doth momentarily obscure the sun,
And cast a gloom upon the sunlit crowd,
Before its hurried journey is outrun.
The momentary darkness can deceive,
And make us fear the light has ceased to be,
But in a moment, we can then believe,
The sun still shines, for all the world to see.
So when thy absence casts a shade so deep,
And doubt's dark specter starts to fill my mind,
I know thy love, a promise it doth keep,
And in its light, a brighter truth I find.
So let this gloom but serve to make us prize,
The lasting sunshine of our loving eyes.

###856###
The painter's brush, though skilled with subtle hand,
Can ne'er portray the beauty of thy grace,
Nor capture what my eyes can understand,
The perfect form and wonder of thy face.
The poet's quill, though dipped in finest ink,
Can only hint at passions that reside,
And of thy virtues, can but faintly think,
And speak of truths thou dost within thee hide.
For in thy soul, a deeper beauty lies,
Than mortal art can ever hope to claim,
A radiant light that sparkles in thine eyes,
And sets my captive spirit all aflame.
So let my love, though poor, still strive to tell,
The boundless worth within thee, loved so well.

###857###
When worldly cares do press with heavy hand,
And steal the peace that makes my spirit whole,
And fill my thoughts with burdens I can't stand,
And take from me my comfort and my soul.
The weight of sorrow doth begin to grow,
And drown the joy that once did brightly gleam,
And all the world seems filled with naught but woe,
And life itself becomes a troubled dream.
But then thy voice, a melody so sweet,
Doth banish shadows, and dispel the fear,
And makes my weary, burdened heart complete,
And brings thy solace ever close and near.
So let me lean on thee, and find my ease,
And in thy love, my troubled spirit please.

###858###
The ancient ruins, standing proud and tall,
Doth speak of glories that have long since passed,
Of empires fallen, and of kingdoms' fall,
Whose fleeting grandeur could not ever last.
The stones do whisper tales of by-gone days,
Of heroes' deeds, and battles fought and won,
And cast a spell in their mysterious ways,
Beneath the moon, and in the setting sun.
So shall our love, though time may seek to fray,
And mar the edges of our fondest vows,
Endure beyond the passing of the day,
And bloom anew, like evergreens on boughs.
For in its depth, a strength doth still reside,
That shall against the ravages of time abide.

###859###
The fragrant bloom that scents the summer air,
Doth draw the bee with promise of sweet prize,
And in its petals, finds a treasure rare,
Reflected in its many-faceted eyes.
The honeyed dew, that glistens on the leaf,
Doth tempt the ant with sustenance and gain,
And satisfies its hunger, past belief,
And eases hunger, banishes its pain.
So does thy love, a nectar rich and deep,
Doth draw my soul and quench its thirsty fire,
And promises the joy I long to keep,
And fills my heart with ever sweet desire.
So let me feast upon this love so true,
And in its sweetness, find my world anew.

###860###
When envious tongues do wag and spread their lies,
And stain the honour that is justly earned,
And seek to dim the lustre of bright skies,
And leave the honest spirit deeply spurned.
The poisoned dart of calumny doth fly,
And wounds the soul with bitterness and hate,
And makes the noblest virtues seem to die,
And seals the slandered soul to cruelest fate.
But thy pure heart, untouched by rumour's blight,
Doth stand a witness to my true intent,
And shines with steadfast, uncorrupted light,
A shield against the falsehoods heaven-sent.
So let them speak, their venom can't prevail,
When thy good favour shall forever hail.

###861###
When Fortune smiles and all my skies are fair,
My heart doth leap with unalloyed delight,
And banish thence all doubt and all despair,
As golden sun dispels the darkest night.
But ah, how swiftly turns her fickle face,
And shadows fall where sunshine lately played,
No longer doth her favour grant me grace,
But leaves my hopes and dreams in disarrayed.
So fragile is the joy that mortals know,
A fleeting guest that doth not long abide,
Like summer flowers that quickly cease to grow,
And in the winter's chilling breath are died.
   Thus is our bliss a momentary gleam,
   A waking phantom in a troubled dream.

###862###
My love, whose eyes like stars do brightly shine,
Doth cast a beam upon my mortal soul,
A heavenly light, a radiance divine,
That makes my shattered spirit strong and whole.
Her voice, a melody that doth enchant,
Doth charm the ear and soothes the troubled breast,
A silken whisper, a melodious chant,
That puts my restless, weary heart to rest.
Her touch, a spark that doth my being fire,
And melts the ice that chilled my lonely days,
A sweet sensation, a fervent desire,
That sets my very inmost soul ablaze.
   So in her presence, all my griefs do cease,
   And I find solace, comfort, and sweet peace.

###863###
The creeping time, with unrelenting pace,
Doth steal away the bloom from beauty's cheek,
And carves deep lines upon a youthful face,
And makes the strong and valiant spirit weak.
The raven locks that once did gleam so bright,
Shall turn to silver, thin and scant and grey,
The dancing eyes that shone with youthful light,
Shall dim and fade and vanish quite away.
The sturdy limb that bore a heavy load,
Shall tremble now and scarce support the frame,
The proudest heart that trod a noble road,
Shall yield at last to Time's relentless claim.
   Yet love, if true, shall scorn this mortal blight,
   And burn more fiercely in eternal light.

###864###
When I do see the fairest creatures rise,
And feel the stirrings of a warm desire,
I know that Nature, with her subtle lies,
Doth forge the fuel for love's consuming fire.
The blushing rose, the lily pure and white,
The gentle dove that coos with loving sound,
All speak of passion, beauty, and delight,
And in their forms, true love may e'er be found.
But when I turn my gaze to thee, my dear,
My heart doth beat a rhythm swift and bold,
For in thy face, all charms do reappear,
A story of pure beauty to unfold.
   So Nature's bounty seems but pale and cold,
   Compared to thee, whose worth cannot be told.

###865###
My muse, thy beauty doth inspire my quill,
To paint in words the wonders of thy grace,
And make the silent, empty pages fill,
With praises due to thy most lovely face.
Thy hair, like threads of spun and golden light,
Doth frame a brow where wisdom hath its seat,
Thy eyes, two pools of deepest, darkest night,
Where truth and gentleness do sweetly meet.
Thy lips, like cherries, ripe and plump and red,
Do promise kisses, soft and warm and deep,
And in their curve, sweet words are softly said,
That lull the weary soul to gentle sleep.
   So let me write, till my last breath is drawn,
   Of thee, my love, from dusk till rosy dawn.

###866###
Why doth the sun, that shines with golden ray,
Not warm my heart when thou art far from me?
The brightest noon doth seem a dreary day,
When from my sight thy presence doth decree.
The birds do sing, their carols sweet and clear,
But their glad songs do mock my lonely state,
No joy can pierce the veil of doubt and fear,
When absence seals my melancholy fate.
The gentle breeze that stirs the verdant leaves,
Doth whisper tales of solace and of rest,
But to my soul, no comfort it receives,
Whilst thou, my love, art absent from my breast.
   So let me pine, and in my sorrow drown,
   Until thy smile shall wear love's radiant crown.

###867###
When I consider how my years do fly,
And see the hastening of my mortal end,
I fear the shadow of the hour I die,
And leave this world, my dearest, absent friend.
For all the treasures I have gathered here,
The worldly gain, the honour and the praise,
Can bring no solace, quell no rising fear,
When I must tread life's final, lonely maze.
But if thy love, a beacon bright and bold,
Shall shine upon me in that final hour,
Then shall my spirit, worth more than fine gold,
Escape the grave, and triumph o'er its power.
   So let thy love my final comfort be,
   And Death itself shall hold no dread for me.

###868###
When jealous thoughts do pierce my weary mind,
And whisper doubts of thy most constant love,
I feel my hopeful spirit left behind,
And sink to depths that I cannot reprove.
The serpent's hiss, the poison of distrust,
Doth taint the sweetness of our shared delight,
And turn my purest faith to bitter dust,
And plunge my day into the darkest night.
Yet when I look into thine honest eyes,
And see no falsehood, nor deceitful gleam,
My foolish fears like fleeting shadows rise,
And vanish as a half-forgotten dream.
   So let me trust, and put my fears to flight,
   And bask once more within thy loving light.

###869###
The world doth oft with empty words deceive,
And praise the deed that hath no honest core,
The hollow flatterer, we do believe,
And cast aside the truth we should adore.
So many speak with tongues of honeyed art,
And weave their webs of falsehood and of lies,
To win the favour of a foolish heart,
And blind the unwatchful, unsuspecting eyes.
But thy plain speech, though blunt it may appear,
Doth hold a truth that shines with steady flame,
More precious far than promises held dear,
That fade and vanish, leaving naught but shame.
   So let me hold thy honest words in store,
   And love their truth, and ask for nothing more.

###870###
When I reflect upon the summer's end,
And see the leaves of gold and crimson fall,
I know that all things beautiful must bend,
And yield at last to Nature's solemn call.
The fervent heat that warmed the sun-drenched days,
Doth fade and dwindle, leaving naught but chill,
The vibrant hues that filled the verdant maze,
Do pale and wither, standing stark and still.
So too, my youth, that once did brightly burn,
Must dim and fade, and leave me weak and old,
To all of Nature's changes I must turn,
And in her ancient lessons be controlled.
   Yet love, like spring, can bid the earth revive,
   And keep my heart eternally alive.

###871###
I do not pride myself on noble birth,
Nor boast of riches that I may possess,
For worldly goods hold little lasting worth,
And breed in men a greedy, vain excess.
The gilded pomp, the honours men pursue,
Are but a fleeting show, a painted scene,
That doth conceal a heart both false and untrue,
And mask the hollow man that lies within.
But in thy love, I find a greater wealth,
A treasure richer than all earthly store,
A balm for every sickness and for stealth,
That keeps my spirit safe forevermore.
   So let me cherish, with a grateful mind,
   The truest riches that in thee I find.

###872###
When outward shows do blind the common eye,
And men do judge by garb and outward mien,
They fail to see the spirit soaring high,
Or know the virtue that lies deep unseen.
The shining armour, and the noble crest,
May hide a craven heart, a soul of dread,
Whilst humble raiment may conceal the best,
And noblest thoughts within a lowly head.
So let me look beyond the outward guise,
And seek the essence of the soul within,
Where truth and goodness ever shall arise,
And where true beauty truly doth begin.
   For in thy heart, I find a noble grace,
   That shines more brightly than a kingly face.

###873###
The fleeting moments, like swift birds in flight,
Do pass me by, and leave me in the dust,
And steal away the hours of pure delight,
Betraying all my fond and hopeful trust.
The youthful vigour, once my proudest boast,
Doth wane and falter, leaving me quite spent,
And I do feel myself a lonely ghost,
Upon life's fading, weary firmament.
But in the memory of thy sweet smile,
I find a solace that doth still sustain,
And in that thought, I shall endure a while,
And banish all the shadows and the pain.
   So let me hold these precious moments fast,
   For in thy love, true joy shall ever last.

###874###
When winter's chill doth grip the barren land,
And icy winds do bite with frosty breath,
The world lies stark, beneath a frozen hand,
And seems to slumber in a gentle death.
The trees stand bare, their leafy crowns all gone,
The rivers cease their murmuring, soft song,
And darkness reigns from dusk till early dawn,
Where life and warmth did lately dance along.
But in my heart, a fire doth brightly burn,
A steadfast flame that Time cannot subdue,
And to its warmth, my spirit shall return,
And find its strength and comfort there anew.
   For love like thine, a constant, guiding star,
   Doth warm me best, no matter where we are.

###875###
My quill doth falter, and my ink runs dry,
When I attempt to speak of thy great worth,
For human tongue can never truly vie,
With all the wonders that thou dost give birth.
The painter's brush, the sculptor's patient hand,
May strive to capture beauty, fair and bright,
But none can fully on this mortal land,
Embody all thy pure and radiant light.
Thy grace, a mystery beyond compare,
Thy virtue, a star that doth forever gleam,
Thy kindness, a balm to banish all despair,
A waking truth within a blissful dream.
   So let my verse, though humble it may be,
   Proclaim the endless excellence of thee.

###876###
When sorrow's cloud doth dim my hopeful eye,
And shadows gather in my troubled soul,
I turn to thee, beneath the weeping sky,
And find a peace that makes me strong and whole.
Thy gentle touch, a balm to soothe my pain,
Thy whispered words, a comfort to my ear,
They wash away the bitter, stinging rain,
And banish all my doubt and every fear.
The storms of life may rage with furious might,
And beat upon me with their chilling blow,
But in thy love, I find a guiding light,
That helps me onward, though the way be slow.
   So let me lean upon thy steadfast breast,
   And find in thee my haven and my rest.

###877###
The passing years, like swift ships on the sea,
Do bear away the bloom of youth and health,
And leave behind a more infirm degree,
And dim the shine of worldly, fading wealth.
The strength that once did make me stand so tall,
Now falters, weak, and bends beneath the strain,
The vibrant colours that did once enthrall,
Now pale and fade, and leave me naught but pain.
Yet in the mirror of thy loving gaze,
I see a beauty that doth still endure,
A youthful spirit that through passing days,
Remains undimmed, and ever shall be pure.
   So let me see myself in thee, my dear,
   And banish age, and conquer every fear.

###878###
When envious tongues do wag with spiteful sound,
And whisper tales of slander and of blame,
They seek to drag my honour to the ground,
And cast a shadow on my honest name.
But falsehood's darts, though sharp they may appear,
Can never pierce the armour of my truth,
Nor can their venom cause a single tear,
When guided by the strength of constant youth.
For in thy heart, a judgment pure and right,
Doth see beyond the malice and the lies,
And in that faith, I find my greatest might,
And smile at all their petty, vain surprise.
   So let them speak, their malice shall not win,
   When thy true love doth ever dwell within.

###879###
The world doth judge by what the eye can see,
And counts the riches that the hand can hold,
But true worth lies in what can never be,
Acquired by coins of silver or of gold.
The gaudy cloak, the jewelled, shining crown,
May mask a soul that's empty, cold, and vain,
Whilst humble garb may hide a heart renowned,
For gentle virtues that shall ever reign.
So when I look on thee, I see a grace,
That doth surpass all outward, earthly show,
A noble spirit shining from thy face,
A truth that only faithful hearts can know.
   For in thy essence, beauty doth reside,
   Where virtue's purest streams forever glide.

###880###
When in the quiet of the evening's hush,
My thoughts do turn to thee, my dearest love,
My heart doth beat with an ecstatic rush,
As if to soar with angels high above.
The moon doth cast its soft and silvery gleam,
Upon the world, now slumbering and still,
And in its light, I see a waking dream,
That doth my very soul with rapture fill.
Thy image, fair, doth haunt my waking hours,
And in my sleep, thy presence I embrace,
More sweet than nectar from the fairest flowers,
More comforting than any earthly place.
   So let me dwell within this loving trance,
   And in thy memory, forever dance.

###881###
When Phoebus doth his golden chariot guide,
And chases hence the shadows of the night,
My soul awakes, with hopeful spirit eyed,
And longs to bask within his radiant light.
But ah, that light, though fair it may appear,
Doth blind the eye that gazes on its gleam,
And fills my heart with a most anxious fear,
That all is but a fleeting, painted dream.
For though the day may promise joy and mirth,
And banish all the sorrows of the dark,
It cannot soothe the aching of the earth,
Nor quench the flames that in my spirit spark.
   So is my love, a sun that shines too bright,
   And drowns my senses in its endless light.

###882###
The rose, that blushes with the morning dew,
And scents the air with perfume sweet and rare,
Though fair it blooms, its beauty is but through
A passing hour, that vanishes in air.
So is thy grace, a blossom on the vine,
That doth enthrall my senses with its hue,
But ere I clasp it, doth thy favour pine,
And leave me longing for what was so true.
The summer's lease hath all too short a date,
And winter's chill doth hasten its decay,
So must thy beauty yield to cruel fate,
And from my sight be borne ere close of day.
   Yet in my heart, thy memory shall reside,
   A phantom bloom, where joys and sorrows hide.

###883###
When I consider how my years are spent,
And see how time doth steal my youth away,
My former pleasures now are wholly rent,
And shadows lengthen at the close of day.
The raven hair that graced my youthful brow,
Is silvered now, with winter's icy hand,
And wrinkles deep upon my visage show,
The weary journey through this mortal land.
I mourn the days of vigour and of might,
When strength did lend me courage for the fray,
But now I shrink before the fading light,
And yield my spirit to the coming grey.
   Yet still I hope, though fading be my flame,
   To find some solace in remembrance' name.

###884###
Thy voice, a music that doth stir my soul,
And fills the void where silent sorrows dwelled,
Doth make my wounded spirit once more whole,
And all my worldly cares are gently quelled.
When thou dost speak, the nightingale doth cease,
To shame its song with melodies so rare,
And gentle zephyrs whisper words of peace,
That banish every trouble and despair.
Oh, would that I could hoard each precious sound,
And keep it safe within my loving breast,
That when the storm of silence doth surround,
My heart might find its comfort and its rest.
   But alas, the ear can hold but fleeting sound,
   And in its absence, sorrow doth abound.

###885###
My love, I cannot measure with a span,
The depth of feeling that my bosom bears,
Nor can I tell, since first this love began,
How much it grows, and conquers all my cares.
It is a sea, whose tides do ever rise,
And drown the shores of reason and of sense,
A boundless firmament before my eyes,
Whose starry light doth banish all offence.
No earthly measure can its stature tell,
No earthly treasure can its worth attain,
It is a bond that time shall never quell,
A burning fever that doth still remain.
   So know, my love, this truth thou canst not flee,
   My heart is thine, eternally for thee.

###886###
The world doth rage with tempest and with storm,
And fortune's wheel doth turn with cruelest might,
But in thy presence, I find shelter warm,
And banish all the terrors of the night.
Thy gentle eye, a haven for my soul,
Doth calm the winds that fiercely buffet me,
And makes my fractured spirit once more whole,
And sets my troubled mind at liberty.
Though worldly woes may press and sorrows sting,
And envious tongues do whisper tales of doubt,
Thy constant love doth every comfort bring,
And puts my every anxious fear to rout.
   So let the tempests beat and fortunes frown,
   Thy steadfast love shall be my earthly crown.

###887###
When envious eyes do cast their baleful stare,
And whisper rumours to my dear one's ear,
I fear the poison that they gladly share,
And dread the moment when my love draws near.
For malice hath a tongue that doth deceive,
And paints the innocent in darkest shade,
And makes the truest heart begin to grieve,
When truth and beauty are by lies betrayed.
Oh, would that all such envious souls might see,
The noble truth that in my heart doth lie,
And know that constant is my love for thee,
And that no slander can its truth deny.
   But alas, the ear is often deaf to truth,
   And listens gladly to the slanderer's ruth.

###888###
My pen doth falter, and my ink doth fade,
When I attempt thy virtues to impart,
For words are weak, and colours are decayed,
To paint the beauty of thy noble heart.
The artist's brush, though skilled and fine it be,
Can ne'er achieve what I do long to show,
The radiant spirit shining forth from thee,
Whose gentle lustre doth forever glow.
The poet's verse, though eloquent and deep,
Doth fail to capture all that thou dost seem,
The secrets that thy loving glances keep,
The waking wonder of a waking dream.
   So let my silence speak what words cannot,
   The adoration that I've never forgot.

###889###
The fleeting hours, that swift do pass us by,
And bear away our youth with hurried pace,
Do make me fear to see them fade and die,
And leave behind no vestige of their grace.
For beauty's bloom, though vibrant it may seem,
Is but a transient guest upon the bough,
And life itself, a momentary gleam,
That vanishes ere we can grasp it now.
So let us seize the moments as they fly,
And hold them dear, ere they be lost to time,
For in their passing, we ourselves shall die,
And leave no echo of our earthly prime.
   Yet in thy love, a timeless beauty dwells,
   That conquers death, and all its mortal spells.

###890###
When absence doth thy dear form hide from view,
And lonely hours do drag with leaden feet,
My soul doth yearn for tidings sent from you,
And longs to hear thy voice, so pure and sweet.
The sun may shine, the birds may sing their song,
But all is barren, empty, and forlorn,
Without thy presence, where I do belong,
My heart doth ache, and weary till the morn.
I count the minutes, and I mark the days,
Until again thy radiant face I see,
And chase away these melancholy ways,
That absence hath inflicted unto me.
   So haste thee back, my love, my guiding star,
   And heal the wound that keeps us now so far.

###891###
The flatterer's tongue, with honeyed words doth weave,
A tapestry of lies, so fair to see,
And makes the foolish heart too soon believe,
The empty promises of vanity.
He speaks of love, where hate doth truly lie,
Of loyalty, where treason finds its nest,
And blinds the eye that looks with simple eye,
And lulls the trusting spirit into rest.
Beware, my love, such siren songs of praise,
For they conceal a serpent in their guise,
And lead thee down to dark and tangled ways,
Where truth is lost, and all thy joy then dies.
   Let honest love, though plain it may appear,
   Be all thou seekest, and thy spirit's dear.

###892###
My sighs, like winds that through the forest blow,
Do whisper tales of love that cannot cease,
And in my tears, a secret grief doth flow,
That finds no comfort, and no sweet release.
My heart, a cage, where sorrow doth reside,
Doth beat its wings against the bars of pain,
And longs for freedom, where it might confide,
Its every sorrow, and its secret stain.
But ah, the bars are strong, the lock is fast,
And no key fits to set my spirit free,
So must I bear this burden, to the last,
And pine in silence for eternity.
   Yet in thy love, I find a fleeting balm,
   That stills the storm, and makes my spirit calm.

###893###
The bloom of youth, though fair it doth appear,
Is but a season, destined soon to fade,
And beauty's hour, though held so passing dear,
Is but a shadow, by the daylight made.
For time, the thief, doth steal with silent tread,
And wrinkles carve where smoothness once did lie,
And strength departs, and vigour lies instead,
Beneath the gaze of his unyielding eye.
So let us not in fleeting beauty trust,
Nor deem our prime eternal and our own,
But build our love on worth that is not dust,
A stronger foundation, where it can be known.
   For outward grace will wither and decay,
   But inner truth shall last beyond its day.

###894###
When I behold the stars in heaven's vault,
And see the moon in silver splendour gleam,
My soul doth yearn, and finds itself at fault,
To think that such perfection is a dream.
The cosmic dance, so ordered and so grand,
Doth stir within me wonder and delight,
And makes me feel a part of that vast land,
That stretches far beyond my mortal sight.
And in that vision, I do see thy face,
Reflected there, a star among the night,
Whose gentle beams do fill this lonely space,
And fill my heart with everlasting light.
   So in the heavens, and in thee I find,
   A beauty that doth captivate my mind.

###895###
My love doth wax, as doth the waxing moon,
And shines with brightness, ever strong and true,
And shall not wane, though sorrow come too soon,
Nor lose its lustre, though the world be new.
For in thy heart, a constant truth I find,
A steadfast anchor in the stormy sea,
That calms the tempest and doth ease my mind,
And sets my anxious spirit ever free.
Though fickle fortune may her favour change,
And friends depart, and earthly joys decay,
My love for thee shall never disarrange,
But burn with ardour, till my dying day.
   So let the seasons turn, the years go by,
   My love for thee shall never cease to fly.

###896###
The winter's chill doth bite with icy breath,
And strips the trees of all their leafy pride,
And nature seems to welcome silent death,
Where all the summer's verdure doth now hide.
The world is clad in garments of the snow,
And silence reigns where birds did sweetly sing,
And all is barren, where the streams do flow,
And life's bright colours to the frost do cling.
But in my heart, a summer doth remain,
A constant warmth, that winter cannot chill,
For in thy love, I find a sweet refrain,
That makes my weary spirit once more thrill.
   So let the world lie frozen and asleep,
   My love for thee, its warmth shall ever keep.

###897###
When I do think upon thy loving smile,
And hear the music of thy gentle voice,
My heart doth leap, and banish every guile,
And in that moment, I can but rejoice.
The world may frown, and fortune may conspire,
To cast me down, and fill my soul with dread,
But still thy image doth my soul inspire,
And lifts me up from where I lay abed.
Thou art the sun that chases clouds away,
The guiding star that lights my darkest night,
And in thy presence, I can safely stay,
And banish all my fears with pure delight.
   So let me dwell within thy loving gaze,
   And lose myself in these most happy days.

###898###
My verse, though humble, doth attempt to trace,
The noble outline of thy virtues rare,
And in each line, I seek to find a place,
To show the world how much thy soul doth bear.
But oh, my skill doth lag behind my will,
And words do falter, when I would impart,
The depth of feeling that doth my heart fill,
And burns with ardour, like a lover's dart.
So let my efforts be a willing plea,
To show the love that in my spirit lies,
And though imperfect, may it speak for me,
And bring a smile unto thy loving eyes.
   For though my ink be weak, and paper thin,
   My heart's true tribute lies deep within.

###899###
The world's applause, a fleeting, hollow sound,
That fades and vanishes ere it is heard,
Is but a bauble, on uncertain ground,
A fickle praise, bestowed by every word.
The crowd doth cheer, and then doth turn away,
To seek new idols, and new songs to sing,
And leaves the past, to greet a brighter day,
And all its former favour doth unstring.
But in thy gaze, a truer worth I find,
A judgment pure, that doth my spirit lift,
And in thy favour, I am well-defined,
A gift more precious than all earthly gift.
   So let the world bestow its empty praise,
   Thy constant love doth brighten all my days.

###900###
When I do sleep, and dreams do fill my head,
And transport me to realms beyond compare,
It is thy image, that doth there be spread,
And fills the void with beauty rich and rare.
We walk through fields, where summer flowers bloom,
And hear the streams in gentle music play,
And banish hence all sorrow and all gloom,
And live as if it were eternal day.
But ah, the dawn doth break, the dream doth flee,
And leaves me here, in waking's lonely state,
To yearn again for sweet society,
And curse the waking hour that seals my fate.
   Yet in my dreams, thy presence doth impart,
   A joy that lingers in my waking heart.

###901###
Whenas the sun doth cast his golden ray,
Upon the dew-kissed fields and meadows green,
My heart doth leap with joy at break of day,
And all the world with beauty is beseen.
The birds do sing their sweet and joyful tune,
As they do flit among the leafy trees,
Beneath the gentle gaze of the pale moon,
Which doth her silver light to darkness ease.
But soon the sun shall sink beneath the west,
And night with all her shadows shall descend,
And my poor heart shall find no place to rest,
Till morning light doth bring a joyful end.
    So let me seize this day with all my might,
    And banish sorrow with my heart's delight.

###902###
The fleeting moments of our mortal span,
Like shadows on a sundial quickly flee,
And youth, the fairest bloom of nature's plan,
Doth wither fast and cease to be.
The wrinkles furrow on a brow so fair,
The silver threads do weave within the hair,
And beauty's reign doth fade beyond compare,
Leaving but dust and sorrow in the air.
Yet in thy eyes a timeless grace I find,
A spark that burns with an eternal flame,
A love that conquers all of humankind,
And whispers to my soul thy cherished name.
    So let us vow to keep this passion bright,
    And banish time with everlasting light.

###903###
When winter's chill doth grip the barren land,
And nature sleeps beneath a snowy shroud,
My thoughts, like birds, do fly at thy command,
And seek thy warmth amidst the frozen crowd.
The icicles, like tears, do hang so low,
From eaves where summer's joy did once reside,
And biting winds do fiercely keen and blow,
Where laughter echoed and where love did guide.
But in my heart, a spring doth ever bloom,
A verdant paradise, untouched by frost,
Dispelling all the winter's chilling gloom,
And counting not the treasures I have lost.
    For thou art spring, and summer, and the sun,
    My dearest love, till all my days are done.

###904###
Hark, gentle muse, and lend thine ear to me,
And guide my quill with thy celestial grace,
That I may sing of her, eternally,
Whose beauty doth outshine all time and space.
Her eyes, like stars, do pierce the darkest night,
Her voice, a melody that soothes the soul,
Her smile, a beacon of celestial light,
That makes my wounded spirit wholly whole.
No earthly treasure can with her compare,
No jewel's gleam, no ruby's fiery hue,
For she is all that's beautiful and rare,
My love, my life, my constant, ever true.
    So let my verse her virtues thus proclaim,
    And set ablaze my ever-burning flame.

###905###
The raven's wing doth cast a shadow deep,
Upon the hopes that danced with morning's gleam,
And sorrow's torrents from my eyes do leap,
Lost in the phantoms of a waking dream.
The world, once bright with colours rich and bold,
Now wears a garb of dull and sombre grey,
And tales of joy are but as legends old,
That whisper of a long-departed day.
Yet in this darkness, still thy face I see,
A guiding light, a solace to my pain,
And though despair doth seek to conquer me,
Thy memory doth make me strong again.
    So let me cling to thee, my guiding star,
    And heal my wounds, no matter where they are.

###906###
When fickle fortune turns her wheel anew,
And casts me down from heights of sweet content,
My spirit quails, my courage doth subdue,
And every hopeful thought is sadly rent.
The storms of life do rage with mighty force,
And buffet me with waves of bitter woe,
And I am tossed upon a restless course,
With naught but tears and anxious sighs to show.
But when I think upon thy gentle hand,
And feel the comfort of thy steadfast love,
I find the strength to bravely make a stand,
And lift my gaze to blessings from above.
    For thou art anchor to my weary soul,
    And makest me again entirely whole.

###907###
The bloom of youth, though sweet and passing fair,
Doth fade too soon, like mist upon the morn,
And leaves behind a world of stark despair,
Where memory doth mock what is outworn.
The laughter gone, the lively step subdued,
The rosy cheek now pale and marked with age,
And all that once with vibrant life imbued,
Is but a whisper on life's fading page.
Yet in thy heart, a youthful spirit lies,
That time itself can never steal away,
A radiant soul that shines within thine eyes,
And brightens still my most despondent day.
    So let us cherish what forever stays,
    And find our youth in love's eternal maze.

###908###
The silent night, with watchful, starry eye,
Doth witness to the secrets I do keep,
Of passion's fire that will not ever die,
And dreams of thee, when weary senses sleep.
The moonbeams paint a path upon the ground,
That leads my yearning spirit to thy door,
Where solace in thy presence may be found,
And all my earthly cares shall be no more.
Though shadows lengthen and the hours grow late,
My faithful heart doth beat for thee alone,
And waits to share with thee a common fate,
Upon love's sweet and undisputed throne.
    So let us join our hands and hearts as one,
    And bid farewell to all that is undone.

###909###
When envious tongues do whisper tales of blame,
And seek to dim the luster of thy name,
My love for thee doth burn with fiercer flame,
And mocks the petty malice of their game.
They know not of the virtues thou dost hold,
The gentle spirit, and the noble mind,
The stories that in thy true heart unfold,
A treasure richer than all humankind.
Let them with slanders their own souls defile,
And poison with their breath the sweetest air,
My faith in thee shall never cease, the while,
For truth and goodness ever shall be there.
    So let them rage, their venom to impart,
    They cannot touch the chambers of my heart.

###910###
The fleeting season of our earthly stay,
Is like a breath, a whisper on the wind,
And all our works, our glories of today,
Are but as dust, by ages left behind.
The mighty empires, built with toil and might,
Do crumble down to ruin and to naught,
And proudest kings are swallowed by the night,
Their triumphs and their conquests all forgot.
Yet in thy love, a lasting truth I see,
A thing more potent than the years can wear,
A bond that binds thy faithful heart to me,
And lifts me far beyond all earthly care.
    So let us build our love on solid ground,
    Where no decay nor earthly loss is found.

###911###
When thou art absent, all the world is dim,
And every sound doth grate upon mine ear,
My spirits droop, my hopes are at the brim
Of utter darkness, filled with chilling fear.
The sun seems pale, the flowers lose their scent,
The birds do sing a melancholy strain,
My very breath with longing is now spent,
And all my joys are turned to bitter pain.
But when thy voice upon my ear doth fall,
Or when thy smile doth greet my eager sight,
Then all is well, and joy doth conquer all,
And banish shadows with its radiant light.
    So grant me, love, thy presence ever near,
    And banish all my doubt and every fear.

###912###
The tempest's rage, the thunder's fearsome sound,
May shake the earth and rend the sky apart,
But in thy love, a refuge I have found,
A steadfast anchor to my beating heart.
Let lightning flash and winds begin to roar,
And waves of sorrow crash upon the shore,
I shall not falter, nor my will ignore,
For thou art strength, and shall my heart restore.
Though trials come, and fortune prove unkind,
And darkling clouds obscure the hopeful day,
Thy constancy, a solace to my mind,
Shall guide me safely on my onward way.
    So let the world its fiercest fury vent,
    My love for thee is not for years but meant.

###913###
The poet's pen, with ink of deepest hue,
Doth strive to capture beauty's fleeting grace,
But finds the task, though earnest and though true,
Doth often fail to paint her matchless face.
For in her eyes, a heaven doth reside,
A depth of feeling, pure and undefiled,
And in her smile, a gentle, loving tide,
That makes the sternest heart become so mild.
No verse can hold the magic of her art,
No rhyme convey the music of her sigh,
She is a masterpiece, a work apart,
That lives within my soul, and shall not die.
    So let my heart her silent praises sing,
    And to her glory, all my tribute bring.

###914###
When doubt doth creep and whisper in my ear,
That love so pure can never long endure,
And seeds of jealousy and bitter fear,
Do plant themselves, and make my heart unsure.
I look to thee, and all my doubts take flight,
Like startled birds that vanish in the blue,
Thy constant faith doth fill my soul with light,
And makes my weary spirit strong and new.
For in thy gaze, a truth I can perceive,
A loyalty that time cannot deface,
And in thy touch, I truly do believe,
In love's eternal, everlasting grace.
    So let me trust in thee, my guiding star,
    And banish fear, no matter where we are.

###915###
The dying embers of a winter's fire,
Do cast a glow, a melancholy gleam,
Reflecting back my soul's profound desire,
To dwell with thee within a waking dream.
The world outside is hushed and cold and grey,
And nature sleeps beneath a frosty spell,
But in my heart, a warmer light doth play,
A secret joy that only we can tell.
For though the seasons change and years do pass,
And time doth march with unrelenting tread,
Our love shall shine, as clear as polished glass,
A light that shall not ever be unfed.
    So let us hold this flame, forever bright,
    And fill our lives with everlasting light.

###916###
When outward show doth hide a hollow heart,
And gilded words conceal a soul of vice,
'Tis then true worth doth truly play its part,
And shines more brightly than a diamond's price.
Let others chase the fleeting, false renown,
And build their fame on sand that shifts and yields,
My love for thee shall never be cast down,
But stand as firm as rock in open fields.
For in thy breast, a noble spirit dwells,
A kindness that doth conquer and subdue,
A grace that with sweet honesty compels,
My heart to beat for thee, forever true.
    So let us scorn the shallow, vain pretense,
    And find our joy in love's true recompense.

###917###
The restless sea, that ebbs and flows with might,
