Doth mirror well the passions of my soul,
That surge and fall with all their dark and light,
And yield at last to thy supreme control.
When tempests rise and toss me to and fro,
And dark despair doth threaten to consume,
Thy gentle voice doth bid the waters go,
And banish all the encroaching, chilling gloom.
Thou art my harbour, safe from every storm,
My guiding star, when all the world is blind,
And in thy love, my spirit finds its warm,
And peaceful rest, for all of humankind.
    So let me anchor here, my love, with thee,
    And sail with thee across life's boundless sea.

###918###
The blossoms fall, the leaves begin to turn,
And nature dons a garment brown and sere,
A lesson that my heart must slowly learn,
That beauty's reign is destined to be dear.
The summer's blush, the verdant, lively green,
Are but a prelude to the winter's reign,
And all the joys that once did grace the scene,
Must fade and pass, and leave behind but pain.
Yet in thy face, a spring doth ever bloom,
A radiant youth that time cannot decay,
Dispelling all the season's chilling gloom,
And turning winter into brightest May.
    So let us find in thee our summer's rest,
    And keep thy beauty ever in our breast.

###919###
When weary from the world's incessant strife,
And burdened by the cares that mortals bear,
I turn to thee, the solace of my life,
And find release from all my earthly care.
Thy gentle touch, thy tender, loving gaze,
Doth soothe the wounds that time hath left so deep,
And lead me through life's labyrinthine maze,
Where troubled thoughts no longer vigil keep.
For in thy presence, peace doth fill my soul,
A quiet joy, a calm I can't explain,
And thou dost make my wounded spirit whole,
And bid my anxious heart to cease its strain.
    So let me rest within thine arms, my dear,
    And find my heaven in thy presence here.

###920###
The golden sun doth sink beneath the hill,
And twilight paints the sky with hues of rose,
My heart with sweet remembrance doth stand still,
And contemplates the love that interflows.
The stars appear, like diamonds in the night,
And twinkle with a soft and gentle gleam,
Reflecting back my soul's intense delight,
Lost in the beauty of a waking dream.
For in thy love, a universe I find,
A boundless realm where joy doth ever reign,
A sacred bond that time can ne'er unwind,
And banishes all sorrow, grief, and pain.
    So let our love, a beacon, shine afar,
    And guide us onward, like a constant star.

###921###
When Phoebus hides his face and leaves the day,
And shadows creep to claim the earthly ground,
My heavy heart doth wander far astray,
Where sorrow's echo doth my soul surround.
The sweet embrace of slumber I do crave,
To banish thoughts that pierce me like a dart,
But restless dreams, like spectres from the grave,
Do keep their vigil, rending me apart.
O, gentle sleep, why dost thou fly from me,
And leave me captive to this waking pain?
My weary eyes do long for liberty,
To find some solace from this bitter reign.
Yet when I wake, the same despair I see,
And hope, a phantom, vanishes again.

###922###
Thy beauty shines, a beacon in the night,
More radiant than the stars in heaven's dome,
It fills my breast with wonder and delight,
And guides my spirit to its rightful home.
Thy voice, a music sweeter than the lute,
Doth soothe my soul and banish all my fears,
A melody that never can grow mute,
That whispers solace to my falling tears.
Thy smile, a dawn that chases gloom away,
Doth paint the world with colours rich and bright,
And bids my frozen heart begin to play,
A joyful tune, bathed in celestial light.
So let me gaze upon thee, day by day,
And lose myself within thy wondrous ray.

###923###
The fleeting hours, like pilfering thieves, do steal
The bloom of youth, that once did grace my cheek,
And leave behind the ravages they deal,
A testament to time, both strong and weak.
The silver threads now mingle with the gold,
Upon my brow, where once youth's banner flew,
And stories of the passing years are told,
In lines etched deep, forever fresh and new.
Yet in thine eyes, a spark of youth remains,
A timeless flame that mocks the hastening years,
And through the winter's bleak and chilling rains,
Thy spirit laughs, dispelling all my fears.
So let us cherish moments, ere they cease,
And find in love our everlasting peace.

###924###
My love for thee, a boundless, surging sea,
Doth know no ebb, no limit, and no end,
It flows and ebbs eternally for thee,
A constant tide, on which my heart doth send
Its deepest vows, its faith, its every sigh,
To anchor fast within thy loving breast,
And ne'er to waver, ne'er to fade or die,
But in thy favour find its final rest.
The storms of life may rage and winds may blow,
And threaten to submerge this fragile bark,
But still my love, like coral, will grow,
And light the ocean with its burning spark.
So fear thou not, my dearest, hold me near,
My steadfast love shall banish every fear.

###925###
The roseate blush that paints thy tender cheek,
Doth shame the dawn, and make the sun retire,
Its fragile beauty, which all hearts do seek,
Sets all my dormant passions into fire.
Thy silken hair, a cascade of the night,
Doth frame a face where all perfection lies,
And in thine eyes, I see a radiant light,
That mirrors heaven in their deep surprise.
When thou dost speak, a symphony I hear,
More sweet than any Nightingale's soft call,
And all my doubts and troubles disappear,
Beneath the charm that doth my senses thrall.
So let me live within this vision fair,
And breathe the perfumed sweetness of thy hair.

###926###
The fickle crowd doth praise and then condemn,
With changing winds their fickle favour turns,
They pluck the flower, then they crush the stem,
And quench the fire that brightly in them burns.
Today they crown, tomorrow they revile,
Their shifting moods no constancy can know,
And he who trusts their favour for a while,
Shall find himself cast down from high to low.
But in thy heart, a truth doth ever dwell,
A steadfast loyalty, a gentle grace,
That shields me from the scorn they loudly yell,
And finds for me a safe and sheltered place.
So let them mock and carp with envious eye,
Thy faithful love shall lift me to the sky.

###927###
When absence doth thy presence keep from me,
The world seems bare, and colours lose their hue,
My heart doth ache with hollow misery,
And every joy is shadowed, dim, and through.
The hours stretch out, like deserts, vast and dry,
And thirst I for the sight of thee again,
My spirit droops, and doth but wish to die,
To end the torment of this lonely pain.
But when thy letter comes, a blessed sign,
That thou art well, and think'st on me with love,
A sudden warmth doth through my being twine,
And hope descends from realms of grace above.
So speed, dear courier, with thy precious load,
And ease the burden of this weary road.

###928###
The world's applause, a momentary gleam,
That fades as swiftly as a morning mist,
A hollow echo of a fleeting dream,
By fickle fortune on the wind is kissed.
The cheers that greet a victor on his day,
Soon turn to jeers when fortune's wheel doth turn,
And those who basked in glory's golden ray,
Must learn to bear the scorn and keenly burn.
But thy regard, a jewel of purest worth,
Doth shine more brightly than the starry host,
It is the anchor of my soul on earth,
The truest treasure that I value most.
So let the masses clamour and pursue,
My dearest prize, my guiding star, is you.

###929###
The winter's frost doth bind the fertile ground,
And silence reigns where summer's birds did sing,
No verdant blade nor blooming flower is found,
And chilling winds their mournful dirge do bring.
The trees stand stark, their branches bare and cold,
As if in grief for summers passed away,
And Nature's tales of beauty, once so bold,
Are locked in slumber, hidden from the day.
Yet in this chill, my love for thee doth bloom,
A constant warmth that melts the icy spell,
And banishes the encroaching winter's gloom,
Within the haven where thy virtues dwell.
So let the season rage with all its might,
My heart shall glow with love's eternal light.

###930###
Thy gentle touch, a balm to soothe my soul,
Doth chase away the shadows of despair,
And makes my wounded spirit once more whole,
And lifts the burden that I sadly bear.
Thy whispered words, like music on the breeze,
Do calm the tempest raging in my breast,
And bring my troubled, anxious heart to ease,
And grant my weary spirit blessed rest.
O, would that I could hold thee ever near,
And feel the comfort of thy sweet embrace,
To banish every doubt and every fear,
And find within thine eyes my resting place.
So let us pledge our troth, and ever be,
My dearest love, eternally with thee.

###931###
The poet's art, a labour long and hard,
To capture truth in verse, both strong and clear,
To weave a spell, with every careful ward,
That shall delight the sense and touch the ear.
But when I strive to paint thy loveliness,
My feeble quill doth falter and doth fail,
No words I find my passion to express,
Or tell the wonders that do me assail.
For thou art more than mortal can conceive,
A perfect mould, where beauty doth reside,
And in thy presence, I can but believe,
That heaven's grace doth on this earth abide.
So let me gaze, and let my heart be still,
And worship thee, with all my willing will.

###932###
When fortune smiles, and skies are clear and bright,
And all the world doth seem a joyful stage,
Then friendships sprout and bloom in pure delight,
And flatterers do fill their flattering page.
They praise thy deeds, they laud thy noble name,
And feast with thee, with laughter and with wine,
But when the clouds obscure the sun's warm flame,
They melt away, like shadows in a shrine.
But thou, my friend, art constant as the star,
That guides the sailor through the darkest night,
Thy faithful heart doth shine from near and far,
And lends my weary spirit strength and light.
So let the fickle crowd their favours lend,
Thy constant truth shall be my dearest friend.

###933###
The rose doth fade, its petals fall to ground,
The lily droops, its perfume starts to cease,
The summer's bloom no longer can be found,
And all the earth doth languish in decrease.
The golden light that gilded summer's day,
Now yields to autumn's melancholic hue,
And all the joys that made the heart to play,
Are lost and gone, like morning's early dew.
But still thy love, a springtime ever new,
Doth burst with life, and banish winter's chill,
A constant bloom, forever fresh and true,
That bids my lonely, waiting heart be still.
So let the seasons change and pass away,
Thy love shall be my bright and summer's day.

###934###
I swear by all the heavens high above,
And by the earth beneath my weary feet,
My constancy, my loyalty, my love,
Shall ne'er grow cold, nor ever know defeat.
Though tempests roar and oceans surge and swell,
And rocks and shoals my fragile bark assail,
My steadfast heart shall break their angry spell,
And through the fiercest gale, shall never fail.
For in thy eyes, a truth I can behold,
A promise whispered, faithful and sincere,
A treasure richer than the purest gold,
That banishes all doubt and every fear.
So let us build our trust, and build it strong,
And love shall be our everlasting song.

###935###
The envious eye doth seek to dim thy grace,
And whisper tales that slander and defame,
They strive to tarnish thy most lovely face,
And cast upon thy virtue burning shame.
But calumny, like lightning, swift doth fly,
And leaves no mark where purity doth dwell,
It cannot wound, though aiming for the sky,
The soul that shines, and casts its potent spell.
Thy goodness shines, a beacon strong and bright,
That mocks the darkness of their bitter tongue,
And fills my heart with ever-growing light,
A joyful anthem, by my spirit sung.
So let them rage and vent their petty spite,
Thy noble soul shall triumph in its might.

###936###
When cares of life do press with heavy hand,
And weary burdens bow my aching head,
I turn to thee, and on thy strength I stand,
As on a rock, where troubled waters spread.
Thy gentle voice, a balm to soothe my pain,
Doth whisper comfort, banishing my dread,
And like the dew upon the thirsty plain,
Revives my spirit, ere my hope be fled.
Thy loving gaze, a star that guides me home,
Through darkest nights, and pathways rough and steep,
Dispels the fears that make my spirit roam,
And lulls my troubled, anxious soul to sleep.
So in thy care, my dearest, let me lie,
And find my peace beneath thy watchful eye.

###937###
The fleeting years, like shadows, quickly pass,
And steal away the vigour of my prime,
They glide away, as swift as blades of grass,
And leave me bound by unrelenting time.
The strength that once did bear me with such ease,
Now falters, and begins to wear and wane,
And lines upon my brow, like ancient trees,
Do tell of journeys, pleasure, and of pain.
Yet in thy heart, a youthful spirit thrives,
A timeless essence, that will never fade,
And through the winter of my passing lives,
Thy love shall be the spring that will not 'bide.
So let us hold each other, till the end,
And in our love, our fading years transcend.

###938###
The fleeting moment, precious and so rare,
That doth on wings of lightning swiftly fly,
If not embraced, leaves naught but deep despair,
And seeds of sorrow sown beneath the sky.
The lover's sigh, the poet's heartfelt rhyme,
The artist's stroke, the warrior's bold deed,
All fade and vanish, lost to passing time,
Unless they sow a more enduring seed.
But our sweet love, a bond that shall not break,
A constant flame that burns with steady light,
Shall live and thrive, for our own precious sake,
And banish darkness with its glorious might.
So let us seize this hour, and hold it fast,
Our love's bright legacy, forever to last.

###939###
When envy's sting doth pierce me to the soul,
And bitter whispers fill the common air,
I turn to thee, and make my spirit whole,
And find a solace from this crushing care.
Thy gentle hand doth wipe away the tear,
That sorrow sheds upon my weary face,
And bids my trembling, anxious heart be clear,
And find within thy love a resting place.
Thy faith, a shield against the shafts of hate,
Doth guard me well, from all their poisoned darts,
And lifts me up above their scornful state,
And mends the breaches in my wounded hearts.
So let them rail, and let their malice grow,
Thy love shall shield me from each cruel blow.

###940###
The muse doth scorn the one whose heart is cold,
And shuns the touch of one who feels no fire,
For tales of passion, bravely to be told,
Must spring from flames of love's intense desire.
My humble muse, though oft she doth complain,
That I do sing of beauty far too great,
Is drawn to thee, again and yet again,
And cannot cease to celebrate thy state.
For in thy form, perfection doth reside,
A living poem, writ in hues so fine,
That all the arts to thee do meekly stride,
And beg a portion of thy light divine.
So let my muse continue to behold,
The fairest story, ever to be told.

###941###
When Fortune smiles, and doth my suit attend,
The world doth seem a place of purest joy,
And all my hopes on gilded wings ascend,
No shade of doubt my spirit can annoy.
My love, a star, doth shine with radiant gleam,
And casts its light upon my humble way,
Dispelling all the shadows of a dream,
And making bright the dullest, darkest day.
But when the clouds of sorrow gather nigh,
And fortune turns her fickle face from me,
My joy doth vanish, and my spirits die,
And all my hopes are lost upon the sea.
Yet in thy love, I find a solace deep,
A balm to heal the wounds that sorrow keep.

###942###
My muse, when thou art silent, I am lost,
No worthy verse my heavy hand can write,
As though my captive thoughts were tempest-tossed,
And banished from the realm of pure delight.
The fairest bloom doth wither in my sight,
The sweetest song doth sound a jarring note,
And all the world is draped in somber night,
As if my weary soul had lost its boat.
But when thy inspiration doth descend,
And whispers music to my waiting ear,
My pen doth fly, my shadowed thoughts transcend,
And beauty blooms, dispelling every fear.
So let thy voice, my dearest muse, inspire,
And set my captive spirit all afire.

###943###
The fleeting hours, like swift-winged birds, do fly,
And steal away the sweetness of the morn,
Leaving behind a silent, mournful cry,
As youth and beauty are of life forlorn.
The crimson blush that graces beauty's cheek,
The sparkling eye that doth all hearts enslave,
The voice so soft, the words so gently speak,
All sink at last into the silent grave.
Then let us seize the moments as they pass,
And drink the nectar of each precious hour,
Before our days like shadows fade, alas,
And winter doth usurp the summer's power.
For time, a thief, doth steal our fairest days,
And leaves us but the dust of memory's haze.

###944###
When I behold thy visage, fair and bright,
My heart doth leap, as doth a captive freed,
And all the world is bathed in golden light,
A wondrous harvest from a hopeful seed.
Thy gentle smile, a sunbeam on my soul,
Doth chase away the shadows of despair,
And makes my wounded spirit once more whole,
And lifts me from the burdens I do bear.
Thy voice, a melody that doth enchant,
Doth serenade my ear with tender grace,
And though my tongue be weak, my heart doth pant,
To speak the love that I cannot erase.
So let me gaze, and let my spirit soar,
And in thy presence, ask for nothing more.

###945###
My dearest love, though distance doth divide,
And oceans wide between us lie,
My constant heart doth evermore abide,
And hold thee close beneath the self-same sky.
For though the miles may stretch in weary length,
And separate our bodies from the sight,
Our souls are bound with an unyielding strength,
And meet each other in the deepest night.
I see thy face in every star I find,
I hear thy voice in every gentle breeze,
And in my dreams, thy form doth fill my mind,
And brings my troubled spirit perfect ease.
So let us trust this bond that cannot break,
And for each other, our true souls awake.

###946###
The summer's lease hath all too short a date,
And autumn's chill doth soon begin to creep,
When leaves of gold their somber fate
Do yield to winter's slumber, cold and deep.
So too the bloom of youth, so fresh and fair,
Doth fade and wither with the passing years,
And silver threads do grace the raven hair,
As sorrow mingles with our smiles and tears.
Yet in thy love, I find a timeless spring,
A garden where no frost can ever blight,
Where beauty's ever-fresh delights do cling,
And banish all the shadows of the night.
So let us hold this love, forever true,
And find our youth renewed in loving you.

###947###
When envy's green eye doth my worth assail,
And whispered slanders seek to dim my fame,
I find my spirit doth begin to quail,
And fear doth whisper thy beloved name.
For should my deeds be judged by cruel decree,
And all my labors cast aside as naught,
Then what remains for thee to cherish me,
When all my worth is by the world forgot?
But then I look within thy gentle eyes,
And see a truth that outward scorn defies,
A love that sees beyond the world's disguise,
And finds the treasure where true virtue lies.
So let them judge, and let them speak their fill,
Thy steadfast love doth make my spirit still.

###948###
The changing seasons doth my thoughts employ,
As nature's cycle doth my heart impress,
From verdant spring to winter's stern alloy,
Each holds a beauty that I must confess.
The budding rose, the robin's cheerful song,
The golden harvest, and the frosty air,
All speak of cycles, fleeting yet so strong,
And life renewed, beyond all earthly care.
And so thy love, though changing it may seem,
Doth hold a constant beauty, ever new,
A timeless essence, like a waking dream,
That doth forever shine, both strong and true.
So let us weather storms, and seasons fly,
Our love, a constant star within the sky.

###949###
When first I saw thee, radiant and fair,
My heart did stumble, and my breath did cease,
As if a vision from the upper air,
Had brought my troubled spirit perfect peace.
Thy gentle gaze, a balm to wounded pride,
Thy tender smile, a sunbeam on my soul,
Did banish all the fears I could not hide,
And made my shattered spirit once more whole.
No earthly treasure can with thee compare,
No jewel so precious, nor no art so fine,
Thou art the essence of all beauty rare,
And in thy love, my dearest life doth shine.
So let me linger in thy matchless grace,
And find my heaven in this hallowed place.

###950###
My tongue doth falter when I speak thy praise,
For words are weak to capture all thy worth,
And all my thoughts in tangled, clouded maze,
Do strive in vain to map thy beauty's birth.
The painter's brush, the poet's finest quill,
Can but essay a fraction of thy grace,
And leave the deepest wonders standing still,
Uncharted regions of thy lovely face.
Yet in my heart, a truer knowledge lies,
A love that sees beyond the outward show,
And understands the truth within thine eyes,
A depth of feeling that doth ever grow.
So let my actions speak what words cannot,
And prove my love, by deeds that are begot.

###951###
When weary, I do seek thy comforting embrace,
And find a solace in thy tender care,
My worldly troubles vanish without trace,
And leave my spirit light, beyond compare.
The storms of life, that rage with furious might,
Do lose their power when I am by thy side,
And all the darkness turns to golden light,
As in thy love, I safely can abide.
Thy gentle hand, that wipes away each tear,
Thy loving words, that banish all my dread,
Do make the path ahead appear so clear,
And lift the burdens that have weighed my head.
So let me lean on thee, my dearest friend,
Until our earthly journey finds its end.

###952###
The world doth judge by outward show and guise,
And measures worth by fleeting, earthly gain,
They see the surface, and they miss the prize,
The hidden treasure, free from worldly stain.
A noble mien, a fortune bright and vast,
May win them praise, and court the common eye,
But virtue's seed, though sown, may not outlast,
The changing winds that 'round their fortunes fly.
But in thy heart, a richer gold doth gleam,
A steadfast truth that doth all tests endure,
A love that shines, a pure and constant stream,
Whose lasting worth is ever strong and sure.
So let them hoard their dross, their fragile might,
My wealth is found in thee, my purest light.

###953###
When absence doth my heavy spirit weigh,
And steals the sunshine from my cheerful days,
I count the hours till thou shalt come and stay,
And chase away these melancholy haze.
The empty room doth echo with thy name,
The silent air doth long to hear thy voice,
And every thought doth burn with love's own flame,
And in thy presence, doth my soul rejoice.
The stars above, though distant, seem to be,
A mirror to the light that thou dost hold,
And in their gleam, I see a part of thee,
A promise whispered, more than can be told.
So hasten, love, and end this painful wait,
And seal anew our everlasting fate.

###954###
The fleeting beauty of a summer's day,
Doth fade too soon, and leave behind the chill,
As nature's vibrant colors steal away,
And winter's frosty breath doth hold them still.
So too the bloom of youth, so fresh and bright,
Doth yield its vigor to the creeping years,
And shadows gather, dimming nature's light,
And bringing with them many silent fears.
But in thy love, a season I do find,
That knows no winter, and no fading hue,
A timeless spring that doth all change outbind,
And keeps my spirit ever fresh and new.
So let us hold this love, forever true,
And in its timelessness, find all things new.

###955###
When cares of life do press with heavy hand,
And shadows gather on my weary brow,
I turn to thee, as to a promised land,
Where peace and comfort do their solace vow.
Thy gentle voice, a balm to wounded ear,
Thy loving gaze, a beacon in the night,
Doth chase away each doubt, and vanquish fear,
And fill my troubled soul with pure delight.
The storms of fortune may with fury blow,
And tempests rage upon life's stormy sea,
But in thy steadfast love, I safely go,
And find a port where I can anchor me.
So let me rest within thy loving arms,
And be forever safe from all alarms.

###956###
My dearest love, though envious tongues may speak,
And spread their poison with malicious art,
My steadfast heart, though sometimes seeming weak,
Doth hold its faith, and will not be apart.
For in thy truth, I find a shield so strong,
Against the slanders that the world doth cast,
And though they strive to do my spirit wrong,
Thy pure affection shall forever last.
Let others doubt, and let them cast their scorn,
My faith in thee no falsehood can efface,
For in thy love, a new hope is reborn,
And shines with an unfading, steady grace.
So let them prate, and let their malice fly,
My constant heart shall ever be thine nigh.

###957###
When I do ponder on the days gone by,
And see the follies that did mar my youth,
I fear that when the final moments lie,
Thy love may wane, and lose its honest truth.
For time, a thief, doth steal our youthful fire,
And leaves behind the wrinkles and the grey,
And passion's flame may dwindle and expire,
As colder seasons hold their somber sway.
But then I look within thy loving eyes,
And see a light that doth all time defy,
A love that blooms, that never truly dies,
And shines for me beneath the same vast sky.
So let us trust this love, that knows no end,
And in its strength, our faithful hearts shall blend.

###958###
The fairest rose, though kissed by morning dew,
Doth fade and wither when the sun doth set,
And all its beauty, once so fresh and new,
Is lost to time, a memory to fret.
So too the bloom of youth, so bright and bold,
Doth yield its vigor to the passing years,
And all its vibrant stories, to be told,
Are hushed by age, and mingled with our tears.
But in thy love, a beauty I do find,
That knows no season, and no fading grace,
A timeless essence, pure and unconfined,
That holds its luster in this fleeting space.
So let us cherish this, our love so rare,
Beyond the reach of time, and earthly care.

###959###
When Fortune frowns, and shadows dim my day,
And all my hopes seem lost upon the breeze,
I turn to thee, and find a brighter way,
A refuge found amongst the rustling trees.
Thy gentle smile, a sunbeam on my soul,
Doth chase away the darkness and the dread,
And makes my wounded spirit once more whole,
And lifts the burdens that have weighed my head.
Thy whispered words, a balm to soothe my ear,
Doth banish all the fears I can't disguise,
And in thy presence, all is calm and clear,
And hope rekindled in my tearful eyes.
So let me linger, safe within thy sight,
And find in thee my solace and my light.

###960###
My dearest love, though words can but portray
A fraction of the feelings I possess,
My heart doth hold thee close, in its own way,
And vows to love thee, truly, I confess.
The passing years may bring their ebb and flow,
And fortunes change, as winds begin to blow,
But this firm truth my constant soul doth know,
My love for thee shall ever brightly glow.
So let us face what futures may arise,
With steadfast hearts, and spirits joined as one,
And find our strength beneath the watchful skies,
Until our earthly pilgrimage is done.
For in thy love, my dearest, I am free,
And in that freedom, find eternity.

###961###
When that the sun doth hide his golden face,
And twilight steals across the weary land,
My heart doth mourn the absence of thy grace,
As shadows lengthen by the fading sand.
The chirping birds their evensong do cease,
And all the world doth sink to silent sleep,
Yet in my soul, no solace can increase,
For thoughts of thee do vigil ever keep.
No slumber comes to ease my troubled mind,
No sweet oblivion can my senses find,
But restless sighs, to thy dear image tied,
Do fill the void where joy hath been denied.
   Thus in the dark, my love doth burn so bright,
   A lonely star that shines throughout the night.

###962###
Thy beauty, like a rose in summer's prime,
Doth so enchant mine eyes, I scarce can breathe,
And stealeth all my thoughts, beyond all time,
A wondrous tapestry that you do wreathe.
The blush upon thy cheek, a rosy hue,
The azure depths within thy gentle eye,
Do paint a picture, ever fresh and new,
That makes the passing hours swiftly fly.
No earthly jewel can match thy sterling worth,
No poet's pen can justly speak thy praise,
Thou art a marvel, sent from heaven to earth,
To set my captive spirit in a blaze.
   So let me gaze, and in thy beauty drown,
   The fairest jewel in this mortal town.

###963###
My love for thee, a constant, flowing stream,
That rushes onward to the boundless main,
Doth mock the shallows of a fleeting dream,
And mocks the doubts that in my bosom reign.
Though tempests rage, and fortune's wheel doth turn,
And outward show doth fade with passing years,
My steadfast heart for thee shall ever burn,
And drown the bitter taste of mortal fears.
As doth the sun the darkness of the night,
So shall my love dispel all shades of woe,
And guide my steps with everlasting light,
Whersoe'er my weary feet may go.
   So doubt me not, though words be weak and few,
   My soul is thine, eternally and true.

###964###
When winter's chill doth bite with icy sting,
And barren branches claw the leaden sky,
No bud nor bloom doth nature's bounty bring,
But frozen earth and winds that sadly sigh.
So doth my spirit languish in despair,
When absent thou, my sun, my joy, my all,
No warmth can penetrate this chilling air,
But darkness reigns, and shadows round me fall.
The laughter of the world doth seem afar,
A hollow sound that brings no sweet release,
My heart a captive to a lonely star,
That shines on thee, and offers me no peace.
   Oh, haste thee back, and banish winter's blight,
   And fill my world with thy returning light.

###965###
The fleeting moments, like swift-footed steeds,
Do gallop onward, heedless of our plea,
And sow the seeds of age, with silent deeds,
That steal the bloom from thee, and eke from me.
The lines of care upon thy brow may trace,
The silver threads that mingle with thy hair,
But still I see the beauty of thy face,
A deeper charm, beyond compare.
For in thine eyes, a wisdom doth reside,
A gentle spirit, tempered by the years,
That makes my love more steadfast and more wide,
And calms my soul, and quells my rising fears.
   So let us age, with love our guiding hand,
   The truest riches in this mortal land.

###966###
If envious fate should tear us far apart,
And cruel distance build a bitter wall,
Still shall thy image dwell within my heart,
And echo softly in my silent call.
Though miles may lie between us, vast and deep,
And oceans roll, and continents divide,
My loyal thoughts their constant vigil keep,
And in thy memory, I shall confide.
No change of scene, nor passing of the days,
Can e'er diminish what my soul doth feel,
But like a star, it shines through misty haze,
And makes my wounded spirit truly heal.
   So let us trust, though trials may arise,
   Our love shall conquer, 'neath all foreign skies.

###967###
The world doth rave of glories, great and grand,
Of empires built, and victories hard won,
But all such triumphs, held within the hand,
Are but as shadows, when the day is done.
For what is power, or a gilded crown,
Compared to one true glance from thy dear eye?
The fame of kings, like withered leaves blown down,
Doth vanish swift, beneath a passing sky.
My truest wealth lies not in minted gold,
Nor lands I own, nor titles I may bear,
But in the tale of our sweet love, untold,
A treasure shared, beyond all earthly care.
   So let the world pursue its fleeting fame,
   I find my joy in whispering thy name.

###968###
When Cupid's shaft hath pierced my foolish breast,
And filled my veins with fire, fierce and bold,
I find no moment's peace, nor needful rest,
But live in dreams, of stories to be told.
Thy voice, a music that doth fill the air,
Thy smile, a sunbeam on a cloudy morn,
Doth banish all my sorrow and despair,
And leave my lonely spirit newly born.
I wander lost, within thy sweet domain,
A willing captive, bound by silken chain,
And gladly bear love's pleasure and its pain,
And pray that this sweet torment may remain.
   For in thy love, all blessings I embrace,
   And find my heaven in thy tender grace.

###969###
The subtle art with which thy wit doth play,
Doth charm my senses, and my reason blind,
And steals my very breath, and bears away
All sober thought, and leaves no trace behind.
Thy words, like jewels, are strung with cunning skill,
Each phrase a treasure, polished bright and keen,
That doth my captive admiration fill,
And paints thee fairest in this mortal scene.
I marvel at the depths of thy discourse,
The swiftness of thy mind, so sharp and clear,
And feel my love take an unyielding course,
Towards thy brilliance, banishing all fear.
   So let me listen, ever to thy voice,
   And in thy wisdom, make my steadfast choice.

###970###
When absence presses, heavy on my soul,
And days stretch long, without a sight of thee,
I feel my spirit falter and lose its whole,
And sink to depths of dark anxiety.
The world seems garish, and its colours fade,
The laughter of my fellows sounds so hollow,
My heart, a lonely lute, in mournful shade,
That plays but one sad tune, and cannot follow
The lighter airs that fill the common ear,
But dwells on thoughts of thee, and waits thy sign,
And longs to hold thee, ever, ever near,
And drink the nectar of thy love divine.
   Oh, when wilt thou return, and ease my plight,
   And flood my soul with thy returning light?

###971###
The changing seasons, each in turn doth show,
The constant flux of nature's grand design,
From verdant spring to winter's chilling snow,
A cycle old, eternally divine.
Yet in this ebb and flow, one truth remains,
My love for thee, a constant, steady flame,
That mocks the passage of all worldly pains,
And whispers softly, aye, thy cherished name.
Though youth may flee, and beauty be undone,
And outward forms may wither and decay,
My heart's true fealty is to thee alone,
And shall endure, until my dying day.
   So let the years their swift progression make,
   My love for thee no moment shall forsake.

###972###
When doubts assail, and whisper in mine ear,
That love like ours is fragile and will break,
I turn to thee, and banish every fear,
For in thine eyes, a deeper truth I take.
Thy steadfast gaze, a mirror to my soul,
Doth show a bond that time cannot erase,
A unity that makes my spirit whole,
And finds its solace in thy warm embrace.
The passing storms that rage against our peace,
Shall serve but to cement our spirits more,
And make our steadfast affection to increase,
Upon a love that knows no earthly shore.
   So let them speak, who know not what they say,
   Our love shall triumph, come what may.

###973###
The world presents a face of fickle guise,
With shifting fortunes, and with fleeting smiles,
Where trust is frail, and promise often lies,
And virtue treads through treacherous, winding miles.
But in thy heart, a sanctuary I find,
A steadfast haven, from the storm's fierce blow,
Where honesty and truth are ever twined,
And gentle kindness doth forever flow.
No false pretence can cloud thy honest brow,
No dark deceit can mar thy spirit bright,
And this it is that binds my soul to thou,
And fills my future with a hopeful light.
   So let me rest, within thy faithful breast,
   And find in thee, my everlasting rest.

###974###
When gazing on the stars, that gem the night,
And pondering the vastness of the skies,
I think of thee, and all thy wondrous light,
That shines within my soul, and never dies.
As constellations guide the sailor's way,
So doth thy spirit be my guiding star,
That leads me onward, through the darkest day,
And keeps me safe, however far.
Thy wisdom, like a beacon, shines so clear,
Thy love, a compass, pointing to the true,
And in its light, I conquer every fear,
And find my purpose, wholly, in my view.
   So let me navigate, by love's decree,
   And find my haven, ever, in thee.

###975###
The world is filled with songs, both loud and low,
Of joyous mirth, and melancholy strain,
But none can match the music that doth flow,
When thy dear voice doth whisper once again.
It is a melody, both sweet and rare,
That stills the tumult in my troubled breast,
And banishes the burden of all care,
And lulls my weary spirit into rest.
No earthly instrument can e'er compare,
With the pure harmony thy lips impart,
A balm it is, to all my hidden woe,
And the sweet music of my beating heart.
   So let me hear, again and yet again,
   The sweetest music, free from worldly pain.

###976###
Though jealous tongues may wag, and gossip's breath,
May seek to taint the purity of our love,
They cannot touch the bond that conquers death,
Sent from the heavens, and the stars above.
My faith in thee is like a sturdy oak,
That stands against the wind, and yields not ground,
Its roots run deep, no tempest can provoke,
Its mighty strength, where true devotion's found.
Let rumour spread its lies, and slander sting,
My heart is thine, and shall remain so true,
And to thy virtue, shall my praises sing,
Forever constant, and forever new.
   So let them whisper, let them cast their blame,
   My soul is bound unto thy noble name.

###977###
When weary days do drain my strength away,
And tasks of life do press with heavy hand,
I dream of thee, and how we spend our day,
Together walking, on some sunlit strand.
Thy gentle touch, a solace to my soul,
Thy loving gaze, a comfort and a guide,
Doth make me feel completely whole,
And puts all worldly troubles to the side.
The simple joys that we in love can find,
Outweigh the riches that the world doth hold,
A peaceful bliss, for heart and weary mind,
More precious far than any minted gold.
   So let us cherish, these our moments sweet,
   Wherein our weary, mortal souls do meet.

###978###
The passing years, like rivers, onward glide,
And bear away the bloom of youthful years,
But in thy love, a constant I do pride,
That calms my soul, and banishes all fears.
The outward show may fade, the colour flee,
The lines of age may etch upon thy face,
But still the essence of thy soul I see,
And find therein a more enduring grace.
As winter's frost gives way to spring's new birth,
So shall thy spirit, ever, brightly gleam,
A timeless beauty, sent from heaven to earth,
More real than any passing, mortal dream.
   So let us age, with love our constant friend,
   A joy that shall endure, until the end.

###979###
When sickness doth assail, and weakness reigns,
And all the world seems dim and far away,
My thoughts of thee do conquer all my pains,
And bring me comfort, at the close of day.
Thy memory, a tonic to my soul,
Doth lift my spirit, when it starts to fall,
And makes me feel completely whole,
And rise again, above the earthly thrall.
The gentle touch of thy remembered hand,
The sound of thy sweet voice, I long to hear,
Doth make me feel I truly understand,
What it means to hold a treasure ever dear.
   So when I'm weak, and falter in my stride,
   Let thy dear image be my constant guide.

###980###
The fleeting joys that mortals seek to chase,
Are like the shadows, that do quickly fly,
And leave behind no lasting, happy trace,
Beneath the ever-changing, passing sky.
But in thy love, a substance I do find,
A truth that time itself cannot efface,
A constant treasure, for my heart and mind,
A pure affection, in this mortal race.
The outward show may wither and decline,
But that which lies within, shall still endure,
A flame that burns, eternally divine,
A love like ours, so steadfast and so pure.
   So let us hold, this treasure in our keep,
   A love that from the deepest well doth leap.

###981###
When Summer's lease hath all too short a date,
And winter's frost doth nip the tender bud,
My love for thee shall never know its fate,
Nor from my steadfast heart be washed like mud.
Though seasons turn and change with swift decree,
And youth doth fade, and beauty takes its flight,
My constant flame shall burn eternally,
A beacon shining in the darkest night.
For as the sun doth rise with morning's grace,
And banish shadows with its golden eye,
So shall my love illuminate this place,
And chase away all sorrow with a sigh.
   Thy worth, dear heart, no time can e'er decay,
   But grows more precious with each passing day.

###982###
When I behold the wrinkles on thy brow,
A testament to years that swiftly flew,
My heart doth ache, and yet I vow,
My love for thee shall ever be anew.
For though the outward form may wax and wane,
And silver threads adorn thy noble head,
Within my breast, the passion doth remain,
A fireside warmth, though youth itself be fled.
As ancient oaks, with roots so deeply set,
Withstand the storms and stand in steadfast might,
So my affection, I shall not forget,
But hold it dear, a pure and guiding light.
   For in thy soul, a beauty I do see,
   That time itself can never steal from me.

###983###
The painted rose, though fair to outward view,
Doth lack the scent that nature doth bestow,
And so it is with love, when it is true,
Its inward worth doth truly make it grow.
For outward show, though pleasing to the eye,
Is but a bauble, easily undone,
But when the heart doth whisper with a sigh,
A deeper, lasting treasure has begun.
The merchant's gold, that glitters in the sun,
May be consumed by avarice and greed,
But love's true coin, though sparingly it's spun,
Shall satisfy our soul's most urgent need.
   So let us seek the substance, not the shade,
   And build our love on foundations that are made.

###984###
When Fortune smiles, and all the world doth cheer,
And pleasures flow like wine from a full cup,
Beware the heart that holds such moments dear,
For easily may joy be lifted up.
But when the clouds do gather, dark and deep,
And sorrow's chill doth penetrate the bone,
Then shall the truest friendships secrets keep,
And lift thee up when thou dost feel alone.
For in the sunshine, many friends abound,
Like summer flies that flit from flower to flower,
But in the storm, no faithful soul is found,
To shield thee from the tempest's raging power.
   So judge thy friends by trials they endure,
   And find in them a comfort ever sure.

###985###
My love is like a garden, richly sown,
With varied blooms of passion, pure and bright,
Each petal kissed by breezes gently blown,
And bathed in sunbeams of a warm delight.
The rose of trust, with thorns that guard its grace,
The lily's bloom, that speaks of innocence,
The violet's hue, that hints of time and space,
And all combined, a sweet magnificence.
And though the winter's breath may seek to blight,
And steal the colour from each tender hue,
My constant care shall shield them from the night,
And keep their beauty ever fresh and new.
   So shall my love, in seasons yet untold,
   A verdant paradise, forever hold.

###986###
When envious tongues do wag with rumour's breath,
And whisper slanders, venomous and foul,
They seek to bring my dearest joy to death,
And make my spirit mourn, and softly howl.
But like a rock, against the surging tide,
My steadfast faith shall stand, unyielding, strong,
And all their petty malice shall be spied,
As idle tales, where truth can do no wrong.
The viper's sting, though sharp, can not prevail,
Against the shield of innocence and right,
So shall my virtue triumph, and not fail,
To shine unblemished in the public sight.
   Let them their slanders cast upon the wind,
   My honest heart shall peace and comfort find.

###987###
The changing moon doth wax and wane above,
A constant cycle, ever in its turn,
And so it is with fickle human love,
That brightly burns, then swiftly doth adjourn.
One day a flame, that leaps with fierce desire,
The next a cinder, cold and dead and grey,
Consumed by passion's unquenched, burning fire,
Or chilled by doubts that lead the heart astray.
But mine, dear heart, shall know no ebb nor flow,
No shifting sands to shift its steady course,
But like the stars, in constant, radiant glow,
My love shall be, with unremitting force.
   So let the world its inconstant tempers show,
   My love for thee, like constant rivers, flow.

###988###
When I do think of all the years we've spent,
And all the trials that we have overcome,
My heart with gratitude is heaven-sent,
And makes my weary spirit cease to hum.
For in the depths of trouble and of pain,
Thy loving hand hath ever been my guide,
And dried the tears that fell like summer rain,
And stood with me, steadfastly, by my side.
The storms of life may rage with fiercest might,
And tempests gather on the distant sea,
But in thy presence, all is calm and bright,
A sanctuary, where my soul is free.
   So let us walk, through futures yet unknown,
   Our love a bond, forever to be shown.

###989###
The fleeting joys that mortals hold so dear,
Are but like bubbles, floating on the air,
That burst and vanish, leaving naught but fear,
And emptiness, and burdens hard to bear.
The lover's kiss, the banquet's rich delight,
The victor's triumph, sung with loud acclaim,
All fade and pass, like shadows of the night,
And leave behind no lasting, worthy name.
But thy dear love, a treasure I possess,
Outshines the gold of kings, the gems of old,
A constant solace in my deep distress,
A story that shall never be untold.
   So let the world its transient pleasures chase,
   I find my heaven in thy sweet embrace.

###990###
When busy thoughts do crowd my troubled mind,
And worries vex me with their constant sting,
A balm of peace in thee alone I find,
A gentle calm, that makes my spirit sing.
The world may spin with all its cares and strife,
And fortunes turn with swift, capricious hand,
But in thy love, I find a richer life,
A solid ground, whereon I firmly stand.
The babbling brook, that murmurs on its way,
May soothe the ear with melodies so light,
But thy dear voice, at close of weary day,
Doth fill my soul with unalloyed delight.
   So let the world its petty discords raise,
   I find my rest within thy loving gaze.

###991###
As sculptors carve from stone a form so grand,
That lives and breathes, though made of lifeless mould,
So thy dear love, by Nature's skilled command,
Hath wrought a spirit, precious to behold.
The outward shell may bear the marks of time,
And lose the bloom that youth did once impart,
But in thy soul, a beauty doth sublime,
That captures and doth captivate my heart.
For like the sun, that shines with steady ray,
Though clouds may sometimes dim its golden face,
Thy inner light doth never fade away,
But shines with ever-increasing grace.
   So let the world its outward semblance praise,
   I love the spirit that within thee stays.

###992###
The swift-winged hours, that fly on silent feet,
Do steal away the moments of our prime,
And leave behind a memory bittersweet,
Of youth's fair bloom, now lost to passing time.
The fairest cheek, that blushes with delight,
The brightest eye, that sparkles with its fire,
Must yield at last to Winter's frosty blight,
And lose the glow of unfulfilled desire.
But in my verse, thy beauty shall endure,
Beyond the reach of age, or earthly decay,
A timeless charm, forever to secure,
And banish all the ravages of day.
   So let thy image in my lines reside,
   Where mortal hands can never turn the tide.

###993###
When doubts do whisper, like a serpent's hiss,
And poison thoughts of fear into my ear,
I turn to thee, and find a perfect bliss,
That banishes all trouble, and all fear.
For in thy steadfast love, a strength I find,
A sturdy oak, against the fiercest gale,
That shall protect my fragile, wavering mind,
And through the darkest hours, shall prevail.
The fleeting fancies of a summer's dream,
May vanish with the morning's golden light,
But thy dear love, a strong and constant stream,
Shall guide me safely through the darkest night.
   So let the world its fleeting shadows cast,
   Our love, a beacon, ever shall hold fast.

###994###
The merchant hoards his gold with greedy eye,
And counts his coins with avaricious care,
But finds no joy beneath the boundless sky,
But only anxious thought, and heavy air.
For riches gained, may vanish in a day,
By fortune's whim, or by a knave's deceit,
And leave the soul in sorrow and dismay,
With naught to comfort, and with naught to meet.
But thy dear love, a wealth beyond compare,
A treasure that no thief can e'er purloin,
Doth fill my heart with riches, rich and rare,
And makes my spirit joyful, and my joy.
   So let the world its earthly treasures claim,
   I hold the riches of thy loving name.

###995###
When I do gaze upon the stars on high,
And see them gleam with an eternal fire,
I think of thee, beneath that distant sky,
And feel the strength of my most deep desire.
For like those stars, in their celestial might,
Thy beauty shines, a never-ending glow,
And fills my soul with an unending light,
A radiant warmth, that none but lovers know.
The moon may hide behind a cloudy veil,
The sun may set, and leave the world in night,
But thy bright image never shall grow pale,
But burn within my heart with constant light.
   So let us be, like stars in firmament,
   Our love eternal, heaven surely sent.

###996###
The fleeting moments, like a hurried stream,
Do rush and tumble to the boundless sea,
And carry off the fabric of a dream,
And all that once was bright and dear to me.
The bloom of youth, the vigour of my days,
The laughter light, that once did fill the air,
Are swept away in time's relentless maze,
And leave behind a burden hard to bear.
But in thy love, a stillness I do find,
A quiet harbour from the storm's fierce roar,
A constant peace, that soothes my troubled mind,
And brings me solace, now and evermore.
   So let the world its restless currents keep,
   My love for thee, a slumber, calm and deep.

###997###
When envious eyes do gaze with jealous fire,
And wish me ill, and whisper words of hate,
I turn to thee, and quench my soul's desire,
For in thy love, I find a nobler fate.
For like a fortress, strong and built of stone,
Thy steadfast faith doth guard me from all harm,
And makes me feel, though I be all alone,
A shield against the tempest's wild alarm.
The viper's venom, though it bite and sting,
Can not prevail against a heart so true,
And all their slanders, as on raven's wing,
Shall fade and vanish, when I look on you.
   So let them rage, and vent their bitter spleen,
   My love for thee, shall ever reign supreme.

###998###
The painted bird, that sings a stolen tune,
Doth lack the song that Nature doth impart,
And so it is with love, beneath the moon,
When it is feigned, and not from out the heart.
For outward show, though pleasing to the eye,
Is but a bauble, easily undone,
But when the soul doth whisper with a sigh,
A deeper, lasting treasure has begun.
The lover's vow, that rings with hollow sound,
May fade like mist before the morning's sun,
But when true passion doth the heart surround,
A bond of spirit, never to be outrun.
   So let us seek the substance, not the guise,
   And build our love on truth, that never dies.

###999###
When Fortune smiles, and all the world doth bless,
And banquets spread, and joyous music plays,
Beware the heart that leaps with happiness,
For fleeting are those bright and golden days.
But when the shadows fall, and tempests blow,
And sorrow's chill doth pierce thee to the bone,
Then shall the truest, faithful spirits show,
And lift thee up, when thou dost feel alone.
For in the sunshine, many friends abound,
Like summer flies that flit from flower to flower,
But in the storm, no faithful soul is found,
To shield thee from the tempest's raging power.
   So judge thy friends by trials they endure,
   And find in them a comfort ever sure.

###1000###
My love is like a fortress, strong and high,
With walls of trust, and battlements of truth,
That shall endure, beneath the watchful sky,
And stand unyielding, in its sturdy youth.
The winds of doubt may howl with furious might,
And tempests rage, and seek to breach its keep,
But in its heart, a constant, steady light,
Shall guard its treasure, buried true and deep.
The fleeting fancies of a common day,
Like scattered leaves, that whirl upon the breeze,
Can not prevail, nor bear its strength away,
But fall like ashes, scattered through the trees.
   So let the world its feeble efforts lend,
   My love's a fortress, that shall never end.
